# Changelog

All notable changes to Velox are documented here.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/),
and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

**Pre-1.0 versioning:** we're on `0.MINOR.PATCH`. MINOR bumps for new
features, PATCH for fixes. The public API is stabilising but not yet
frozen; breaking changes land on MINOR until `1.0.0`.

## [Unreleased]

### Added

- **Customer credit balance now applies to day-1 and cancellation invoices (2026-07-11, ADR-088).** A credit-holding customer's card was charged full price on the subscription's first invoice and the final-on-cancel invoice — out of parity with every surveyed platform (Stripe, Chargebee, Lago, Orb, Metronome: none exclude first/final invoices from automatic application). The balance now applies at finalize; the card is charged only the remainder; a fully covered invoice settles paid with no payment attempt. A failed credit application queues for the retry sweep and never charges the pre-credit amount.

### Fixed

- **Card-less customers now get the setup-link email for sweep-mediated invoices — exactly once (2026-07-11, ADR-087 follow-up).** A proration invoice (mid-period upgrade) is collected only by the auto-charge retry sweep, which silently skipped no-PM invoices every tick — the customer was never told and the invoice aged into overdue with zero contact; the same silence covered any invoice whose finalize-time PM lookup errored. The sweep now sends the setup-link email once, gated by a durable `no_pm_notified_at` marker that finalize-time senders also stamp (no duplicates across paths, no email-per-tick, and a customer without an address self-heals when one is added). Migration 0145.

- **Finalizing a zero-due manual invoice now lands it paid instead of stranding it "awaiting payment" forever (2026-07-11, ADR-087 follow-up).** The collect step's early return skipped the settle arm the engine's cycle/threshold/tax-retry writers all carry (ADR-066; Stripe parity: zero-amount invoices auto-mark paid) — a manual invoice finalized with nothing due sat finalized/payment_pending permanently, an un-actionable overdue attention item. Draft/tax-pending invoices cannot slip through: the settle re-reads status and the store's MarkPaid guard rejects both.
- **Post-finalize collection now survives a client disconnect (2026-07-11, ADR-087 follow-up).** The manual-finalize collect step ran entirely on the HTTP request context: closing the tab mid-charge aborted the Stripe call at its most ambiguous moment and killed the charger's 'unknown' outcome-persist, the retry flag, and the setup-link email in the same stroke — a possibly-charged customer with zero local record. Collection is now detached from the caller's cancellation (in the manual handler AND the engine pipeline, whose day-1/final-on-cancel callers also arrive on request contexts) and the manual charge carries the same 30s deadline as the engine's.
- **Manual-invoice finalize: transient charge failures now queue for the retry sweep instead of dead-ending (2026-07-11, ADR-087 follow-up).** The decline arm assumed every charge failure starts dunning — true only for definite declines; a breaker-open/transient/ambiguous failure started no dunning and set no retry flag, leaving the invoice with no retry path at all. Failures are now classified: definite declines stay dunning-owned (no flag — a second retry owner is a double-charge window); everything else sets auto_charge_pending, which the sweep's payment_status='pending' predicate keeps safe.
- **Manual-invoice finalize: a "ready" payment setup without a payment-method ID now queues for retry + emails the setup link instead of dead-ending (2026-07-11, ADR-087 follow-up).** The readiness check tested setup status but not the card token it was about to charge; an empty token drew a guaranteed charger rejection into the no-retry decline arm — no flag, no dunning, no email. The predicate now requires the PM ID, routing that state to the self-healing arm, matching the engine's collect sites.

- **A transient payment-setup read error no longer emails "payment method needed" to customers who have a card on file (2026-07-11, ADR-087).** All four post-finalize collect paths conflated "couldn't determine payment state" with "no payment method"; the shared collection pipeline now queues the invoice for the retry sweep (which re-resolves) and stays quiet. Same fix class: an invoice whose pre-charge reload failed used to silently drop out of every retry path — it now lands on the retry sweep too. The four hand-copied collect blocks (cycle close, day-1, final-on-cancel, threshold fire) are now one pipeline, so this class can't re-drift per-site.

### Security

- **Go toolchain bumped 1.25.11 → 1.25.12 (2026-07-09).** Picks up the `crypto/tls` fix for GO-2026-5856 (a Go standard-library vulnerability that `govulncheck` began flagging in CI); no application code change — go.mod + the CI `go-version` pins only.

### Added

- **Late usage events are now observable: `velox_usage_late_event_total` + a WARN per >24h-late live event (2026-07-10).** A live event stamped in the past is accepted (late events are industry-standard; rejecting breaks retries and stream pipelines), but one landing inside an already-finalized period is stored and never billed — previously with zero operator signal. Late live events now increment a counter and log the customer/meter/timestamp; backfill-origin events are excluded (the documented-safe intentional path). Whether to true-up closed periods or reject past a window remains a deferred billing-policy decision — this ships the visibility, not the policy.

### Changed

- **Recipes reworked to an idempotent, additive “apply” (2026-07-08, ADR-085, supersedes ADR-083/084).** Installing a recipe adopt-or-creates the shared catalog (meter + prices + bindings) by key and **generates one fresh plan** wired to the meter — it never adopts a plan by code, never republishes a price, and never mutates anything a live subscription bills under, so re-applying is a safe no-op that returns the existing instance instead of a 409, and a freshly-built plan can’t inherit a missing meter (silent-$0 is structurally impossible). This **dissolves** the whole plan-collision / conformance / provenance / under-billing class rather than fencing it with a gate. **No uninstall** — a recipe hands off operator-owned objects (plans carry live subs; the catalog is shared), so nothing is safe to retract; retire a plan by archiving it. Also removed the dead `force` flag and unused sample-data scaffolding, and de-jargoned the dashboard recipe UI for operators. Deferred behind named triggers: additive updates from a newer template version, a “newer version available” nudge, and an explicit opt-in reprice-migration for existing subs. See ADR-085 for the full rationale, rejected alternatives (ADR-083’s gate; the never-merged ADR-084 reuse-and-warn), and industry grounding.
### Fixed

- **A misconfigured deployment now refuses to boot instead of silently changing money math (2026-07-10).** The billing engine's 24 collaborators are wired via setters (the engine and its peer services are mutually referential, so construction-time injection can't cover them all) — and ~10 production paths branch on a nil collaborator with a *different money outcome* (a nil credit-granter silently skips a cancel refund; a nil credit-note adjuster skips a tax reversal; a nil headroom reader disables the overcharge cap). `engine.MustValidate()` now runs at boot after the last collaborator is wired and panics naming **every** nil field; a reflection drift-guard keeps a future 25th collaborator from escaping the check, and a boot-proof integration test constructs the real server against a real database so a dropped `Set*` call fails in CI, not at 3am. (Stage 1 of design-review redesign #3 — the per-dependency deletion of the nil arms themselves follows separately.)

- **Omitted `reset_billing_cycle` now defaults to `false` — keep the billing anchor on a threshold fire (2026-07-10). Behavior change.** The PATCH default was `true` behind a comment claiming Stripe parity; verified wrong — Stripe's `reset_billing_cycle_anchor` defaults to *false* (anchor unchanged), and keep-anchor is Lago/Orb/Metronome's only mode. The flip also keeps silent-default operators clear of the ADR-066 §5 `{in_advance × reset=true}` interaction. Explicitly-supplied values are unaffected (pointer field); the dashboard dialog's checkbox default flipped to match. Free at zero customers, breaking later — which is why it ships now.

- **A final-on-cancel invoice can no longer be silently mis-billed by a transient read failure (2026-07-10).** The cancel bill's segment-aware builder swallowed two errors its cycle-close analog fails loudly on: a change-log read failure silently billed a changed sub's final invoice as one full-window line at the current plan's rate, and a segment whose plan couldn't be hydrated was silently dropped — underbilling with no operator signal. Both now fail the cancel bill (the operator's cancel retries), matching the cycle path's fail-loud contract (`feedback_no_silent_fallbacks`). Pinned by two tests that assert no invoice is created on either failure.
- **"Resend setup link" no longer reports success for an email that was never sent, and the banner states verifiable behavior instead of asserting a completed send (2026-07-10).** The setup-link notifier treated a customer with no email address as a silent no-op (returned plain success), so `POST /{id}/resend-setup-link` answered `200 {"status":"sent"}` and the operator got a success toast for a send with no recipient. The notifier now returns a **typed outcome** (`sent` / `skipped_no_email`): the endpoint answers a typed **409 `no_email_on_file`** naming what actually works (add an email, or copy the link from the customer page), and the engine's finalize/threshold/cancel logs state the real disposition ("setup-link email skipped: customer has no email on file") instead of a premature "notifying customer". The no-PM banner's has-email copy now reads *"the engine emails the customer a setup link when an invoice finalizes… the invoice timeline and Sent emails show whether it was delivered"* — stating engine behavior and pointing at the delivery record, rather than "has been emailed", which the classifier cannot verify (false under a suppressed address or delivery failure). Establishes the typed-effect-outcome rule prospectively (design-review principle amendment): returning nil for a skipped effect is forbidden. Endpoint dispositions + banner copy pinned by tests.

- **`payment_method.attached` / `payment_method.updated` are now subscribable webhooks (2026-07-10).** Velox has emitted both events since the payment-methods arc — but they were never added to the emit catalog (`KnownWebhookEventTypes`), so an endpoint subscribing to events Velox actually fires was rejected with *"unknown event type — Velox never emits it."* Both are now in the catalog, the docs event table, and the dashboard's event picker (new "Payment method" group); the emit sites use the typed constants so the catalog can't drift from the emits again. Found by the 2026-07-10 design census.

- **A tax-deferred proration invoice is now auto-retried instead of sitting draft forever (2026-07-10).** The mid-cycle plan-change (proration) writer deferred correctly on a tax failure — draft, `tax_status=pending` — but its DTO mirror lacked the three deferral facts, so the row landed with `tax_error_code=''`, which never matches the tax-retry reconciler's retryable-code filter: the invoice was **never picked up for retry** and sat unfinalized/uncharged until an operator manually retried off a context-free banner. This was the third documented field-drop on the same hand-copied mirror (provider provenance and the reverse-charge legend were the first two — the mirror is slated for dissolution into a shared `domain.TaxFacts` value type per the 2026-07-10 design review). The mirror + adapter + writer now carry `tax_deferred_at` / `tax_pending_reason` / `tax_error_code` (the local failure arm classifies via the same `tax.Classify` taxonomy the engine uses), and the writer stamps `billing_timezone`, which every engine writer stamps and this one omitted. Mutation-verified tests on both deferral routes.

- **A spend-threshold invoice for a customer with no payment method is now queued for charge-on-attach and the customer is emailed the setup link (2026-07-10).** The threshold fire's collect arm had no no-PM branch: unlike cycle-close invoices, a threshold invoice for a card-less customer was never flagged `auto_charge_pending` (so attaching a card later charged nothing) and never triggered the setup-link email — it sat unpaid until it aged into overdue. The arm now mirrors the cycle path exactly (queue + notify) for finalized invoices; a tax-deferred *draft* fire is queued-but-quiet — `auto_charge_pending` is set (inert while draft: the sweep filters `status='finalized'`; the charger refuses non-finalized invoices by pre-existing guard) so the sweep collects the invoice the moment tax retry finalizes it, since the tax-retry path itself has no collect arm; no email while totals aren't final. Pinned by mutation-verified tests for the no-PM arm and the draft arm. Found by the 2026-07-10 design-quality census; the draft semantics were corrected by the same review's verification pass.

- **Clock-pinned relative-time UI can no longer silently revert to wall-clock, and two credit-expiry validation bugs it was hiding are fixed (2026-07-10, ADR-086).** Every dashboard surface that renders a value *relative to "now"* — "X ago", "in N days", cycle %, rolling usage windows, due/expiry badges — must read "now" from a clock-pinned entity's `frozen_time`, not the browser clock, or it lies once the clock is advanced. The #410/#411/#413 audit fixed the *instances* by threading an optional anchor, but every helper still fell back to `?? Date.now()` — so a newly-added surface that forgot the anchor reverted to wall-clock, a silent regression visible only after a clock advance. The relative-time helpers (consolidated in `web-v2/src/lib/effectiveNow.ts`) now take a **branded `EffectiveNow`** constructed *only* via `effectiveNow(frozenISO)` (the clock's frozen time when pinned, wall time when not) or an explicit `wallClockNow()` (the forensic/egress layer — audit log, email/webhook outbox — and never-pinned entities like API keys / webhook endpoints), with **no `Date.now()` fallback anywhere** — so omitting the anchor is now a **compile error**, not a runtime bug. A second, independent gate — an ESLint `no-restricted-syntax` rule banning raw `Date.now()` / argless `new Date()` in app code — stops a hand-rolled computation bypassing the helpers (genuine calendar/infra uses opt out with a one-line reason). The type gate immediately surfaced **two real latent bugs the instance-sweep had missed**, both *input validation* rather than display: a clock-pinned customer's **credit-expiry** date validation (the customer invoice composer and the credit-grant dialog) checked "must be a future date" against wall-clock, so a customer frozen in 2027 would wrongly accept a 2026 (sim-past) expiry — both now anchor on the customer's simulated now. Closes the **FE half** of the ADR-086 24-finding simulated-data audit (the backend sweep-gates + teardown are the other half, above). Drift-guard `web-v2/tests/effectiveNow.test.ts` (`npm test`, on Node's built-in runner — no new deps) proves each helper measures against the anchor via a frozen-2027 assertion a leaked `Date.now()` would fail. FE-only; no schema or wire-shape change.

- **A simulated (test-clock) invoice with no subscription is no longer auto-charged or dunned by the wall-clock scheduler (2026-07-09, ADR-029).** The auto-charge and dunning sweeps excluded clock-pinned work via a `subscriptions … test_clock_id` join, which a **customer-pinned one-off** (no `subscription_id`, so nothing to join through) fell straight past — so it got charged/dunned against wall-clock the moment a test card attached, violating ADR-029 ("the wall-clock scheduler never charges a clock-pinned invoice") and potentially emailing a real address about a simulated invoice. All five wall-clock invoice sweeps (`ListAutoChargePending`, `ListFailedWithoutDunningRun`, dunning `ListDueRuns`, and tax `ListPendingTaxRetry` / `ListPendingTaxCommit`) now gate on the invoice's **own durable `is_simulated` flag** — catching every simulated invoice, subscription-owned or one-off — while the catchup `…ForClock` paths still drive the simulated ones in simulated time; generalizes the same `is_simulated=false` gate `ListPendingTaxReversal` already shipped. Real-Postgres tests on all five sweeps. Test-mode only (simulated invoices are `livemode=false`). Part of the ADR-086 simulated-data-lifecycle arc — this is the *live-clock* half (a simulated invoice must not be swept while its clock is still alive); the *deleted-clock* half is the teardown below. The tax sweeps have catchup counterparts (`ListPendingTaxRetryForClock` / inline `CommitTax` on Advance) that drive simulated-invoice tax in sim time. No schema change.

- **Deleting a test clock now tears down its entire simulated customer graph, and the clock is hard-deleted (2026-07-09, ADR-086, migration 0144).** Previously (ADR-016) a clock delete *soft*-deleted the clock and merely *detached* its customers (`test_clock_id → NULL`) while cancelling their subs — which left every simulated invoice, credit note, usage event, and ledger entry behind with its "I'm simulated" pin nulled, so the wall-clock sweeps grabbed the orphans (the leak class the audit found in 24 places, e.g. a detached one-off invoice with no subscription to gate on). `testclock.Delete` now removes the clock and, in one transaction, every customer pinned to it and every row those customers own — invoices + their line-item / dunning / tax children, credit notes, subscriptions (+ items / changes / thresholds), usage events, the credit ledger, per-customer config, and portal rows — deleted **bottom-up** so the financial-row `RESTRICT` guards (migration 0015) never trip, and the customers **last** so their `ON DELETE SET NULL` fires on nothing. After it runs no simulated row survives, so *no* wall-clock plane can act on one; the deletion is still recorded in the audit log, and phantom-MRR from `canceled_at = NULL` subs is gone because the subs are deleted, not canceled. This is the Stripe test-clock model (a sandbox customer is discarded with its clock) and it retires the soft-delete machinery — the `test_clocks.deleted_at` column, its partial index, and 8 now-vestigial `deleted_at IS NULL` read filters are dropped (migration 0144). Completeness is mechanized so it can't rot: two schema-discovering arch-tests assert every `customer_id` table is torn down or allowlisted-with-reason (**Layer A** — which caught `customer_discounts`, missing from the set, and a since-dropped table) and that the delete set is FK-closed so a teardown can neither abort nor leave a dangling reference (**Layer B**), atop a real-Postgres integration test and a mutation-verify. Chosen over a heavier "durable `sim_clock_id` discriminator on every table" alternative that teardown makes unnecessary at zero customers (ADR-086 *Alternatives considered*). Test-mode only (`livemode=false`).

- **Analytics now excludes simulated (test-clock) data from every aggregate metric (2026-07-09, ADR-086).** The dashboard overview, MRR / revenue charts, and usage analytics aggregate rows onto a shared **wall-clock** time axis (revenue over real dates, MRR, period counts), but ~26 of those queries carried no simulated-data filter — so in **test mode** a test-clock customer's simulated invoices / subscriptions / usage (whose timestamps are stamped at the clock's frozen time) were summed into the real-time figures, inflating counts and landing in the wrong time buckets. (Live mode was always clean — simulated data is `livemode=false`, never in the live view; production numbers were never affected.) Every aggregate now excludes simulated rows, per-table because there is no uniform discriminator: `invoices` / `credit_notes` gate on the durable `is_simulated` flag, `customers` / `subscriptions` on `test_clock_id IS NULL`, and `usage_events` / `customer_credit_ledger` / `invoice_dunning_runs` via the owning customer / invoice (fragments documented in `internal/analytics/simfilter.go`). Per-row DISPLAY surfaces (customer / invoice lists, detail pages) are deliberately unchanged — they correctly *show* simulated rows, badged; only shared-axis *aggregates* exclude, and the catchup / `…ForClock` plane is the inverse (it drives only simulated rows, in simulated time). The completeness guard is **behavioral, not a brittle grep** (that "does this SELECT exclude simulated?" predicate is undecidable): `TestOverview_ExcludesSimulatedData` asserts that adding a full simulated customer graph — every timestamp in-window, every discriminator set — moves **no** overview number, so a new aggregate that forgets its filter fails CI (mutation-verified: stripping the revenue filter makes a simulated $777 invoice leak into Revenue and the test goes red). Test-mode only; no schema change.

- **A simulated (test-clock) downgrade clawback is no longer issued against wall-clock time by the background reconciler (2026-07-09, ADR-029 / ADR-086).** When a downgrade claws back unused prepayment, the engine issues the clawback credit note in-band at the subscription's (possibly simulated) time — but if the source invoice's payment is still in flight, the note is *deferred* (`issue_pending`, ADR-059) and re-driven by a reconciler once the source settles. That reconciler (`RetryPendingClawbackIssue`) keyed only on `livemode`, so in test mode it swept **simulated** clawback drafts too and re-issued them against real `now()` — firing a (test-mode) Stripe refund + tax reversal on a simulated note at wall-clock time, violating the ADR-029 disjoint-flows invariant. Now the wall-clock reconciler gates `is_simulated = false` (the CN-path tax-reversal reconciler already did), and a new catchup counterpart `RetryPendingClawbackIssueForClock` runs during **Advance** (Phase 3.7 — after the charge phase, so a source that just settled this advance is terminal and its deferred clawback can re-drive): scoped to the clock's customers, it binds the clock's `frozen_time` so the note's `issued_at`, the credit-ledger grant / amount-due relief, and the tax reversal all stamp in simulated time. Mirrors the auto-charge / dunning / tax `…ForClock` catchup hooks. The advance summary and the "Last advance results" card gain a **Clawbacks issued** count. A real-Postgres test proves the wall-clock scan excludes the simulated draft, the catchup scan returns only the clock's, and the issue stamps `issued_at` at frozen time (a 2027 date that wall-clock could never produce). Test-mode only; no schema change.

- **The date-picker calendar no longer gets clipped inside a card (2026-07-08).** The shared `DatePicker` rendered its calendar as an in-flow absolute popover, so every `Card`'s `overflow-hidden` (there for rounded corners) cut it off at the card edge — most visibly on the customer **Margin** card, where the open calendar showed only its first week. It now renders through Base UI's `Popover` (Portal/Positioner/Popup — the same primitive `dropdown-menu`/`select`/`tooltip` use), so the calendar portals to `<body>` and escapes the clip. Base UI (not a hand-rolled portal) so a date-picker used *inside* a dialog (credit-grant / API-key expiry / subscription pause) stays dialog-safe: a calendar-day click doesn't dismiss the enclosing dialog. Also: the selected day now reads distinctly from a hovered one, and opening keeps the caret in the input (so ArrowDown on a half-typed date no longer flashes an error). Shared component — the fix lands on every date field.

- **`create_preview` no longer silently overstates a capped subscription — it now warns when its estimate excludes an overlay the real invoice applies (2026-07-08).** The invoice preview is a full-period *estimate* that deliberately doesn't replicate two things the cycle bill does: usage-cap scaling and mid-period segment proration (ADR-045). For the common/wedge case (no cap, no mid-period change) preview equals the invoice, but for a sub with a blocking `usage_cap_units` the preview showed the *uncapped* total — a number the real invoice won't match, in the exact "predictable spend" direction usage-native peers (Orb) treat as a headline guarantee. Rather than replicate the overlays (a deferred ADR-045 follow-up), the preview now surfaces the divergence on its existing `warnings[]` channel: a capped sub with billable usage gets "…excludes the subscription's usage cap…"; a sub whose plan/quantity/item set changed mid-period gets "…excludes mid-period proration…". The mid-period check counts only true mid-*life* changes (plan swap / quantity / removal) — the `subscription_items` insert trigger writes an `'add'` row for every item at creation, so a naive "any change row" test would have false-warned on every subscription in its first billing period (caught by the real-Postgres test). Clean subs stay warning-free. Honesty now; cap-accurate previews land when a design partner turns caps on. Guarded by `TestCreatePreview_EstimateScopeWarnings` (cap / mid-period / clean, mutation-verified). No wire-shape or schema change — `warnings[]` already existed.

- **The Customer dashboard now reads simulated time everywhere on a test-clock-pinned customer — the cost-dashboard cycle bar, "Last invoice · X ago", the usage-activity window, and the margin window (2026-07-08).** A subscription pinned to a test clock stamps its billing-period bounds, invoice `created_at`, and usage-event timestamps in *simulated* time (`subscription/service.go` and `usage/service.go` bind `clock.Now(ctx)`), but four relative-time surfaces on the Customer detail page still measured against the browser's wall clock. The "Usage This Period" cycle bar read **"Day 0 of 31 · 0%"** even after the simulation had advanced a full cycle to close (it should read "Day 31 of 31 · 100%"); the "Last invoice · X ago" line collapsed a simulated-future invoice to "just now"; and the Activity 7/30/90-day + Margin "Last 30 days" presets queried a wall-clock range sitting entirely *before* the simulated events, so both cards read **$0 / "no usage"** on a customer with a full month of simulated activity. Each surface now resolves its "now" from the owning entity's test-clock `frozen_time` (customer / subscription `test_clock_id` → `frozen_time` via a new shared `useClockFrozenMap` hook), falling back to `Date.now()` only for genuine wall-clock entities — the same effective-now pattern already used by the Due/Expiry badges, invoice-attention, and dunning rows; the shared hook also retires the copy-pasted clock map whose omission here caused the miss. Found by an exhaustive site-set audit of the whole "wall-clock now under a test clock" class (59 sites inspected, 6 confirmed, 0 false positives); the two remaining confirmed sites — the Invoices-list due countdown and the Dashboard recent-invoices "X ago" for **one-off** invoices — are a named follow-up (see the next entry). No backend change; wall-clock customers are byte-for-byte unaffected.

- **Invoices list: a one-off invoice on a test-clock-pinned customer now counts its due date against the simulation, not wall-clock (2026-07-08).** Closing the test-clock relative-time pass: the Invoices-list "Due in N days" badge resolved its "now" only through the invoice's *subscription* clock, so a MANUAL one-off invoice (no subscription) on a clock-pinned customer fell back to wall-clock — showing e.g. "Due in 61d" (green, not-urgent) while the engine, on simulated time, already saw it past due. It now falls back to the customer's own pin (ADR-027), mirroring the invoice-detail page; wall-clock invoices are unchanged. It reuses the customer / subscription / clock lookups the page already builds — **no backend JOIN**, matching the invoice list's deliberate frontend-resolution choice (the same `test_clock_id → frozen_time` maps used for the row's clock badge). The last site in the class — the Dashboard "recent invoices · X ago" label — is closed by the next entry.

- **Dashboard "recent invoices · X ago" now reads simulated time — closing the whole test-clock relative-time class (2026-07-08).** The sixth and last audited site: the Dashboard recent-invoices feed rendered its relative timestamp against wall-clock, so a clock-advanced invoice (whose `created_at` is stamped in simulation time) collapsed to "just now". It now resolves each row's baseline from the **customer's** test-clock `frozen_time` — the pin is customer-level and immutable and subscriptions inherit it (ADR-027), so the customer resolves *both* subscription and one-off invoices with no subscriptions fetch — via the shared `useClockFrozenMap` plus a by-id lookup of only the ≤5 customers shown. `formatRelativeTime` gained an optional baseline arg; its genuinely wall-clock callers (api-key expiry, "Updated X ago", webhook events) pass nothing and are byte-for-byte unchanged, and a non-pinned customer resolves to `undefined` → `Date.now()`. With this, all six confirmed sites of the "wall-clock now under a test clock" class are closed; no backend change.

- **LiteLLM usage ingest now honors a customer's test clock, instead of silently landing simulated usage at wall-clock time (2026-07-07).** The usage service already stamps events at a test-clock-pinned customer's `frozen_time` when the caller omits a timestamp (Stripe-parity, ADR-030) — the direct `POST /v1/usage-events` door relies on it. But the LiteLLM mapper *always* manufactured a non-nil timestamp (`endTime → startTime → time.Now()`), so when a payload carried no start/end (a synthetic or test-clock ingest), the injected `time.Now()` was treated as an explicit timestamp and the service skipped the clock resolution — the event landed at wall-clock, in the wrong billing period. That silently broke the flagship *advance-clock → ingest via LiteLLM → see it billed* simulation whenever usage was placed into a period other than "right now" (the basic ingest-then-advance-once demo happened to work only because the clock started at wall-clock). The mapper now leaves the timestamp **nil** when the payload has neither `endTime` nor `startTime`, so the usage service supplies the customer's effective-now (frozen_time when pinned, wall-clock otherwise) — matching the direct door exactly; real LiteLLM proxies that send call timestamps are unaffected, and there is no production/livemode impact (livemode skips the resolver, so wall-clock is correct there). Also closed the guard gap that let this regress: `lint-clock` — which forbids bare `time.Now()` on clock-pinned entities — wasn't scanning `internal/integrations/litellm`; it now does. Pinned by a mapper test (nil when start/end absent, verbatim when present) atop the existing service test that maps nil → frozen_time.

- **Usage invoice lines now show the configured rate ($0.000003), not a repeating, inflated back-computed one ($0.00000333333333) (2026-07-07, migration 0142).** A sub-cent usage line — e.g. 6,000 tokens billed 2¢ at a configured $3.00/1M = 0.0003¢/token — rendered its unit price as `$0.00000333333333`: the *effective* rate (`amount ÷ quantity`) at 12 decimals. That value is not just ugly, it's **inflated** — the true 1.8¢ was rounded up to 2¢, so `2¢ ÷ 6,000` overstates the configured 0.0003¢ rate by ~11% and reads like a glitch on the surface an AI-infra customer inspects first. Verified against how the industry actually renders usage rates (Stripe shows the *configured* `unit_amount_decimal`, which terminates; exact `qty × unit = amount` reconciliation is *not* an industry requirement — ProjectWorks / ERP.net / the EU e-invoice standard all display `qty × unit ≠ rounded amount`), the fix stamps the **actually-billed configured rate** onto flat-mode usage lines (`nominal_unit_amount_decimal`) and displays it across the dashboard, hosted page, and PDF via one `DisplayUnitAmountDecimal()` source — no frontend change (the wire's `unit_amount_decimal` just gets cleaner). The rate is **stamped at build**, not derived on read, precisely because a customer price override preserves the `rating_rule_versions` id while swapping the price — reading that row back would show *list* price on every negotiated line; the engine stamps the override-applied rate, so a customer on a deal sees their deal's rate. **Only flat single-rule lines** get it: graduated/package usage (a blended rate — no single nominal exists), prorated base fees (the effective per-seat amount is the honest figure; the full plan price would misrepresent a partial period), and manual/add-on lines (whole-cent unit already equals nominal) all keep the effective rate — scoped by a per-line-type audit of all invoice-line writers. Historical lines are unchanged (no backfill; NULL nominal → effective, as before). Pinned by a domain display test (nominal wins, inflated effective is what it replaces), a `nominalRate` helper test (flat stamps, graduated/package refuse to fabricate a rate), and a real-Postgres override-trap regression (the negotiated 5¢ rate is stamped and round-trips, not the 1¢ list at the persisted version). **Follow-up (2026-07-08):** the customer **Activity panel** and the **public cost dashboard** were still deriving the effective `amount÷qty` in the frontend — which rounded a sub-cent output-token rate down to **$0.0000** — so they now carry the same backend rate as the invoice via one shared `domain.DisplayUnitAmountDecimalFor` source (nominal for flat rules, effective for tiered), stamped from the same override-applied live rule; the frontend renders that value with **no client-side fallback** (an absent rate is a visible signal, not a silent proxy), and the invoice's `nominalRate` now delegates to that source so the three surfaces can't drift. Still deferred: a per-million display scale for token meters (`$3.00 / 1M tokens`), a genuine meter-config feature.

- **The no-payment-method banner no longer claims a setup link was emailed when the customer has no email address (2026-07-07).** On a finalized-unpaid invoice with no card on file, the operator attention banner unconditionally read *"the customer has been emailed a setup link … resend the link if they haven't acted"* — but the engine's finalize-time setup-link email (`NotifyNoPaymentMethod`) **skips silently when the customer has no address on file** (it treats a missing email as "a delivery gap, not a billing failure" and returns without sending). So on exactly the invoices where it mattered most — a B2B customer created via API with no email — the banner told the operator to wait on, or resend, an email that was never sent and *can't* be sent (the resend path has no recipient either), stranding the invoice until it went overdue. The banner now splits on email presence, driven by a new `AttentionContext.CustomerHasEmail` signal the invoice service reads from the customer record: with an email it keeps the emailed-a-link copy (and de-jargons the old *"open the customer page to drive setup live"* into *"…to copy the link and share it with them directly"*); with **no** email (or when the address can't be determined) it reads *"No payment method on file. The engine emails a setup link only when the customer has an email address on file — open the customer page to copy a secure setup link and share it with the customer directly, or add an email…"* and **drops the dead "Resend setup link" action**, leaving the one workable path (copy a link / add an email). That copy states the engine's *behavior* rather than asserting the customer's email state, so it stays honest even on the rare read-error fallback (it never flips back to the "we emailed a link" lie). The email lookup is lazy — only the finalized-unpaid-no-PM invoices that actually reach the banner incur a customer read, so list views don't pay a per-row lookup. The single-purpose `CustomerClockReader` was generalized to `CustomerReader` (it already returned the whole customer). Pinned by domain classifier tests for both variants and a service-layer test covering the read-error fallback and the lazy-fetch guard (has-PM / non-pending / paid all skip the lookup). Deliberate boundary: a customer who *has* an email but whose SMTP send fails is still shown the emailed-a-link copy — that's a logged, alertable infra failure, not the silent no-address product state this fixes. No schema change.

- **Documentation truth pass — 30 stale/incorrect statements corrected across the docs (2026-07-07).** A code-grounded audit of every doc (README, SECURITY, the ops runbooks, integration + design docs, ADRs, MANUAL_TEST) found and fixed claims that contradicted the shipped code. The prospect-facing ones mattered most: SECURITY.md claimed Argon2id passwords (it's bcrypt cost 12), listed a `cmd/velox-import` binary and Helm/Terraform/`charts/` artifacts and three compliance docs that don't exist, and tracked MFA under "WorkOS/Clerk" which ADR-014 explicitly rejects; the README described API keys as "HMAC-rotated on a 72h window" (they're salted-SHA-256 with an optional up-to-7-day grace; the 72h window is webhook signing). The operator runbook shipped an offline-payment SQL snippet that violates the `payment_status` CHECK constraint and never zeroed the balance, documented two inert `BILLING_*` env vars and a nonexistent `payment_setups` table, and claimed the scheduler has no leader election (it does). Also corrected: the LiteLLM "5xx on DB down" claim (it returns 200 with `errors[]` or 401 at auth), backup-considerations naming several dropped/renamed tables, tax-calculation still documenting the removed `fallback_manual` policy, MANUAL_TEST flows exercising the deleted feature-flags subsystem, and two ADRs (010's UTC-billing-math superseded by 058/077; 024's `source`/`is_simulated` primitives shipped). No code changed — docs only.

### Added

- **HA readiness: the SPOF register and the multi-replica plan (2026-07-06).** `docs/dev/ha-readiness-2026-07-06.md` — a six-tier, adversarially verified audit (28 findings, every claim carrying its file:line) answering three questions before any pilot's security review asks them: what is a single point of failure (with blast radius and lost-vs-delayed honesty), what actually breaks if you run two replicas today (10 verified hazards — and 17 verified-SAFE surfaces so future audits don't re-flag them: complete scheduler lock coverage, SKIP-LOCKED outbox claims, DB-backed sessions/idempotency, exactly-once invoice generation), and where downtime costs money (one place: the ingest edge — **verified against LiteLLM source: at stock config LiteLLM retries nothing and drops the batch on any send failure**, so callback events fired at a down or restarting Velox are lost client-side unless `max_retries` is configured; recovery is idempotent spend-log replay with a hard deadline at period finalize). Ends with the scoped multi-replica work list; the build trigger stays "design partner approaching production cutover". `docs/self-host.md` and `deploy/README.md` were contradicting each other about whether leader election existed (it does) — both now state one truth and link the audit.

### Fixed

- **The auto-charge sweep and a dunning retry can no longer charge the same invoice concurrently (2026-07-06 — HA-readiness hazard #11, the fast-follow from hazard #1's review).** The two charge paths mint Stripe idempotency keys that differ *by construction* (the `velox_purpose` suffix that keeps their emails deduplicated), so Stripe cannot collapse a concurrent pair — and the dunning retry charged on nothing but `amount_due > 0`, with no payment-status gate at all. Both paths now share one per-invoice charge lease: the dunning retry claims with `payment_status IN ('pending','failed')` — `'unknown'` deliberately excluded, so an ambiguous outcome (a Stripe timeout that may be a real payment) waits for the reconciler instead of being blind re-charged. That exclusion also closes a subtler same-tick single-replica window: the billing half's unknown outcome followed seconds later by the dunning half's due retry. A lost claim maps to the existing transient-skip signal, so no dunning attempt is burned on a charge that never reached Stripe.

- **The auto-charge sweep can no longer double-charge under a dual-leader window (2026-07-06, migration 0141 — HA-readiness hazard #1).** The sweep was the one lock-gated money path with no row claim: if a Postgres failover released the scheduler's advisory locks mid-tick, two leaders could both process the same invoice, and the second leader's post-credit-apply refresh would mint a **different** Stripe idempotency key from the first leader's outcome write — two PaymentIntents, one invoice. Each invoice now takes a per-invoice CAS claim (5-minute lease) before the charge leg: the claim re-asserts the full eligibility predicate, so a rival's outcome or a webhook settle landing between list and claim refuses the claim instead of charging stale state. Design points that survived adversarial review: the claim deliberately never touches `updated_at` (the idempotency key derives from it — key stability is what makes a re-claimed retry converge on the *same* PaymentIntent), leases expire in DB wall-time (frozen test clocks can't wedge them), the shared list methods stay claim-blind (a claiming list would have starved dunning enrollment), and the two provably-pre-Stripe skip paths release the lease so retries aren't delayed. Pinned by real-Postgres claim-collision, dual-leader-charges-once, predicate-recheck, and updated_at-stability tests. The review also surfaced a pre-existing sibling hazard (sweep vs dunning retry diverge keys via the purpose suffix) — filed as a named fast-follow in the HA-readiness doc.

- **A production Redis outage no longer locks operators out of the dashboard (2026-07-06).** `/v1/auth` mounted the general rate limiter, which fails CLOSED in production — so a Redis blip 429'd login itself, re-introducing exactly the DoS the in-code design note said was avoided (the brute-force control on auth is the always-on Postgres-backed lockout, not the limiter). `/v1/auth` now has its own limiter instance with identical limits that never fails closed. The boot logs claiming rate limiting "will fail open" unconditionally (false in production since the fail-closed change shipped) now state the real split, and four more comment/doc lies the HA audit caught were corrected: the LiteLLM "retries on 5xx" claim (ADR-033 amended — it retries nothing at stock config), the spend handler's "5xx on DB down" comment (it returns 200 with errors[] or dies at auth as 401), the shutdown comment claiming parent-ctx cancellation reaches the test-clock catchup (it deliberately runs on Background and can hold shutdown up to 10 minutes — size deploy grace accordingly), and a wrong advisory-lock constant name.

- **Billing emails reach the whole finance team — additional recipients + a credit-note send (2026-07-06, ADR-082, migration 0140).** Every automatic email targeted exactly one address, and credit notes had **no send surface at all** — an engine-issued clawback or card-refund credit note moved real money with no document reaching the customer. Customers now carry `additional_emails` (up to 10, stored **encrypted** like the primary, normalized/deduped server-side): they're CC'd — one message, visible Cc header, per-recipient SMTP envelope — on invoices, receipts, dunning warnings/escalations, payment-failed notices, and the new credit-note email. Credential-bearing emails (payment-setup links, password resets, invites) structurally never CC. `POST /v1/invoices/{id}/send` gains a tri-state `additional_emails` override (absent → stored list, `[]` → primary only, list → exact override) — **behavior change**: legacy `{email}`-only send bodies now CC the customer's stored list, the Orb-parity default. New `POST /v1/credit-notes/{id}/send` emails the CN PDF (issued CNs only) and shows up on the invoice timeline + customer Sent-emails. Failure semantics are deliberate: a suppressed primary blocks the whole send (never downgraded to CC-only), a dead CC address is dropped with its bounce attributed to *that* address (a leaked CC rejection previously would have flipped the primary customer to bounced), and a mid-send transport failure retries the whole message safely. Dashboard: customer form "Additional billing emails" field, CC field on the invoice send dialog, Send action on issued credit notes. During a mixed-version deploy window, old dispatchers deliver primary-only (degraded, never wrong).

- **Team invites — the shared password dies (2026-07-06, ADR-081, migration 0139).** One workspace previously meant one login: the installing engineer, the billing operator, and finance all shared a single email+password, and the append-only audit log — a feature the README sells — was attribution-blind with one user. Settings → Team now invites teammates by email: tokenized accept links (sha256-stored, single-use CAS, 7-day expiry, one pending per email) ride the transactional email outbox; a NEW teammate sets their password on the accept page and lands signed in, an EXISTING account is attached but must sign in with its own password (inbox possession alone must not open an already-privileged account). Removal deletes the membership AND revokes the target's sessions (sessions pin the tenant — without revocation a live session keeps full access), with self-removal and last-member guards. Membership endpoints are dashboard-session-only (API keys have no human to attribute the act to); invalid/expired/revoked/used tokens collapse into one generic error (no enumeration oracle); accept endpoints share the auth rate limiter. Deliberately NO RBAC: every member holds the full permission set; `role` is recorded (`user_tenants` CHECK expanded owner→owner/admin/member) for the future split and the UI says so. Audit events: `member.invited`, `member.joined`, `member.invite_revoked`, `member.removed`.

- **Paid commit invoices can finally be refunded — at the price they were bought (2026-07-06, ADR-080, migration 0138).** Phase 1 shipped commits with no paid-state unwind: credit notes 409'd, and a migration-month mistake (wrong amount, wrong customer, churn with unused commit) was a dead end. The relief leg closes it with the **telescoping price-ratio cap**, settled by a three-lens design panel and verified mechanically: `f(k) = RoundHalfToEven(GrossPaid × k, Granted)`, each relief refunds `f(K+r) − f(K)` where `K` is the cumulative credits retired by prior reliefs — so a discounted commit (pay $9,000, granted $10,000, $4,000 drawn) refunds exactly **$5,400**, never $6,000 face (draw-at-discount/refund-at-face arbitrage) nor $5,000 (consumption charged at face), and *any* sequence of partial reliefs sums to exactly the same cash with zero rounding drift. `POST /v1/credit-notes` gains a `commit_relief` block (`retire_cents` or `retire_all` — cash is always server-derived, never operator-supplied): ONE coordinator transaction creates the credit note, issues it, and retires the credits, so a crash can never leave cash refunded with credits still drawable; the credit-balance channel is structurally forbidden (it would refund the very block being retired); offline-paid commits (the migration norm) default to the out-of-band channel. A racing drawdown shrinks a `retire_all` instead of failing it, and an explicit over-ask fails with the live remaining. New `credit.commit_retired` webhook (in-tx), `commit_retired_cents` on the credit-note document, and the ADR-078 follow-up row is resolved. Unpaid commits keep the void path; expired commits are earned breakage (409); mixed-line commit invoices and dispute modeling stay gated with named triggers. Also: the ADR index had rotted at 064 — rows 065–080 backfilled.

### Changed

- **DP-readiness register relocated to the private planning repo (2026-07-06).** `docs/dev/dp-readiness-2026-07-05.md` moved to the internal `velox-ops` repo, following the 2026-04-28 public/private doc split: the register is a design-partner conversation playbook (pre-frame framing, pitch guidance), not consumer/operator documentation. The purely technical audit documents under `docs/dev/` (full-product audit, money-path playbook) remain public.

### Fixed

- **Dashboard auth events now actually reach the audit log (2026-07-06).** Every auth-event audit write — `login`, `logout`, `mode_changed`, `password_reset_requested/completed` — had been silently failing since the events were added: the `/v1/auth` endpoints run outside session middleware, so their ctx carried no livemode and the audit writer's tenant transaction refused to open. The handler logged an error and moved on (audit is best-effort on auth paths), so logins worked while the SOC-2 trail stayed empty — the exact attribution story the audit page sells. Auth events now stamp the session's mode (pre-auth events stamp test mode, the dashboard's default view), and the invite e2e pins that `login` / `member.invited` / `member.joined` rows actually land.

- **The pause-collection 422 stops lying about the product (2026-07-06).** Requesting the unsupported `void`/`mark_uncollectible` pause behaviors returned "…require an uncollectible invoice status **that does not yet exist**" — false since ADR-064 shipped mark-uncollectible as a live endpoint *and* a dunning final action in the same install; the API contradicted the product to exactly the API-first engineers evaluating it. The message now states the real deferral (auto-resolving each paused cycle's draft isn't implemented). Two MANUAL_TEST lines still asserting the removed hard-pause (`status=paused`) corrected to the real contract (`pause_collection_behavior` set, status stays `active`).

### Added

- **Commit burndown surfaces (2026-07-06).** "How much of customer X's $50k commit is drawn, and when does it expire?" — the hybrid commit+usage DP's primary finance question — was answerable only by reconstructing the raw credit ledger, and the headline Credit Balance mixed money-backed commit liability with free promotional credits in one number. New `GET /v1/credits/grants/{customer_id}`: per-grant granted/drawn/remaining/expiry (the same `amount − consumed` arithmetic the drain order runs on) plus remaining split by cost-basis class (`commit` / `promotional` / other). The customer page gains a **Credit grants** burndown table (kind badges, per-grant drawdown) and the Credit Balance stat shows a "Commit $X · Promo $Y" subline — the kind-subtotal split the reassessment made an explicit acceptance criterion. Peer anchor: Metronome/Orb surface commitment burndown prominently in customer views.

- **Versioned releases (2026-07-06).** Upgrades were unauditable: images published as `:latest`/`:sha` only, `git tag` was empty (the compose `.env.example` suggested pinning `v0.1.0` — a tag that didn't exist), and `velox version` printed a hardcoded April date on every build (also pinned as the `Velox-Version` response header) — the first incident question, "what version are you running?", was unanswerable. Now: a build-time stamp (`internal/version`, ldflags-injected; `dev` when unstamped), `velox version` and the `Velox-Version` header report it, pushing a `v*` git tag publishes pinnable `ghcr.io/…/velox:vX.Y.Z` **and** `…/velox-dashboard:vX.Y.Z` images (the dashboard image is now published at all — previously compose could only build it from source), and main keeps `:sha`/`:latest` with a `dev-<sha>` stamp. Peer anchor: Lago tags releases and explicitly documents "avoid the latest tag". `v0.1.0` is tagged with this release.

- **Margin window picker + Stripe-checklist refund events + a webhook-claim concurrency proof (2026-07-06).** Three small DP-readiness closures: **(1)** the customer Margin card gains a window picker (7/30/90 days + custom dates) — the API always took `from`/`to`, the UI just hardwired last-30-days, and "margin over a custom window" is the first month-end finance ask. **(2)** The dashboard's Stripe webhook checklist adds `charge.refund.updated` / `refund.updated` / `refund.failed` — the backend consumes them for async refund truth (ADR-063), but an operator following the 6-event checklist never subscribed, so a refund that later failed at Stripe stayed "pending/succeeded" forever — a money-visibility bug that only manifests in prod config (`stripe listen` forwards everything, so dev never reproduces it). **(3)** The webhook retry worker's `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` claim gets the same two-workers-race-disjoint real-Postgres test the email outbox already had (the reassessment flagged the asymmetry) — multi-replica safety is now pinned on both dispatchers.

- **The ops kit stops lying: real queue-depth gauges, a working scheduler alert, and a truthful runbook (2026-07-06).** The shipped Grafana dashboard queried three gauges the binary never exported (`velox_email_outbox_pending`, `velox_webhook_outbox_pending`, `velox_dunning_active_runs`), masked by `OR vector(0)` — the backlog panels flatlined at 0 through any real SMTP/webhook pile-up, and the runbook's scheduler-age page-tier alert had no metric at all. Now: the four queue-depth gauges are real (scrape-time COUNTs on a bypass tx — the app role's RLS would report a healthy-looking 0 forever; a failed metric query reports −1, never a lying 0), including the new `velox_creditnote_pending_issue_drafts` (ADR-059 rider — deferred drafts produce **no error logs by design**, so the gauge is their only surface), plus `velox_scheduler_last_run_timestamp_seconds` for the liveness alert. **Alarm restoration:** the payment reconciler passed a literal `capturedCents=0` to `SettleSucceeded`, structurally disabling the ADR-068 `payment.amount_mismatch` alarm on the webhook-drop backstop path — it now threads the PI's real `amount_received`. **Runbook/copy truth:** the "hit `POST /v1/admin/reconcile-payments`" fix cited an endpoint that has never existed; two SEV-1 steps instructed enabling a read-only mode Velox doesn't have (now: revoke keys / stop the container / deactivate endpoints via PATCH); §5 and the `payment_unconfirmed` attention banner promised the reconciler "resolves this automatically" while it deliberately skips `requires_action` PIs forever (copy now says what actually self-heals and what needs the operator); the credit-note store comment claiming deferred drafts are "surfaced by repeated ERROR logs" (they never log) is corrected. ADR-062's migratable-effect count amended 4→5 per the reassessment.

- **The compose stack ships the dashboard (2026-07-05).** `deploy/compose` handed out "dashboard owner credentials" with **nothing to log into** — the stack was API-only, and every operator surface the pilot depends on (Stripe connect, dunning, margin, invoices, audit log) required a laptop `npm run dev`, against a pitch that is literally "runs in your own VPC". A new `velox-dashboard` container (multi-stage `Dockerfile.dashboard`: `npm ci && npm run build` → static nginx) serves the built SPA behind the existing front proxy on the **same origin as the API** — no CORS, no build-time `VITE_API_URL` (the app falls back to `window.location.origin`). The front proxy routes `/v1|/health|/docs` to the API and everything else to the SPA with client-route fallback, and the SSE webhook stream gets a dedicated location (buffering off, long read timeout — the general 35s read timeout would have severed it). Peer anchor: Lago's self-host compose ships a `front` container beside the API.

- **Webhook consumer documentation (2026-07-05, `docs/webhooks.md`).** The DP's first integration task is a webhook receiver, and until now the `Velox-Signature` format, the delivery envelope, the retry ladder, and the event catalog existed only in Go source. The new doc covers: signature verification with copy-paste Node/Python verifiers (HMAC-SHA256 over `t.body`, dual-`v1=` rotation handling, timestamp tolerance), the envelope (`{id, event_type, created_at, data}` — dedupe on `id`), the six-attempt/~26.5h retry ladder and 2xx success criterion, the delivery contract (which events enqueue transactionally with their state change vs post-commit best-effort; at-least-once; no ordering guarantee), endpoint management incl. the 72h dual-signing rotation, and the full per-event catalog with provenance fields. The README's API-reference line stops overclaiming ("Full endpoint list" at ~34/76 routes) and states the spec's actual coverage honestly.

### Fixed

- **Webhook endpoints are editable, and phantom subscriptions are impossible (2026-07-05).** Two DP-readiness fixes on the webhook config surface: **(1) Event names are validated.** `CreateEndpoint` accepted any string and `matchesEvent` silently never fired — a Stripe-trained subscriber to `invoice.payment_failed` (real name: `payment.failed`) got silence forever, and **Velox's own three recipes** shipped endpoints subscribed to two phantom names (`invoice.payment_failed`, `subscription.updated`). Create/update now validate against the canonical emit catalog (`domain.KnownWebhookEventTypes`; `*` and `invoice.*`-style prefix wildcards still work), unknown names 422 with the real-catalog pointer, and the recipes subscribe to the real events. **(2) `PATCH /v1/webhook-endpoints/endpoints/{id}`** updates url / description / events / active **without rotating the signing secret** — previously the only mutation path was delete+recreate, which minted a new secret and forced a receiver redeploy, and recipe-created endpoints (inactive, placeholder URL, no edit surface anywhere) were permanently dead weight. The dashboard gains an Edit dialog (shared event picker with the create flow), and the webhook-endpoint routes are now in the OpenAPI spec.

- **Meters can gain a default rating rule after creation (2026-07-05).** `meters.rating_rule_version_id` — the DEFAULT rate applied to usage that no dimension pricing rule claims — could only be set at meter CREATE, and no recipe sets one: when a provider ships a new model, its events matched no `(model, token_type)` rule and the revenue was silently dropped at cycle close (a server-log WARN nobody tails), with no operator remedy short of recreating the meter. New `PATCH /v1/meters/{id}` makes the binding (and name/unit/aggregation) settable post-create, validating the rule exists — a typo'd default that silently prices nothing is the exact failure this closes. Peer anchor: Orb's matrix pricing requires a `default_unit_amount`, so unmatched usage is always priced.
- **Test invoices now say so (2026-07-05).** The hosted invoice page rendered a test-mode invoice indistinguishably from a real one — the outreach demo itself (a test key) makes unmarked test invoices the first DP-facing artifacts. The hosted payload now carries `livemode` and the page shows an amber **"Test mode — no real payment will be collected"** banner (Stripe Checkout self-discloses the same way); the public cost-dashboard JSON carries `livemode` too, so partner embeds get the field in the contract **before** the first integration rather than as a mid-pilot schema addition. Also: the dashboard's webhook **event picker gains the Credits group** (`credit.balance_low` / `balance_depleted` / `balance_recovered`) — the README sells these by name as the commit-drawdown top-up primitive, but a DP following the least-privilege path (subscribe to specific events) couldn't select them without hand-typing.

- **Subscription lifecycle webhooks can no longer be silently dropped (2026-07-05, DispatchTx subscription subset).** `subscription.created` / `.activated` / `.canceled` / `.trial_ended` — the events a provisioning/entitlements webhook consumer depends on — were dispatched *after* their transaction committed, from ~10 scattered sites (handler, service sweeps, engine schedule paths). A crash or disconnect in the commit→dispatch window dropped the event **with no row anywhere**: nothing to replay, nothing to reconcile (the old deferral's "recoverable by consumer reconciliation" mitigation named a mechanism that doesn't exist). The four events are now enqueued into the transactional outbox **inside the transition tx** by the subscription store's writers — one emit site per transition (create, activate, the three cancel writers, the two trial-end writers), covering the operator API, the engine's schedule paths, and the trial sweeps at once. Payload provenance is preserved (`canceled_by` operator/schedule, `reason=trial_end_cancel`, `triggered_by` operator/schedule) and the CAS transitions make each event exactly-once (a losing duplicate cancel enqueues nothing; a rolled-back cancel takes its event with it). The ten superseded dispatch sites are deleted — single writer. The remaining ~12 notification events (item/pending-change/collection/etc.) stay post-commit with an updated, honest deferral row.

- **Credit drains now record WHICH blocks they consumed (2026-07-05).** `drainPositiveBlocks` always computed the per-block `(block, amount)` attribution list for every drawdown and clawback — then discarded it, writing the consuming ledger entry's metadata as `{}`. Deferring the eventual per-block reversal redesign is fine; deferring the *data* was irreversible — every drain permanently destroyed the attribution any future per-block unwind or commit-burndown report needs. Both drain paths (invoice apply + negative adjustment) now stamp `{"drained_blocks": [{block_id, take_cents}, …]}` into the entry metadata (zero behavior change otherwise). Rider from the same reassessment: `GrantTx` silently dropped `grant_kind` (the struct literal omitted the field `Grant` carried), so every in-tx grant — the credit-note and proration paths — minted a NULL-kind block, misclassified into the paid drain class and invisible to kind-scoped reporting; it now carries the kind and enforces the same "commit is reserved" gate as `Grant`. Also struck four stale ADR follow-up rows the reassessment caught lying (ADR-057's window was closed by ADR-061 weeks ago; Bug B resolved by #381; the receipt-email row's "sub-ms" claim; the DispatchTx row's nonexistent "consumer reconciliation" recovery).

- **A cross-interval plan-swap refund can no longer be lost to a crash (Bug B, deferred by ADR-056 — closed 2026-07-05).** The swap's OLD-period refund ran entirely post-commit on the request ctx: a crash or client disconnect between the swap commit and the refund permanently lost the customer's unused prepayment — the retry 400s on the same-plan guard, no reconciler re-derives a missed swap refund, and the "surfaced at ERROR, never silent" comment was false under process death. Both of ADR-056's re-arm triggers had fired (idempotency middleware landed but is opt-in; the ICP's commit pricing makes in_advance the pilot default), so the deferred fix shipped as the `BillOnCancelDraftsTx` transplant: when every OLD-period funding invoice is **paid** (the dominant case), the refund credit notes commit as `issue_pending` **drafts inside the swap tx**, post-commit Issue relays the external legs, and a never-issued draft self-heals via the existing (reason-agnostic) clawback reconciler. A draft-create failure rolls the whole swap back — never a swapped sub with a silently-lost refund. Unpaid funding declines to the legacy post-commit relief exactly like the cancel path. The cancel and swap paths now share one allocation/draft trunk and one unused-base arithmetic helper (single source). Rider: the dashboard's item dialogs (add item / change plan / change quantity) now send an `Idempotency-Key` per dialog open — item mutations fire prorations and refund credit notes, so a network-level retry must replay the original response, not re-run the money effects.

- **Free/included allowances are now expressible — and the recipe catalogs are current and numerically right (2026-07-05).** Three pricing-surface fixes from the DP-readiness register: **(1) Zero rates are legal.** Authoring rejected a $0 flat rate or a $0 graduated tier ("unit price must be greater than 0"), making "includes N free tokens" — on virtually every AI-infra pricing page — inexpressible except via per-customer credit grants. Zero now passes (flat, tiers, and packages; the rating engine always accepted it — the gate was authoring-only); negative rates stay rejected (a negative *rate* is a discount misspelled — credits are the discount primitive, ADR-039). Stripe documents a $0 first graduated tier as the canonical free-tier shape. **(2) Recipe catalogs refreshed.** The Anthropic recipe priced a mid-2024 lineup two generations stale; it now carries the 4.5 generation (opus/sonnet/haiku 4.5 at published per-million rates) plus the legacy 3.x families proxies still route (dropping them would leave that traffic unbilled). The OpenAI recipe adds the gpt-5.1/gpt-5/-mini/-nano and gpt-4.1/-mini/-nano families. The Replicate recipe billed the A100 at **14¢/second (~$504/hour, ~100x retail)** under a comment claiming 1.4¢/s — rates now track published per-second retail (A100 0.14¢/s, +H100), and aggregation switched from `last_during_period` over cumulative totals (which bills only the LAST event per GPU class — silently wrong the moment two jobs overlap) to `sum` over per-interval deltas. **(3) Mapper↔recipe coherence is CI-locked.** The LiteLLM mapper learns the new model families (claude-*-4-5, gpt-5*, gpt-4.1*; dated ids and provider prefixes normalize as before), and a new test asserts every family token the mapper can emit has a pricing rule in its recipe — the exact drift that let the catalogs rot ("ingests fine, silently doesn't bill at cycle close"). demo.sh, README, MANUAL_TEST, litellm.md, and the Provider-costs page all speak the current model generation.

- **The ingest path no longer rides the 100/min CRUD rate bucket (2026-07-05).** LiteLLM POSTs one callback per LLM call, so any real AI-infra traffic above ~1.7 calls/s exhausted the general GCRA bucket within the first hour of wiring the proxy — and LiteLLM retries only on 5xx, so every 429 was a **silently dropped, permanently unbilled event**. `/v1/usage-events*` and the LiteLLM adapter now ride a dedicated bucket (default **1,000 req/s per key** — peer anchor: Stripe meter events allow 1,000 calls/s; Orb's *test mode* alone allows 2,000 events/min) that deliberately never fails closed, even in production: for ingest, a Redis blip dropping revenue data outranks the DoS argument that closes the general bucket. Both limits are now env-tunable (`VELOX_RATE_LIMIT_INGEST_PER_SEC`, `VELOX_RATE_LIMIT_GENERAL_PER_MIN`).
- **The Usage Events dimension filter actually filters now (2026-07-05).** The dashboard's dimension box (`model=gpt-4o`) sent a `dimensions` param the server silently ignored — the event log and stat cards re-rendered **unfiltered data presented as filtered**, actively misleading during pilot pricing validation. The param is now real: comma-separated `key=value` pairs matched via JSONB containment (`properties @>`, served by the existing GIN index; multiple pairs AND; boolean/number values matched typed, so `cached=true` matches the boolean). Malformed input → 422, never treated-as-absent — silently dropping a filter is the exact bug class this fixes. List and aggregate share the same WHERE builder, so the stat cards can't disagree with the table.

- **Five latent money bugs from the deferral reassessment (2026-07-05, sprint PR-1).** The DP-readiness adversarial pass (#376/#377) found five bugs no customer had hit yet only because no customer exists; all fixed with real-Postgres regressions: **(1) Silent double-billing on shared meters.** Migration 0026 dropped the one-live-sub-per-customer index "deferring to application policy" — policy that never existed — while cycle close aggregates usage by customer+meter with **no subscription filter**: two live subscriptions whose plans share a meter each invoiced the same tokens. Now a meter-overlap guard (this is that policy, scoped to the money invariant) rejects creates, item adds, and plan swaps — immediate *and* scheduled, `pending_plan_id` counts as billed — that would put one meter on two live subs (or twice on one), with a 409 naming the conflicting subscription and meter; disjoint-meter multi-subs stay allowed. **(2) Batch ingest double-billed on keyless retry.** `/v1/usage-events/batch` committed one tx per event, so a mid-batch abort (client timeout, dropped connection) left a committed prefix that the standard retry-the-whole-batch re-ingested — events without idempotency keys have no dedup defense. Batches are now **all-or-nothing** (one tx), validation failures return every failing index with zero writes, idempotency replays count as `deduplicated` success instead of 206 + error strings (the LiteLLM door's contract, now on both front doors), single-event replays return **200 + the original event** with `Idempotent-Replayed` (Stripe shape) instead of a bare 409, and an over-cap body gets an honest 413. **(3) Transaction-mode poolers silently halt billing.** Session advisory locks gate every singleton worker; behind PgBouncer transaction mode / RDS Proxy the unlock can land on the wrong server session, stranding the lock so every replica skips every tick forever — while `docs/ops/postgres-requirements.md` claimed "transaction-pooler safe with caveats". Boot now runs a topology self-check (backend-PID stability + two-conn lock/contend/release ownership) and **refuses to start** on definite pooling evidence; the doc tells the truth. **(4) Receipt-drop window was seconds wide, not "sub-ms".** The settle paths' email enqueues sat *below* Stripe network calls on the request ctx — a webhook client disconnect or a crash during those calls dropped the receipt/failed-payment enqueue (which has no reconciler behind it). Enqueues now run **first post-commit**, the whole side-effect block is detached from caller cancellation (`context.WithoutCancel`), ordering is documented cheapest-to-lose-last with an append-only-at-end rule. **(5) Offline payments audited and webhooked as $0.** `RecordOfflinePayment` read `amount_due` *after* MarkPaid zeroed it, so every wire/cheque recording told the audit trail and `invoice.payment_recorded` integrators that a zero-value payment landed; both now carry the booked `amount_paid`.

### Added

- **The golden path is now a CI gate (2026-07-05).** A new `golden-path` CI job bootstraps a fresh tenant, starts the API, and executes `scripts/demo.sh` for real on every push — recipe → test-clock customer → LiteLLM token ingest → provider cost rates → simulated month → finalized invoice + PDF → margin report. The demo script rotted silently for months once (it 422'd at step 6 while printing a success banner); now any API change that breaks the documented first-run experience fails the build instead of the next prospect.
- **The front door now works — and sells the wedge (2026-07-05).** A fresh-eyes 4-lens audit (runtime walkthrough, README truth, positioning, demo currency) found the prospect funnel broken: `scripts/demo.sh` 422'd at subscription create and at every usage ingest against the current API, hid the failures behind `>/dev/null`, printed an unconditional success banner, and — even fixed — could never mint a same-day invoice (a fresh subscription isn't due for a month). **Rewritten wedge-first and verified end-to-end**: one `anthropic_style` recipe call → customer on a **test clock** → LiteLLM-shaped token payloads (15 dimensioned events) → provider cost rates → simulated month → finalized invoice with per-`(model, token_type)` lines + PDF → **67% margin report**, with fail-fast checks on every call and rerun-safety. **Two real LiteLLM bugs fixed along the way**: list-typed `request_tags` metadata failed scalar dimension validation and silently rejected *every* token event on tagged calls (unbilled traffic; now joined to a sorted scalar, regression-tested), and replay dedup matched `ErrAlreadyExists` while the store returns `ErrDuplicateKey` — every proxy retry filled `errors[]` although the DB dedup was working. **README rewritten**: the flagship curls no longer point at a domain that doesn't resolve (`api.velox.dev` → localhost), prepaid commits are market truth #2, per-customer margin/COGS and the LiteLLM drop-in are first-class wedge bullets + comparison-table rows, the wedge-in-code example now closes the loop with a commit sale and a margin call, a real invoice excerpt shows what the engine produces, and the design-partner CTA offers white-glove *self-host* support instead of nonexistent "hosted access". Doc-code lies fixed in `docs/integrations/litellm.md` (7: callback name, phantom `livemode` field, dead host, "per-row 422" that is actually `errors[]` in a 200, `tags`→`request_tags`, cost-metadata claims, a verify step using an unsupported query param) and MANUAL_TEST FLOW X15 (canonical `model` family vs `model_raw`, replay asserts `errors[]` empty, joined `request_tags`). OpenAPI's two lying core schemas corrected (subscriptions create takes `items[]`, not `plan_id`; usage ingest takes `external_customer_id`/`event_name` with decimal quantity). `make bootstrap` re-run recipes now use the make-CLI var form and `.env.example` no longer declares empty bootstrap vars that clobbered caller env. GitHub repo description now names the differentiators.

- **Provider cost tables + per-customer margin (2026-07-05, ADR-079, migration 0137).** Velox now answers the question no billing engine answers in-app (verified: Orb/Metronome/OpenMeter all push COGS analysis to your warehouse): **"what did serving this customer cost me vs what did I bill them?"** Operators enter what THEY pay LLM providers in a **provider cost table** (`/v1/provider-costs` + dashboard page) keyed by provider/model/token type with decimal per-token rates (micro-dollar granularity). Every usage event is **stamped with its COGS at ingest** — snapshot semantics: later rate edits never rewrite history — via the single ingest funnel (live, batch, backfill, and LiteLLM paths all covered), resolving the raw model id first, then the model family. A new **margin report** (`GET /v1/customers/{id}/margin` + customer-page card) shows rated usage revenue vs provider cost with an honest attribution rule: per-model margin renders only where pricing rules actually pin the model — everything else lands in an explicit "not model-attributed" bucket, never a heuristic split. Events that predate a matching rate are counted honestly ("uncosted") rather than backfilled. The operator usage CSV export gains `provider_cost_micros`/`provider_cost_source` columns for warehouse reconciliation. Also corrected a doc-code drift: LiteLLM's per-call `response_cost` was never persisted (and being a whole-call figure across up to 3 events, stamping it would have triple-counted COGS — the design panel caught this); per-half observed-cost stamping is a named fast-follow. COGS is operator-facing only — it never renders on the customer-facing cost dashboard.

- **Prepaid commits + drawdown, phase 1 (2026-07-05, ADR-078, migration 0136).** Velox's credit-block ledger gains the commit primitive — the headline pricing shape for AI-infra customers (sell **commit + usage**): an operator composes a manual invoice with a **commit line** ("pay $9k, grant $10k of credits, expires never/at a date"); **finalizing the invoice grants the credit block in the same transaction** (`grant_kind='commit'`, linked to its funding invoice, fund-once enforced by a partial-unique index; a funding error fails finalize loudly — never a purchase that silently granted nothing). **Voiding** an unpaid commit invoice retires the grant's remaining balance in the void transaction (consumed stays consumed; the legal uncollectible→void sequence retires exactly once; uncollectible alone leaves the block live as a collections stance). **Commit invoices are cash instruments:** the customer's credit balance can never pay one (closes the "credits buy credits" hole where a card-less customer's commit invoice settles with its own just-granted credits), and credit notes are blocked on them with a typed error until the phase-2 refund-retire leg. **Drawdown order** is now cost-basis-aware: explicitly-marked `promotional` grants burn before all paid-class blocks (commits + existing unclassified credits), NULL-safely (`IS NOT DISTINCT FROM` — a bare `=` would invert the order for every legacy grant). **Balance alerts** (green field): `credit.balance_low` (per-tenant threshold), `credit.balance_depleted`, `credit.balance_recovered` outbound webhooks, enqueued transactionally with the ledger write; payloads carry `customer_id`/`balance_cents`/`threshold_cents`. Prerequisite hardening in the same ship: status-flip CAS on finalize/void/uncollectible (a pay-vs-void race can no longer void a paid invoice; void-vs-finalize can no longer resurrect an annulled one), one global lock order (invoice-row → customer advisory → ledger rows — removes a reachable 3-way deadlock), and the credit-apply path re-reads the invoice in-tx (a drain racing a settle no longer burns credits into an already-paid invoice). API: `commit_granted_cents`/`commit_expires_at` on line items, `grant_kind`+`expires_at` on POST /v1/credits/grant, `credit_balance_low_threshold_cents` on settings. Removed the phantom `VELOX_BILLING_ALERTS_INTERVAL` compose var. Design peer-verified across Metronome/Lago/Stripe/AI-infra + a 6-lens adversarial panel (`docs/design-prepaid-commits.md`). Dashboard support (composer commit fields, Credits kind badges, Settings threshold input) lands in the companion frontend PR.

- **Failed/pending refunds are now surfaced proactively (2026-06-28).** A credit-note's Stripe refund leg is **operator-retried**, not auto-swept (unlike the tax-reversal recovery) — money-out is treated conservatively. But the only place a stuck refund showed was a red "refund failed" badge buried in the Credit Notes list, so an owed-but-unsent refund could sit unnoticed. Now: **(1)** the dashboard shows a **"N refunds need attention"** alert (danger severity, mirroring the failed-payments alert) whenever an issued credit note has a `failed`/`pending` refund, linking to **(2)** a filtered Credit Notes view — `?refund_status=needs_attention` (new server-side filter; `needs_attention` → `refund_status IN ('failed','pending')`) with a dismissible chip. The count comes from a new `refunds_needing_attention` field on the analytics overview (real refunds only — `is_simulated = false`). This closes the discoverability gap behind the operator-triggered `RetryRefund` design (the retry action + red badge already existed; operators just had to *find* them). No migration, no schema change. Backend: `analytics/overview.go` count + `creditnote` list `refund_status` filter; frontend: dashboard alert + Credit Notes filter/chip.

- **Set a service period when creating a manual invoice (2026-06-27).** The **New invoice** dialog (customer page) gained an optional **Service period** field — two date inputs for the inclusive dates the invoice covers. It maps to the invoice's `billing_period_start/end`, which the backend, the Invoices-list "Period" column, the invoice "Period" row, the PDF, and the hosted page already render — the data model and API supported a service period all along; only the create UI didn't expose it (so a manual invoice always showed no period).
