The operator enters **inclusive** dates ("Jun 1 – Jun 30"); they're stored half-open at tenant-TZ start-of-day (ADR-058, via `startOfDayInTZ` with an end+1-calendar-day step) so a manual invoice reads identically to a subscription-cycle period. Both-or-neither + start≤end are validated; blank = a one-off charge with no period. Verified industry-standard before building — Stripe (`invoiceitem.period`, optional, renders + feeds revenue recognition), Chargebee, Zuora, and QuickBooks all carry a per-invoice/per-line service period (Xero is the lone holdout). Frontend-only (`CustomerDetail.tsx`); `tsc` clean. Per-*line* service periods (Stripe `invoiceitem.period` on individual lines) remain deferred — the invoice-level period covers the common case.

- **Per-reconciler recovery metric + a uniform sweep driver (2026-06-25, internal).** The six background recovery sweeps (payment-unknown reconciliation, tax-retry, tax-commit, tax-reversal, clawback-issue, credit-note-tax-reversal) now run through one ~25-line ordered driver that emits a uniform metric **`velox_reconciler_sweeps_total{reconciler,mode,outcome}`** (`outcome` = `run`/`advanced`/`error`) — previously only auto-charge retries were metered, so an operator couldn't alert on, say, a **stuck tax-reversal or clawback backlog**. The `run` series increments every tick so a reconciler that *stops* running is also alertable. Behaviour-preserving and net-negative LOC: it replaces six near-identical copy-pasted log blocks in the scheduler with one driver + an explicit ordered registration (guarded by an order-asserting test, since the tax-before-auto-charge sequencing is load-bearing); each reconciler's re-drive body and eligibility SQL are unchanged. The single-method `Reconciler` interface is also the seam the future obligation-queue drainer (ADR-062) plugs into as "one more reconciler" — no rewrite. `payment_unknown` (a Stripe state-sync) rides the metric envelope but is documented as never migrating to the queue. No migration, no behaviour change. Guarded by `TestScheduler_ReconcilerOrder` (exact order), `TestScheduler_Reconcilers_NilDepsSkipped`, and `TestRunReconcilers_OrderSkipErrorsMeterAlways` (nil-skip, error-never-aborts, metric-fires-even-on-a-0/0-tick).

- **Test clock "Last advance results" summary (2026-06-13, migration 0119).** After advancing a test clock, the operator had to hunt across the Invoices, Audit, and Dunning pages to learn what the catchup actually did. The clock detail page now shows a **"Last advance results"** card once the clock polls back to `ready`: the simulated span it covered plus the per-phase counts — invoices generated, trials activated, collections resumed, spending thresholds crossed, tax retries, auto-charges retried, credit grants expired, dunning steps advanced (only non-zero rows shown; all-zero reads as an honest "nothing was due"). The counts are **exact**, not derived from a time-window query: the billing catchup already computed a processed count per phase and simply discarded it, so this captures those returns into a `domain.AdvanceSummary` and persists it as a `last_advance_summary` JSONB column on `test_clocks`, returned on `GET /v1/test-clocks/{id}`. The summary is written on **both** the success and the partial-failure transition (a `had_errors` flag caveats the latter), so a failed advance still shows what completed before it broke. Matches the Stripe/Chargebee shape — the clock object carries the after-advance information, no separate endpoint or advance-events table. Deliberately scoped to counts for v1; the **invoiced dollar total and collected/uncollected split** are the flagged fast-follow (they need either a new dependency or an engine-signature change, so they're not bundled here). The simulated `advanced_from → advanced_to` span comes from the pre-advance frozen_time captured before `MarkAdvancing` overwrites it (threaded on the catchup job); on a retry the two collapse and the card shows only the destination. Guarded by `TestRunCatchup_RecordsAdvanceSummary` (exact counts + span on success, summary-persists-with-`had_errors` on partial failure) and the real-Postgres `TestPostgresStore_AdvanceSummary_RoundTrips` (JSONB scan/round-trip). No new endpoint; the loosely-typed TestClock response needed no OpenAPI change.

- **Server-side list search, invoice date/customer/past-due filters, and full-dataset ⌘K search (2026-06-12).** Eight operator-efficiency fixes from the dashboard ergonomics audit, all rooted in one architecture gap: list search/date filters ran client-side over the current 25-row page (inputs even said "Search within page…"), so a match on page 2+ silently returned nothing. **(1) Backend search params.** `GET /v1/customers`, `/v1/invoices`, `/v1/subscriptions` accept `?search=` — invoices match invoice number, subscriptions match display name/code (SQL `ILIKE`, metacharacters escaped via the new shared `postgres.EscapeLike`); customers match name/email/external ID/ID **post-decryption** (PII columns are encrypted at rest so SQL can't see them; the store runs a bounded 5000-row decrypt-and-match scan — the equality-only email blind index can't serve a substring box; upgrade path at scale = a search-token column, not a bigger cap). Customer name/email sorts order by plaintext on the search path. **(2) Invoices date range + customer filter server-side.** `?from`/`?to` (shared `timefilter` contract, inclusive both ends, malformed input → 400) bound `created_at`; the customer page's `/invoices?customer=…` deep-link now actually filters (the Invoices page previously ignored the param — and the Sent-emails card linked `?q=`, a key that never existed; both fixed, with a dismissible customer chip). **(3) "Past due" tab** on the Invoices list — server-side predicate (`finalized` + `due_at < now()` + payment not succeeded/processing), Stripe's list segment; deliberately computed from `due_at` because the `invoices.payment_overdue` column has no writer and is always false (documented in code). **(4) ⌘K palette searches the full dataset** — debounced `search=` queries replace the old cached-first-50-rows fuzzy match, and customer rows now show email (support often only knows the email). **(5) Copy affordances:** the customer page's External ID and the subscription page's customer ID gained CopyButtons. Search inputs debounce 300 ms, reset to page 1, and stay visible on zero-result queries; URL-state filters keep working. Also fixes subscription `display_name` sort (now maps to the real column; the old code proxied to `created_at` behind a comment claiming the column required a JOIN that the schema doesn't need). Guarded by `TestPostgresStore_ListSearch` (encrypted-at-rest match, status compose, pagination, plaintext sort), `TestBuildInvWhere_*` (escaping, date range, overdue, placeholder numbering), `TestBuildSubWhere_*`, `TestEscapeLike`. OpenAPI list-endpoint params documented + artifacts regenerated. No schema change.

- **Audit log: jump to an entity's history, and export the action detail (2026-06-12).** Two completeness gaps from the audit-subsystem audit. **(1) Entity → audit deep-links.** Customer, Invoice, and Subscription detail pages now carry an **"Audit log"** button that opens `/audit-log` pre-filtered to that resource (`?resource_type=…&resource_id=…`, a filter the page already supported) — previously there was no path from a record to "what happened to this," only the global sidebar. **(2) Export includes metadata.** The Audit Log CSV export emitted nine columns but silently dropped `metadata`, so the action detail an operator needs in a compliance pack (prorated amounts, old/new plan, `cancel_at`, the `meta.action` discriminator) lived only in the expanded UI row. The export now has a **Details** column carrying the metadata JSON. Frontend-only; verified via `tsc`.

- **`invoice.paid` outbound webhook (2026-06-12).** Velox now emits `invoice.paid` whenever an invoice transitions to paid — the single most-wanted billing webhook (provision access, send a receipt, reconcile on the integrator's side). It fires from **every** settlement path, exactly once: card payment, credits covering 100%, an operator-recorded offline payment, dunning recovery, and the payment reconciler's fallback. Emitted **transactionally** from the `MarkPaid` primitive — enqueued in the same DB transaction as the finalized→paid transition (ADR-040 outbox) — so it can't double-fire on a duplicate settle (the already-paid re-mark is a no-op that returns before the emit) and can't be lost if the transition commits. This is cleaner than dispatching from each of the 9 `MarkPaid` call sites and structurally avoids the miss/double-fire that approach risks (notably the reconciler's bare-MarkPaid fallback, which no caller-side dispatch would cover). Payload: `invoice_id`, `invoice_number`, `customer_id`, `subscription_id`, `amount_paid_cents`, `currency`, `paid_at`. Subscribable from the dashboard webhook-endpoint event picker. Guarded by `TestMarkPaid_FiresInvoicePaidOnceOnTransition` (one event on the transition, zero on re-mark).

### Changed

- **The billing timezone is now an org-level setting, not a per-subscription snapshot (2026-07-04, migration 0135, ADR-077 — supersedes ADR-074).** The three entries below (the ADR-074 arc: per-sub snapshot + its subscription/invoice display companions) are **reversed in model**: subscriptions no longer carry a `billing_timezone`. The deferred adversarial panel ADR-074 promised is what caught the flaw — **no billing platform anchors each *subscription* in its own frozen timezone.** Verified across six peers: Stripe's `billing_cycle_anchor` is a UTC instant with a display-only, freely-changeable dashboard zone; Lago and Orb attach timezone to the **org/customer** (default UTC); Metronome and the target market's own vendors (AWS/OpenAI/Anthropic) bill usage in UTC. The per-sub snapshot modeled a case that doesn't exist (two subs in one tenant billing on different calendars), and its display divergence (a frozen sub zone vs. the live tenant zone) was the *sole source* of the ~8-bug render class the ADR-075 arc chased. **Now:** billing math anchors on the one org timezone (`tenant_settings.timezone`, default UTC) — the three `subscriptionLocation`/`subLoc` helpers are deleted and all ~30 call sites resolve `tenantLocation(ctx, tenantID)` directly; the resolved zone is **denormalized onto the invoice at issue** (`invoices.billing_timezone`, kept from PR2 — that is where document-date stability actually belongs, on the immutable issued document, not speculatively on every running sub). Migration 0135 drops `subscriptions.billing_timezone` (added days earlier on the same arc, pre-launch, zero customers). A per-**customer** timezone override is deferred as a strictly-additive future extension (Lago/Orb's model) — not per-subscription, and not built without a named design-partner need. ADR-075 (canonical UTC wire) and ADR-076 (lint-tz + FE required-zone types) are unchanged and still earn their keep. Guarded by the rewritten `TestHandler_Get_PeriodDisplayTZ` (period renders in the org zone under two different org TZs, mutation-locked), the affected real-Postgres subscription/billing/invoice suites (the new INSERT/scan round-trips without the column), and the migrate up/down round-trip (0135's down recreates + backfills the column).

### Fixed

- **Dunning-policy gaps: a tenant with no *default* policy no longer breaks the billing catchup, and a recipe/first policy now works out of the box (2026-07-05, ADR-036 amendment).** Three linked gaps in dunning-policy resolution. **(G1) No policy was ever auto-default:** `upsertPolicyTx` hardcoded `is_default=false`, so the recipe's `"AI default retry"` policy — and any tenant's first manual policy — was created non-default; `GetDefaultPolicy` then returned not-found and dunning silently never ran until an operator explicitly `SetDefaultPolicy`'d. Now the **first policy per `(tenant, livemode)` is born `is_default=true`** (computed in-statement as `NOT EXISTS(… WHERE is_default)`, RLS-scoped; the partial unique index is the race backstop) — both recipe and manual creates inherit it, and `is_default` stays truthful in the DB (rejected a read-time "resolve-to-sole" that would have made `is_default` lie and introduced a 1→2-policy silent-stop cliff). **(G3) No effective policy hard-errored the money path:** the no-payment enrollment sweep routed `ErrNotFound` up as a per-invoice error, so an unpaid cycle invoice on a default-less tenant made the billing catchup report `had_errors`/`internal_failure` every tick (surfaced live during an S2 dry-run). Now `StartDunning` maps **only** that `ErrNotFound` to a deliberate-skip `InvalidState` (the same class as a *disabled* policy, which the enrollment adapter already swallows) — an unconfigured optional feature can't poison core billing (the SMTP-unset precedent); a real infra error still fails loud. **(G2)** Plain bootstrap deliberately seeds **no** dunning policy (seeding would shadow a recipe's own) — covered by the skip. Companion cleanup: `startDunningWithRetry` short-circuits the deliberate skip so disabled/no-policy tenants stop burning 3 retries and emitting a misleading "operator must start manually" error. Design chosen via a divergent panel. Guarded by real-Postgres `TestUpsertPolicy_AutoDefaultFirst` (first→default, second→not, livemode-scoped), `TestStartDunning_NoPolicyConfigured` (maps to InvalidState, not raw ErrNotFound), the adapter swallow test, and `TestStartDunningWithRetry_SkipsInvalidState`. No migration.

- **The timezone-display invariant is now enforced in CI, not just documented (2026-07-04, ADR-076, internal).** The ADR-074/075 arc fixed ~8 render-site bugs of one shape — a civil-day date formatted without an explicit zone, rendering in the process/host zone. That was "correct by developer discipline," and discipline demonstrably drifted. New guards make it correct-by-CI: **(1)** `make lint-tz` (grep gate, wired into the CI lint job, same convention as `lint-clock`) fails the build on a date-only `.Format` that doesn't render through an explicit `.In(loc)` zone — bare `.Format` and `.UTC().Format` on a calendar date both fail (the exact cancel/plan-swap credit-note bug) — and also asserts the ADR-075 process-UTC pin is present; a genuine UTC/filename case carries a same-line `//tz:ok`. **(2)** The frontend civil-day helpers (`formatCivilDate`, `formatCivilPeriod`) now *require* their timezone argument, so TypeScript flags any civil-date render that forgot to name its zone. A `civil.Date` type (the Java/Temporal approach) was considered and **not adopted**: Go's `time.Time.Format` is callable on every value, so a type can't forbid it — the lint is the complete-as-Go-allows enforcement, and adding the type would be a second partial mechanism that doesn't remove the lint. Both gates are mutation-verified. Also fixed a duplicate-invoice error detail that formatted its period in UTC instead of the invoice's billing timezone.

- **Four more customer-facing dates now render in the billing timezone (2026-07-04, ADR-074/075 follow-up).** A product-wide timezone sweep (every backend module + every frontend date surface) closed the last residuals in the same class as the ADR-075 audit. **(1)** The **cancel-proration** and **plan-swap-refund** credit-note line descriptions (`billing/engine.go`) formatted the period + change date with `.UTC().Format` — one civil day early on a positive-offset billing zone (e.g. a Tokyo sub's "period 2026-01-31 …" for a period that starts Feb 1) on a customer credit note; now `.In(subscriptionLocation)`. **(2)** The **public hosted-invoice page** rendered Due/Received/Voided dates with a bare `formatDate()`, but that route is unauthenticated so it had no tenant timezone and fell back to the *viewer's browser zone* — a due date that could sit a day off from (and contradict) the PDF downloadable on the same page. The payload now carries `billing_timezone` and the page renders those dates in it (UTC fallback, matching the PDF). **(3)** The subscription timeline's "Period Start" dot used a bare `formatDate()` (live display TZ) while its paired "Period End" dot used the frozen billing TZ — they could contradict each other after a tenant-TZ change; now both use the billing TZ. The sweep also **confirmed** the earlier four fixes correct, found all other emails clean, and correctly left operator-dashboard analytics bucketing (UTC `date_trunc`) alone as a separate reporting-timezone decision. No schema change.

- **API timestamps are canonical UTC, and customer-facing document dates render in the billing timezone (2026-07-04, ADR-075).** The API serialized `time.Time` fields (`created_at`, `billing_period_start/end`, …) in whatever timezone the value carried — and DB-read values didn't stay UTC: pgx decodes `timestamptz` via `time.Unix`, which lands in `time.Local` (the server process's zone). So on a non-UTC host the wire emitted a host-dependent offset (`…+05:30`) instead of canonical `…Z`; the app already minted instants in UTC (`clock.Now().UTC()`), only the DB-read path dissented. Now the process is pinned to UTC (`time.Local = time.UTC` as the first statement of `main()`), so every timestamp serializes host-independently as `…Z`. The instants are unchanged — no consumer that parses them (`new Date`, any RFC3339 parser) is affected — and billing math never read `time.Local` (it anchors in explicit zones, ADR-058/074), so nothing computed changes. **Companion fix from the blast-radius audit:** four customer-facing renderers (invoice PDF Issued/Due/Paid/Voided, credit-note PDF dates, the dunning "we'll try again on ⟨date⟩" email, and proration invoice-line labels) formatted a DB-read timestamp with a naive `.Format(...)` — implicitly the host zone — so they were pre-existingly TZ-naive (host/UTC, never the business's zone) and would have shifted a calendar day near midnight on a non-UTC host. These now render in the invoice/subscription **billing timezone** (ADR-074), UTC-fallback for legacy rows, matching the document's period. Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestInvoice_Timestamps_SerializeAsCanonicalUTC` (wire is `…Z`, mutation-locked) and `TestProrationLabels_RenderInBillingTZ` (label renders in the billing TZ, mutation-locked).

- **Invoice period range now displays in the invoice's own billing timezone, not the live tenant zone (2026-07-04, migration 0134, ADR-074 amendment).** The companion to the subscription fix below, on the invoice surface. An invoice's `billing_period_display` (the inclusive "Jun 1 – Jun 30" shown on the detail page, Invoices-list Period column, PDF, hosted page, and portal) was computed on read in the live tenant TZ — so after a tenant changed its timezone, a finalized invoice's *displayed* period shifted a day, even though the invoice is an immutable financial document. The billing timezone is now **denormalized onto each invoice** (`invoices.billing_timezone`, copied from the owning subscription's snapshot at creation across all four engine/threshold invoice-creation sites) and the read-path display + PDF/hosted fallback render in that zone; the frontend line-item "Covers …" note passes `invoice.billing_timezone` too. **No backfill:** an existing invoice's period was computed under whatever TZ was live when it was generated — not recoverable from stored data — so legacy rows stay NULL and fall back to the live tenant TZ (exactly what they show today); only invoices created after migration 0134 render in the anchor zone. Display-only — the invoice wire (`billing_period_start/end`, half-open RFC3339) is unchanged. Guarded by `TestInvoice_PeriodDisplay_AnchoredInBillingTZ` (snapshot vs. fallback, mutation-locked) and the real-Postgres `TestPostgresStore_BillingTimezone_RoundTrips` (the column persists through INSERT + scan — only a real round-trip catches a dropped column).

- **A subscription's period range now displays in its own billing timezone, not the live tenant zone (2026-07-04, ADR-074 amendment).** The ADR-074 fix below froze billing *math* to a per-sub snapshot but left the *display* of the period range ("Jun 1 – Jun 30") reading the live tenant timezone — so the moment an operator changed the tenant timezone, a running sub's *displayed* range shifted by a day even though its billing didn't: an IST-anchored period `[May 2 00:00 IST, Jun 1 00:00 IST)` read "May 2 – May 31" in Kolkata but "May 1 – May 30" in New_York (the inclusive last-day step only lands on the right civil date in the zone the boundary is midnight in — the snapshot). The backend now authors **`current_billing_period_display`** on the subscription (computed on read in the sub's billing TZ, the exact peer of `invoice.billing_period_display`), and the dashboard renders it verbatim instead of recomputing the range in the browser (which defaulted to the live tenant zone). Auxiliary labels the backend doesn't author — trial range, single period-end date, cycle-progress caption — now receive the sub's `billing_timezone` explicitly. Event instants ("Renews", "Next billing") legitimately stay in the current zone. The wire contract stays half-open; this is a derived display field. Invoice period-range display gets the same anchor-TZ treatment in an immediate follow-up (a denormalized `invoices.billing_timezone` column); until then invoices keep their prior live-TZ display — a pre-existing behavior, only observable for a tenant that has changed TZ. Guarded by `TestHandler_Get_PeriodDisplayTZ` (snapshot anchors the range; legacy empty-TZ falls back to live tenant TZ; mutation-locked against a tenant-TZ read).

- **Changing a tenant's timezone no longer silently re-times running subscriptions (2026-07-04, ADR-074).** A subscription's billing calendar was half-frozen: the anchor *day* was persisted per-sub (so a Jan-31 sub stably bills month-end), but the anchor *timezone* was read live from tenant settings at every date computation. So changing the tenant timezone — a control that reads as presentational — silently shifted the future billing boundaries of subscriptions that were **already live**, re-introducing the mixed-anchor drift (a period anchored under UTC rolling into an IST-anchored next period moves by 5.5 hours, occasionally onto a different calendar day, perturbing proration and revenue timing). Now the billing timezone is **snapshotted onto each subscription at creation** (the peer of the anchor day) and is immutable thereafter; all period-boundary and proration math reads the snapshot. Changing the tenant timezone is now **display-only for running subscriptions** (dashboard/PDF dates still render in the current zone) and only governs **newly-created** ones — matching Stripe's stored `billing_cycle_anchor` model. Existing subscriptions are backfilled with their tenant's current timezone (migration 0133), so there is zero behavior change for anything already running.

- **The MRR numbers stopped lying (2026-07-03).** Three defects in the dashboard's MRR/movement analytics, one of them permanent: **(1)** the point-in-time MRR reconstruction ignored item *removals*, so every removed subscription item kept counting in "MRR 30 days ago" forever — the previous-MRR baseline (and everything derived from it: trend arrows, net revenue retention) drifted upward without bound. **(2)** every MRR sum mixed currencies — a €99 plan added 9900 "cents" to a USD MRR total (revenue on the same page was already correctly scoped); all MRR/ARR/movement figures are now scoped to the tenant's default currency, matching the page's currency label. **(3)** adding or removing an item on a continuing subscription moved headline MRR but appeared nowhere in the movement breakdown (New/Expansion/Contraction/Churned), so movement Net never reconciled with the actual MRR delta — adds now count as expansion and removals as contraction, and the reconciliation holds even through remove-then-restore sequences. No schema change; the queries ride the indexes shipped on 2026-07-03 (migration 0130/0131).

- **Self-hosting stopped being a dead end (2026-07-03, ADR-073).** Three roots fixed together. **(1) One bootstrap.** `POST /v1/bootstrap` used to mint a tenant and two test keys, full stop — no dashboard login (bootstrapped installs could never sign in), no live-mode key (no path to charging real cards), no settings row, while the `make bootstrap` CLI did all of that; the two writers had already drifted. Both are now thin callers of one bootstrap routine: one all-or-nothing transaction creates tenant + settings + test/live/publishable keys + the dashboard owner, inputs are validated **before** anything is written (a bad password can no longer half-provision an install that then answers "already bootstrapped" forever), concurrent calls are serialized (exactly one succeeds), and a bootstrapped install answers a uniform 409 to any probe — responses no longer reveal whether a guessed token was valid. Credentials return exactly once with `Cache-Control: no-store`. **Breaking:** the endpoint's key prefixes are now mode-marked (`vlx_secret_test_…`/`vlx_secret_live_…`) and the response fields renamed to match. **(2) `APP_DATABASE_URL` is real — and production refuses the default password.** The documented variable was never read; the runtime (RLS-enforcing) connection was always derived as `velox_app:velox_app` — a password printed in the public docs, which the production compose stack actually used. The variable is now honored verbatim; `staging`/`production` refuse to boot when it's missing, carries an empty/default password, or points at a role that can bypass RLS (superuser/`BYPASSRLS` — catches a copied `DATABASE_URL`); short bootstrap tokens (<16 chars) are refused too. The compose stack generates the role from a required `VELOX_APP_DB_PASSWORD` (existing volumes: one `ALTER ROLE` — recipe in `deploy/compose/README.md`), and ships `redis` in-stack (production fail-closes the rate limiter; without Redis every auth/bootstrap call would 429) plus `TRUST_PROXY` so rate limits and audit logs key on real client IPs, not the nginx container. **(3) Racing replica boots can no longer corrupt migration state.** The hybrid migration runner decided what to apply from unlocked reads — two replicas booting together could double-apply, rewind the recorded version, or push a `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` file down the transactional path (a deployment-wide crash-loop). The loop now serializes on an advisory lock (acquired by polling: a *blocking* acquire deadlocks against `CONCURRENTLY`'s snapshot wait — caught by the racing test); the losing replica finds the work done and skips. Also: an ops-docs truth sweep (runbook/backup/postgres-requirements/grafana pointed at `/v1/healthz`-style endpoints that 404 — real: `/health`, `/health/ready`, `/metrics`; phantom `VELOX_OWNER_*`/`VELOX_DASHBOARD_*`/`STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET` env vars removed; both quick starts gained the missing `cp .env.example .env`; the README's "embeddable `<CostDashboard/>`" claim replaced with the token-authenticated JSON endpoint that actually ships; `deploy/README.md` no longer advertises Helm/Terraform/k8s paths that don't exist).

- **Invoice emails and webhooks stopped double-sending under load — and SMTP got strict (2026-07-03, ADR-072).** Both delivery queues marked an entire batch's outcomes in one transaction at the end: when a late row ran long, the whole batch's marks were lost and **already-delivered invoice emails were re-sent** on the next tick. Batches now claim rows with a lease and record each outcome immediately and irrevocably; attempt counts advance at claim time so a crashing row still ages toward the dead-letter queue instead of retrying forever; a poisoned row can no longer stall the rest of its batch; and emails that can never succeed (unparseable payload, known-bounced recipient) fail immediately instead of retrying for three days. Webhook events are now created **atomically with all their delivery records** (a crash mid-fan-out used to strand events that no retry would ever pick up, or mint duplicate events receivers can't dedupe), a delivered webhook can never be flipped back to pending by a slow worker's stale write, and the retry worker is leader-elected across replicas. **Breaking / self-host note:** SMTP now enforces STARTTLS strictly — the old opportunistic upgrade could be silently stripped to plaintext by an on-path attacker. Local no-TLS sandboxes (Mailpit/MailHog) must set `SMTP_TLS=none` explicitly (the shipped compose/.env already do); `SMTP_TLS=none` is refused in production; the boot log prints the active transport mode. If a stale config lands emails in the dead-letter queue after upgrading, fix the config and requeue: `UPDATE email_outbox SET status='pending', attempts=0, next_attempt_at=now() WHERE status='failed'`.

- **Every customer is now selectable everywhere — and the dead feature-flag subsystem is gone (2026-07-03, migration 0132).** Dashboard pickers loaded one 50-customer page and filtered it client-side, so past the 50th customer things quietly broke: the **create-subscription dialog couldn't select them at all** (their first subscription was uncreatable from the dashboard — it only even listed customers who already had subscriptions), credits couldn't be granted to them, usage events couldn't be filtered to them, and reference labels across Dunning, Plan Detail, and Webhook Events decayed to raw IDs. Pickers now search the server as you type (any name, email, or external ID, no cap), and reference labels fetch exactly the customers on screen. The **feature-flags subsystem was deleted** (API, storage, tables): no code path ever read a flag — the features it claimed to gate all shipped hard-wired — and inert config with its own API surface is a standing audit cost. The rollback migration recreates the tables with their original seed rows.

- **Usage ingestion and the customer usage view got honest (2026-07-03).** A usage event with **quantity 0 was silently billed as 1 unit** — integrators emitting zero-usage records (a request that consumed nothing billable) were charging their customers one unit per event on sum-metered pricing, invisible until the invoice. Zero now means zero (count meters still count the event; Stripe parity — no silent default). Batch-ingest errors now name the failing row (`event[17]: quantity …`) instead of a bare message across a 500-event batch. And the **customer usage view finally prices like the invoice will**: it honored neither customer price overrides nor the period-open version pin (ADR-070), so the running-spend figure was wrong for exactly the negotiated-rate customers who watch it — it now resolves the same rule + override the cycle close bills.

- **The payment-recovery funnel stopped fighting the customer (2026-07-03).** Three fixes on the path a failed-payment customer actually walks: the **payment-update page now carries the company's own branding** (name/logo/brand color from tenant settings) instead of a "Velox" header no customer recognizes — on a page reached from a dunning email, an unknown brand reads as phishing; a **transient error while opening the payment form no longer permanently kills the emailed link** (the single-use token is restored when the form fails to open; a link consumed by a *successful* open stays dead, and canceling at the payment form now gets honest copy about requesting a new link instead of pointing at the dead one); and the **dunning escalation email speaks to humans** — it said "Action taken: mark_uncollectible" verbatim to the debtor, and told customers to "settle via the link" even when the invoice had been closed for online payment (that path now points to support, and the subject/copy match what actually happened: subscription canceled, paused, or under review).

- **Security hygiene on the public and auth surfaces (2026-07-03).** Password-reset requests are now throttled **per target address** (3 emails/address/hour, silently — the response never changes, so account enumeration stays impossible); the per-IP limiter alone let one caller flood a victim's inbox. Request logs no longer record capability tokens: the public hosted-invoice and payment-update URLs carry bearer-equivalent secrets in the path, and every view was writing a live payment credential into the log sink — logs now record the route pattern (`/v1/public/invoices/{token}`), with unmatched probes redacted. The public payment-update surface gained the same tight per-IP rate bucket as hosted invoices (it previously had **no** rate limit — free token brute-force), and the one-time bootstrap endpoint is rate-limited too. CSV exports stopped lying twice: a mid-stream failure now appends a machine-checkable `EXPORT_INCOMPLETE` final record instead of silently truncating a 200-OK file, and exports get a 5-minute window instead of being killed at the general 30-second cap mid-download.

- **Removing a subscription item counts as churn again (2026-07-03, migration 0129).** The MRR change log is written by a database trigger, but when item removal became a soft delete (migration 0102) the trigger stopped seeing removals — every item removed since then wrote **no contraction event**, silently overstating MRR movement in analytics, with no error anywhere. The replacement trigger records the soft delete as the removal (stamped at the removal instant, so simulated-time removals land on the right date), records an un-delete as an addition, and ignores bookkeeping on already-removed rows. Two ride-along indexes: tenant-wide time-window analytics queries no longer scan the whole usage-events table (0130, built concurrently — no ingestion stall), and per-item change-history lookups are indexed (0131).

- **Tenant settings saves are merge-safe and validated at the door (2026-07-03).** A partial settings update via the API silently **wiped every field it didn't mention** — updating just the tax rate reset the company address, invoice prefix, and payment terms to defaults, with no error. Updates now merge: absent fields keep their values, present fields (including explicit `""`/`0`) set them. Validation moved to save time where the operator can see it: an unloadable timezone previously saved fine and then broke billing-cycle date math at the next close (`Mars/Olympus_Mons` → 422 now, and `"Local"` is rejected as not a fixed zone); currencies are canonicalized to uppercase on save (a stored `usd` broke downstream currency filters); invoice prefixes are restricted to letters/digits/hyphens (slashes and spaces corrupted PDF filenames and invoice-number parsing); and **Net 0** payment terms (due immediately) is finally expressible — the old code silently coerced it to Net 30.

- **Invoice PDFs and invoice emails now tell one consistent, correct money story (2026-07-03).** The currency symbol on PDFs was shared mutable state — two invoices rendering at the same moment (an email and a download, two operators, the public hosted page) could stamp each other's currency symbol onto every money field of a finished document. It's now scoped per render (race-detector-locked in CI). The emailed, downloaded, and hosted PDFs also each assembled their own context and had drifted: the **emailed** PDF omitted the buyer's address and any credit notes, and **no** invoice PDF carried the buyer's tax ID (credit notes already did — EU/GST B2B invoices need it too). One shared builder now feeds all three, and the buyer's registration prints as a `Tax ID:` line. More in the same pass: the invoice email's "Amount due" figure is now the actual **amount due** (it showed the pre-credit total) and the payment receipt states the amount **actually charged**; manual line items multiplying to beyond int64 are rejected with a clear 422 instead of persisting a negative total, and unknown `line_type` values get a 422 instead of a raw database error; and an **uncollectible** invoice's hosted page now shows an honest "this invoice is closed — contact support" banner instead of a dead end (the dunning escalation email links straight to it).

- **Negotiated prices survive rule publishes, and one billing period now has exactly one price (2026-07-03, ADR-070).** Publishing a new version of a rating rule silently detached every customer price override on it — the negotiated customer reverted to list price at the next invoice with no warning. Overrides now follow the **rule** (its `rule_key`), not a frozen version id, and every rating path — cycle close, mid-period cancel, spending-threshold fires, invoice preview, and the operator preview — resolves the **version and override in force when the billing period opened**: a mid-period publish or override edit prices from the *next* period, a threshold fire and its cycle close can never bill one period at two different rates, and preview now always matches the invoice it predicts. More in the same pass: overridden customers' preview totals no longer silently drop their lines (the patched override keeps the rule's currency — this also un-breaks threshold fires for usage-only customers whose every rate is negotiated); a transient database error during rating **aborts the run and retries** instead of silently billing a negotiated customer at list price; overrides can finally be **removed** (`DELETE /v1/price-overrides/{id}` — list price from next period, history kept); malformed graduated tier tables (non-increasing bounds, no catch-all) are **rejected at creation** with a clear 422 instead of wedging invoice generation at cycle close; changing a rule's currency is blocked while customer overrides reference it (their cent amounts would be silently reinterpreted); concurrent rule publishes no longer 409 spuriously (version numbers allocate in SQL); and **reinstalling a recipe after uninstall works** — it reconnects to the objects the operator kept instead of failing on duplicates, never overwriting their edits. **Upgrade note:** existing overrides are re-keyed automatically; if a customer held overrides on multiple versions of one rule, the highest-version one stays active and the rest are kept inactive for audit. Migration 0128.

- **Expired credit really is gone: expiry now retires the grant, atomically (2026-07-03, ADR-071).** The expiry sweep wrote the "-$X expired" ledger entry but left the grant's drainable headroom open, so credit the ledger had already written off could still be spent: a billing run applying credits *as of* a past instant (test-clock catchup, cross-period replays) re-drained expired grants — and in a race with the sweep itself, the sweep expired credit that had just been spent, driving the customer's balance **negative**. Now expiry retires the block and appends its ledger entry in one transaction, holding the same lock the credit-application path uses: replayed and concurrent sweeps converge on exactly one expiry entry per grant, and once retired a grant is never re-drained, for any backdated timestamp. Migration 0127 retires grants expired by the old code (their headroom was still open — including any re-opened by this bug). Also fixed in the same pass: a **manual credit deduction** whose only backing was expired-but-unswept credit used to book anyway (same negative-balance mechanics) — it now fails with a clear "balance is expired credit pending the expiry sweep" error — and positive manual adjustments now carry the same $1M fat-finger cap as grants.

- **Canceling a trial now means what it says: the customer is never charged (2026-07-02, ADR-069).** Scheduling a cancellation on a trialing subscription was broken end to end: "cancel at period end" silently pointed at the end of the first *paid* month (not the trial), an explicit cancel date at the trial's end was rejected as invalid, and — worst — any of the four places that auto-activate an expired trial could race the cancellation and **activate, bill, and auto-charge a customer who had already canceled**. Now: cancel-at-period-end on a trial means **cancel free at trial end** (Stripe semantics), an explicit date may be exactly the trial end or a clean period boundary (dates in between are rejected with both boundaries named), the trial-end cancel emits **no invoice** and fires exactly one `subscription.canceled` webhook (never `trial_ended`, which integrators read as "billing begins"), and every activation path is blocked at the database level while a cancellation is pending — a cancel that lands mid-race wins, and a cancellation the customer rescinds (or a trial that gets extended) is never terminated off stale state. Ending or extending a trial while a cancellation is scheduled returns a clear 409 instead of silently overriding it. The API now exposes a derived `cancel_effective_at` — the authoritative "when does it actually cancel" — and the dashboard banner and cancel dialog read it (the dialog on a trial now says "At trial end — the customer won't be charged"). Also fixed: immediately canceling a trial that expired moments earlier (before the scheduler activated it) no longer bills a partial period, and the day-1 invoice for paid-upfront plans now commits atomically with every activation path (two paths previously lost the fee on failure while logging it as "deferred"). No migration.

- **Paying an invoice twice is now structurally hard — and loudly visible when money still goes wrong (2026-07-02, ADR-068).** The hosted invoice's Pay button minted a **fresh** Stripe Checkout session on every click with no expiry (Stripe default: 24 hours) and no cleanup on payment: two devices, a re-opened email, or an impatient double-click each produced another live payment link, and a second successful charge was **silently discarded** — the money existed only in Stripe. Now: **(1)** one invoice holds at most one live session (a claim ledger with a DB-enforced uniqueness guard; every retry, crash recovery, and concurrent click converges on the *same* Stripe session via an idempotency key), sessions expire Stripe-side after 1 hour, and every exit from the payable state — payment, void, credits — closes the invoice's sessions inside the same transaction, with a best-effort Stripe expiry sweep on settle. **(2)** If a duplicate charge still lands (the bounded ≤1h residual), it is never silent: a **Critical banner on the invoice** (shown even though the invoice is "paid" — that's precisely where a double charge lives), a `payment.duplicate_charge` webhook, and an audit trail naming both PaymentIntents. Charges captured for a stale amount raise `payment.amount_mismatch` instead of silently mis-booking the paid figure (which caps refunds), and a payment landing on a voided invoice raises its own event instead of the webhook retrying forever. **Upgrade note:** sessions created before this version are not deduplicated; they expire within 24h. Migrations 0125–0126.

- **Archiving a customer is now honest — it blocks instead of silently letting billing continue (2026-07-02, ADR-067).** Archiving did nothing to a customer's subscriptions: invoicing, card auto-charges, and payment reminders all continued while the dialog claimed "billing will stop." Now archive is **blocked with a clear 409** while any subscription still bills (the error names the exact subscriptions to cancel first), archived customers and archived **plans** accept no new subscriptions (Create and both plan-swap paths), and the dialog copy states precisely what archive does: hides the customer, blocks new business, keeps unpaid invoices collectible. Deliberately NOT auto-cancel: cancelling runs the final-invoice + card-charge path, so "archive to stop billing" would itself charge cards in a loop. Also ships the **billing-profile currency guard**: a profile currency that mismatches a billing subscription's plan currency is rejected — it silently re-labeled plan prices in another currency ($100 plan invoiced as €100, no conversion) — plus ISO-4217 validation and canonical uppercasing. All guards mutation-verified.

- **The hosted invoice page now actually updates after you pay (2026-07-02).** After Stripe Checkout redirected back, the page promised to "update automatically" but never refetched — every payer whose redirect beat the webhook saw an eternal spinner **with a live Pay button**, the direct feeder for double-charged cards. Now it polls every 3 seconds until the backend's authoritative payment status turns terminal: success → paid state; failure → honest "your card was not charged" banner with Pay re-enabled; still settling after 3 minutes (async payment methods) → honest copy, and Pay stays hidden — you will not be charged twice.

- **Peak/last-metered usage never split-bills across a spend-cap fire — and a mid-period cancel no longer double-charges after one (2026-07-02, ADR-066 §4–5).** Non-additive aggregations (`max`, `last_during_period`, `last_ever`) can't be split across two invoices: billing the peak once on a threshold fire and again at cycle close double-charges (`max[0,t1) + max[t1,end) ≥ max[0,end)`). Now: **(1)** under `reset_billing_cycle=false` a fire **defers** every non-additive bucket — its line is dropped from the threshold invoice and the cycle close bills it over the **full period** exactly once (previously the close clamped it to the post-fire residual window, so a pre-fire peak was billed by *nobody*). The deferred amount still counts toward the `amount_gte` cap (it's committed spend — for GPU-concurrency pricing it can be most of the bill), and the invoice header now charges only the rendered lines (no phantom money). **(2)** Under `reset=true` the bucket rides the fire but is *excluded* from the cap — counting it would refire one invoice + card charge per scheduler tick on any steady peak. **(3)** Classification is per pricing-rule **bucket**, not per meter (one meter can carry sum and max rules), and the close-side decision keys on the fire invoice's **persisted lines** — never the operator-mutable reset flag, so clearing a threshold between fire and close changes nothing. **(4)** A **pure**-max/last crossing emits no invoice (nothing billable until close) — instead of erroring every scheduler tick it now records one `subscription.threshold_deferred` timeline/audit artifact per cycle. **(5)** The **immediate-cancel** final invoice — the period's second closer, which previously ignored fires entirely — now shares the same watermark protocol as the cycle close: after a fire it re-bills neither the pre-fire usage nor the base, and bills deferred peaks full-window. All seams mutation-verified, with real-Postgres locks for the empty-residual peak, the config-flip, and the cancel-after-fire double-charge. No migration.

- **Spend-cap money semantics: prorated base on reset fires, atomic fire→reset, $0 invoices settle (2026-07-02, ADR-066).** Three money fixes in the threshold fire path, designed under a three-lens adversarial panel that materially corrected the original plan. **(1) Prorated base.** With `reset_billing_cycle=true` a fire re-anchors the cycle, so the cycle close never true-ups the fired window's base — yet the threshold invoice carried the FULL month's base: a sub crossing 3×/month paid its base fee 3×. Fires now bill the elapsed fraction, prorated against **the plan's own full interval** (the panel rejected the drafted current-period-length denominator — it over-billed re-anchored stubs by ~43%, mid-cycle-created periods up to ~2×, cross-interval items ~12×, and could divide by zero), with the standard `(prorated X/Y days)` description and a reconciling unit price. `reset=false` is byte-identical. **(2) Atomic fire→reset.** The invoice insert and the cycle re-anchor used to be two separate writes with a swallow-and-continue failure arm; a crash between them stranded the reset forever (the fire-once probe blocked every retry) — which, with proration, becomes permanent base under-billing. They now commit in one transaction; a failure rolls both back and the next tick retries cleanly (fault-injection verified on real Postgres: injected re-anchor failure → zero invoices persisted → clean retry fires once). **(3) $0 invoices auto-mark paid** in both writers (threshold + cycle close). A $0 finalized invoice (free-rated usage crossing a quantity cap) was stranded `payment_pending` forever — never charged, never paid, permanently "awaiting payment" in the attention queue. Now settled immediately (Stripe parity: zero-amount invoices are marked paid with no payment attempt; `invoice.paid` fires and means "settled", not "money received"), including a heal for rows stranded by a crash between create and mark-paid. All fixes mutation- or fault-injection-verified. The max/last (non-additive meter) split-billing semantics are decided in ADR-066 §4 and ship next.
- **Threshold scan: no boundary double-bill, no re-fire burn, full fleet coverage (2026-07-02, ADR-065).** Three defects in the spend-cap scan kernel (`ScanThresholds`/`scanOneThreshold`), from the full-product audit's P1 cluster. **(1) Boundary skip:** a crossing first observed on/after the period boundary (scheduler downtime, or the crossing landing in the last inter-tick window) used to fire with a `[period_start, now)` window that spilled into the next period — and since the cycle close's dedup watermark is scoped to the current period's threshold invoices, the spilled usage billed **again** at cycle close. Now the scan skips once `now` reaches `period_end` and the same-tick natural cycle bills the whole elapsed period through the full-fidelity path (proration, item changes, terminal-cancel — none of which the threshold fire path has). Deliberate semantic: no `threshold_crossed` event for a boundary-observed crossing; the cycle invoice is the artifact. **(2) Fire-once probe:** with `reset_billing_cycle=false` the crossed running total stays crossed after the fire, so every subsequent tick re-evaluated and re-fired — each doomed attempt committing an invoice-number increment (a permanent sequence gap the operator sees) and running a **paid** Stripe Tax calculation before the dedup index rejected the insert (~600 burned numbers + tax calls per cycle). The scan now probes for an existing threshold invoice this cycle (one indexed lookup) and short-circuits; the partial unique index remains the correctness seam for true concurrent races. **(3) Full drain:** the scan fetched a single `ORDER BY id LIMIT batch` page per tick with no cursor — and since fired subs still have thresholds configured, the same first page came back every tick, so subscriptions beyond the first `batchSize` were **never scanned**: spend caps silently disabled past 50 subs. Both scan paths (cron + test-clock catchup) now cursor-drain the entire candidate set; the probe is what keeps the drain affordable. All three mutation-verified: `TestScanOneThreshold_BoundarySkip`, `TestScanThresholds_FireOnceProbe_NoReEvaluate`, `TestScanThresholds_DrainsPastBatchSize` (unit), plus a real-Postgres invoice-number no-burn assertion added to `TestThresholdScan_Idempotent`. Store contract change: `ListWithThresholds`/`ListWithThresholdsForClock` take an `afterID` cursor. No migration.
- **`POST /v1/billing/run` now bills only your own tenant — it no longer runs (or leaks) every tenant's billing (2026-07-02).** The manual billing trigger called the scheduler's *unscoped, cross-tenant* sweep, so any tenant's secret key kicked off a billing cycle for **all** tenants, and the response returned other tenants' subscription IDs plus raw database/Stripe error text. It now bills only the caller's own subscriptions (a new tenant-scoped due-subscription query fenced by Row-Level Security), **fails closed with 403** for a tenant-less platform key (never falling through to the global sweep — that stays scheduler-only), drains the tenant's full due set rather than just the first 50, and returns only the caller's own subscription IDs with a generic failure class while full error detail goes to the server log. Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestGetDueBillingForTenant_ScopesToTenant` (mutation-verified: reverting to the cross-tenant sweep makes another tenant's subscription appear in the caller's run) plus the 403 / sanitized-error / no-infinite-loop unit tests. No migration, no schema change.
- **An oversized Stripe webhook now fails with a clear "payload too large" instead of a misleading "invalid signature" (2026-07-02).** The webhook receiver silently truncated request bodies at its 64KB cap; a legitimate event larger than that then failed signature verification over the truncated bytes and died as a 400 "invalid signature" — so after ~3 days of Stripe retries the event was permanently lost, with logs pointing the operator at a phantom signing-secret problem instead of the real cause. The receiver now detects an over-cap body and rejects it as **413 `payload_too_large`** with an ERROR log naming the cap and the consequence, so the failure is attributable and the cap can be raised deliberately if a large event shape is legitimate. Low probability for Velox's event shapes (payment intents, refunds, setup intents are all small) — this fixes the diagnostic, not a live loss. Guarded by `TestWebhookHandler_OversizedBodyIs413NotSignatureFailure` (a validly-signed oversized event → 413, mutation-verified against the old truncating read).
- **A recipe with a mismatched dunning retry setup now fails cleanly at install time instead of stalling collections later (2026-07-02).** The dunning policy saved through a recipe skipped the save-time check that the retry schedule has enough entries for the configured number of retries (the API path enforced it; the recipe path's code comment claimed the recipe layer validated it, but it only checks the final action). A recipe with, say, 4 retries but only 2 intervals would install fine and then stall that customer's collection campaign mid-run with a background-tick error. Both save paths now run the same validation and defaults through one shared chokepoint, so an invalid recipe is rejected with a clear message when the operator installs it. All built-in recipes were already valid — this was latent, not live. Guarded by `TestUpsertPolicyTx_ValidationParity` (mutation-verified).
- **Every table that stores tenant data is now enforced by database-level Row-Level Security — and a new test makes it impossible to forget again (2026-07-02, migration 0124).** Two auth-domain tables (`dashboard_sessions`, `user_tenants`) carried a `tenant_id` column but had no RLS at all — the last two outside the "every tenant table gets ENABLE + FORCE + a `tenant_isolation` policy" rule. Not exploitable today (both are reached only via the RLS-bypass connection, keyed by the session-token hash or the user id — the login flow has no tenant context yet), but the protection was behavioral rather than structural: a future tenant-scoped query ("this tenant's active sessions", "this tenant's members" once invites land) would have had zero database-level isolation. Migration 0124 fences both; nothing changes for existing access. The bigger half of the fix is `TestRLSIsolation_EveryTenantTableIsFenced`: instead of a hand-maintained table list, it **discovers every `tenant_id` table from `information_schema`** and asserts each is fully fenced (ENABLE + FORCE + policy) — which is how it caught `user_tenants`, a gap the prior audit's manual sweep missed. Any future tenant table missing RLS, or fenced with `ENABLE` but not `FORCE` (the historic `stripe_provider_credentials` gap, where the table owner silently bypasses the policy), now fails CI instead of waiting for an audit. Deliberate exceptions require an explicit allowlist entry with a written reason; the allowlist ships empty.
- **The `payment.failed` webhook can no longer be lost to a crash (2026-07-02).** The event was dispatched *after* the database commit that marks the invoice failed — a crash in that window meant integrators never heard about the failure, and a duplicate Stripe delivery would skip the re-send. It is now enqueued into the webhook outbox **inside the same transaction** as the failed-stamp (the exact mirror of `payment.succeeded` on the paid path, ADR-040): if the transaction rolls back there's no event, if it commits the event is durable. Exactly-once semantics are unchanged — a same-PI redelivery doesn't re-enqueue, a new retry attempt's failure is a genuinely distinct event and fires again, and a stale failure arriving after the invoice settled never emits. The customer-facing failure email deliberately stays post-commit (same reasoning as the receipt email — email resolution doesn't belong under the invoice row lock). Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestMarkPaymentFailed_EnqueuesPaymentFailedInTx` (in-tx enqueue + gate, mutation-verified; a failed enqueue rolls the whole failed-stamp back) and the updated `TestSettleFailed_*` exactly-once suite. No migration, no schema change.
- **A failed payment always reaches dunning now, even if the app crashes at the wrong moment (2026-07-01).** When a payment failed, dunning was started right after the invoice was marked failed but *outside* that database commit — so a crash (or an exhausted retry) in the sub-second window in between could leave the invoice failed with collection retries never scheduled, and a duplicate webhook delivery would skip the restart. The invoice was still visible in the attention banner for an operator to act on, but automatic recovery didn't happen. A new `dunning_backfill` recovery sweep now finds finalized, still-owed, failed invoices that have no dunning run and starts one — idempotently (the per-invoice uniqueness guard means the sweep and the normal path can never double-start), state-agnostically (an invoice with a run in *any* state, including a resolved one, is left alone so a recovered invoice is never re-dunned), and behind a short cool-off so the normal inline path wins the common case. Clock-pinned (test-clock) invoices are excluded. Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestListFailedWithoutDunningRun_CandidateSet` (candidate vs. every exclusion, mutation-verified on the state-agnostic filter) and the engine-level `TestEnrollFailedWithoutDunning_*` sweep tests. No migration, no schema change.
- **Activating a subscription can no longer resurrect one that was canceled at the same moment (2026-07-01).** `Service.Activate` reads a draft subscription, then persists `status='active'` via `store.Update` in a separate step. That `UPDATE` targeted the row by id alone, so a `draft→canceled` cancellation landing in the window between the read and the write was silently clobbered back to `active` — a terminated subscription resurrected into a live billing state with fresh period bounds, and a `subscription.activated` webhook fired on it. `Update` now carries the same `status = 'draft'` transition guard every sibling state-change already uses (`transitionInTx`'s `WHERE status IN (…)`): a racing cancel makes the activation fail cleanly with an invalid-state conflict, and the canceled subscription stays canceled. Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestActivate_StoreUpdate_GuardsAgainstConcurrentCancel` (the in-memory fake replaces the whole row and can't model the predicate, so this needs a real DB). No migration, no schema change.
- **A card payment now clears the "in dunning" state immediately, and dunning resolution is exactly-once — no duplicate `dunning.resolved` webhooks (2026-07-01).** Two coupled fixes. **(1) Prompt card-recovery resolve.** When a card payment settled an invoice that was in dunning, the run was left `active` (a stale red badge) until the dunning sweep's paid-pre-check floor cleared it on the next tick — the background-settle paths (credits / threshold / auto-charge) already resolved via the engine, but the card path's dunning seam was start-only. `payment.SettleSucceeded` now resolves the run immediately (a new `DunningResolver` seam, best-effort, symmetric with the engine's #317 resolver). **(2) Exactly-once resolve (CAS).** Adding that second resolver surfaced a latent non-idempotency: `dunning.resolveRunNow` fired the resolved timeline row **and** the outbound `dunning.resolved` webhook *unconditionally*, so any two resolvers of the same run — the new card-settle resolve racing `processRun`'s own resolve on a synchronous retry-success, or an operator resolve racing an automated one — would double-notify integrators. The resolve transition is now a **CAS** (`store.ResolveRun`: `UPDATE … WHERE state <> 'resolved'`, RowsAffected-gated), and the timeline row + webhook fire **only on the winning transition** — so every resolve path (the sweep floor, retry-success, `ResolveByInvoice`, and the operator `Service.ResolveRun`, all now routed through the one CAS) emits exactly one `dunning.resolved` per recovery. Production was always correct on end-state (the floor backstops; the run always ends resolved); this makes it *prompt* and *exactly-once*. The synchronous retry-success path records the correct `attempt_count` too: `processRun` now persists the attempt **before** the charge (record-before-effect — which also makes the retry loop crash-safer: an attempt can't be lost mid-charge), and its retry-path writes are guarded on `state <> 'resolved'` (`UpdateRunIfActive`) so a concurrent settle-webhook resolve landing during the charge window is never clobbered back to active (a transient skip fully rewinds the attempt, but only while the run is still active). The **terminal (exhaust) path is resolve-safe too**: `exhaustRun` re-reads invoice status *immediately before* its irreversible final action, so a payment that settles mid-tick — after the tick-start paid-pre-check but before exhaust runs, across the retry's Stripe round-trip — resolves the run instead of canceling a now-paying customer's subscription; and its escalation and action-failure-rollback writes are the same guarded `UpdateRunIfActive`, so a settle that resolves the run *during* the terminal action neither clobbers `resolved`→`escalated` nor fires a contradictory `dunning.escalated` on top of the `dunning.resolved`. Guarded by `TestResolveRunNow_Idempotent_FiresEventOnce`, `TestServiceResolveRun_Idempotent_AfterAutomatedResolve`, the real-Postgres `TestResolveRun_CAS_ExactlyOnce`, `TestProcessRun_RecordsAttemptBeforeCharge_ResolverSeesFullCount`, `TestProcessRun_TransientSkip_FullyRewindsPersistedState`, `TestExhaustRun_LatePaidRecheck_DoesNotCancel`, `TestExhaustRun_ResolvedDuringTerminalAction_NoEscalatedClobber`, `TestSettleSucceeded_ResolvesDunningRun`, and `TestSettleSucceeded_ResolverErrorDoesNotFailSettle`. No migration, no schema change.

- **Proration charge invoices enroll for auto-charge atomically — a failed enrollment no longer strands a committed, unpaid charge (2026-07-01).** Adding an item / upgrading a plan / increasing a quantity on a paid subscription mid-period cuts a proration **charge** invoice, which must be enrolled for the auto-charge sweep (`auto_charge_pending = TRUE`) so the customer's card is charged. Enrollment previously ran as a best-effort write **after** the item-change transaction committed; if it failed (a DB blip in that post-commit window), the charge invoice sat committed-but-**unenrolled** and unpaid forever — the sweep only scans `auto_charge_pending = TRUE`, no reconciler scans `FALSE`, so nothing ever collected it (the only signal was a lone ERROR log). Enrollment now runs **inside** the item-change transaction — a new tx-aware `SetAutoChargePendingTx` on the invoice store, called via an `enrollAutoChargeTx` helper before the commit in the atomic add/update wrappers — so an enrollment failure rolls the **whole** change back (the operator gets a clean error and retries) instead of leaving an item added with a silently-stranded charge. The non-atomic fallback path (used only when the DB handle isn't wired, e.g. narrow unit tests) is unchanged — it still enrolls post-create inline, as there's no tx to ride. Guarded by `TestAddItem_EnrollAutoChargeFailure_RollsBackItemAdd` (an in-tx enrollment failure rolls the add back). No migration, no schema change.

- **Refund status now reflects Stripe's *async* outcome instead of a create-time guess — a refund that later fails is no longer recorded as succeeded (2026-06-28, ADR-063).** Stripe refunds are asynchronous: `Refund.create` often returns `pending`, and the final `succeeded`/**`failed`**/`canceled` lands later via a webhook (a `pending` refund can flip to `failed` — bank reject / insufficient platform balance → money back to the *platform*, customer gets nothing). Velox recorded `refund_status=succeeded` optimistically from the create-call (dropping Stripe's actual status) and handled **no** refund webhooks — so a refund Stripe later failed stayed silently `succeeded` (a real money-wrong, invisible state). Fixed: **(1)** `CreateRefund` now returns Stripe's real status and `Issue()`/`RetryRefund` record it faithfully (`pending` when Stripe says pending, not a blanket succeeded — the common healthy card refund still returns `succeeded` synchronously); **(2)** a new status-driven handler for `charge.refund.updated` / `refund.updated` / `refund.failed` (admitted via `endpointAuthoritativeEvent`, matched to the credit note by `stripe_refund_id`, applied **monotonically** so a stale out-of-order `pending` can't clobber a terminal, reusing the existing event-id dedup) reconciles the async outcome — the webhook is the source of truth; **(3)** a refund with no matching credit note (Stripe-dashboard/direct-API refund) is ack'd permanently and never fabricates a credit note, with a bounded 15-min redelivery for the rare create→webhook race. Stripe's 5 statuses collapse into the existing 4-value `refund_status` CHECK (`canceled→failed`, `requires_action→pending` — no migration). Because faithful `pending` makes pending common, the just-shipped #319 "refunds need attention" alert/count was **co-refined** to `failed` OR (`pending` older than 72h) at both the dashboard count and the Credit Notes filter — fresh pending is normal async settlement (neutral badge), and the aged-pending arm doubles as the backstop for a never-delivered webhook (there's no refund poll yet). The refund leg stays operator-retried (`RetryRefund`), not auto-swept — money-out is conservative; this makes stuck refunds *visible and correct*. Guarded by `TestIssue_RecordsTruePendingRefundStatus`, `TestApplyRefundWebhook_FlipsThenMonotonic`, `TestApplyRefundWebhook_UnknownRefundIsNotFound`, `TestHandleWebhook_RefundUpdated_*`, `TestMapStripeRefundStatus`. Deferred (ADR-063): a refund-poll reconciler, a dedicated `canceled` enum (+migration), and ingesting external dashboard refunds.

- **A paid invoice no longer keeps an active dunning run (stale red badge) when it was settled by a background path — and the dunning sweep can no longer dun, or cancel the subscription on, an already-paid invoice (2026-06-27).** Resolving a dunning run on payment was wired into the invoice **handler** only (operator record-payment, collect, void). An invoice settled by a **background** path — the auto-charge sweep applying customer **credits**, a threshold-close credit settle, or the `billOnePeriod` credit cover — called `MarkPaid` without resolving the run, so a fully-paid invoice was left with an `active` dunning run: a stale red badge, and worse, when the run's next action came due the sweep would re-attempt it and, **at max retries, could fire the terminal action (pause collection / cancel the subscription) on a fully-paid invoice** — the charge short-circuits at `$0` due, but `exhaustRun` runs *before* that and had no paid-check. Fixed in two layers, treating this as an idempotent, non-money-exactly-once state effect (post-commit best-effort, **not** a coordinator-tx — the ADR-040/056 framework calibrated by criticality): **(1) prompt** — the billing engine gained a `DunningResolver` seam (wired directly to `dunning.ResolveByInvoice`, which no-ops when there is no active run) and calls it right after the three background credit-settle `MarkPaid` sites, so the run resolves to `payment_recovered` immediately — and in *simulated* time on a clock-pinned invoice, within the same test-clock advance; **(2) floor** — `dunning.processRun` now carries a paid-pre-check that runs **before** the max-retries → `exhaustRun` branch: if the invoice is already terminally settled (`paid`/`succeeded` → `payment_recovered`; `voided`/`uncollectible` → `manually_resolved`) it resolves the run in place and returns, never ticking an attempt, emailing, retrying, or firing a terminal action. The pre-check gates on terminal **status** (not `amount_due ≤ 0`, which a mid-tax-retry draft can momentarily show) and falls through to the normal path on a fetch error (no attempt burned on a DB blip). The floor is the durable backstop for *every* settle path, present and future; the prompt clears the confirmed symptom immediately. The symmetric card-recovery gap (`payment.SettleSucceeded` also leaves dunning active — its dunning seam is typed start-only) is documented as a fast-follow and is covered by the floor on the next tick. No migration; reuses the existing resolution value, dunning event, and webhook. The shared transition was factored into one `resolveRunNow` helper (used by `ResolveByInvoice`, the retry-success branch, and the pre-check). Guarded by `TestProcessRun_*` (paid resolves without retrying; **max-retries-paid does not cancel the subscription**; gates on status not amount-due; voided → manually_resolved; invoiceGet-error falls through) and the extended `TestRetrySweep_FullyCreditCovered_MarksPaidWithoutCharge` (a background credit settle resolves dunning as `payment_recovered`).

- **Issuing a credit note is now atomic and recoverable — a crash can no longer leave a credit "issued" with its money effect un-applied, and a failed tax reversal no longer over-remits forever (2026-06-25, ADR-061, migration 0123).** `creditnote.Issue()` flipped a credit note `draft→issued` in its **own** committed transaction, then ran the money effects in *separate* steps afterward: the internal effect (reduce `amount_due` on an unpaid invoice, or grant the credit to the customer's balance on a paid one) and the external ones (Stripe refund, upstream tax reversal). A crash **after** the flip but **before** an effect left the credit note durably `issued` with the effect never applied — most visibly a credit-balance note shown as completed that the customer never received, with no automatic recovery (re-Issue refused: `status!=draft`); and the tax reversal was outright fire-and-forget (a transient Stripe failure logged a WARN and issued the note anyway, leaving the tenant **over-remitting output tax** with no retry). Fixed by making `Issue()` a coordinator transaction (ADR-056): the `draft→issued` CAS and the internal effect now commit **together** on one `*sql.Tx` (`TransitionStatusTx` + `ApplyCreditNoteTx`/`GrantForCreditNoteTx`) — a crash mid-tx rolls **both** back (the note stays `draft`, so `RetryPendingClawbackIssue` re-drives it cleanly), and a crash post-commit leaves the note `issued` with the effect already applied, so a re-entry loses the CAS and never re-applies. The reduction/grant is therefore **idempotent by construction** (exactly one CAS-gated caller), so PR2 adds **no source-dedup row** — that's recorded as the first brick of the deferred `amount_due`-derived-ledger (ADR-061). The external tax reversal stays post-commit (it can't share a DB tx) but is now **recoverable**: on failure it sets a durable `credit_notes.tax_reversal_pending` marker (migration 0123) and raises the log **WARN→ERROR**, and a new CN-scoped sweep `RetryPendingCreditNoteTaxReversal` (scheduler tick) re-drives it with the same per-CN `velox_tax_rev_<cn.ID>` key. Recovery eligibility is **derived from durable state** (an issued credit note with no reversal stamped against a tax-bearing source) — the marker is only a fast-path index, **not** the sole key — so even the compound failure where the reversal *and* the marker write both fail is still recovered, mirroring the void-path #310 design (whose eligibility is likewise the default persisted state). This is its own sweep — **not** the existing #310 `RetryPendingTaxReversal`, which scans only voided/uncollectible invoices and keys off `invoices.tax_reversed_at`, so a credit-note reversal stamped on a **finalized/paid** invoice is structurally invisible to it; and **not** routed onto the `webhook_outbox` (that's a customer-notification fan-out — an internal obligation would leak to `'*'`-subscribed endpoints). This closes the two gaps ADR-057 carried as inherited-but-open (the unpaid-source `ApplyCreditNote` not being idempotent; the post-flip partial-issue re-entrancy window), so the cancel-proration relay (`engine.IssueCancelDrafts`) is now safe to re-drive and its "manual reconcile" log was removed. Consolidating the four bespoke re-drive sweeps (tax-commit #267, tax-reversal #310, clawback-issue, this one) onto one durable obligation queue — built by generalising `webhook_outbox`, **not** Temporal (reintroduces the dual-write) or River-for-now (needs a pgx-native tx) — is the committed PR3 (ADR-062). Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestIssue_GrantFailure_RollsBackCAS` (an in-tx grant failure rolls the CAS back → the note stays `draft`, no issued-but-ungranted orphan, then a clean re-drive succeeds), the in-memory `TestRetryPendingCreditNoteTaxReversal_ReDrivesAndClears` (failed reversal → marked pending → sweep re-drives + clears + stamps), the extended `TestIssue_ReversalFailureStillIssuesCN` (failure now sets the marker), and the existing CAS-idempotency suite (unchanged, still green).

- **A canceled customer's prorated refund credit can no longer be silently lost in a crash — the in_advance cancel-proration credit is now created atomically with the cancel (2026-06-24, ADR-057 extension).** When an `in_advance` subscription is canceled mid-period, the customer is owed a credit for the unused, already-paid portion. That credit was issued **post-commit, fire-and-forget**: `Cancel` flipped the subscription to `canceled`, committed, then `BillOnCancel` computed and issued the credit in a *separate* step. Transient/cap failures were loud (ERROR "manual credit required"), but a **crash between the cancel commit and that step silently dropped the obligation** — no record the customer was owed anything. The credit-direction sibling of the create/cancel revenue leaks (#306/#307); industry-confirmed (Stripe/Orb/Lago/Chargebee/Recurly all make the cancellation credit a durable, recoverable record). Fixed by reusing the ADR-057 draft-in-tx machinery (**no new migration, no new reconciler**): when every funding invoice for the period is **paid** (the dominant case), the credit notes are now created as `issue_pending` **drafts inside the cancel transaction** (`BillOnCancelDraftsTx`, on the same `*sql.Tx` as the status flip — the established `BillFinalOnImmediateCancelTx` precedent), so a draft-create failure **rolls the whole cancel back**; the external Stripe tax reversal + balance grant relay **post-commit** (`IssueCancelDrafts`), and a never-issued draft is recovered by the existing `RetryPendingClawbackIssue` sweep. The engine owns the capability (the subscription service has no creditnote dependency and never sees the cancel tx); `settleUnusedAcrossFunding` was split into a pure `allocateUnusedAcrossFunding` (carrying the #276/#277/#278 over-credit invariant — net→gross clamp + remainder loud-fail) and a thin consumer, with the existing post-commit path behavior-unchanged. **Scope (PR1): paid funding sources only** — any **unpaid** funding source declines the in-tx path and stays on the post-commit `BillOnCancel` (its `amount_due`-reduce and `Void` legs are not idempotent yet); a mixed paid+unpaid set therefore stays fully post-commit, coherent because the silent crash-loss being closed is *cash owed back*. The inherited post-flip partial-issue gap (Issue() flips `status='issued'` then a side-effect fails → invisible to the `status='draft'` reconciler, manual reconcile, 0093-dedup-safe) is **not** closed here. Settled-unpaid relief + the partial-issue re-entrancy fix are the tracked PR2 follow-up (gated on an idempotent unpaid-source `ApplyCreditNote`). Guarded by `TestBillOnCancelDraftsTx_*` (all-paid creates drafts not issue; any-unpaid declines; draft-error rolls back; multi-source respects headroom), `TestCancel_*` (the service wiring: draft path issues + skips `BillOnCancel`; declined → fallback; draft-error fails the cancel), and the real-Postgres `TestCancelCredit_PaidInAdvance_DraftAtomicAndReconcilerRecovers` (draft created in-tx, post-commit issue *skipped* to simulate the crash, `RetryPendingClawbackIssue` lands the credit exactly once + deduped on a second sweep).

- **Outbound webhook events no longer vanish silently when their enqueue fails (2026-06-24).** Ten lifecycle-event dispatch sites (subscription trial-ended / collection-resumed, invoice finalized / voided / marked-uncollectible / payment-recorded, engine invoice-finalized) called `_ = events.Dispatch(...)`, discarding the error — so a transient DB hiccup on the outbox enqueue dropped the event with **zero signal**. The dispatcher is durable *once the enqueue commits* (ADR-040 outbox + worker retries), so the swallowed error was the one real steady-state loss vector. Each producer now routes through a small `dispatchEvent` helper that **ERROR-logs** an enqueue failure (matching the dunning/payment/engine sites that already did), turning a silent drop into an alertable signal. Found by the dual-write audit's systemic-root pass, which confirmed **no money event is fire-and-forget** — `invoice.paid` / `payment.succeeded` are already enqueued *in the settlement transaction* via the invoice store, and the rest are notifications (durable once enqueued, recoverable by consumer reconciliation). The deeper fix — making lifecycle-event emission **atomic** with its state change (a `DispatchTx` seam threading each store's `*sql.Tx`) — is a ~16-site/6-package refactor deliberately **deferred** until the first webhook-consuming design partner needs guaranteed lifecycle delivery (tracked in `docs/adr/README.md` Open follow-ups). No behavior change beyond the added logging; no migration.

- **A failed tax reversal on void/uncollectible no longer leaves the tenant over-remitting forever — a recovery sweep now re-drives it (2026-06-24, migration 0122).** When an invoice is voided or marked uncollectible, Velox reverses its committed Stripe Tax transaction so the authority stops counting it as collected. That reversal is an external Stripe call and was **best-effort**: a transient failure (Stripe 5xx/timeout) logged a WARN and moved on, with **no retry and no reconciler** — so the tax stayed reported-as-collected and the **tenant over-remitted output tax until someone reconciled it by hand**. The tax-**commit** path already had a recovery reconciler (#267 `RetryPendingTaxCommit`); the symmetric **reversal** path had none — the exact "first-practice committed, second-practice left best-effort" asymmetry the dual-write audit targets. Fixed by adding the mirror sweep: a new self-clearing marker column `invoices.tax_reversed_at` (NULL on a voided/uncollectible `stripe_tax` invoice that still carries a `tax_transaction_id` = "reversal not confirmed"), a `ListPendingTaxReversal` scan, and `RetryPendingTaxReversal` on the scheduler tick (right after the commit reconciler) that re-drives the reversal. Re-reversal is **idempotent at Stripe** — it reuses the invoice-stable `inv_taxrev_<id>` reference, so re-reversing an already-reversed transaction is a deduped no-op (the same dedup the void path and product-audit G1 already rely on); on success it stamps `tax_reversed_at` and the row drops out of the scan.
