The inline failure log was bumped **WARN → ERROR** so a sustained failure is alertable *today*, before the sweep even runs. `MarkUncollectible` was also reordered to flip the status **first** then reverse (mirroring the post-#29 `Void`), so a reversal that fails *after* the flip now lands `uncollectible` with `tax_reversed_at` NULL and is itself recovered by the sweep — closing a pre-existing window where a status-write failure could strand a reversal on a still-`finalized` invoice. Bounded to a 24h freshness window (anti-churn + grandfathers pre-migration voids without a data backfill; a transient blip resolves in seconds-to-minutes; a sustained >24h failure ages out to manual reconcile, with the ERROR as the signal — the same recovery model as the commit reconciler). Simulated/test-clock invoices are excluded via the durable `is_simulated` flag (covers both subscription- and customer-pinned one-offs). **Deliberately wall-clock only** — no test-clock (`ForClock`) half, the same scope-cut #267 made (test-mode voids can't mis-report real tax; replaying the clock recovers them). **Known limitation:** the re-drive recomputes the reversal amount, so if an invoice's credit-noted total *changes* while a reversal is pending-failed (e.g. a credit note issued on an uncollectible invoice), the same-reference re-drive can hit a Stripe idempotency mismatch — surfaced as the loud per-tick ERROR (→ manual reconcile), never silent; not auto-fixed because varying the key by amount would reintroduce the G1 same-reference double-reversal under-remit. Guarded by `TestRetryPendingTaxReversal` (success stamps + falls out of scan; failure stays pending + aggregates the error + recovers when Stripe heals; unwired → inert) and the real-Postgres `TestListPendingTaxReversal_FindsOrphanAndSelfClears` (the orphan is found, then `MarkTaxReversed` self-clears it). When an invoice is voided or marked uncollectible, Velox reverses its committed Stripe Tax transaction so the authority stops counting it as collected. That reversal is an external Stripe call and was **best-effort**: a transient failure (Stripe 5xx/timeout) logged a WARN and moved on, with **no retry and no reconciler** — so the tax stayed reported-as-collected and the **tenant over-remitted output tax until someone reconciled it by hand**. The tax-**commit** path already had a recovery reconciler (#267 `RetryPendingTaxCommit`); the symmetric **reversal** path had none — the exact "first-practice committed, second-practice left best-effort" asymmetry the dual-write audit targets. Fixed by adding the mirror sweep: a new self-clearing marker column `invoices.tax_reversed_at` (NULL on a voided/uncollectible `stripe_tax` invoice that still carries a `tax_transaction_id` = "reversal not confirmed"), a `ListPendingTaxReversal` scan, and `RetryPendingTaxReversal` on the scheduler tick (right after the commit reconciler) that re-drives the reversal. Re-reversal is **idempotent at Stripe** — it reuses the invoice-stable `inv_taxrev_<id>` reference, so re-reversing an already-reversed transaction is a deduped no-op (the same dedup the void path and product-audit G1 already rely on); on success it stamps `tax_reversed_at` and the row drops out of the scan. The inline failure log was bumped **WARN → ERROR** so a sustained failure is alertable *today*, before the sweep even runs. `MarkUncollectible` was also reordered to flip the status **first** then reverse (mirroring the post-#29 `Void`), so a reversal that fails *after* the flip now lands `uncollectible` with `tax_reversed_at` NULL and is itself recovered by the sweep — closing a pre-existing window where a status-write failure could strand a reversal on a still-`finalized` invoice. Bounded to a 24h freshness window (anti-churn + grandfathers pre-migration voids without a data backfill; a transient blip resolves in seconds-to-minutes; a sustained >24h failure ages out to manual reconcile, with the ERROR as the signal — the same recovery model as the commit reconciler). Simulated/test-clock invoices are excluded via the durable `is_simulated` flag (covers both subscription- and customer-pinned one-offs). **Deliberately wall-clock only** — no test-clock (`ForClock`) half, the same scope-cut #267 made (test-mode voids can't mis-report real tax; replaying the clock recovers them). **Known limitation:** the re-drive recomputes the reversal amount, so if an invoice's credit-noted total *changes* while a reversal is pending-failed (e.g. a credit note issued on an uncollectible invoice), the same-reference re-drive can hit a Stripe idempotency mismatch — surfaced as the loud per-tick ERROR (→ manual reconcile), never silent; not auto-fixed because varying the key by amount would reintroduce the G1 same-reference double-reversal under-remit. Guarded by `TestRetryPendingTaxReversal` (success stamps + falls out of scan; failure stays pending + aggregates the error + recovers when Stripe heals; unwired → inert) and the real-Postgres `TestListPendingTaxReversal_FindsOrphanAndSelfClears` (the orphan is found, then `MarkTaxReversed` self-clears it).

- **Voiding an invoice no longer silently strips the customer of credits they paid it with — the consumed-credit reversal is now atomic with the void (2026-06-24, ADR-056).** When an invoice was voided (operator action, or dunning's `manually_resolved` write-off), the status flip committed first and the **consumed-credit reversal** — handing back the customer-balance credits that had been applied to that invoice (applied credit reduces `amount_due` without touching the ledger, so a void must re-grant it) — ran **afterward as a separate, WARN-swallowed handler step**, in *two* call sites (the invoice void handler and the dunning void path). A transient failure there (a DB blip on the ledger append) left the invoice **voided but the credits still consumed** — the customer permanently loses the credits they paid with, with **no reconciler** to re-drive it. The void/credit sibling of the create/cancel revenue leaks from the first-vs-second-practice dual-write audit (same root: a load-bearing internal second write left best-effort after the first committed). Fixed by folding the reversal **into** `invoice.Service.Void` as the single writer: the new `Store.UpdateStatusWithReversal` flips the status **and** runs the credit reversal (`credit.ReverseForInvoiceTx`, appending the reversal grant on the **same** `*sql.Tx`) in **one transaction**, so a reversal failure **rolls the void back** — the invoice never lands voided-with-credits-consumed. The external steps (Stripe tax reversal, PaymentIntent cancel, `invoice.voided` dispatch) stay post-commit/best-effort and now run **after** the void durably commits; the dunning path drops its own reversal call and reads the PI id off the `Void` return. The 0106 dedup index keeps the in-tx reversal exactly-once across redelivery. The coordinator-`*sql.Tx` callback pattern mirrors `subscription.CreateWithBill`; the cross-domain reversal rides a callback so `internal/invoice` still imports no peer package. **Behavior change:** a hard reversal failure now fails the void (operator/dunning retries) instead of silently shorting the customer. **No migration.** Guarded by `TestVoid_CreditReversalAtomic` (reversal failure rolls the void back and skips the post-commit tax reversal; success commits both then reverses tax), the rewired `TestResolveRun_ManualVoid_RoutesThroughServiceAndGatesSideEffects`, and the real-Postgres `TestUpdateStatusWithReversal_ReversalFailure_RealTxRollsBackVoid` (status stays draft) / `_Success_CommitsVoidAndCreditGrant` (the grant commits on the shared cross-store tx).

- **Trial-end activation no longer leaks the first-period base fee — `EndTrial` and trial-expiry are now atomic (2026-06-24, ADR-056).** The two trial→active transitions — operator `EndTrial` and the wall-clock trial-expiry scan (`ProcessExpiredTrials`) — flipped the subscription to `active` and committed, then billed the day-1 `in_advance` invoice **best-effort post-commit**, swallowing a failure with the same false "deferred to next cycle close" claim the create/cancel paths had (the cycle scheduler skips the just-elapsed `in_advance` segment, so it's a **permanent revenue leak**). The trial-end siblings of the create/cancel leaks from the dual-write audit. Fixed by making both atomic: new `Store.EndTrialEarlyWithBill` / `ActivateAfterTrialWithBill` flip the status **and** insert the day-1 invoice (`BillOnCreateTx`) in **one transaction**, so a billing failure rolls the activation back (the sub stays `trialing` and is retried next tick) rather than orphaning an active sub with no invoice. External steps (tax commit + auto-charge) run post-commit via `FinalizeOnCreateInvoice`. **Behavior change:** a hard day-1 billing failure now fails the trial-end (operator retries) / leaves the sub trialing for the next scan, instead of silently dropping the base fee. **No migration** — reuses the `BillOnCreateTx`/coordinator pattern; the store transitions gained `…InTx` bodies shared with the new `…WithBill` variants (all existing callers unchanged). Guarded by `TestCreate/...EndTrial day-1 billing failure rolls the early-end back (atomic)` (sub stays trialing) and the `TestProcessExpiredTrials` BillOnCreateTx assertions; the real-tx rollback mechanism is the same one proven by the create/cancel real-Postgres tests.

- **Immediate cancel no longer silently leaks the partial-period invoice — cancel is now atomic (2026-06-24, ADR-056).** Canceling a subscription mid-period flipped it to `canceled` and committed, then emitted the final partial-period invoice (in_arrears base + usage from `current_period_start → canceled_at`) **best-effort, post-commit**: a `BillFinalOnImmediateCancel` failure was logged at ERROR with a comment pointing at a "product-audit G3 deferred reconciler" — which **never existed**. So a failed final invoice left a **canceled subscription with an uninvoiced partial period: a permanent revenue leak.** The other confirmed revenue leak (with the create path) from the first-vs-second-practice dual-write audit. Fixed by making cancel **atomic**: the new `Store.CancelAtomicWithBill` flips the subscription to `canceled` and runs the final-invoice insert (`BillFinalOnImmediateCancelTx`) in **one transaction** — a billing failure rolls the cancel back rather than orphaning an uninvoiced canceled sub. The external steps (tax commit + auto-charge) run post-commit via the existing `FinalizeOnCreateInvoice`, and the `in_advance` cancel-proration **credit** (`BillOnCancel`, whose credit-note carries an external Stripe tax reversal) stays post-commit/best-effort as before. The 430-line build is untouched — the tx is threaded only at the invoice insert. **Behavior change:** a hard final-invoice failure now fails the cancel (the caller retries) instead of silently dropping partial-period revenue. **No migration.** Guarded by `TestCreate/...a final-on-cancel billing failure rolls the cancel back (atomic)` and the real-Postgres `TestCancelAtomicWithBill_BillFailure_RealTxRollsBackCancel` (a billFn failure leaves the subscription `active`, not canceled).

- **A failed day-1 invoice no longer silently leaks the first-period base fee — subscription create is now atomic (2026-06-24, ADR-056).** When an `in_advance` subscription was created with `start_now`, the day-1 invoice (the upcoming period's base fee) was billed **best-effort, after** the subscription row had already committed: a `BillOnCreate` failure was swallowed with a WARN claiming the base fee would be "deferred to next cycle close." That backstop was **false** — the cycle scheduler bills the *upcoming* period and **skips the just-elapsed `in_advance` segment**, so a dropped day-1 invoice was a **permanent revenue leak**, never recovered. Found by the first-vs-second-practice dual-write audit (the second confirmed revenue leak, alongside the cancel path). Fixed by making create **atomic**: the new `Store.CreateWithBill` inserts the subscription (+ items) and runs the day-1 invoice insert (`BillOnCreateTx`) in **one transaction**, so a billing failure rolls the whole create back rather than leaving an active subscription with no first-period invoice. The external steps (tax commit + auto-charge) still run post-commit via `FinalizeOnCreateInvoice` (Stripe calls must never ride a DB tx) and are recoverable by the existing reconciler/retry sweeps. **Behavior change:** a hard day-1 billing failure now fails the create (the caller retries) instead of silently orphaning a sub — a tax-pending invoice still finalizes as a draft and does not block. The coordinator-`*sql.Tx` pattern (ADR-056) and `BillOnCreateTx`/`FinalizeOnCreateInvoice` already existed for the cross-interval swap; this wires them into `Create`. **No migration.** Guarded by `TestCreate/...rolls back the create (atomic)` and the real-Postgres `TestCreateWithBill_BillFailure_RealTxRollsBackSubscription` (a billFn failure leaves zero subscriptions persisted).

- **An ambiguous charge outcome can no longer silently strand a possibly-paid invoice (2026-06-24).** When a card charge returned an *unknown* result (Stripe 5xx/timeout/network — the PaymentIntent may have actually **succeeded**), the engine recorded `payment_status='unknown'` + the PaymentIntent id so the reconciler could later resolve it against Stripe. But that write was fire-and-forget — `_, _ = UpdatePayment(...)` discarded both the return **and the error**. It is the *sole* thing that enrolls the invoice into the reconciler's unknown-payment sweep, so if it failed (a transient DB blip) the invoice was **never enrolled** and the PaymentIntent id was **never persisted** — a possibly-succeeded charge orphaned, with no signal: **silent under-collection.** Found by the first-vs-second-practice dual-write audit. Fixed by making the load-bearing write retry with bounded backoff (`persistChargeOutcomeWithRetry`, mirroring the existing `startDunningWithRetry`), and on permanent failure **failing loud** — a `CRITICAL` log carrying the PaymentIntent id so an operator can reconcile manually (the no-silent-fallbacks rule). The caller's charge-error return is unchanged, so the existing unknown-vs-decline classification (and the reconciler defer) is unaffected. **No migration.** Guarded by `TestPersistChargeOutcomeWithRetry` (recovers after transient failures; surfaces an error after exhausting retries).

- **A saved card is no longer silently dropped when its `setup_intent.succeeded` arrives before the customer link is written (2026-06-23).** When a customer saved a card via the operator add-card or hosted "update payment" Stripe Checkout flows, Stripe sent two webhooks — `setup_intent.succeeded` (carries the card) and `checkout.session.completed` (writes the Velox-customer ↔ Stripe-customer link) — in **either order**. If the setup-intent arrived first, the handler couldn't resolve which Velox customer the card belonged to (Stripe Checkout doesn't copy session metadata onto the SetupIntent, and the link wasn't written yet), so it returned `nil` — which the webhook layer treats as success and **permanently dedup-marks**. Stripe's automatic redelivery then short-circuited, the card was never recorded, the customer detail page showed no payment method, and the unpaid invoice looped in auto-charge retry forever (the [no-card limbo, ADR-060](#) — reached here via a *dropped* card). The sibling of #271, whose fix landed on only one of the three save-card flows. Fixed two ways: **(1)** the two Checkout flows now stamp `velox_customer_id` on `setup_intent_data.metadata`, so the SetupIntent is **self-resolving** — resolution no longer depends on the link or event ordering; **(2)** when a setup-intent *with a card* still can't resolve its customer, the handler now returns a **transient** (non-`ErrNotFound`) error instead of `nil`, so the webhook layer writes **no** dedup row and Stripe **redelivers** — by which point a sibling `checkout.session.completed` (or the link-write) has resolved the customer. Stripe bounds redelivery to ~3 days, so a genuinely-foreign event can't loop unbounded. A setup-intent with **no** payment method is still acked (nothing to attach). Deliberately did **not** make the creation-time link-write fatal: `EnsureStripeCustomer` has no idempotency key on the Stripe customer create, so a fatal persist would leak duplicate Stripe customers and break the documented concurrent-first-PM-action race tolerance — stamping the SetupIntent is the clean equivalent. **No migration.** Guarded by `TestHandleWebhook_SetupIntent_UnresolvedCustomerRedelivers` (transient error, no dedup row, no attach) and `TestHandleWebhook_SetupIntent_NoPaymentMethodAcks`.

- **Five more termination-sink fixes from the liveness audit — dunning self-heals, ambiguous retries don't write off paid invoices, tax orphans recover post-`paid`, stranded webhooks re-claim (2026-06-23).** A batch of confirmed sinks from the same product-wide liveness/termination-invariant audit that produced ADR-060, all silent and reachable, none needing a migration. **(1) Dunning terminal-action failure no longer silently records "done."** When a dunning campaign exhausted and its `final_action` mover (pause / cancel / mark-uncollectible) *failed* (a Stripe blip, a conflicting state, a DB error), the run was still flipped to `escalated` — but escalated runs are excluded from both due-run pickers, so the action was **never re-attempted** and the dashboard showed a clean "escalated" beside an invoice/sub that never actually got closed. Now a failed mover keeps the run `state=active` with `resolution=action_failed` and `next_action_at` set, so the picker re-attempts it until it succeeds (`AttemptCount` is unchanged, so the clock-catchup no-progress guard still exits — no infinite loop). **(2) An ambiguous dunning-retry outcome no longer burns an attempt or writes off a possibly-paid invoice.** The dunning retrier mapped only the "call never happened" transient to a skip; an *unknown* charge outcome (Stripe 5xx/timeout/network — where the PaymentIntent may have actually **succeeded**) was counted as a failed attempt and could exhaust the campaign → cancel the subscription or mark the invoice uncollectible on a charge that really went through. Unknown now maps to the same skip the inline charge path already uses (the reconciler resolves it); a *definite* decline still counts and escalates. **(3) Tax-commit orphans are recovered after the invoice flips to paid/voided/uncollectible.** On the common synchronous finalize+auto-charge path the invoice reaches `paid` in the same flow, but the #267 commit-reconciler only scanned `status='finalized'` — so an orphan (Stripe tax committed, local `tax_transaction_id` write failed) was never recovered and a later credit-note/void couldn't reverse its tax (the tenant over-remits). The reconciler now also scans `paid/voided/uncollectible` within the existing 24h Stripe-calc window. *(Caveat: this fully closes the credit-note over-remit; the narrower void/mark-uncollectible-within-one-tick race needs the auto-charge-deferral follow-up, tracked.)* **(4) A stranded `pending` webhook delivery is re-claimable.** A freshly-created delivery has `next_retry_at` NULL (set only after the first attempt's outcome); if that goroutine died first, the claim predicate `next_retry_at <= NOW()` never matched (`NULL <= NOW()` is never true) and the webhook was silently never delivered. The predicate now includes `next_retry_at IS NULL` (the sibling tax-retry claim already did this). **(5) Two lying comments deleted** (`engine.go`, `threshold_scan.go`) that claimed a "pause-resume auto-finalize chain" which doesn't exist — pause-collection drafts stay draft until an operator finalizes them. Guarded by `TestExhaustRun_ActionFailure_*`/`_ActionSuccess_Escalates`, `TestClassifyDunningRetryError`, the real-Postgres `TestListPendingTaxCommit_IncludesNonFinalizedOrphans` and `TestListPendingDeliveries_ClaimsNullRetryOrphan`. The deferred sink — an issued credit note whose credit-grant leg failed mid-issue (customer shorted) — is **not** in this batch: its recovery scan predicate and migration footprint need a design decision first.

- **Card-less subscriptions no longer accrue unpaid invoices forever — they now enter dunning and reach a terminal (2026-06-23, ADR-060).** A finalized invoice for a customer with **no saved payment method** was flagged `auto_charge_pending`, emailed once, then retried by the auto-charge sweep **forever** — with nothing to charge, it never reached a terminal (pause/cancel/uncollectible). A card *decline* already starts dunning inline (`ChargeInvoice`), so the declined-card customer escalates; but the *no-card* path was an absorbing sink: the subscription stays active, keeps drafting invoices, and the unpaid balance grows unbounded with no escalation. Found by a product-wide liveness/termination-invariant audit (the same class as the void-tax and proration sinks). Fixed by routing card-less `auto_charge_pending` invoices into the **same dunning machinery** the declined-card path uses: a new scheduler step (and a symmetric test-clock catchup phase) enrolls each stalled candidate via the idempotent `StartDunning`, running **after** the auto-charge retry so only the genuinely card-less invoices remain (a decline already cleared the flag + started its own run; a success cleared the flag). The dunning retrier already treats "no payment method" as a real failed attempt, so the campaign ticks through grace + retries and exhausts to the policy `final_action` — the card-less delinquent now reaches a terminal. Adding a card mid-campaign lets the existing auto-charge sweep collect it and the run resolves `payment_recovered`. A tenant with dunning **disabled** keeps the no-card invoice un-dunned (deliberate — the same outcome the declined-card path gets with dunning off; the adapter swallows the disabled state rather than spamming a per-invoice error every tick). `StartDunning` is idempotent (one run per invoice), so the sweep is safe to run every tick. **No migration** — reuses the existing `auto_charge_pending` flag, the `ListAutoChargePending`(`...ForClock`) candidate queries, and the dunning state machine; the engine gains a `DunningStarter` interface wired in `router.go` (nil = inert, for local dev/tests). Guarded by `TestEnrollStalledForDunning_*` (enrolls the card-less candidate, inert when unwired, collects per-invoice errors) and `TestDunningStarterAdapter_*` (disabled → swallowed skip, real error → propagated). The broader lifecycle phases this audit surfaced (operator `collection_health` signal, opt-in first-payment gate, `unpaid` access-revoke terminal, usage spend-caps) remain trigger-gated for a design partner.

- **Invoice mutations are blocked or deferred while a payment is in flight — closes the status-strand and automated-clawback (`amount_paid` under-record) vectors end-to-end (2026-06-22, ADR-059).** An end-to-end audit asked which paths mutate an invoice while its charge is still settling (`payment_status` `processing`/`unknown` — reachable in *seconds* on cards, but in *days* under async bank methods like ACH/SEPA, which is how most B2B annual contracts pay). It found two unguarded classes, both now fixed. **(1) Status-strand (operator-reachable).** `invoice.Service.Void` and `MarkUncollectible` flipped status + reversed tax with no `payment_status` check — so a charge that later succeeds would strand captured money on a voided invoice, or (for uncollectible, which `MarkPaid` is still allowed from) leave the tenant **under-remitting** output tax on a real collected sale. Both now reject an in-flight invoice with a **409**, *before* any tax reversal. `RecordOfflinePayment` widened its guard from `processing` to `processing`+`unknown` (closes the ambiguous-charge double-collect window). And dunning's `manually_resolved` resolution — a **second, less-guarded void writer** that called the raw store `UpdateStatus(Voided)`, reversing no tax and emitting no `invoice.voided` event — now routes through `invoice.Service.Void` (single void writer: guards + tax reversal + event), with its inline PI-cancel/credit-reversal gated on the void actually succeeding (so an in-flight invoice's live charge isn't canceled behind a refused void). All guards share one canonical predicate, `domain.InvoicePaymentStatus.IsInFlight()`, so the definition can't drift across call sites (the drift this audit found). Matches Stripe ("you can't void, edit, or mark uncollectible an invoice with open payments"). **(2) Amount-drift / automated clawback ("Part B", now closed).** The automated ADR-050 unpaid-source clawback (mid-period cancel/downgrade/qty-decrease/item-removal) reduced `amount_due` on an in-flight funding source → `MarkPaid` then recorded `amount_paid` off the lowered figure → under-record (and naively skipping it instead would *over-charge* — the customer paid the full amount and never gets the unused portion back). **Fixed by deferring the *issue*, not the create:** the clawback is still created as a draft, but `Issue()` now no-ops while the source is in flight (leaving it `issue_pending`), and the `RetryPendingClawbackIssue` reconciler issues it once the source settles — at which point `Issue()`'s existing payment-status branch picks the channel automatically (settled paid → credit the unused share; settled failed → reduce `amount_due` to the consumed portion). So `amount_due` stays full through settle, `MarkPaid` records the full captured amount, and the credit lands after. The reconciler scan now skips drafts whose source is in flight (correlated `NOT EXISTS`) and **drops its prior 24h window** — an ACH/SEPA source can sit `processing` for days, so a fixed horizon would silently age the deferred draft out and drop the relief. `Issue()` also voids a deferred draft whose source was annulled (voided/uncollectible) before settling, so it can't double-reverse tax. **Reconciler-only, no settle-hook** (a `payment`→`creditnote` import would break the zero-cross-peer-import rule; the draft→issued CAS already guarantees exactly-once), and **no migration** (the `issue_pending` draft from migration 0121 *is* the durable deferred record). Design pressure-tested by two pre-build adversarial panels: the first scoped the status guards + single void writer (catching that the naive engine void-skip would silently under-credit a mixed funding set); the second designed Part B (catching that reusing the 24h-windowed scan would silently drop a deferred draft once its source settled late — the blocker). This closes Parts A **and** B for full capture; **Part C** (record `amount_paid` from the PI's `amount_received`) is **not reachable** in Velox's PaymentIntent-only full-capture model and is documented, not deferred. A stale-deferred-draft alarm (surface a clawback wedged on a never-settling payment so an operator can intervene) is a tracked *observability* follow-up — the obligation is durably captured and auto-issues on settle, so it doesn't affect correctness. Guarded by `TestInFlightGuards` (Void/MarkUncollectible/RecordOfflinePayment reject in-flight, allow pending/failed/paid, no tax reversal on a blocked void), `TestResolveRun_ManualVoid_RoutesThroughServiceAndGatesSideEffects` (dunning routes through the service voider; in-flight → void refused → PI-cancel/credit-reversal skipped), `TestAutomatedClawback_DeferUntilSettleCycle` (processing → drafted-not-issued; settle PAID → credit, FAILED → reduce, voided source → orphan draft voided), and the real-Postgres `TestListPendingClawbackDrafts_DefersInFlightSource` (in-flight skipped; an aged draft still issues once settled — proving the window is gone).

- **Operator credit notes are blocked while a payment is in flight — closes the operator vector of the `amount_paid` under-record edge (2026-06-22).** A credit note that reduces an invoice's `amount_due` while its payment is still in flight (`payment_status` `processing`/`unknown`) would, at settle, make `MarkPaid` record `amount_paid` off the now-lower `amount_due` — under-sizing the refund cap (credit-note refunds are capped at `amount_paid`). Reachable today only via the rare off-session-SCA (`requires_action`) path that lingers in `processing`; common under a future async payment method. **Fixed:** `creditnote.Service.Create` (the operator path) now rejects an amount-reducing credit note on an in-flight invoice with a **409** ("settle or cancel the payment first, or wait for charge reconciliation"). This is consistent with Stripe's open-payment lifecycle posture (Stripe blocks void/edit/mark-uncollectible while a payment is open, and points you to cancel the PaymentIntent) and with Velox's own existing `RecordPayment` in-flight guard — framed as a Velox safeguard, not a literal Stripe credit-note parity claim. PAID invoices (`payment_status='succeeded'`) take the refund/credit-balance branch and are never gated. The **automated** clawback (`CreateAndIssueAdjustment`, the ADR-050 unpaid-source mid-period cancel/downgrade) calls the `create()` core **directly** and is structurally NOT gated — it must proceed on a processing source; deferring its reduction until settle is the tracked **Part B** follow-up. **Part C** (record `amount_paid` from the PI's `amount_received` — only load-bearing under partial capture) also stays deferred; both are gated on a first async/SCA or partial-capture design partner (`docs/adr/README.md` "Open follow-ups"). Design pressure-tested by a pre-build adversarial panel, which caught that keying the automated bypass on the existing `IssuePending` flag would have **broken the ADR-050 clawback** (`CreateAndIssueAdjustment` never sets `IssuePending`) — hence the structural `create()`-direct bypass instead. No migration. Guarded by `TestCreate_InFlightPaymentGate` (operator CN on processing/unknown → 409; pending/paid → allowed; automated clawback on processing → still proceeds).

- **`payment.succeeded` now commits atomically with the invoice paid-flip — no longer lost in a post-commit crash (2026-06-22).** On a card settlement, `SettleSucceeded` flipped the invoice to paid (enqueuing `invoice.paid` inside that transaction) and then fired `payment.succeeded` + the receipt email **post-commit, each in its own transaction**. A process crash in that sub-millisecond window left the invoice correctly `paid` but **permanently dropped `payment.succeeded`** — the only event carrying the Stripe `payment_intent_id` (used for PI-keyed reconciliation): Stripe's redelivery hit the already-paid guard and skipped, and the payment reconciler only sweeps *unsettled* invoices, never re-touching a paid one. **Fixed** by enqueuing `payment.succeeded` inside the same transaction as the paid-flip + `invoice.paid` (new `MarkPaidCardSettlementTransition`, gated on the finalized→paid transition so it's exactly-once; non-card settlement paths — credits-cover, offline record-payment, dunning recovery, reconciler bare-MarkPaid — are unchanged and still emit only `invoice.paid`) and removing the now-redundant post-commit `fireEvent`. This is the transactional-outbox pattern the codebase already uses for `invoice.paid` (ADR-040), extended to the one event that had regressed to a post-commit dual-write. **Durability tiering, by design:** the consistency-critical events (`invoice.paid`, `payment.succeeded`) are now in-tx and crash-safe; the **receipt email stays post-commit best-effort** — at-least-once is the correct contract for email (it has dispatcher retry + 72h DLQ once enqueued), and making it in-tx would pull customer-email resolution + the suppression-list read under the invoice row lock — with a documented upgrade trigger (marker + reconciler re-fire) if a design partner needs guaranteed receipts; the card stamp stays post-commit (cosmetic + a Stripe network call that must never be held under the row lock). No happy-path behavior change (consumers see the same `payment.succeeded`, same table, same dispatcher), no migration. The symmetric `SettleFailed` move (`payment.failed` + failed-email in-tx; dunning-start stays post-commit, already idempotent via its `UNIQUE`-per-invoice constraint) is a tracked follow-up. Design pressure-tested by a 5-lens adversarial panel before building — it caught a wrong-tx atomicity-regression trap (routing the enqueue through the wrapper methods opens its own tx → silent no-fix) and an email suppression-gate bypass, and found a leaner approach than the first design. Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestMarkPaidCardSettlement_EnqueuesPaymentSucceededInTx` (card → `invoice.paid` + `payment.succeeded` once, gated; non-card → `invoice.paid` only) and `TestMarkPaidCardSettlement_RollsBackPaidFlipIfEventEnqueueFails` (a failed in-tx enqueue rolls the paid-flip back).

- **Subscription downgrade / removal / quantity-decrease clawback credit note is now created atomically with the item change, and the common post-commit failure is recovered (2026-06-20, ADR-057, migration 0121).** A hands-on test of the RemoveItem flow confirmed a money gap the earlier atomic-proration work missed: on a mid-cycle downgrade / item-removal / qty-decrease against a PAID source, the tax-reversing **clawback credit note** was created **and** issued **post-commit, fire-and-forget** — the item change committed, then the clawback ran outside the tx with its failure only logged (`"customer not yet credited, reconcile manually"`). So a `credit_notes` write failure (or a crash in that window) **removed the item but silently never credited the customer** — no rollback, no retry, money owed to the customer dropped. (The charge side — upgrades / qty-increases — was already atomic via the in-tx proration invoice; only the credit side was exposed, and `atomicRemoveItemWithProration`'s "a credit failure rolls back the delete" docstring was aspirational, not true.) **Fixed** by splitting the clawback across the tx boundary: the credit note is now created as a **DRAFT inside the item-change tx** (`createClawbackDraftsTx` → `CreateAdjustmentDraftTx` → `store.CreateUnderInvoiceLockTx` on the coordinator-owned `*sql.Tx`, ADR-056), so a create failure **rolls the item change back** (all-or-nothing — the customer is never removed-and-uncredited because a *create* failed); it is **issued post-commit** (the Stripe Tax reversal is an external call that must not ride the DB tx); and if `Issue()` **never ran** (a crash in the post-commit window, note still `status='draft' AND issue_pending=true`) the new **`RetryPendingClawbackIssue`** reconciler (wired into the scheduler tick next to `RetryPendingTaxCommit`) re-issues it on the next tick — safe by construction, since a still-`draft` note has applied nothing yet. Adds `credit_notes.issue_pending` (**migration 0121**, additive metadata-only — operator-created drafts default `false` and are never auto-issued). The non-atomic fallback path (no coordinator tx) is unchanged, and upgrades/qty-increases are a no-op on the new path. **Known residual gap (tracked, not closed here):** a *partial* issue — `Issue()` flipped the status to `issued` (its own committed tx) but a later side-effect then failed — is `status='issued'`, so the reconciler's `status='draft'` scan never sees it; it surfaces via a loud `ERROR` log and needs manual reconciliation. Closing that needs a re-entrant `Issue()` (the unpaid-source `ApplyCreditNote` is not yet idempotent) + an `issue_pending`-regardless-of-status scan, deliberately scoped out to keep the shared `Issue()` path untouched. The void/uncollectible `reverseInvoiceTax` (the other fire-and-forget member of this class) is a flagged fast-follow. Guarded by the real-Postgres `TestCreateUnderInvoiceLockTx_RollsBackWithCallerTx` (draft create participates in the caller's tx → rolls back with it) and the service-level `TestRetryPendingClawbackIssue` (reconciler re-issues an Issue-never-ran draft).

- **Marking an invoice uncollectible then voiding it no longer reverses the committed tax twice (2026-06-19, product idempotency/atomicity audit G1).** `Void` permits an already-`uncollectible` invoice (annulling a bad debt is a legitimate operator action), but `MarkUncollectible` and `Void` filed their Stripe Tax reversals under **different** references (`inv_uncoll_<id>` vs `inv_void_<id>`) that don't dedup — and a tax reversal doesn't change the credited basis the reversal amount is computed from — so the dunning-gives-up→annul sequence **reversed the same tax transaction twice, under-remitting the tenant's output tax.** Fixed by using one **invoice-stable reversal reference** (`inv_taxrev_<id>`) on both terminal transitions, so the second reversal dedups at Stripe (same reference + idempotency key `velox_tax_rev_<ref>`) to exactly one — and self-heals if a prior reversal had failed. Manual/none tax providers have no committed transaction, so they were never affected. From the same product-wide audit (verdict: idempotency + atomicity are real, reachable, and Stripe/Orb/Lago-faithful — this was the one reachable money bug): the **final-on-cancel** invoice failure now logs at ERROR (matching the sibling credit leg) so a dropped partial-period invoice is alarmable; the tax-reversal credit-note-total fallback logs at ERROR with a reconcile note; and a stale `PauseAtomic` doc comment (hard-pause was removed in PR-8 / migration 0090) was corrected. No migration. Guarded by `TestUncollectibleThenVoid_ReversesTaxWithOneStableReference`.

- **Cross-interval plan swap no longer silently drops the new period's first invoice (2026-06-19, ADR-056).** An adversarial audit of the proration write paths found the immediate **cross-interval** plan swap (e.g. monthly→yearly on an `in_advance` plan, same cadence) ran four writes across two stores with **no shared transaction**: refund → plan write → watermark advance → bill new period. The watermark advanced *before* the new-period bill, and a `BillOnCreate` failure — which fires on a **routine** tax-calc hiccup (Stripe Tax `customer_data_invalid`, missing address, provider blip), no crash needed — was swallowed with a log line claiming `"scheduler catchup will retry"`. **That was false:** the cycle close skips already-prepaid `in_advance` base segments and the watermark had already moved past the new period, so the new plan's day-1 base was **never billed — a permanent, silent revenue leak.** Fixed by restructuring the swap **atomically** on one coordinator-owned `*sql.Tx` (the pattern the add/quantity proration path already uses, ADR-030): the plan write + watermark advance + new-period invoice insert now commit **together** via new `*Tx` store/engine methods (`UpdateBillingCycleTx`, `BillOnCreateTx`), so the watermark can never advance unless the new invoice committed — a failed in-tx bill rolls the whole swap back and surfaces loudly. The external Stripe steps (the OLD-period refund, the new invoice's tax commit + auto-charge) run **post-commit** (`FinalizeCrossIntervalSwap`), never inside the tx. `BillOnCreate` was factored into compute (`buildOnCreateInvoice`) / persist / finalize with **identical behavior for its existing callers**. No migration. The narrow, credit-note-cap-bounded **double-credit on a full crash-retry** (the refund's post-commit step is not yet idempotent) is **knowingly deferred** — trigger to revisit: a real `in_advance` design partner or idempotency-key middleware. Also closed a sibling silent-fail: the cycle **idempotent-skip heal path** now propagates a failed watermark advance instead of swallowing it (a swallowed heal stranded the watermark and re-billed the skip every tick with no alert). Guarded by `TestUpdateItemTx_CrossIntervalAtomic` (atomic in-tx bill, rollback on failure, deferred refund/finalize, cross-cadence rejection) and `TestBillOnePeriod_HealPathPropagatesAdvanceError`.

- **Anniversary subscriptions on the 29th/30th/31st now bill month-end correctly instead of ratcheting off it (2026-06-18, ADR-055, migration 0120).** An adversarial audit of the billing date-math found a real bug: an **anniversary** monthly/yearly subscription anchored on a high day-of-month permanently drifted its billing day after the first short month. The cycle advance was *self-referential* — it added one interval to the *previously computed* boundary via Go's `AddDate`, which overflows `Jan 31 + 1mo` to "Feb 31" → **Mar 3**, and then kept advancing off the drifted value: `Jan 31 → Mar 3 → Apr 3 → May 3 …`, locked on the 3rd forever (day-30 → the 2nd, day-29 → the 1st, leap Feb-29 yearly → Mar 1). The operator's chosen billing day was lost, no invoice was dated in February, and the proration denominator for those subs was contaminated. This diverged from Stripe/Chargebee/Lago, which clamp to the month's last day and restore. **Fixed** by persisting the operator's intended anchor day (new `subscriptions.billing_anchor_day`, set at activation in the tenant timezone) and advancing to `min(anchorDay, lastDayOfMonth)` from that stable anchor — so `Jan 31 → Feb 28 → Mar 31 → Apr 30 → May 31 → Jun 30 → Jul 31 …` and a leap Feb-29 anchor bills Feb 28 in common years, Feb 29 in leap years. The anchor is recomputed when the cycle re-anchors to "now" (cross-interval plan swap, threshold reset); the threshold-reset path also now re-snaps calendar subs to the 1st (a secondary fix from the same audit). The column is **additive** — `0` (calendar-monthly and legacy/unset rows) preserves the exact prior behavior, so calendar billing is unchanged. Supersedes ADR-058's "anniversary month-end overflow is not a bug" note. Guarded by `TestAnniversaryMonthEnd_ClampsAndRestores`, `TestYearlyLeapAnchor_ClampsAndRestores`, `TestAnniversaryAnchorDayZero_LegacyFallback`, `TestAnchorDayFor`.

- **Invoice Unit Price now shows sub-cent rates at full precision instead of `$0.00` (2026-06-17, ADR-054).** A usage line for a sub-cent rate (e.g. 1,000 units billed $3.00 — a $0.003/unit rate) rendered **Unit Price $0.00** while the Amount was correct: the line stored the per-unit price only as whole `unit_amount_cents`, back-derived from the rounded amount (`round(300 ÷ 1000) = 0`), and both dashboard and PDF printed it at two decimals. The amount was always right; the unit column just looked wrong (and `1,000 × $0.00 ≠ $3.00`), which matters for the AI-token/usage case where sub-cent rates are normal. Fixed by surfacing a **full-precision per-unit price, derived on read** — a new `unit_amount_decimal` (decimal cents, e.g. `"0.3"`) computed once as `amount_cents ÷ quantity` (capped at 12 dp, Stripe `unit_amount_decimal` parity) and served on the invoice line; the dashboard, the PDF, and the public hosted page render it via the decimal-aware `formatRate`, which never collapses a sub-cent rate to `$0.00`. It's the **effective** rate, so `quantity × unit` reconciles with the rounded amount and it stays well-defined for blended/tiered lines. **No migration, no backfill** — the value is derived from the authoritative persisted `amount_cents` + `quantity`, so storing it would only risk drift; every existing line is fixed on read. Matches the two-track precision model peers converge on (Stripe/Chargebee/Recurly show the unit price at full precision and round only the line amount/total). Line amounts and totals stay whole-cent int64 (ADR-045 unchanged). Guarded by `TestEffectiveUnitAmountDecimal` (sub-cent, fractional qty, zero-qty guard, negative credit line) and `TestInvoiceLineItem_MarshalJSON_CarriesUnitAmountDecimal`. Credit-note line items share the whole-cent shape and are a deferred same-pattern follow-up.

- **Tax "customer data invalid" attention message reads cleanly (2026-06-17).** The invoice-detail message for the `tax.customer_data_invalid` attention said *"…is missing or malformed data the tax provider requires…"* — a broken parallel (`is missing data` ✓ but `is malformed data` reads as "the profile *is* the data") and "malformed" is engineering jargon for a finance/ops/support reader. Now: *"The customer's billing profile **has** missing or **invalid** data the tax provider requires (postal code, country, or tax ID)."* Both branches bind to `data` and the wording stays plain. Copy-only; the ADR-009 wire-shape example was kept in sync. No code-path or schema change.

- **Deleting the default card now promotes a replacement atomically and syncs it to Stripe (2026-06-17, ADR-053 follow-up).** When an operator removed the customer's default card, Velox auto-promoted the newest remaining card to default — but the detach and the promotion were **two separate transactions**, and the promotion updated only Velox's DB, never Stripe. Two gaps: (1) a crash or a transient DB error on the promote left the customer with active cards but **no default**, silently gating auto-charge off until the next card action; (2) Stripe's `invoice_settings.default_payment_method` drifted stale. Both closed: detach + promote-newest now run in **one transaction** (`DetachAndRebalance` — a transient failure on the promote rolls the detach back too, so the "≥1 active card ⇒ exactly one default" invariant always holds), and the promoted default is **best-effort synced to Stripe** for dashboard/Checkout display parity (cosmetic since #281 made the charge path read Velox's default directly — a Stripe failure logs + audits a `stripe_sync_error` and never blocks the detach). Guarded by `TestDetach_PromotesNewestAndSyncsStripe`, `TestDetach_PromotionStripeSyncFailureStillSucceeds`, and the real-Postgres `TestDetachAndRebalance_AtomicPromote`. No migration.

- **Auto-charge now charges the exact default card Velox resolved, not whatever Stripe picks (2026-06-17, ADR-053).** Which saved card gets auto-charged was decided in two independent places that had to agree: Velox's `payment_methods` default row, and Stripe's `customer.invoice_settings.default_payment_method`. The charge passed only the Stripe **customer** id to the PaymentIntent and let Stripe select the card (its own default, else the most-recently-created card), while the engine *gated* the charge on Velox's `is_default` row — so one store decided *whether* to charge and a different store decided *which card*. They can diverge: the operator "Make default" action syncs both, but the **auto-promotion when the default card is deleted** updated only Velox's DB, never Stripe, and any future default-write path could forget the same sync. Now **Velox is the single source of truth**: `PaymentReadiness.ResolveForCharge` returns the default card's Stripe PaymentMethod id (the gate *and* the selection), it's threaded through every charge entry point — cycle finalize, subscription-create, final-on-cancel, threshold scan, the auto-charge sweep, manual operator charge, and dunning retry — and the PaymentIntent names that **exact** card. Stripe's implicit "default-then-newest-card" selection is **deleted**; `invoice_settings.default_payment_method` is now a best-effort cosmetic mirror that can never drive a charge. A charge with no resolved PM **fails loud** (no silent fallback to a guessed card) — the gates already require a default first, so an empty id is a surfaced wiring bug, not a cue to let Stripe pick. Matches Stripe's documented off-session pattern (specify `payment_method` explicitly). Guarded by `TestChargeInvoice_Success` (the resolved PM is threaded into the PaymentIntent) and `TestChargeInvoice_RequiresPaymentMethod` (empty PM → error, no Stripe call). **No migration.** Follow-ups (now cosmetic/fail-safe, not correctness): sync the auto-promoted default to Stripe for dashboard display; make detach+promote a single transaction.

- **Proration-audit follow-ups + funding-set invariant guard (2026-06-15).** A deep audit of the proration flows (after the multi-invoice fixes below) caught three residual issues and the process gap that produced the whole class. **(1) Mixed paid/unpaid funding set:** on a cancel/swap whose period was funded by a paid invoice *and* a partially-paid upgrade invoice, the unpaid invoice's share was clamped to its `amount_due` and the overflow **silently dropped**. It now water-fills the un-relievable overflow onto the paid invoice (which credits the customer); the loud-fail is reserved for an all-paid set that genuinely can't absorb the credit. **(2) Void/uncollectible tax under-reversal:** `reverseInvoiceTax` used `amount_paid + amount_due` as "remaining un-reversed," but **applied customer credit** reduces `amount_due` without reversing tax — so a voided invoice that had credit applied **under-reversed** its output tax (tenant over-remits). It now reads the credited total directly (`total − Σ non-voided credit notes`). **(3) The root-cause process gap:** the "one invoice funds a period" assumption was implicit, so when periods became multi-invoice nobody re-audited the readers. It's now an **enforced invariant** — `make lint-funding-set` (in CI) fails on any new single-row period lookup (`FindBaseInvoiceForPeriod`/`GetByProrationSource`) in proration decision code without a `// single-invoice-ok:` justification. Guarded by `TestSettleUnusedAcrossFunding_MixedPaidUnpaid_NoSilentDrop` and `TestVoid_CreditApplied_TaxNotUnderReversed`. No migration.

- **Downgrade clawback fans across funding invoices; cancel/swap credit is now headroom-aware (2026-06-15).** Completes the multi-invoice proration work. (1) A mid-period **downgrade / quantity-decrease / item-removal** clawed back the removed value against the single `FindBaseInvoiceForPeriod` invoice — so after a prior upgrade split the period across two invoices, the clawback could exceed that one invoice's credit-note cap and loud-fail (manual reconcile). Now it fans across **every** funding invoice: a **plan downgrade** reverses **LIFO** (the most-recent/upgrade invoice first, undoing the latest price level against *its* own tax and leaving the still-active base plan untouched); **fungible** quantity/item changes split **proportionally**. Each piece is capped at its invoice's remaining headroom, and resolution runs read-only inside the atomic item-change transaction so genuine headroom exhaustion **rolls the change back pre-commit** (clean 409) instead of a post-commit reconcile gap. Industry-anchored: Stripe flexible-billing mode reverses the original charge, and per-charge credit memos are the dominant downgrade model. (2) The merged cancel/swap fan-out sized shares against raw subtotal, so a **downgrade then cancel** could overrun the upgrade invoice whose headroom the downgrade already consumed — it now caps each share at **remaining** creditable (`creditnote.Service.CreditedCents`) and **water-fills** the overflow onto invoices that still have room (`money.AllocateByWeightCapped`), failing loud only when the period's combined headroom is genuinely exhausted. New `money.AllocateLIFO` + `AllocateByWeightCapped` primitives (exhaustively unit-tested). **No migration.** Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_Downgrade_LIFOAcrossFundingInvoices` (downgrade after upgrade targets the upgrade invoice, base untouched), `TestSettleUnusedAcrossFunding_HeadroomSpill`, and the allocator suites.

- **Mid-period upgrade then cancel no longer silently overcharges (2026-06-15).** When an `in_advance` subscription was upgraded mid-period (which cuts a *second* proration invoice for the same cycle) and then immediately canceled, the customer was credited **$0** for their unused prepayment instead of the full amount. The cancel-proration credit is sized off the post-upgrade base — correct, and equal to the unused prepayment across **both** funding invoices — but it was issued as a single credit note against the one invoice `FindBaseInvoiceForPeriod` resolves (the day-1 base invoice, since the upgrade invoice's base-fee line carries the change date, not the period start). That one invoice is too small, the credit note's per-invoice cap hard-errored, and the cancel path swallowed the error to a silent $0. Now a new `FindFundingInvoicesForPeriod` resolves **every** invoice that funded the cycle (base ∪ the mid-period `subscription_update` invoice, via its already-populated header columns — no migration), and the credit is **fanned across them**: a largest-remainder partition of the one authoritative figure (never an independent per-invoice recompute, which would over-credit on upgrade→downgrade→cancel), each piece capped at its own invoice and reversing its own proportional tax. The same multi-source settlement now runs for **cross-interval plan-swaps** (a swap after a prior upgrade had the identical latent cap). A credit that still can't be issued now **fails loud** — `slog.Error` "customer not credited; manual credit required" — instead of a silent warning, while keeping the terminal cancel/swap itself non-blocking on a transient credit failure. Matches the industry superset (Stripe credit-balance ledger + per-debit-split / Recurly); Lago shares Velox's pre-fix single-invoice constraint. Guarded by `TestBillOnCancel_FansAcrossUpgradeInvoice` (full $153.33 across two credit notes, was $0) and `TestAllocateByWeight` (partition sums exactly; over-credit guard). The **downgrade-clawback** leg shares the single-source resolution but claws back only the *removed* value, so correct multi-invoice attribution needs its own design — tracked as a fast-follow; it already fails loud today (no silent drop).

- **Void / mark-uncollectible no longer double-reverses tax (2026-06-15).** Voiding or marking-uncollectible a finalized-but-unpaid invoice unconditionally fired a **full** tax reversal — but such an invoice can already have adjustment credit notes (the ADR-050 downgrade/cancel relief), each of which already reversed its own tax slice. The full reversal then re-reversed the already-reversed portion, under-remitting the tenant's output tax to the authority. Void/MarkUncollectible now reverse only the **remaining** un-credit-noted gross (`amount_paid + amount_due`); full-mode is preserved when no credit note exists. Guarded by `TestVoid_PartialTaxReversalAfterPriorCreditNote`.

### Security

- **Velox fails closed when it can't enforce RLS in staging/production (2026-06-12).** Multi-tenant isolation relies on Row-Level Security, which only applies to the non-owner `velox_app` role Velox connects as for request-time queries. If that role couldn't be derived from `DATABASE_URL` or the pool couldn't open, boot previously **fell back to the admin pool with a warning** — meaning every request ran as the table owner and bypassed tenant isolation on every table. The most likely self-host misconfig (a superuser `DATABASE_URL` + no `velox_app` role) silently disabled isolation behind one WARN line. Now, with `APP_ENV=staging` or `production`, Velox **refuses to start** in that situation rather than serve cross-tenant data; `local` keeps the warn-and-continue (single-tenant dev box). Documented the `velox_app` role requirement in `docs/self-host.md` (the compose path already auto-creates it). No schema change.

- **Publishable API keys no longer carry any tenant-wide scopes (2026-06-12).** `vlx_pub_` keys are browser-embeddable (they ship in client-side JS) and previously held `customer:read` + `invoice:read` + `usage:read` + `subscription:read`. With the route gating, that let any visitor of a page embedding the key list every customer's PII (`GET /v1/customers`), pull every invoice PDF, read tenant revenue (`/v1/analytics/*`), and bulk-export full datasets (`/v1/exports/*.csv`). An earlier pass removed the *write* scopes (a visitor could create customers / fake usage) but left the reads — yet tenant-wide reads in a browser key are the same exposure class, and Stripe's `pk_` equivalents deliberately can't list customers or read revenue. No Velox browser flow needs these reads (the cost dashboard and hosted/payment pages authenticate with their own per-resource tokens, not publishable keys), so publishable keys are now **authenticate-only** (empty scope set); re-add a narrow, purpose-built scope when a concrete browser use case names one. Guarded by the updated `TestHasPermission_PublishableRestricted` / `TestRequire_PublishableKeyRestricted` (all reads + writes now 403). No schema change.

- **`feature_flag_overrides` now enforces Row-Level Security (2026-06-12, migration 0113).** It was the last tenant-scoped table created in 0001 without RLS — every other tenant table got `ENABLE` + `FORCE` + a `tenant_isolation` policy, but this one was missed. Under the supported `velox_app` (non-owner) deploy role, per-tenant feature-flag overrides were readable and writable across tenants. Added the same tenant-only policy the rest of the schema uses (`bypass OR tenant_id = app.tenant_id`) with `ENABLE` + `FORCE`; the table is account-level config with no `livemode` column (per 0020), so the policy is deliberately tenant-only and carries **no** livemode predicate. The four override store methods (`GetOverride`/`SetOverride`/`RemoveOverride`/`ListOverrides`) now run inside a `TxTenant` transaction so the policy filters to the caller's tenant — a bare-pool query would have matched zero rows under FORCE RLS. `feature_flags` itself is global (no tenant_id, no RLS) and stays on the pool. No operator-visible behavior change (the override management API derives its tenant from the authenticated principal, never the URL — IDOR was already blocked at the handler; this closes the database-layer gap). Guarded by `TestRLSIsolation_FeatureFlagOverrides` (cross-tenant read + write denied, policy asserted tenant-only) and the migration round-trip test.

- **`stripe_provider_credentials` now enforces `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` (2026-06-12, migration 0111).** This table holds each tenant's encrypted Stripe secret keys — the most sensitive rows in the schema. It had RLS `ENABLE`d with a tenant-isolation policy (0032) but, unlike every other tenant-scoped table (the 0006 pattern), never `FORCE`d it. `ENABLE` without `FORCE` exempts the table **owner** from RLS, so a deployment whose `DATABASE_URL` points at the owning role (the default on self-managed Postgres) silently bypassed tenant isolation on exactly this table. Added the missing `FORCE`; the down reverts to ENABLE-only. Caught by the migration round-trip test.

### Removed

- **Inert invoice-reminder scheduler phase removed (2026-06-13, ADR-029 §6 amended).** The billing scheduler (cron) and the test-clock catchup orchestrator each carried an "invoice reminders" phase that only ever **queried invoices approaching `due_at` and logged the count** — no reminder email was ever dispatched. Deleted both hooks, their `InvoiceReminder` / `ReminderLister` interfaces, the `Service.ListApproachingDue` / `…ForClock` entries, the two `PostgresStore` queries, and the wiring in `cmd/velox` + the router. Rationale: a proactive **pre-due** payment reminder to the customer is a B2C/SMB pattern, not the B2B/AI-infra norm Velox targets — operators own collection, and **dunning** (post-due) is the real money-protection path that already works. Carrying inert scaffolding for an unbuilt, off-wedge feature is the doc/code-that-lies this codebase deletes rather than maintains; the disjoint catchup orchestrator now ends at Phase 5 (dunning). No schema change; rebuild trigger is a design partner explicitly asking for pre-due reminders (then it returns as a real outbox-dispatching phase). The operator-initiated **"Send reminder" / "Email payment link"** invoice action is unrelated and unchanged. Verified: `go build`/`vet`/`-short` green across `billing`, `testclock`, `invoice`, `api`. From the periodic-jobs / machinery audit (wire-or-delete → delete).

- **Customer self-serve portal removed (2026-06-09, ADR-051).** Deleted the magic-link customer portal (`/portal`) — backend `internal/portalapi` (`/v1/me/*`) + `internal/customerportal` (portal sessions `vlx_cps_…` + magic-links `vlx_cpml_…`), the three frontend portal pages + `portalAuth.ts`, and the `/v1/public/customer-portal` + `/v1/customer-portal-sessions` routes (~3,000 LOC). Multi-platform research (Stripe/Chargebee/Recurly/Zuora + Orb/Metronome/Lago + OpenAI/Anthropic/Modal/Replicate) showed a hosted self-serve subscription portal is a **B2C/SMB pattern, not the B2B/AI-infra norm** — AI-native peers ship embeddable cost/usage surfaces + APIs and let the vendor build their own UI; B2B customers pay/are-managed operator-side. **Nothing customers rely on broke:** card collection stays operator-driven (send-setup-email / copy-link → Stripe-hosted Checkout; `paymentmethods.Service` intact for charging), payment is via the hosted-invoice public token, cost/usage via the cost-dashboard public token, and lifecycle (cancel/resume) via the operator dashboard. The `customer_portal_sessions` / `customer_portal_magic_links` tables are **retained** (ADR-039 coupon precedent — thin rebuild if a B2C/SMB ICP ever needs it; no DROP migration). Customer auth surfaces are now hosted-invoice token + cost-dashboard token only. Verified: `go build`/`vet`/`-short` + frontend `tsc -b && vite build` all green.

### Changed

- **Customer tax status: engine-determined reverse charge is now the steered B2B path; domestic reverse charge is flagged (2026-06-15, ADR-052).** From an e2e audit of the customer billing-profile tax override. The three statuses (`standard`/`exempt`/`reverse_charge`) are correct and Stripe-parity, but the manual `reverse_charge` flag short-circuits to $0 *before any tax engine runs* — which silently zero-rates a **domestic** sale (reverse charge is cross-border B2B only; a buyer in the seller's own country is taxed normally). Stripe (and Chargebee) instead **determine** reverse charge from the buyer's tax ID + jurisdiction and treat the manual flag as an unconditional exception. Velox already forwards the buyer tax ID to Stripe for `standard` customers (Stripe then applies reverse charge only where valid, VIES-validated), so this is now the **steered path**: the dashboard reframes `Standard` as "add a Tax ID for B2B — reverse charge is applied automatically (cross-border)" and presents `reverse_charge`/`exempt` as explicit manual overrides. A **non-blocking warning** is logged at compute time when `reverse_charge` is set on a buyer in the seller's registration country, so the likely-wrong override is visible instead of silently under-collecting. No computation change (the override is still honored — it's the only mechanism for manual/none providers), no schema change. A save-time hard block was deliberately rejected (it can't fire when company country is unset, misreads the empty-customer-country case, and can't model multi-registration — an adversarial design review confirmed warning-not-block). Deferred (trigger: first EU design partner): real multi-registration enforcement + VIES validation; structured exempt reason codes wait for the first US sales-tax partner. Guarded by `TestDomesticReverseCharge` (fires domestic, never on cross-border or incomplete data).

- **List-page layout tweaks from the all-pages density audit (2026-06-13).** Customers: the External ID column duplicated the sub-label already shown under every name — dropped (4 columns now, sub-label gains truncation + hover). Invoices: the payment chip no longer restates the lifecycle badge on settled rows (paid ⇒ "succeeded", voided — pure noise; it stays on open invoices where pending/processing/failed is the signal), and the PDF column is an icon button instead of a labeled "Download". Webhooks events tab: the ID column printed the constant `vlx_whevt_` prefix + 2 distinguishing characters — now shows the id tail with a copy button. MeterDetail: dropped the no-value Created column from the dimension-rules table. CustomerDetail: the bottom card grid goes single-column below lg (was a hard 2-col squeeze at split-screen widths) and Sent emails spans the full row instead of leaving a half-row gap; the invoice composer's Type column now fits its longest option. Deliberately skipped: Pricing Rules row navigation (no rules detail page exists to navigate to — building one is new scope, not a layout tweak).

- **Credits ledger redesigned to the industry ledger shape (2026-06-13).** The customer ledger table had 7 columns — two of them low-value ("Invoice" holding only a "View invoice" link, "Expires" mostly em-dashes) — which on common window widths pushed **Amount and Balance off the right edge** and clipped the Expires dates: a money ledger showing no money. Now 5 columns (Date · Type · Description · Amount · Balance), Stripe-style: the description itself is the invoice link ("Applied to invoice DEMO-000906"), a grant's expiry renders as subtext under its description, and expiry rows read **"Grant expired"** with the machine id demoted to mono subtext (the stored description text is unchanged — it is load-bearing for the backend's expiry dedup LIKE-match; a structured grant-reference column is the flagged long-term fix). CSV export keeps the full column set including invoice id.

- **Dashboard consistency sweep (2026-06-13).** Batch 3 of the frontend UX audit. Money: `formatCents` now renders thousands separators ($10,000.00 — every money surface), and the audit-log metadata amounts use it too. Navigation: browser tab titles are real ("Invoices · Velox", "INV-2026-0042 · Velox" — every tab previously read "web-v2"), and the sidebar keeps the section highlighted on detail pages (/customers/:id highlights Customers; /plans and /meters highlight Pricing). Safety: deleting a dunning policy asks via a proper dialog (was the native browser confirm()), and webhook secret rotation has a pending state + double-submit guard. Data: the webhook live tail resolves customer names (was raw IDs), credit notes fetch an explicit 100-row window with an honest truncation notice (the implicit server default silently capped the list at 25), and ⌘K plan results deep-link to the plan page (was the list). Copy: the Recipes and Usage Events empty states drop engineering jargon and gain a next action; status badges on API keys / test clocks route through the shared status palette. A11y: the invoice PDF preview overlay is a real dialog (role, aria-modal, Escape closes). Deferred with reason: the Credits confirm-dialog currency symbol stays $ — the ledger doesn't carry currency to that dialog yet; plumbing it is the fix, not a hardcoded symbol swap.

- **Detail pages and primary actions now show real loading feedback (2026-06-12).** From the frontend UX audit, batch 2 of 3. (1) All six entity detail pages (invoice, customer, subscription, plan, meter, test clock) replaced their full-page spinner — which hand-rolled a breadcrumb fallback and visibly shifted layout when data arrived — with a shared `DetailSkeleton`: the real breadcrumb in its final position plus a stable header/stat/body ghost layout (the detail-page sibling of the list pages' `TableSkeleton`). (2) Primary action buttons that fire multi-second backend calls (Finalize, Collect Payment, Activate, End trial now, Resume collection, scheduled-cancel Undo, payment-method Set-as-default/Remove) now show an in-button spinner + progress label ("Collecting…") instead of silently dimming. (3) The Dashboard's Recent Invoices card showed the "No invoices yet" empty copy **while still loading** — it now shows ghost rows, and the empty copy no longer references internal navigation jargon. (4) Dunning policies: plain "Loading…" text → skeleton rows, and the bare "No policies yet" line → a proper empty state explaining what a policy does with a New-policy action. Frontend only.

- **Audit Log page: operator names, humanized rows, copy button, and seek pagination (2026-06-12).** The UX tail of the audit-subsystem audit. **(1) Operator names.** Dashboard-operator rows (`actor_type='user'`, from #225) now resolve to the user's display name or email — the read query joins `users` the same way it already joined `api_keys`/`customers`; pre-fix they rendered the raw `user` enum. **(2) Humanized rows.** The action badge shows "Subscription Item Updated" instead of the raw `subscription.item_updated` enum; metadata labels case acronyms ("IP Address", not "Ip Address"); structured metadata values (e.g. the settings-change `{field: {from,to}}` map) render as JSON instead of `[object Object]`; subscription item add/remove/update rows now carry the sub's code as their label (they passed an empty label before); the expanded Resource ID gets a copy button; trial-ended / item-added / item-removed / settings-updated rows get proper descriptions. **(3) Seek pagination.** Numbered offset pages re-ran a `COUNT(*)` on **every** page view — and the RLS policy's bypass OR-branch makes that COUNT an all-tenant sequential scan — so deep paging (and the CSV export, which paid the COUNT on each of up to 500 export pages) degraded badly. The list now pages Stripe-style with Previous/Next over the **existing** cursor API (`?after=`, shipped 2026-05-29 but never used by the frontend): only page 1 computes the total; every deeper page and every export page after the first seeks in O(log N) with no COUNT. The export loop hops onto cursors after its first page. Also: removed the ghost `subscription.plan_changed` frontend branches (no backend writer) and three dead audit-action constants (`archive`/`unarchive`/`redeem`). Frontend + one read-query join; no schema change; `tsc` + Go integration tests green.

- **Quantity-increase proration invoices now render the two-line credit/charge pair (2026-06-12).** Raising an item's quantity mid-period produced a single line whose **Quantity was the new total but whose Amount was the delta-only charge** — so the derived unit price was a fiction and the row's own arithmetic didn't close (1 → 3 seats at $100/seat, half period: qty 3 × unit $33.33 = $99.99 against Amount $100.00 — integer truncation, visible on the invoice face). Quantity changes now get the same ADR-048 Phase C treatment as plan upgrades, the shape Stripe stamps for quantity updates too: *"Unused time on 1 × Seat (after \<date\>)"* (negative, old quantity) + *"Remaining time on 3 × Seat (after \<date\>)"* (positive, new quantity) — both lines name the same plan, so the seat counts carry the contrast, every unit price is the true prorated per-seat rate, and **qty × unit = amount exactly on both lines**. Same `splitUpgradeProration` partition (split runs AFTER the single tax call; invoice subtotal/tax/total byte-identical to the old net). Item **add** keeps the single net line — `oldAmount` is 0, there is nothing unused to credit. Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_QuantityIncrease_RendersTwoLines` (line coherence asserted) + `TestUpdateItem_ItemAdd_KeepsSingleLine`. No schema or API change.

- **Subscription "current period" displays now show the inclusive last covered day too (2026-06-09, ADR-058 follow-up).** Completes the companion invoice change (below) for the React subscription surfaces: the subscription-detail current-period range + its timeline "Period End" dot, the plans-page subscriptions table, the cost-dashboard cycle bar, and the invoice line-item "Covers <range>" now read **"Jun 1, 2028 – Jun 30, 2028"** (the last day covered) instead of the exclusive "Jun 1 – Jul 1". **Event/boundary dates deliberately keep the exclusive instant** — "Renews Jul 1", "Cancels Jul 1", "Ended Jul 1", "Next billing", "keeps access until" each name an event that fires *on* the boundary, so the day-before would be wrong; only period *coverage ranges* shift. Implemented with two small TS helpers in `web-v2/src/lib/dates.ts` (`formatCivilDate`, `formatCivilPeriod`) that mirror the Go `domain.InclusiveDisplayEnd` / `FormatInclusivePeriod` exactly (calendar-day step-back in tenant TZ, en-dash, empty/clamp rules) — **not** a new backend field or DB column. Rationale: these surfaces are client-rendered and already receive the raw half-open `current_billing_period_start/end` over the wire, so the inclusive day is derived at render from data already present — no new API field, no read-path plumbing, and storage stays half-open `[start, end)` (the canonical, gap-free, instant-precise fact; the inclusive day is a tenant-TZ, date-granularity *projection* that would go stale on a timezone change if persisted). The invoice keeps its backend `billing_period_display` because the PDF is server-rendered with no client to compute it; the canonical calendar math stays pinned by the Go `TestFormatInclusivePeriod`. Frontend-only; no schema, no API change. (web-v2 has no test runner today, so the TS mirror was verified against the Go edge-case table — IST/UTC/LA hosts × June, year-boundary, leap Feb, NY-DST-span, yearly, non-midnight end — via a throwaway parity script; a committed FE regression guard would need vitest, flagged as a follow-up.)

- **Invoice billing period now displays the inclusive last covered day (2026-06-09, ADR-058 follow-up).** Invoices showed the half-open *exclusive* boundary — "Jun 1 – Jul 1" for a June period — which is the universal *storage* convention but not how most leaders *display* it (Stripe, Zuora, and Lago render the inclusive last covered day — Stripe's API even labels `period.end` "inclusive"; Chargebee and Recurly render the exclusive boundary — a common convention, not universal). They now render **"Jun 1 – Jun 30"**: the last day actually covered, date-only, in the tenant timezone. Storage stays half-open `[start, end)` and the raw `billing_period_start`/`billing_period_end` API fields are unchanged (SDK contract); a new computed, read-only `billing_period_display` field carries the formatted string. One Go helper (`domain.FormatInclusivePeriod`) authors it for the PDF, hosted invoice, portal, dashboard, and invoice list, so the period can't drift across the Go and TS runtimes — and the inclusive end is a CALENDAR-day step in the tenant TZ, not a 24h instant subtraction (the ADR-058 trap). One-off invoices with no period omit it. (This display convention is precisely what would have made the ADR-058 timezone off-by-one visible on the invoice in the first place.) Subscription period displays get the same treatment in the companion change below. Guarded by `TestFormatInclusivePeriod` (IST vs UTC, single-day, sub-day clamp, one-off omit).

### Fixed

- **Hosted invoice page now shows the tax-exemption legend (2026-06-14).** A `tax_status=exempt` customer's invoice rendered the "Tax-exempt — &lt;reason&gt;" disclosure on the PDF and the dashboard, but the **public hosted invoice page** showed a bare $0-tax invoice with no notice — the `tax_exempt_reason` field was dropped from the hosted-invoice safe projection (`viewInvoice` / `toViewInvoice`), so the SPA never received it (reverse-charge was projected and rendered, exempt was not). Added the field to the projection and an exemption notice on the page (gated `tax_exempt_reason && !tax_reverse_charge`, mirroring the dashboard). A legally-required exemption disclosure shouldn't be visible to the operator but invisible to the customer paying the invoice. Found during Test 2 (reverse-charge / exempt proration legend) verification. Guarded by `TestViewInvoice_CarriesTaxExemptReason` (projection carries the reason end-to-end). No schema change.

- **Proration tax now commits to a Stripe `tax_transaction` on test-clock (simulated) subscriptions (2026-06-14).** From manual proration testing (B7.5): an immediate mid-cycle upgrade on a `stripe_tax` customer pinned to a test clock produced a proration invoice with `tax_calculation_id` set but `tax_transaction_id` **blank** — the calculation was made at Stripe but never committed, so the proration tax was charged to the customer yet not reported to the authority (and a later void couldn't reverse it — the reversal guards on `tax_transaction_id`). Root cause: the `CommitTax` expiry guard (which blocks committing a calculation older than Stripe's 24h TTL) measured the calc's age with `clock.Now(ctx)` — the **ctx-bound simulated clock**. A customer on a test clock advanced more than 23h past real wall-clock (e.g. a proration after advancing the clock to mid-period, ~15 days) made `simulated_now − created_at` exceed the window, so the guard **falsely "expired" a calculation created seconds ago in real time** and skipped the commit. The calc row's `created_at` is the DB's real `now()`, and the TTL it gates is a Stripe-side **real-world** property (Stripe knows nothing about a Velox test clock), so the guard now measures **real elapsed time** on both sides. Production wall-clock subscriptions are unchanged (their ctx is already wall-clock-bound, so `clock.Now(ctx)` already equalled real time); only the simulated path was wrong. The legitimate guard still fires for a real draft genuinely held >24h. Note the wall-clock commit reconciler (`RetryPendingTaxCommit`) deliberately **excludes** clock-pinned invoices, so before this fix nothing recovered the orphan; with the inline commit now succeeding, the orphan isn't created in the first place (a transient inline-commit failure on a clock-pinned invoice remains a pre-existing, un-reconciled gap that is **test-mode-only** — clock-pinned invoices are `livemode=false` by construction, so no real tax reporting is at stake; documented at `ListPendingTaxCommit` and in ADR-029 §3 with a build trigger). Guarded by `TestCommitTax_ExpiryGuardIgnoresSimulatedClock` (fresh calc + far-future ctx clock → commits) and `TestCommitTax_ExpiryGuardTripsOnRealAge` (genuinely-stale calc → still rejected, so the fix didn't disable expiry). No schema change.

- **A card saved via the hosted "update payment" / operator add-card Checkout link now actually lands on the customer (2026-06-14).** A customer who completed the Stripe-hosted Checkout setup link had their card saved **at Stripe** (attached, set as the customer's default) but Velox never recorded a `payment_methods` row — so the dashboard kept showing "no payment method" and the finalized invoice's `auto_charge_pending` never cleared (it had no local card to charge, so nothing changed state). Root cause was a two-layer dependency on metadata that Stripe Checkout doesn't propagate: **Checkout never copies a session's metadata onto the SetupIntent it creates**, and the hosted update-payment (`public_handler.go`) and operator add-card (`checkout.go`) flows set `velox_*` metadata only on the session (the third, portal, flow set `setup_intent_data.metadata` and worked). So the `setup_intent.succeeded` event arrived with **empty** metadata, and two gates dropped it: (1) the inbound webhook HTTP handler skipped any event whose object lacked a `velox_tenant_id` marker — before processing even began; and (2) the handler that writes `payment_methods` keyed the customer off the SetupIntent's metadata. Rather than make every current and future session-creation site remember to copy metadata onto the SetupIntent, the fix recognizes a Velox-originated SetupIntent **from the object itself**: (1) `setup_intent.*` events are now admitted on the endpoint's already-authoritative tenant (per-tenant secret + HMAC) instead of requiring a `velox_tenant_id` marker — the cross-tenant *mismatch* guard is unchanged; and (2) the webhook resolves the customer from the SetupIntent's authoritative `customer` field via a new `customers.GetByStripeCustomerID` lookup whenever `velox_customer_id` metadata is absent. Metadata, when present (portal flow), still wins as a fast-path; a transient lookup error surfaces so Stripe redelivers rather than dropping the card; an unknown Stripe customer (not ours) skips as before; `payment_intent.*` still requires the metadata marker so a tenant's own unrelated charges at the same endpoint aren't ingested. This makes PM persistence authoritative-by-construction instead of best-effort-by-metadata, killing the whole class of "card saved at Stripe, invisible in Velox."
