Guarded by `TestWebhookHandler_SetupIntentEmptyMetadata_StillAttaches` (end-to-end through the real HTTP gate: empty metadata → resolved + attached), `TestHandleWebhook_SetupIntent_ResolvesCustomerByStripeID`, `…_MetadataWinsOverResolver` (resolver untouched when metadata present), `…_ResolverTransientErrorRedelivers` (DB blip → redeliver, no attach), and the real-Postgres `TestPostgresStore_GetByStripeCustomerID` (1:1 lookup + fail-closed on unknown/empty). No schema change.

- **A customer's billing-country is validated to ISO-3166 alpha-2 at save time (2026-06-14).** From the tax-flow audit. `UpsertBillingProfile` already format-validated phone, tax ID, and tax status, but accepted the billing `country` verbatim — so a direct API call saving `"USA"` (or garbage) got a silent 200, then detonated at invoice-compute time as an opaque Stripe-side `customer_tax_location_invalid` rejection (Stripe Tax and payments both require alpha-2 for every address). The country is now normalized (trim + upper, so `" us "` → `"US"`) and rejected with a clean 400 if it isn't a two-letter code — the same `^[A-Z]{2}$` check the tenant `company_country` already uses, and the same direct-API-bypass class as the exempt-reason / buyer-tax-id enforcement above (the dashboard sends a code from a fixed list). Guarded by `TestCustomerService_BillingProfile` (non-alpha-2 rejected, lowercase/padded normalized). No schema change.

- **Mid-period change outcomes now surface on the timeline and the invoice, for every change type (2026-06-14).** Cross-path audit of one class of bug: the proration/credit/adjustment a subscription change produces was computed and applied correctly, but never shown to the operator. Two root causes, both fixed end-to-end. **(1) Subscription activity timeline.** The three atomic proration wrappers (`atomicAddItemWithProration`, `atomicUpdateItemWithProration`, `atomicRemoveItemWithProration`) computed the outcome into a local `detail` and dropped it — so the `item_added` / `item_updated` / `item_removed` audit rows were structurally unable to carry it, and the feed showed "Plan changed" / "Item removed" with no amount. All three now return the detail; a shared `addProrationMeta` stamps `proration_type` + amount + currency into the audit row, and a shared `prorationPartLabel` renders it across all four change types — so the timeline reads "Plan changed · Pro → Starter · Immediate · Open invoice adjusted $54.44", "Item removed · Pro · Credit $54.44", etc. (currency-correct, no hardcoded `$`). **(2) Invoice page.** The "↳ Tax reversed $X (Stripe Tax)" disclosure and the credit-note reason lived only in the post-payment-adjustments block, which renders only for *paid* invoices — so an adjustment credit note against an *unpaid* invoice (the downgrade-on-unpaid path) showed a bare "Credit CN-0024 -$54.44" with no reason and no reversal disclosure, even though a real Stripe Tax reversal was filed. A shared `TaxReversedLine` component + `creditNoteReasonLabel` now render on **both** pre- and post-payment credit-note rows; the Credit Notes list also humanizes the machine reason codes and labels all-zero-channel adjustment CNs "applied to invoice" instead of "—". No billing-math change — purely surfacing what already happened. Guarded by `TestAddProrationMeta_StampsOutcome` + `TestDescribeSubscriptionAction_RendersProrationOutcome` (round-trip across all four change types + non-USD). The updateItem audit write was also moved to after proration resolves, so the cross-interval / cross-cadence (legacy orchestrator) path stamps the outcome too — not just the atomic path. Known remaining (deferred, need new API surface, not production-reachable): item-add/item-remove only stamp the outcome on the atomic path (their legacy path is the unwired-db test scaffold, never the wired production path); Credits-ledger provenance links + a CustomerDetail credit-note summary.

- **A tax transaction committed at Stripe but lost locally is now recovered, so a later void can't over-report tax (2026-06-14).** The tax-flow audit's deepest finding. When a `stripe_tax` invoice finalizes, `CommitTax` creates a Stripe `tax_transaction` (reporting the tax to the authority) and persists its id locally. If the Stripe commit **succeeded but the local `tax_transaction_id` write failed** (a DB blip, or a crash between the two), the invoice ended up finalized with a calculation id but **no transaction id** — and since the void / mark-uncollectible reversal guards on `tax_transaction_id != ''`, a later void would **silently skip the reversal**, leaving the tax authority reporting tax collected on an annulled invoice. Two changes close this: **(1)** `Commit` now sends a deterministic **Idempotency-Key** (keyed on the invoice), so a re-commit within Stripe's 24h window returns the **original** transaction — never a duplicate — instead of a "reference already used" error (Stripe's reference-uniqueness also prevents duplicates outright, and beyond 24h the calculation has expired so the engine's expiry guard blocks the re-commit, ruling out a late duplicate). **(2)** a background **commit reconciler** (`RetryPendingTaxCommit`, on the wall-clock scheduler tick alongside the existing tax-retry reconciler, ADR-017) scans finalized `stripe_tax` invoices with a calculation id but no transaction id and re-commits each — recovering the lost id. Self-healing: a re-commit whose persist fails again is simply retried next tick until it sticks; once persisted the invoice falls out of the scan. Clock-pinned invoices are excluded (the catchup path owns those). Guarded by `TestRetryPendingTaxCommit` (reconciler targets only orphans) and the real-Postgres `TestListPendingTaxCommit_FiltersToOrphans` (the SQL filter excludes committed + non-stripe invoices). No schema change.

- **Tax input integrity: exemptions now require their supporting data, an unknown tax provider fails loud, and `none`-mode renders exemption legends (2026-06-14).** Three hardening fixes from the tax-flow audit. **(1) Non-standard tax statuses are enforced server-side.** Setting a customer to `tax_status=exempt` now requires a `tax_exempt_reason`, and `reverse_charge` now requires a buyer `tax_id` — the dashboard already guarded both, but a direct API call could save an `exempt` invoice with a blank audit reason or a `reverse_charge` invoice with no buyer VAT number (a legally unsupportable $0 invoice). Now a 400 with a field error. **(2) An unrecognized `tax_provider` fails loud instead of silently emitting $0 tax.** The resolver's `default` case returned `NoneProvider` for any unknown string — so a corrupted/hand-edited settings value (the API already constrains writes to `none`/`manual`/`stripe_tax`) silently zero-taxed every invoice. It now errors, surfacing the misconfiguration as a stuck billing cycle rather than silent under-collection that nobody notices until an audit — consistent with ADR-041's no-silent-fallback rule. **(3) `tax_provider=none` now honors the customer's exemption status.** `NoneProvider` ignored `tax_status`, so a `none`-tenant's `reverse_charge` or `exempt` customer got a bare $0 invoice with no legend; it now routes through the same `exemptResult` helper as the manual/stripe providers, so the legally-required reverse-charge / exemption notice renders. Guarded by `TestCustomerService_BillingProfile` (exempt/reverse enforcement), `TestResolver_Routing` (unknown → error), and `TestNoneProvider_HonorsExemptionStatus`. Two stale resolver/engine comments claiming a "fall back to manual" that ADR-041 removed are corrected. No schema change.

- **A reverse-charge or tax-exempt customer's mid-cycle proration invoice now carries its exemption status (2026-06-14).** From the tax-flow audit. Every invoicing path stamps the customer's `tax_reverse_charge` flag and `tax_exempt_reason` onto the invoice — except the subscription **proration** path: `ProrationTaxResult` and its adapter carried every tax field (rate, provider, calculation id, status) *except* those two. So a B2B reverse-charge customer (EU VAT, Indian GST RCM) who upgraded or changed quantity mid-cycle got a proration invoice with `tax_reverse_charge=false` and a blank exempt reason — silently dropping the **legally required reverse-charge / exemption legend** on exactly that invoice, while the rest of the customer's invoices carried it. The engine already computes both fields (`TaxApplication.TaxReverseCharge` / `TaxExemptReason`); they're now plumbed through `ProrationTaxResult`, the adapter, and the proration invoice construction. Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_ProrationCarriesExemptionStatus` (reverse_charge flag + exempt reason both reach the created invoice). Backend-only; no schema change.

- **The no-payment-method invoice nudge now resends the setup link it claims to, instead of the hosted-invoice "pay" email (2026-06-14).** On a finalized invoice with no card on file, the attention card said *"the customer has been emailed a setup link … resend the link if they haven't acted"* and offered a **"Resend payment link"** button — but the button opened the generic "email this invoice" dialog and sent the **hosted-invoice** "view/pay your invoice" email, a *different* link from the one referenced. (For a no-card customer both eventually reach Stripe Checkout, so nothing broke; the copy and the action just disagreed.) The no_payment_method state is built around auto-charge-on-attach — the engine charges once a card is added — so the matching action is to re-send the **payment-method setup link** (`POST /v1/invoices/{id}/resend-setup-link` → `NotifyNoPaymentMethod` → Stripe Checkout in *setup* mode), which is now what the button does. It goes straight to the customer (no recipient modal) with a "Setup link resent" toast, and the button is relabeled **"Resend setup link"** to match the card's wording. Every other attention reason (awaiting_payment, payment_failed, overdue) keeps the existing behavior — the email dialog sending the hosted-invoice pay link, where the operator confirms the recipient. From the S7 manual-test walkthrough.

- **The self-service payment-update link now works for a customer setting up their first card, and a failed attempt no longer burns the link (2026-06-13).** When an invoice finalizes for a customer with no saved card, Velox emails a tokenized "set up payment method" link. Opening it dead-ended for the exact case it exists to serve: the public handler read `customers.stripe_customer_id` and returned **"customer does not have a Stripe payment setup"** when it was empty — but a customer setting up their *first* card has no Stripe Customer yet. Worse, the single-use token was **consumed before** that check, so the failed first click burned the link and the retry showed **"invalid or expired token"** (two confusing errors for one broken flow). The handler now **lazily creates the Stripe Customer on demand** via the same `EnsureStripeCustomer` helper the operator "Add payment method" and hosted-invoice Pay flows already use (it pre-populates email/name/address/tax status and persists the id), so the first-payment-method link opens Stripe Checkout instead of erroring. And the token `Consume` moved to **immediately before** the Checkout-session create, so a recoverable precondition failure (Stripe not yet connected for the mode, a transient error) no longer spends the link — the customer can retry the same email. The TOCTOU guarantee is unchanged (exactly one Checkout session per token). Frontend behavior verified against the live flow; MANUAL_TEST D4 updated.

- **Dunning "Manually resolved" option relabeled "Void invoice" so operators don't void a payment they collected (2026-06-13).** The resolve-dunning dialog's middle option was labeled **"Manually resolved"** with the description *"Issue resolved through other means (offline payment, negotiation, etc.)"* and benign (default) styling — but its actual effect is a **full void**: the invoice flips to `status='voided'`, any applied credits are reversed off the customer's balance, and the pending PaymentIntent is canceled. An operator who **collected a payment offline** (cash, wire, cheque) and picked this option — exactly what the "offline payment" copy invited — would **annul the invoice and erase that revenue from the books** instead of recording it. The void behavior is itself legitimate (annul an invoice billed in error or waived), so the fix is the copy, not the mechanism: the option is now **"Void invoice"** with destructive (red) styling and copy that describes the annulment and explicitly steers offline payments to **"Payment recovered"** (which marks the invoice paid). The resolution-history label for that path now reads **"Voided"** to match. Frontend-only; the backend resolution value (`manually_resolved`) and its void semantics are unchanged. From the MANUAL_TEST audit (the flow's own "behavior mismatch worth revisiting" note).

- **A concurrent duplicate `payment_intent.payment_failed` no longer double-sends the "payment failed" email or double-fires the `payment.failed` webhook (2026-06-13, migration 0118).** This is the failed-path twin of the success-path fix shipped the same week. Stripe delivers webhooks at-least-once, and Velox's inbound dedup is a non-atomic read pre-check (`WasProcessed` runs before the dedup row is claimed), so two deliveries of the *same* failed charge that race — or a reconciler recovery racing the original webhook — both slip past the already-settled guard and each ran `SettleFailed`'s notifications: the customer got **two "payment failed" emails** and integrators got **two `payment.failed` events**. (Dunning was already safe — `StartDunning` is `UNIQUE` per invoice; only the event + email leaked.) Unlike the success path, failure is **non-terminal** — an invoice legitimately re-fails once per dunning retry, each a distinct PaymentIntent that *should* notify again — so the dedup key is the PaymentIntent, not the status. And the synchronous charge path stamps `payment_status='failed'` (same PI) **without** notifying, deferring that to the webhook, so a status-keyed gate would wrongly suppress the webhook's notifications entirely. The fix adds an authoritative marker `invoices.failure_notified_pi` written **only** by the notification path: a new `MarkPaymentFailedReportingTransition` (`SELECT … FOR UPDATE`) reports whether this delivery is the first to notify for the failing PI, and `SettleFailed` fires the event + email only for that first delivery (the duplicate logs and returns). A new retry on a fresh PI still notifies; an out-of-order failure for an already-paid invoice still no-ops. Guarded by `TestSettleFailed_ConcurrentRedeliveryFiresSideEffectsOnce`, `TestSettleFailed_InlinePresetThenWebhookStillNotifiesOnce`, `TestSettleFailed_NewRetryPIFiresAgain`, and the real-Postgres `TestMarkPaymentFailedReportingTransition_FlagsTheRealNotification`. From the periodic-jobs / machinery audit (the SettleFailed concurrent path, previously deferred as lower-risk).

- **An engine-issued credit note no longer shows a simulated timestamp in the invoice's "Real-time activity" lane (2026-06-13, migration 0117).** The invoice timeline splits into two lanes: **Activity** (billing lifecycle events that run in *simulated* test-clock time) and **Real-time activity** (wall-clock emails + Stripe outcomes). Credit notes are the one event with **two** issuance time domains — an **engine clawback** on a clock-pinned subscription (downgrade/cancel proration) stamps `issued_at` in *simulated* time, while **operator HTTP issuance** always stamps wall-clock — but every credit-note row was routed to the wall-clock lane unconditionally, so a simulated clawback's `issued_at` (e.g. a far-future test-clock instant) appeared under "Real-time activity," which the UI labels as wall-clock. The fix plumbs the fact authoritatively rather than guessing: a new `credit_notes.is_simulated` column is stamped at write-time (`true` only when the engine clawback path issues against an already-simulated invoice — `input.IsSimulated && inv.IsSimulated`; the operator path leaves it `false`), the timeline event carries the per-credit-note flag, and the frontend lane rule routes a simulated credit note to **Activity** (with the simulated badge) and an operator credit note to **Real-time activity**. Guarded by `TestCreate_IsSimulated` (engine-on-simulated → true, operator-on-simulated → false, engine-on-non-simulated → false). No data backfill ships (pre-launch; any existing rows default `false`, the correct value for every operator-issued note and harmless for the rare pre-existing simulated clawback, which can be corrected directly in the local DB).

- **Deleting a test clock no longer strands the next subscription of its customers (2026-06-13).** A customer pinned to a test clock kept pointing at it after the clock was deleted, so a new subscription created for that customer **inherited the dead clock** (ADR-027 moves the pin to the customer and new subs inherit it) — and then never billed: the wall-clock scheduler skips clock-pinned subs, and the catchup/Advance path skips subs whose clock is deleted, so it sat forever with its initial period. Root cause: `customers.test_clock_id` carries `ON DELETE SET NULL`, but ADR-016 made clocks *soft*-deleted (`deleted_at`, never a row DELETE), so that FK cascade never fired — and ADR-027's cascade only handled subs, not the customer pin it introduced. Clock delete now **detaches its customers** (`test_clock_id → NULL`) in the same transaction as the existing sub-cancel-cascade — realizing the `SET NULL` the schema intended. Customers have no period fields to go stale (unlike subs, which is why subs are canceled, not detached), so detaching is safe: the customer returns to wall-clock and its next subscription is a clean, billable wall-clock sub. The clock-detail "attached customers" surface goes empty for a deleted clock (intended); "which customers ran on this clock" stays answerable via the canceled subs' retained pointers. ADR-016 + ADR-027 amended. Going-forward behavior only — no data-repair migration ships (pre-launch; any rows already broken are corrected directly in the local DB). Guarded by `TestPostgresStore_Delete_DetachesPinnedCustomers`.

- **Two Prometheus metrics that always read zero are now wired (2026-06-13).** `velox_billing_cycles_total` + `velox_invoices_generated_total` (via `RecordBillingCycle`) and `velox_usage_events_ingested_total` (via `RecordUsageIngested`) were defined and exported on `/metrics` but **never incremented** — anyone graphing them saw a flat zero, implying the billing scheduler never ran and no usage was ever ingested. The eight sibling counters (payment charges, dunning runs, credit ops, …) are wired, so these two were oversights. `RecordBillingCycle(generated)` now fires per mode-pass right after `RunCycle` (so `invoices_generated` accumulates the live+test totals), and `RecordUsageIngested(1)` fires on every successful store insert in the single `usage.Service` ingest funnel that all paths (live POST, batch, backfill, LiteLLM) pass through — idempotency replays error out of the insert and aren't counted, so it's true ingest throughput, not request volume. Fire-and-forget calls on already-tested hot paths (no dedicated increment test, matching the other wired counters). From the periodic-jobs / machinery audit.

- **A concurrent duplicate `payment_intent.succeeded` no longer double-sends the receipt email or double-fires `payment.succeeded` (2026-06-13).** Stripe delivers webhooks at-least-once. Two deliveries of the *same* succeeded charge that race — both read the invoice while it's still `processing`, so both slip past the fast-path already-paid guard — each ran `SettleSucceeded`'s post-paid side-effects: the customer got **two receipt emails** and integrators got **two `payment.succeeded` webhooks**. (The serial redelivery case was already guarded; only the truly-concurrent window leaked. `invoice.paid` was never affected — it's enqueued inside `MarkPaid`'s transaction, so it was already once-only.) `MarkPaid` already serializes concurrent callers via `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` and one of them is the real finalized→paid transition; it now **reports that transition** (new `MarkPaidReportingTransition`, with the old `MarkPaid` a thin wrapper so its ~20 other call sites are untouched), and `SettleSucceeded` fires the email + event only for the transition-winner. The loser logs and returns. Guarded by `TestSettleSucceeded_ConcurrentRedeliveryFiresSideEffectsOnce` (two racing settles → exactly one email + one event; red pre-fix at two each) and `TestMarkPaidReportingTransition_FlagsTheRealTransition` (the store-level flag against real Postgres). From the periodic-jobs / machinery audit (H7).

- **Outbound webhook retries now run the full backoff ladder, including the final 24h step (2026-06-13).** The delivery retry schedule defined five backoff slots — 1m, 5m, 30m, 2h, **24h** — but the permanent-fail guard was `attempt_count >= maxAttempts(5)`, which gave up on the 5th attempt *before* the 24h slot could ever be scheduled. So a failing endpoint exhausted retries after ~2.5h instead of the ~26.5h the ladder implies, and the 24h backoff was dead config (present in the array, never reached). The guard now fails only once every backoff slot is spent (`attempt_count > maxRetries`), so all five slots — through the 24h tail — are used: a transient endpoint outage up to a day now recovers instead of permanently dropping the event after a couple of hours. The misleading `maxAttempts` name (it counted total attempts, but the comment and array treated each slot as a per-retry delay) is now `maxRetries`. Guarded by `TestRetryLadder_AllBackoffsReachable`, which walks every slot and asserts the permanent fail lands one attempt after the 24h retry (red under the old `>=` guard). From the periodic-jobs / machinery audit.

- **Webhook replay writes its delivery rows on the correct livemode partition (2026-06-13).** Replaying a **test-mode** webhook event fanned the redelivery out via `go s.deliver(context.Background(), …)` — a bare context with no livemode pinned. Because `postgres.Livemode(ctx)` defaults to **true**, the replay's `CreateDelivery` / `UpdateDelivery` writes ran under the **live** RLS partition: the delivery row was invisible in the test-mode dashboard and its foreign key pointed at a test-mode event across the mode boundary. The normal `Dispatch` path already pinned `postgres.WithLivemode(context.Background(), event.Livemode)` before its delivery goroutine, and `RetryPendingDeliveries` pinned `d.Livemode` — only the `Replay` goroutine was missing it. Now it pins the clone's livemode the same way (and the sync path re-pins too, so a caller ctx in the wrong mode can't leak through). Live-mode replays were unaffected (default already matched). Guarded by `TestReplay_PinsLivemodeOnDelivery`, which exercises the real async goroutine path under `-race` and asserts a test-mode replay's delivery is written with `livemode=false`. From the periodic-jobs / machinery audit (H5).

- **Test-clock "+1mo" quick jump advances a calendar month, not 31 days (2026-06-13).** The Advance dialog's `+1mo` preset added a fixed `31 × 24h`, so a clock frozen Jun 15 prefilled **Jul 16** — one day *past* the Jul 15 monthly cycle boundary the preset exists to hit (and +31d from Feb 15 landed Mar 18, three days past). It now adds one calendar month (same day-of-month); month-end overflow (Jan 31 → Mar 3) deliberately matches the engine's own Go `AddDate` month arithmetic, which doesn't clamp either. SPA-only; verified via `tsc`. Tier B nit from the test-clock design audit.

- **A panic during test-clock catchup no longer strands the clock at "advancing" (2026-06-13).** `RunCatchup` flipped the clock to `internal_failure` on *errors*, but a **panic** in any billing phase bypassed that path: the worker's recover (added earlier to keep the process alive) only logged, leaving the clock at `status='advancing'` — a state with **no operator exit** (Advance requires `ready`, Retry advance requires `internal_failure`), wedged until someone hand-edits the row. `RunCatchup` now recovers panics itself and takes the same internal_failure flip as the error path — on a detached ctx (the panic may stem from ctx expiry), with a generic operator-safe reason (panic strings carry Go internals the dashboard banner must not leak, ADR-026) and the full stack in slog for support. Covers the queued-worker path and the inline path both. Guarded by `TestRunCatchup_PanicMarksClockFailed` (status flip + reason populated + no panic-string leak). Tier A item from the test-clock design audit.

- **Usage ingestion works in simulated time on test clocks (2026-06-13).** The flagship test-clock demo — advance a month, ingest usage, see it billed — broke at ingest: every path (live POST, batch, backfill, LiteLLM — all funnel through one service) gated event timestamps against **wall-clock** `time.Now()`, so on a clock advanced into the future every simulated-time event was rejected as *"must not be in the future"*, and events posted without a timestamp landed at wall-clock — *before* the simulated current period, where the next Advance never bills them. Ingest now resolves the **customer's effective now** (the pinned clock's `frozen_time`; wall-clock when unpinned): no-timestamp events land at frozen_time, the future-skew gate and Backfill's past-only gate compare against simulated now, and events past `frozen_time + 5min` are rejected (Stripe Test Clocks shape — meter events live on the customer's simulated timeline). The operator usage-summary endpoint's default window ("current month") follows the same effective now, so it reports the frozen month after an Advance. **The production hot path pays nothing:** test clocks are test-mode-only (DB CHECK), so live-mode ingest skips the per-event clock lookup entirely — guarded by `TestIngest_LivemodeSkipsResolver`. Also guarded by `TestIngest_TestClockPinnedCustomer` (frozen-time default / sim-timestamp accepted / past-frozen rejected / unpinned unchanged), `TestBackfill_TestClockPinnedCustomer`, and `TestIngest_CtxBoundEffectiveNowWins`. Tier A item 1 from the test-clock design audit.

- **Billing thresholds with `reset_billing_cycle=false` no longer double-bill at cycle close (2026-06-13).** When a threshold fired mid-cycle without resetting the cycle, the period-end invoice re-billed everything the threshold invoice had already collected: usage was aggregated from the original `period_start` (re-billing everything before the fire), and the **full in_arrears base fee** was emitted again (the threshold invoice bills it unprorated). A $1,000-cap customer who crossed on day 10 paid the cap, then paid the first 10 days of usage *plus the entire base fee* a second time at month end. The cycle close now reads the cycle's threshold invoice as a **"billed through" watermark** (`MAX(billing_period_end)` of non-voided threshold invoices in the period): usage intervals clamp to start at the watermark, and in_arrears base lines are skipped entirely. Keyed on the *invoice* — ground truth — rather than the mutable threshold config, which also covers two recovery shapes: an operator removing thresholds after a mid-cycle fire, and a `reset_billing_cycle=true` fire whose cycle advance failed (that cycle would previously also double-bill on the next tick). A **voided** threshold invoice doesn't count — the money went back, so the full period is billable again. Wall-clock cron and test-clock catchup both covered (shared `billOnePeriod`). Known accepted imprecision (documented in code): an item *added* after the fire in the same cycle is under-billed by its partial-period base — the safer failure vs. the over-billing alternatives. Guarded by `TestCycleClose_AfterThresholdFire_BillsOnlyResidual`, `…_ThresholdsRemovedAfterFire_StillBillsResidual`, `…_VoidedThresholdInvoice_BillsFullPeriod`, `…_NoThresholdInvoice_FullPeriodUnchanged`. Closes the second critical from the periodic-jobs audit (with #240).
- **Activity timelines tell the whole story, and the finalized webhook fires from every path (2026-06-13, migration 0116).** From the timeline/notifications audit (16 confirmed findings, 7 refuted; the two-lane simulated-vs-wall-clock design itself verified sound). **The contract bug (bigger than first found):** `invoice.finalized` fired only from the operator HTTP handler — the tax-retry auto-finalize skipped it, and the pre-push adversarial review then proved the **entire engine path** (cycle / create / cancel-final / threshold invoices, i.e. normal billing) had **never emitted it at all** (engine invoices are born finalized and never pass `Finalize`). It now emits from `service.Finalize` AND the engine's shared born-finalized helper — exactly once per invoice (drafts that finalize later via tax retry emit from the service path only). The same review surfaced the identical asymmetry on `invoice.voided` (engine-triggered voids via the unpaid-prebill relief skipped it) — also moved to the service layer, single-writer. **Invoice timeline:** credit notes/refunds now appear as dated chronology rows ("Refund issued — $X", issued notes only); marking uncollectible records `uncollectible_at` (migration 0116) and renders a "Marked uncollectible — written off as bad debt" row (previously the operator-driven write-off left no chronology at all); operator-recorded offline payments read "Payment recorded (offline)" instead of masquerading as card payments; decline reasons now show on canceled payment attempts too; and a written-off invoice's page stops polling forever (`uncollectible` joined the terminal states). **Subscription feed:** scheduled-plan-change applications and spending-threshold crossings now write audit rows (both previously fired webhooks with no timeline trace — the feed showed the intent but never the outcome); item changes show the proration outcome ("Plan changed · Basic → Pro · Proration invoice $50.00") with the invoice id in metadata; item removals name the plan that left; cancel-credit amounts render the tenant currency instead of a hardcoded `$`; the feed requests the store's real 100-row cap instead of a silently-clamped 200. **Elsewhere:** the period-progress bar now shows "Cancels <date>" on scheduled cancels and "Collection resumes" when paused (instead of a false "Next Billing"); webhook delivery rows say "Delivery #N" (the number is a global sequence, not per-endpoint attempts); credits-ledger dates carry a full-timestamp tooltip. Credit-note rows carry source `credit_note` and route to the real-time lane on simulated invoices (operator-issued CNs stamp wall-clock time — sorting them among simulated billing rows would mis-order the story). Deferred with reasons: a canonical paid-transition audit row (NO settlement path writes one today — the review bounded this as a system-wide convention to fix once at the settlement layer, not per-site), unifying Dashboard alert counts with the attention classifier (disagreement bounded to period-window edges; needs a count endpoint), and audit rows for Stripe-webhook payment outcomes (the audit subsystem is under active rework in a parallel session).

- **`last_ever` pricing rules no longer double-bill events claimed by period rules (2026-06-13).** The multi-dim aggregation runs two passes: period-bounded modes (sum/count/max/last_during_period) and `last_ever`. The period pass correctly lets ALL rules compete for each event (top-priority match claims it, exactly once) — but the `last_ever` pass ranked **only last_ever rules** when claiming, so an event already claimed by a higher-priority sum/max/count rule was claimed *again* by a lower-priority `last_ever` rule and **billed twice** (reproduced live: two events produced sum=52 AND last_ever=42 on the same invoice). The `last_ever` claim now mirrors the period pass exactly — LATERAL top-1 across all rules, keep only events whose *winner* is last_ever — making the in-code "claim semantics are identical" contract actually true. Guarded by `TestAggregateByPricingRules_LastEverDoesNotDoubleClaim` (both priority orders) plus the existing aggregation contract suite. From the ingestion-machinery audit (high, adversarially verified + reproduced).

- **Credits are applied before every card charge — threshold scan, retry sweep, and dunning retries (2026-06-13).** Three siblings of the cycle path's credit handling never received its 2026-05-30 fix, and together they formed an overcharge loop. **(1) Threshold scan:** a failed credit application logged a warning and **charged the card the full pre-credit total anyway** — no `creditApplyOK` gate (the exact bug `billOnePeriod` fixed). It now flags the invoice for the retry sweep and skips the inline charge and the fully-credited MarkPaid, mirroring the cycle path. **(2) Auto-charge retry sweep:** `processAutoCharge` charged the raw `amount_due` without re-applying credits — so the very invoices the cycle path *deferred to protect from overcharge* were overcharged when the retry fired. The sweep (wall-clock and test-clock catchup both — shared code) now applies credits first (idempotent: `ApplyToInvoiceAtomic` drains `min(due, balance)`), settles fully-covered invoices from the balance without touching the card, and skips the tick on a failed application rather than charge pre-credit. **(3) Dunning retries:** the retry adapter also charged raw `amount_due`; it now applies credits first — a fully-covered invoice resolves the dunning run with **no card charge**, and a failed application maps to the transient-skip path so it doesn't burn a dunning attempt. Guarded by `TestRetrySweep_*` (reduced charge / credit-settled / skip-on-failure / nil-wired legacy) and `TestThresholdScan_Credit*` (gate + remainder-charge). From the periodic-jobs audit (2 critical + 1 high, adversarially verified).

- **Customer list name/email sort now orders by plaintext, not ciphertext (2026-06-13).** `display_name` and `email` are encrypted at rest, so the list page's SQL `ORDER BY` on those columns ordered the *ciphertext* — effectively random to an operator clicking the Name or Email header. With encryption active, those sorts now take a bounded decrypt-then-sort path (the `listSearch` pattern: scan the most recent rows up to the cap, decrypt, sort by plaintext, paginate in memory — exact under the cap, window-truncated above it, same documented upgrade path of a derived sort-token column). Self-hosts running without an encryption key keep the plain SQL sort. The search path already sorted by plaintext; the no-search list path was the gap. Guarded by `TestPostgresStore_ListSortByEncryptedColumn` (asserts alphabetical order on genuinely encrypted-at-rest data, both directions + in-memory pagination; verified red on the unfixed store — "Zebra Systems" sorted first).

- **Customer PII no longer enters the append-only audit log (2026-06-12).** Audit rows copied customer email addresses (customer-update `email`, setup-link `to` on both the operator and engine-fired paths, invoice-send `to`) and the buyer `tax_id` (billing-profile upsert) into `metadata` — but `audit_log` is append-only at the DB level (UPDATE/DELETE/TRUNCATE all trigger-blocked), so PII written there could **never be erased**, a dead end for a GDPR deletion request, and it bypassed the AES-GCM at-rest encryption those same fields get on the `customers` table. The rows now record the *fact*, not the value: `email_changed: true`, `tax_id_set: true`, and send rows carry the customer/invoice ids — the addresses live only on the mutable, erasable customer/profile rows the audit row links to, and the **email outbox** remains the delivery record for "what address did we actually send to." Deliberately kept: display names as `resource_label` (the log is unusable without them) and **operator** emails on auth rows (the actor's own identity is the audit log's purpose). Also fixes a #234 regression this work's new test caught: the audit read-query's `users` join referenced `u.display_name`, which the post-ADR-011 `users` table (migration 0069) doesn't have — operator actor names now resolve from `u.email`. Guarded by `TestAudit_NoCustomerPIIInMetadata` — an integration test through the real handler → Logger → Postgres path asserting no `@`-bearing or tax-id values land in metadata and the change-flags do.

- **Settings changes are audited field-by-field (2026-06-12).** `PUT /v1/settings` produced only the generic middleware catch-all row — `action="update"`, `resource_type="setting"`, `metadata={"path":"/v1/settings"}` — with no record of **which** fields changed or their before/after values, even though settings carry the compliance-sensitive knobs (`audit_fail_closed`, `default_currency`, `timezone`, Net terms, tax config, company identity). Notably, **disabling the fail-closed audit policy itself left no field-level trace**. The settings handler now snapshots the pre-change settings, and on save writes one audit row with `metadata.changed = {field: {from, to}}` for every changed field — keyed by the wire (JSON) field names via a generic struct diff, so **new settings fields are covered automatically** without touching the audit code. No-op saves write nothing (the catch-all still records the request). The pre-change read failing skips the diff rather than blocking the save. No secrets live in `tenant_settings` (Stripe credentials are a separate, encrypted table), so before/after values are safe to record. Wired via a narrow `SettingsAuditRecorder` interface. Guarded by `TestDiffSettings` (JSON-name keys, from/to, cleared-omitempty → nil, identity/timestamps excluded, no-op → empty). Closes H3 from the audit-subsystem audit.

- **Engine-generated invoices and trial auto-expiry now leave an audit trail — and TTFI counts every first invoice (2026-06-12).** The billing engine creates most invoices **born finalized** (cycle close, subscription create, cancel-final, threshold) — and none of those wrote a `finalize` audit row; only the manual HTTP endpoint did. Locally, **603 of 614** finalized invoices had no audit trace, and the **time-to-first-invoice metric** (which reads `MIN(created_at)` of finalize rows) reported **nothing** for any tenant whose first invoice was engine-generated — the normal path. Fixed at two levels: **(1)** `invoice.Service.Finalize` now writes the canonical finalize row (covers the operator endpoint AND the tax-retry auto-finalize chain; the handler's own write was removed — and with it the **duplicate-row bug** where one operator mark-uncollectible / record-offline-payment produced TWO identical audit rows, since handler and service both wrote one). **(2)** A new `engine.auditInvoiceFinalized` helper writes the row for born-finalized engine invoices at all four creation sites, with `triggered_by` = the invoice's billing reason and sim context (`test_clock_id` + `sim_effective_at`) on clock-pinned subs; drafts (tax-pending / pause-collection) are skipped — they get their row when the tax-retry chain finalizes them. **Also:** trial auto-expiry now writes the same `trial_ended` audit row the operator End-Trial path writes (`triggered_by=schedule`), on all three automatic paths (wall-clock scan, test-clock catchup, engine cycle-close flip) — previously only webhooks fired. Deliberately NOT audited: payment settlements and credit auto-expiry — payments are covered by `payment.succeeded`/`failed` webhook events + the invoice timeline, and credit expiry is itself an immutable ledger entry; duplicating them into `audit_log` would be a second mechanism for the same record. Guarded by `TestAuditInvoiceFinalized` (row/draft-skip/sim-context), the extended `TestProcessExpiredTrialsForClock`, and the updated invoice service tests (finalize + action rows, exactly one each). Closes the engine-coverage gap from the audit-subsystem audit.

- **Auth events are now audited — login, logout, mode change, password reset (2026-06-12).** The dashboard auth surface (`/v1/auth`) wrote **zero** audit rows: it mounts outside the audit middleware, and `internal/user` had no audit wiring at all — so operator sign-ins, sign-outs, and password resets left no trace (a SOC-2 CC6.1 gap; "log both successful and failed access attempts"). The auth handler now records, attributed to the operator (`actor_type='user'`, scoped to their tenant): **login** success, **logout**, **mode change** (test/live), **password-reset requested** (against the matched account; anonymous actor → `system`), and **password-reset completed** (the high-value account-takeover signal). **Failed logins and lockouts** are deliberately *not* in the per-tenant `audit_log` — there's no resolved tenant pre-auth, and recording email-existence there would be an enumeration oracle — so they go to the structured **security log** (`slog`, with email + IP + reason), the correct home for pre-auth events. Wired via a narrow `user.AuditRecorder` interface (keeps `internal/user` decoupled) + a new `Service.TenantForUser` to scope the reset-completed row. Guarded by `TestLogin_AuditsSuccessAsOperator`, `TestLogin_FailureNotInAuditLog`, and `TestConfirmPasswordReset_Audits` (each asserts the actor resolves to the operator, not `system`). Builds on the actor-identity fix (#225). Tier 1 of the audit-coverage work; engine/background event rows follow separately.
- **Credit notes: atomic creation, no synthesized numbers, and a PDF that adds up (2026-06-12).** Three integrity fixes to the credit-note subsystem from the invoice-coherence audit. **(1) Atomicity.** The CN header committed inside the per-invoice advisory-lock transaction, but each line item was then inserted in its own separate transaction — a crash or failure mid-loop left an **orphan credit note with a non-zero total and zero lines**, which `Issue()` would still act on (it reads the header total). Lines now travel into `CreateUnderInvoiceLock` and commit in the same transaction as the header — both or neither (the ADR-030 atomic-proration pattern). **(2) Numbers.** A failed credit-note-number allocation was silently swallowed and replaced with a synthesized `CN-YYYYMM-<unixnano%1e6>` — non-monotonic and collision-prone, exactly the no-silent-fallbacks failure mode; a duplicate document number corrupts downstream accounting. Allocation errors now abort the Create (the caller retries), and an unwired generator is a loud config error — same contract as invoice numbering. **(3) PDF honesty.** CN line amounts are deliberately **gross** (ADR-048 anchors the reversal on what the customer paid) while the header subtotal is net — but the PDF labeled the net row "Subtotal", so a $110 single-line CN showed a $100.00 "Subtotal" that visibly didn't match the line above it. The row now reads **"Total excluding tax"** and renders only when there is tax to exclude (on a zero-tax CN net == gross, and printing the same figure twice would read as a bug); lines sum to **Credit Total**, every figure on the document reconciles, and the stored schema/API are unchanged. Deliberately NOT changed: CN lines stay gross (gross-anchored reversal is the ADR-048 design), and fractional CN quantities (a `quantity_decimal` column) stay deferred — CN amounts are derived qty × unit so the document always reconciles; revisit when a design partner credits fractional usage. Guarded by `TestCreate_LinesCommitWithHeader` + `TestCreate_NumberAllocatorErrorAborts`.

- **Audit log: CSV export honors the tenant timezone, and the recorded IP can't be client-forged (2026-06-12).** Two forensics-correctness fixes from the audit-subsystem audit. **(1) Export date window.** The Audit Log page's on-screen list converts the picked dates to tenant-TZ start/end-of-day instants (`startOfDayInTZ`/`endOfDayInTZ`), but the CSV **export** passed the raw `YYYY-MM-DD` strings, which the backend anchors at UTC — so for any non-UTC tenant the exported compliance file covered a window shifted from the on-screen list by the UTC offset, silently dropping (or adding) rows near each day boundary. Export now wraps the dates identically to the list query. **(2) Forgeable IP.** `audit.ExtractClientIP` read `X-Forwarded-For` / `X-Real-IP` *unconditionally*, so any client could spoof `audit_log.ip_address` — even though the global `TrustedRealIP` middleware already resolves the real client IP under a proxy-trust policy (and the boot log claims forwarding headers are ignored when `TRUST_PROXY` is unset). It now reads the host of `r.RemoteAddr` (the `TrustedRealIP`-corrected value) and never re-trusts the raw headers, matching the IP policy the rate limiter and request logs already use. Guarded by `TestExtractClientIP` (forged XFF ignored) + the existing middleware audit tests; export TZ verified via tsc + the list/export parity. (The session-record IP in `internal/session` shares the same unconditional-header pattern — a separate, related follow-up.)

- **Audit log now records WHICH operator acted, and can't be wiped by `TRUNCATE` (2026-06-12, migration 0115).** Two integrity fixes to the audit subsystem an audit found load-bearing. **(1) Actor identity.** Since the dashboard moved to session cookies (ADR-011), `session.applyToCtx` stamps `WithUserID` but never `WithKeyID`, and both audit writers (`Logger.Log` and the catch-all middleware) resolved the actor *solely* from `auth.KeyID` — so **every dashboard operator action was logged as `actor_type='system'`/`actor_id='system'`**, indistinguishable from the background scheduler and from each other. The log could not answer the one question it exists for: who did this. Both writers now share an `audit.ResolveActor(ctx)` helper resolving `customer → user → api_key → system` in priority order, so session operators record `actor_type='user'` with their user id (the `'user'` value the schema's CHECK constraint reserved but no code ever wrote). **(2) TRUNCATE hole.** The append-only guarantee (migration 0011) is a `BEFORE UPDATE OR DELETE FOR EACH ROW` trigger, but Postgres never fires row triggers on TRUNCATE, and the runtime `velox_app` role holds TRUNCATE (original `GRANT ALL`, never revoked) — so `TRUNCATE audit_log` erased the entire tamper-evidence log in one trigger-silent, RLS-bypassing statement. Migration 0115 adds a `BEFORE TRUNCATE FOR EACH STATEMENT` trigger reusing the existing `audit_log_immutable()` function, blocking it for every role (verified live: `TRUNCATE` now raises "append-only; TRUNCATE is not permitted"). The test harness's table-reset disables triggers transaction-locally (`session_replication_role=replica`) so it can still wipe between tests. Guarded by `TestResolveActor` (priority table) + the extended `TestAuditLog_AppendOnly` (TRUNCATE case). First of a tiered audit-subsystem hardening; coverage/UX gaps tracked separately.
- **Usage caps are now enforced on the immediate-cancel invoice (2026-06-12).** `BillFinalOnImmediateCancel` billed **raw** usage while cycle close scales quantities down to the subscription's `usage_cap_units` (OverageAction `block`) — so a capped customer who immediate-canceled mid-period was billed for above-cap usage the cycle writer would have capped (overbilling, surfaced by the adversarial review of the cancel-path fix below). The cancel path now computes the same proportional cap scale over the partial window (the window IS the final cycle's entire billable extent, so the per-cycle cap applies whole) and applies it in both the single-rule and multi-dim branches. Guarded by `TestBillFinalOnImmediateCancel_UsageCapApplied` (cap 750k against 1.5M raw → exactly half the uncapped charge; verified red on the unfixed engine).

- **AI token usage is now billed on immediate cancel (2026-06-12).** `BillFinalOnImmediateCancel` — the final partial-period invoice a mid-period cancel emits — had no multi-dim pricing-rules branch: a meter priced via dimension-match rules (the ADR-044 `tokens` shape, one rule per `{model, token_type}`, no meter-linked default rule) hit the single-rule guard's `RatingRuleVersionID == "" → skip` and was **silently dropped**, so a customer could consume a period of token usage and cancel for free (with no base fee, no invoice was emitted at all). The cycle path, preview, and the threshold scan all carry the `AggregateByPricingRules` fork — the comment on the cycle fork literally calls its absence "the wedge breakage" — and the cancel path now takes the same fork: one usage line per claimed rule, priced per-bucket with override support, `quantity_decimal` stamped, `… - canceled mid-period` description. The single-rule path is byte-identical to before. Guarded by `TestBillFinalOnImmediateCancel_MultiDimMeterBilled` ($3.00 input + $7.50 output = $10.50 invoice that pre-fix never existed; verified red on the unfixed engine) + `TestBillFinalOnImmediateCancel_SingleRuleMeterStillBilled`.

- **Threshold invoices no longer drift from the canonical invoice writer (2026-06-12).** Field-by-field audit of the threshold (hard-cap early-finalize) writer against the cycle writer found four omissions, all fixed: (1) **`is_simulated` was never stamped** — a threshold invoice fired on a test-clock-pinned sub (via the clock catchup's threshold scan) rendered without the Simulated badge while sibling cycle/proration invoices on the same clock showed it (the dashboard reads the flag authoritatively, no timestamp inference); guarded by `TestThresholdFire_ClockPinned_StampsIsSimulated`, verified red pre-fix. (2) **`tax_error_code` was dropped** — a typed tax failure (e.g. `customer_data_invalid`) on a threshold invoice persisted without the code, so the dashboard banner couldn't say "fix the customer's address" and webhook consumers couldn't branch on cause. (3) **usage lines lost `quantity_decimal`** — fractional usage quantities were truncated to integers with no exact-quantity field, the qty × unit ≠ amount incoherence class. (4) The finalization status was a hand-rolled tax-only check instead of the shared `domain.InvoiceFinalizationStatus` gate — the pause-collection arm was missing (currently unreachable: paused subs are skipped upstream, but the gate was wrong-by-construction for any future relaxation of that skip).

- **Day-1 and cancel invoices no longer fall back to Net-0 terms (2026-06-12).** `BillOnCreate` and `BillFinalOnImmediateCancel` used `netDays := 0` as the settings-unreadable fallback while the cycle writer, threshold writer, and the proration handler all use 30 — so on a settings read failure the subscription-create / cancel invoice stamped `due_at == issued_at` (immediately overdue, dunning fires on day 0) while sibling invoices stayed Net-30. Both now fall back to 30. Narrow blast radius: the trigger is a legacy settings row with non-positive terms (validation now clamps new writes, and a hard settings outage fails the invoice earlier, in tax-apply) — fixed for writer consistency.

- **Hosted invoice page now shows exact fractional usage quantities (2026-06-12).** The public hosted-invoice JSON dropped `quantity_decimal`, so a fractional-usage line (1.5 GPU-hours at $6.67/hr = $10.00) rendered as **Qty 1 × Unit $6.67 against Amount $10.00** — arithmetic that visibly doesn't close, on the page the customer pays from. The invoice PDF already formats via `QuantityDecimal`; the hosted payload now carries it (`quantity_decimal`, decimal string, omitted for whole quantities) and the page renders it with the dashboard's exact fallback logic. Guarded by `TestViewInvoice_FractionalQuantity_CarriesQuantityDecimal`.

- **Proration invoices now honor the tenant's Net payment terms and carry a billing reason (2026-06-12, migration 0114).** The mid-period change invoice (plan upgrade / quantity increase / item add, cut by the subscription handler) hardcoded **Net 30** while every engine invoice (cycle / create / cancel / threshold) reads the tenant's configured terms — so a Net-15 tenant saw two invoices on the same subscription with different TERMS, and the proration invoice's `due_at` (and therefore dunning/overdue timing for send-invoice customers) was wrong. It also persisted a NULL `billing_reason`, the only invoice writer that stamped none, so the dashboard couldn't label what triggered it. Now: the handler resolves Net terms through the engine (`NetTermsReader`, same resolution as cycle/create; Net-30 fallback only when unwired in narrow tests), derives `due_at` from them, and stamps `billing_reason = subscription_update` — Stripe's exact reason for the same invoice class. CHECK constraint expanded in migration 0114 (0091 drop-and-recreate precedent); OpenAPI `InvoiceBillingReason` enum updated + Go/TS clients regenerated. Existing rows keep their stored values (no backfill — pre-launch). Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_ProrationInvoiceStampsTenantNetTerms` (+ fallback test).

- **Forgot-password no longer promises an email that can't be sent on an unconfigured server (2026-06-12).** On a self-hosted deployment with SMTP unset (or `DASHBOARD_BASE_URL` unset), the request-reset flow showed "if an account exists … we've sent a link" and then nothing arrived — there is **no** stdout/log fallback for the reset link (ADR-011 removed it), so the operator had no path to complete a reset, and a stale frontend comment wrongly claimed the link was logged. The 200 response now carries a server-global `email_delivery: 'ok' | 'not_configured'` flag — computed from deployment config (SMTP wired AND `DASHBOARD_BASE_URL` set), **independent of whether the email matched a user**, so it leaks no account existence (anti-enumeration preserved). When `not_configured`, the page shows a callout: "Email delivery isn't configured on this server — no reset link can be sent; configure SMTP and `DASHBOARD_BASE_URL`, see `docs/ops/email-setup.md`." `user.NewHandler` takes the SMTP-configured bool from `email.Sender.IsConfigured()` at boot. `go build`/`vet`/user tests + `tsc -b && vite build` green.

- **OpenAPI spec no longer documents dead endpoints or rejects-on-arrival enum values (2026-06-12).** The published spec (`api/openapi.yaml`, served at `/docs/api` and the source of the generated Go + TS clients) documented four routes that return 404 — `POST /v1/subscriptions/{id}/change-plan` (plan changes go through `PATCH /v1/subscriptions/{id}/items/{itemID}`), the singleton `GET`/`PUT /v1/dunning/policy` (replaced by the `/v1/dunning/policies` CRUD collection, ADR-036), `POST /v1/webhooks/stripe` (the real route requires `/{endpoint_id}`), and `GET /v1/metrics` (Prometheus is at `/metrics`, no `/v1`) — so a client generated from the spec got 404s on documented calls. It also shipped three stale enums that drift from the DB CHECK constraints: `InvoiceBillingReason` was missing `subscription_cancel` (migration 0091), `AttentionReason` was missing `no_payment_method`, and `AttentionAction` was missing `add_payment_method` / `update_payment_method` / `connect_tax_provider`. Removed the dead paths and corrected the enums; regenerated the Go (`internal/api/generated`) and TS (`web-v2/src/lib`) clients. (The stale `final_action` enum was inside the deleted dunning singleton, so it's gone too — the correct values live on the `/policies` collection, which is part of the separate spec-backfill effort.) This is the first of three: a route↔spec CI parity guard and backfilling the ~116 undocumented routes are tracked follow-ups. No behavior change — spec/doc only.

- **Mid-cycle upgrade / add-item / quantity-increase invoices now actually collect (2026-06-11).** A plan upgrade (or add-item, or quantity increase) creates a **proration charge invoice** — but it was finalized and then **never charged**. Unlike engine cycle/create invoices (which enroll for auto-charge at finalize), the proration invoice is created in the subscription HTTP handler (`handleItemProration`), which had **no collection step**: the invoice came out `finalized` + `pending` + `auto_charge_pending=false`, so neither the wall-clock sweep (`RetryPendingCharges`) nor the test-clock catchup (`RetryPendingChargesForClock`) — both of which require `auto_charge_pending=true` — ever picked it up. The upgrade delta just sat unpaid until someone clicked **Collect Payment**. (Surfaced when an operator advanced a test clock expecting the upgrade charge to settle and nothing happened.) Now the handler **enrolls** the freshly-created charge invoice into the existing auto-charge sweep, so it collects on the timeline-correct worker — wall-clock cron for live subs, test-clock catchup on advance for clock-pinned subs — exactly like a cycle invoice. Enrollment (not an inline charge in the request) is deliberate: it reuses the one collection mechanism and respects the disjoint-flows invariant (ADR-028/029) — charging inline from a wall-clock HTTP request would duplicate the charge path and wall-clock-charge a *simulated* invoice. The sweep's `status='finalized' AND payment_status='pending'` filter means enrolling a still-draft (tax-pending or pause-collection) invoice is safe — it stays parked until it finalizes. Downgrade/credit paths are untouched. Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_Upgrade_EnrollsProrationInvoiceForAutoCharge` + `TestUpdateItem_Downgrade_DoesNotEnrollForAutoCharge`. No schema change. *(Known follow-up: the no-payment-method email that cycle invoices fire at finalize isn't yet fired for proration invoices — the upgrade is operator-initiated so the operator sees the unpaid invoice; deferred.)*

- **"Payment scheduled" banner tells the truth on a simulated invoice — advance the clock, not "next tick" (2026-06-11).** A finalized, unpaid invoice with `auto_charge_pending=true` shows a `payment_scheduled` attention banner reading "the engine will attempt the charge on its next tick." For a **test-clock-pinned** invoice that's a lie: the wall-clock scheduler sweep deliberately **excludes** clock-pinned invoices (ADR-028/029 disjoint flows — `ListAutoChargePending` filters out subs with a `test_clock_id`), so the retry only fires when the operator **advances the test clock**. In real time the invoice sits indefinitely — so an operator who adds a payment method and waits sees nothing happen and reasonably thinks it's broken. The banner now branches on `is_simulated`: simulated invoices read **"Auto-charge runs on the next test-clock advance — advance the clock to trigger it, or use Charge now to collect immediately."** Wall-clock invoices are unchanged. Backend-only (the attention `message` is already rendered verbatim by the frontend); guarded by an extended `TestClassifyInvoiceAttention_PaymentScheduled` (asserts the wall-clock vs simulated copy and that the simulated message never promises a tick). No schema change.

- **Public payment-update flow no longer dead-ends on a blank page after Stripe (2026-06-11).** A customer who clicked the "set up your payment method" email link, completed Stripe Checkout, and returned landed on a **blank page**: the return URL came from `PAYMENT_UPDATE_RETURN_URL`, shipped in `.env.example` as `http://localhost:5173/update-payment/done` — a route the SPA does not serve (it has `/update-payment` and `/payment-method-added`, with no catch-all), so React Router rendered nothing. Root cause was an incomplete migration: the operator-driven "Add payment method" flow was already fixed to return to the public `/payment-method-added` page (and split success/cancel via `?status=`), but the **public** email-link flow (`payment.PublicPaymentHandler`) was never updated — it pointed Stripe's `success_url`/`cancel_url` at one un-split URL, and its empty-env fallback was `/customers/{id}?payment=updated`, an operator **ProtectedRoute** that would bounce a session-less customer to login. Fixed by pointing `PAYMENT_UPDATE_RETURN_URL` at `/payment-method-added` (`.env.example`), changing the handler's fallback to the same public route, and appending `?status=success|cancel` so the page's existing cancel-copy branch actually renders (mirrors the paymentmethods setup-session flow). Documented the previously-undocumented env var in `velox --help`. Guarded by `TestAppendStatusQuery`. **Local action after pulling:** set `PAYMENT_UPDATE_RETURN_URL` to the new value in your `.env` and restart the backend.

- **Mid-cycle plan-change proration invoices now carry the simulated flag on a test clock (2026-06-09).** A dashboard plan change (upgrade / downgrade / quantity / item-add) on a clock-pinned subscription generates a proration invoice via `handleItemProration` — which, unlike every engine invoice path (cycle bill, `BillOnCreate`, threshold, all of which stamp `IsSimulated: sub.TestClockID != ""`), never set the flag. So the invoice persisted `is_simulated=false` even though its `created_at`/`issued_at` are on simulated (test-clock) time, and the dashboard showed **no "Simulated" marker** on it while the sibling cycle invoice on the same sub showed one. The proration invoice now stamps `is_simulated` from the sub's test clock at write time, matching the engine paths and the authoritative-flag contract the frontend reads (the badge deliberately never infers simulation from a future date — see the no-heuristic-proxy rule). Affects every clock-pinned mid-cycle proration invoice. Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_PlanChange_StampsIsSimulatedFromTestClock` (clock-pinned → true, wall-clock → false). No schema change.

- **Subscription billing dates are now computed in the tenant timezone, not the host timezone (2026-06-09, ADR-058).** Period boundaries and the proration denominator used `time.AddDate` (advance one month/year), which is timezone-sensitive, on a `time.Time` whose `Location` was the host process zone (pgx scans `timestamptz` as `time.Local`) — *not* the tenant's billing timezone. For any tenant in a non-UTC zone this produced boundaries one calendar day off whenever the UTC instant mapped to a different calendar date locally (month-end + offset): a sub started **June 1** (IST) got a **31-day** first period (`Jun 1 → Jul 2`) instead of the correct 30-day June anniversary (`Jun 1 → Jul 1`), and a mid-cycle upgrade then over-charged ~3.3% by dividing a 31-day-period numerator against a 30-day denominator. An audit found the defect was **systematic** across the billing surface — period creation, post-trial first period, cross-interval swap, cycle-close re-anchor, and every mid-cycle upgrade/downgrade/cancel/swap proration — plus a Feb-skip in the calendar branch (a Jan-31 calendar anchor rolled to `Mar 1`, losing February) and a leap-boundary off-by-one for yearly anniversaries. Fixed with one shared tenant-TZ-anchored advance helper (`domain.addIntervalIn`) that all month/year advances route through (so the result depends only on the tenant zone, never the value's provenance or the host `time.Local`), `loc` threaded through `AddBillingInterval`/`fullBillingCycleDays`/`advanceBillingPeriod` (the subscription handler gains a `TenantLocator` → `engine.TenantLocation`), and a snap-to-first-then-advance fix for the calendar branch. Day-grade adds (trial end, due dates) are TZ-invariant and unchanged. **Deliberately not changed:** Go's `AddDate` overflows `Jan 31 + 1mo → Mar 3` in every zone — there is no Feb-28 clamp and we did not add one. UTC-timezone tenants and UTC-host deployments are unaffected. Guarded by new provenance-independence regression tests (same instant, UTC- vs Local-located, must yield the same tenant-anchored result — the prior suite built every input in UTC and was blind to the class) + month-end/leap cases. A separate follow-up will align the period *display* to the industry-standard inclusive-last-day convention ("Jun 1 – Jun 30").

### Changed

- **In-flight payment banner is honest + age-aware (2026-06-07, ADR-049 Phase 4).** The "Payment is in flight at the provider" banner used a static Info message and the "Payment outcome unconfirmed" banner carried a greyed-out, non-functional "Check provider" button. Now that Velox confirms a processing payment automatically — inline from the synchronous charge response (Phase 3) or via the reconciler backstop (Phase 2) — the copy says so truthfully, and the in-flight banner escalates **Info → Warning** when a *real* invoice has been `processing` past the expected-settle window (6h default — anomalous for a card, which should have settled inline or via the reconciler), pointing the operator at Stripe rather than falsely promising auto-resolution. The Warning is aged off `updated_at` (no new column) and is **suppressed for simulated invoices** (a clock-pinned invoice's age is sim-time, not a real-world duration, so a wall-clock age check would false-positive). The dead disabled "Check provider" button was removed (a greyed-out button is a small UI lie); an on-demand re-check action is deferred until real stuck-payment pressure — see ADR-049. Guarded by `TestClassify_PaymentProcessing_AgeAware` + `TestClassify_PaymentUnconfirmed_NoDeadAction`. Completes the ADR-049 arc.

- **Payment settlement consolidated into a single primitive (2026-06-07, ADR-049 Phase 1).** Terminal payment transitions (`→ succeeded` / `→ failed`) were written in ~10 places across four packages, each firing a *different* subset of consequences — the inbound webhook was the only complete settler (mark + sim-time `paid_at` + card stamp + `payment.succeeded`/`payment.failed` event + dunning + customer email), while the reconciler, the synchronous charge response, and the engine paths fired bare subsets. That drift is a latent bug: e.g. a *dropped* `payment_intent.payment_failed` webhook recovered by the reconciler marks the invoice failed but never dunns or notifies the customer (silent under-collection). Extracted the webhook's full success/failure logic into one idempotent `SettleSucceeded` / `SettleFailed` primitive (`internal/payment/settlement.go`) that owns the complete side-effect set plus the out-of-order guard; the two webhook handlers now resolve the invoice and delegate (discover-then-settle). **Behavior-preserving** — the existing webhook tests are unchanged and green, plus direct primitive tests lock the source-independent contract. This is the foundation for the subsequent phases (reconciler convergence, synchronous-charge-response settle, age-aware in-flight surfacing); see ADR-049 for the full arc and the deferred async/dispute tail. No user-visible change in this phase.

- **Mid-cycle plan upgrades now invoice as two lines — "Unused time on …" + "Remaining time on …" (2026-06-06, ADR-048 Phase C).** A plan upgrade's proration used to show a single opaque net line ("Plan upgrade proration: Starter → Pro = $18.00" — "I upgraded to $50, why $18?"). It now renders the structurally-correct two-line shape every reference platform converges on (Stripe / Recurly / Chargebee / Orb): a **negative** credit *"Unused time on Starter (after Jun 13, 2026)"* (−$12.00) plus a **positive** charge *"Remaining time on Pro (after Jun 13, 2026)"* (+$30.00), netting to the same $18.00. **The invoice total/tax/subtotal are byte-for-byte unchanged** — tax is still computed once on the net (the provider never sees a negative line: Stripe Tax rejects them and manual clamps them), then the stored lines are partitioned *after* the tax call, with the charge half (and its tax) derived as the residual so `credit + charge == net` and `creditTax + chargeTax == tax` exactly. The credit line carries the negative reversed-tax slice; per-jurisdiction rollups (web + PDF) still sum to `tax_amount_cents`. Scoped to real plan changes — item-add and quantity changes keep the single net line (no distinct old plan to credit). Inclusive-tax invoices keep the single line (the carve-out makes the net ≠ proration amount). No new line type, no migration (`base_fee`, no `>= 0` CHECK on `amount_cents`). Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_PlanUpgrade_RendersTwoLines`, `TestUpdateItem_PlanUpgrade_TwoLineTaxApportionsAndTiesOut` (asserts the provider got a single positive line + the line/invoice tie-out), `TestUpdateItem_AddAndQuantityChange_KeepSingleLine`, and `TestSplitUpgradeProration` + a fuzz partition-invariant. Completes #184 (ADR-048).

- **Plan-change proration math extracted to a pure, exactly-tested helper (2026-06-05).** The immediate plan-change proration amount — `(newAmount − oldAmount) × remainingDays ÷ totalDays`, banker's-rounded — was computed inline in `handleItemProration`, so it could only be exercised through the full handler (plans + invoices + tx wiring), and the existing engine proration tests assert *tolerance ranges* (±2–20¢) that can't catch a rounding or off-by-a-cent regression. Pulled the formula into a pure `prorationCents(old, new, remaining, total int64) int64` (`internal/subscription/proration_math.go`) — the single source of truth, pure-integer per ADR-042 (no float64 in the cents path; the operator-facing `ProrationFactor` stays a display-only float). New `proration_math_test.go` pins it to **exact cents**: the B7.4 reference case (30-day period, 18 days remaining → `(5000−2000)×18 ÷ 30 = $18.00`), the round-up/round-down variants, the negative downgrade credit, half-to-even ties reached through the formula, the `totalDays<=0` guard, and a `math/big` differential sweep across 11 day-ratios and deltas up to **$36M** asserting `prorationCents` equals the overflow-proof oracle on every point (the "no float ULP drift up to ~$36M" guarantee a tolerance range can't give). Behavior is unchanged — this is a refactor + test hardening. MANUAL_TEST FLOW B7 gains the exact-amount assertion.

- **Simulated/test-clock markers de-duplicated on detail pages (2026-06-03).** A detail page already carries the simulation context once — the page-level "Currently at &lt;sim time&gt;" banner plus a single entity marker in the header. Repeating a badge on every row underneath was noise. Removed three redundant markers: (1) the per-row "Test clock" badges on Customer Detail's embedded **subscriptions** and **recent-invoices** lists — every row shares the one customer's clock, so the badge said nothing the banner didn't; (2) the duplicate second header chip on Invoice Detail — the header showed both a "Test clock" chip next to the number *and* a "Simulated" chip next to the status pill, on top of the banner, so the sub-only "Test clock" chip went (the authoritative "Simulated" chip stays — it also covers manual one-off invoices); (3) the per-row "Simulated" chip on the Invoice Detail **activity timeline**. The activity chip *looked* informative (it read each row's own `is_simulated`, so rows could in principle differ) but provably cannot: the timeline already routes the only wall-clock rows (customer emails always, plus standalone Stripe payment rows when the invoice is simulated) into a *separate* "Notifications"/"Real-time activity" lane, so every row left in the Activity card is stamped from the one invoice-level `is_simulated` and the chip fired identically on 100% of them — the same redundancy class as the embedded-list rows. Industry parity confirms the cut: Stripe, Orb, and Lago all surface test/simulated state once per page/account/environment (a global toggle + banner), with no precedent for a per-event-row badge on an activity log. **Unchanged:** the page banners, the single header entity marker on Customer/Subscription/Invoice detail, and **all** badges on the global list pages (Dashboard, Customers, Subscriptions, Invoices, Dunning) where rows belong to different entities and a per-row marker is the only signal. Rule of thumb: a per-row badge earns its place only where rows can differ; where every row inherits the parent entity's clock, the page-level banner is the single source. Frontend-only.

- **Per-unit pricing rates are now arbitrary-precision decimals, so sub-cent-per-unit prices bill exactly (2026-06-01, ADR-045).** AI token pricing is sub-cent-per-token — $3.00 per 1,000,000 tokens = 0.0003 cents/token — which `int64` cents cannot represent. The flagship `anthropic_style` recipe had `flat_amount_cents: 300` *commented* "$3.00 per million," but in per-unit `flat` mode that bills **$3.00 per token** — a 1,000,000× overcharge. Fixed by widening the three PER-UNIT rate fields (`flat_amount_cents`, `overage_unit_amount_cents`, graduated-tier `unit_amount_cents` on rating rules + price overrides) from `int64` to decimal (Stripe's `unit_amount_decimal` model — a decimal string up to 12 places, where the customer is still charged a whole integer-cent amount; open-source Lago likewise carries `BigDecimal` amounts). DB columns go `BIGINT → NUMERIC` (migration 0108); on the JSON wire these fields are now **strings** (`"0.0003"`), matching how Velox already serializes decimal quantities. **Fixed fees stay whole `int64` cents** — `base_amount_cents`, `package_amount_cents`, and every invoice line amount + total; `ComputeAmountCents` still rounds the final charge to whole cents (you cannot bill a fractional cent). The `anthropic_style` / `openai_style` recipes are re-authored per-token (published $/1M ÷ 1,000,000), and decimal precision lets the derived cache multiples (0.1× / 1.25× / 2×) be exact instead of cent-rounded; `replicate_style` (per-second whole-cent rates) is unchanged.

### Fixed

- **Mid-period changes on an UNPAID prebill no longer silently vanish — credits adjust the open invoice, charges are blocked (2026-06-08, ADR-050).** A plan up/downgrade, quantity change, add/remove item, or cross-interval swap on an `in_advance` plan whose current-period prebill was finalized but **not paid** used to *silently defer* — the change applied, but no invoice, credit, or operator-visible artifact was produced (`handleItemProration` returned nil; `BillOnPlanSwapImmediate` skipped). Two bugs hid there: a **downgrade/removal** credit against an unpaid period was never re-fired if the invoice was later paid/voided, so the customer's credit **vanished**; and the behavior was **inconsistent** with mid-period **cancel**, which already settles an unpaid prebill correctly (void / reduce `amount_due`). Now one policy, branching on the net proration sign and reusing the same payment-aware `CreateAndIssueAdjustment` primitive cancel uses: a **net credit** (downgrade / removal / qty-decrease) issues a tax-reversing **adjustment credit note** that reduces the open invoice's `amount_due` (capped at amount due, proportional tax reversed) — **not** a refundable balance credit, since no cash was funded; a **net charge** (upgrade / add / qty-increase) is **blocked** with a 409 (`unpaid_invoice_blocks_change` — "settle or void the outstanding invoice first") rather than stacking a second receivable, and the atomic proration tx rolls the change back so nothing half-applies. The engine's unpaid-prebill relief (`relieveUnpaidPrebillOnCancel` → `relieveUnpaidPrebill`) was generalized so the cross-interval **swap** path settles consistently with cancel (previously a silent skip). Industry-convergent, verified across Stripe (`proration_behavior=none` on unpaid), Chargebee (Adjustment vs Refundable Credits), Recurly (block past-due), Lago (credit-not-refund), and Orb (adjustment vs refund credit note). PAID-source behavior is unchanged. Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_Downgrade_UnpaidSource_AdjustsNotRefundableCredit`, `TestUpdateItem_Downgrade_UnpaidSource_CapsAtAmountDue`, `TestUpdateItem_Upgrade_UnpaidSource_Blocked`, and the `BillOnPlanSwapImmediate` unpaid-adjustment subtest. No schema migration.

- **A synchronously-confirmed card charge settles immediately, not on the webhook (2026-06-07, ADR-049 Phase 3).** Velox creates PaymentIntents with `Confirm: true, OffSession: true`, so for a card Stripe returns the terminal status in the create RESPONSE (`succeeded`) — but the charge path discarded `result.Status` and **always** set `payment_status=processing`, then waited for the `payment_intent.succeeded` webhook to mark it paid. That left every card payment dependent on webhook delivery, and on a **test clock** it stuck visibly: the create call returned `succeeded` inside the operator's Advance, but the invoice sat at "Payment is in flight at the provider — awaiting confirmation" because the settling webhook arrives in *wall-clock* time (and in local dev only with `stripe listen` forwarding), decoupled from the simulated timeline. The charge path now branches on `result.Status`: `succeeded` settles **inline** through the shared primitive (mark paid + receipt + `payment.succeeded` + card stamp, on the simulated timeline for clock-pinned invoices), so the invoice resolves in-request; genuinely in-flight statuses (`processing`/`requires_action` — async methods, off-session SCA) stay `processing` and await the webhook + reconciler backstop (Phase 2). Fixes all charge initiators at once (cycle billing, threshold, portal pay-now, operator charge-now, dunning retry) since they share `ChargeInvoice`. The later webhook is an idempotent no-op (the primitive's already-paid guard). Portal pay-now now returns a `succeeded` invoice immediately for synchronous cards (the SPA already handles it — it keeps a short trailing poll for the receipt/card rows then stops); docs updated. Guarded by `TestChargeInvoice_SyncSuccessSettlesInline` + `TestChargeInvoice_ProcessingStaysProcessing`. (This is the fix for the originally-reported test-clock stuck-`processing`.)

- **A dropped payment webhook recovered by the reconciler now fully settles — dunning + notification included (2026-06-07, ADR-049 Phase 2).** Stripe delivers webhooks at-least-once and can drop them (endpoint down past the 3-day retry, misconfigured, or 2xx'd-but-lost). The payment reconciler — the backstop that re-queries Stripe for stuck charges — only flipped `payment_status` and fired *none* of the consequences the webhook does: a recovered failure marked the invoice `failed` but **never started dunning, emitted `payment.failed`, or emailed the customer** (silent under-collection), and a recovered success skipped the receipt + `payment.succeeded`. The reconciler now routes recovered terminals through the same `SettleSucceeded`/`SettleFailed` primitive the webhook uses (ADR-049 Phase 1), so a backstop recovery is byte-identical to the webhook — it replicates the customer-email suppression from the PI `velox_purpose` (a recovered dunning-retry failure won't double-notify) and binds simulated `paid_at` on clock-pinned invoices. **Also** generalizes the sweep from `payment_status='unknown'` to additionally cover stale `processing` (the dropped-webhook backstop for an in-flight charge), with its own longer cool-off (30m default, vs 60s for `unknown`) so the webhook always wins the common race, terminal-status-only transitions, and a fresh-read race guard that skips an invoice the webhook settled during the Stripe round-trip. No schema change. Guarded by `TestReconciler_RecoveredFailureRoutesThroughSettler`, `TestReconciler_DunningRetryFailureSuppressesEmail`, `TestReconciler_StaleProcessingSweptToSucceeded`, `TestReconciler_RaceGuardSkipsWebhookWinner` + the direct primitive tests. (Test-clock `processing` is addressed separately in Phase 3 — synchronous settle from the charge response.)

- **Cancel + plan-swap prebill clawbacks now reverse proportional tax (2026-06-06, ADR-048).** When a paid `in_advance` prebill is partially clawed back — a **mid-cycle cancel** (`BillOnCancel`) or **plan swap** (`BillOnPlanSwapImmediate`) — the engine credited the customer the **net** unused base only and reversed **no** output tax. But the customer paid **gross** (net + tax) for that unused slice, so a net credit left them short by the tax fraction when it later offset a gross invoice, and the tenant's tax liability stayed overstated.
