Both paths now route the clawback through the tax-reversing **credit-note** primitive (`CreateAndIssueAdjustment`, the same one the unpaid-prebill relief already uses): the net is grossed up via the source invoice's own `Total/Subtotal` ratio, the **gross** is credited to the customer's spendable balance, and the proportional output tax is reversed against the source invoice's committed `tax_transaction` (no-op for manual/none providers). The cash outcome is unchanged for zero-tax invoices and corrected upward by the tax slice for taxed ones; the unpaid-prebill relief path is untouched. Extracted into a shared `creditUnusedPrebill` helper with a net-grant fallback for narrow tests where the credit-note adjuster isn't wired. Guarded by `TestCreditUnusedPrebill` + `TestBillOnCancel_PaidPrebillReversesTax`. First slice of the credit-clawback tax-reversal work (#184).

- **Downgrade / quantity-decrease / item-remove clawbacks now reverse proportional tax (2026-06-06, ADR-048).** Phase B of #184. A mid-cycle **plan downgrade**, **quantity decrease**, or **item removal** on a paid `in_advance` prebill credited the customer the **net** unused amount via a bare credit-ledger grant and reversed **no** output tax — the same cash-short / liability-overstated bug the cancel + plan-swap paths just fixed, on the third clawback surface. The subscription handler's downgrade-credit branch now grosses the net up by the resolved paid source invoice's `Total/Subtotal` ratio and routes it through the tax-reversing **credit-note** primitive (`CreateAndIssueAdjustment`): the **gross** the customer paid for the unused slice lands on their spendable balance and the proportional output tax is reversed against the source invoice's committed `tax_transaction` (no-op for manual/none providers). The handler gained a narrow `CreditNoteIssuer` dependency (`*creditnote.Service` satisfies it directly); the legacy bare-net grant stays only as the fallback when the issuer is unwired or no paid source invoice was resolved. The CN is issued **after** the atomic item-change tx commits — the credit-note service isn't tx-aware and its tax reversal is an external Stripe call (same post-commit pattern as the proration tax-commit). No schema migration: a client retry of the same downgrade is rejected at `UpdateItem`'s no-op gate (item already on the new plan/qty), so the CN can't be issued twice, and the source invoice's over-credit cap is the hard backstop. Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_Downgrade_RoutesGrossTaxReversingCreditNote`, `TestUpdateItem_QuantityDecrease_RoutesGrossCreditNote`, `TestUpdateItem_Downgrade_FallsBackToNetGrantWhenIssuerUnwired`, plus `TestGrossUpByInvoiceRatio` + `TestClawbackReason`. The upgrade two-line display (Phase C) is the remaining slice.

- **Proration tax is now committed to the tax provider, not just charged (2026-06-06).** An immediate plan-change proration invoice *calculated* tax correctly (e.g. `$17.00 × 8.875% = 151¢` on the prorated net) and charged the customer — but it showed a **blank `tax_provider`** and the Stripe Tax calculation was **never committed into a reportable tax transaction**, unlike the cycle/create invoice paths which both `CommitTax`. So the proration tax was collected but invisible to the tenant's Stripe Tax reports → **under-remittance**. Root cause: `prorationTaxApplierAdapter` dropped `TaxProvider`/`TaxCalculationID` (the `ProrationTaxResult` struct lacked the fields), so the invoice header was never stamped and the handler had no calculation id to commit; and the proration path never called `CommitTax`. Fixed by carrying `TaxProvider`/`TaxCalculationID` through the adapter onto the proration invoice, and committing the calculation once the invoice row is durable — inline on the non-atomic path, after `tx.Commit` on the atomic path (the commit is an external Stripe call and must not ride the DB tx). No-op for manual/none providers (no calculation id). Mirrors the engine's calculate-then-commit contract. Guarded by `TestUpdateItem_ProrationStampsProviderAndCommitsTax` + `TestUpdateItem_ProrationManualProviderDoesNotCommit`. *(The companion gap — downgrade/negative-proration credits not reversing proportional tax — is now fixed too; see the credit-clawback tax-reversal entries above, ADR-048.)*

- **Dashboard invoice lines render the exact fractional quantity (2026-06-06).** Follow-up to the `quantity_decimal` backend fix: the operator invoice-detail line showed the truncated integer `quantity` while the PDF/API already had the exact decimal. Declared `quantity_decimal` in the OpenAPI `InvoiceLineItem` schema (regenerated Go DTO + TS types), and the React invoice-detail line now renders the decimal when present (`1.5`), falling back to the integer for older rows. Whole quantities still show thousands separators. Completes the fractional-quantity fix across all surfaces (data, PDF, API, dashboard).

- **Fractional usage quantities no longer truncate on invoice lines (2026-06-06).** A usage line's quantity was stored as `int64`, so fractional usage (e.g. 1.5 GPU-hours, or a cap-scaled meter) was truncated — the line showed `Qty 1 × $10 = $15`, i.e. `quantity × unit ≠ amount`. The **charge was always correct** (the amount is priced on the full decimal quantity); only the displayed quantity lied, and any consumer multiplying `quantity × unit` (PDF, exports) saw inconsistent math. Fixed with industry-standard parity (Stripe `quantity_decimal`, Chargebee `quantity_in_decimal`): a new `quantity_decimal NUMERIC(38,12)` column (migration 0110) carries the exact quantity, the integer `quantity` is retained truncated for back-compat, and line amounts stay whole cents. The cycle engine populates it on every usage line; the invoice PDF renders the exact decimal (whole quantities keep thousands separators); the API already returns it (`quantity_decimal`). Guarded by `TestPostgresLineItem_QuantityDecimalRoundTrip` (1.5 survives the store round-trip; `quantity` stays 1). The single shared `domain.AddBillingInterval`-style approach: no behavior change to integer-quantity lines (the AI-token core), which is everything today. Follow-up: dashboard invoice-line display will render the decimal too.

- **Audit follow-ups: escalated-dunning resolution, webhook success-rate, credit "used" stat (2026-06-06).** Three correctness fixes from the calculation audit (none affect a customer charge). (1) **Escalated dunning runs couldn't be resolved.** `GetActiveRunByInvoice` filtered `state NOT IN ('resolved','escalated')`, so when a customer paid out-of-band *after* retries exhausted, `ResolveByInvoice` found nothing and the run stayed `escalated` forever (never emitting `dunning.resolved`). Now excludes only `resolved`. (2) **Webhook endpoint `success_rate` counted pending deliveries in the denominator** (`succeeded / COUNT(*)`), depressing the rate whenever deliveries were in flight; now computed over completed deliveries only (`succeeded / (succeeded + failed)`) via a shared `endpointSuccessRate` helper. (3) **Credit-balance `TotalUsed` double-counted expiry** — it summed every negative ledger entry (`amount_cents < 0`), which includes `expiry` rows already counted in `TotalExpired`; now filters `entry_type = 'usage'`. The available `BalanceCents` was always correct — only the Credits-tab breakdown stat was off. Guarded by `TestResolveByInvoice_ResolvesEscalatedRun` and `TestEndpointSuccessRate`; the in-memory test mocks (which had replicated the dunning + webhook bugs) were corrected too.

- **Dashboard analytics accuracy: yearly-MRR truncation, currency scoping, and period scoping (2026-06-06).** Three operator-facing reporting fixes (no customer charge is affected). (1) **Yearly MRR truncated per-unit before scaling by quantity** — `(base_amount_cents / 12) * quantity` floors the monthly figure first, so `$100/yr × 10` reported `(10000/12)×10 = 8330¢` instead of `(10000×10)/12 = 8333¢`. Reordered to multiply-before-divide at all sites (`analytics/overview.go` current-MRR + new/churned/movement, `analytics/mrr_movement.go`, `billing/metrics.go`); expansion/contraction deltas inherited the error twice. (2) **Revenue chart summed mixed currencies** — `analytics/revenue_chart.go` had no currency filter, adding USD + EUR + … into one meaningless total; now scoped to the tenant default currency like the overview. (3) **`AvgInvoiceValue` averaged all-time** while its sibling period metrics were period-scoped (and `paid_invoices` lacked the currency filter); both are now currency + period scoped consistently. The tenant-default-currency lookup is extracted to a shared `defaultCurrencyFor` helper. Guarded by `TestComputeDashboard_YearlyMRR_MultiplyBeforeDivide` (qty>1, the only case the bug shows).

- **Mid-cycle plan/quantity proration on a stub period no longer over-charges (2026-06-06).** Immediate plan-change, quantity-change, add-item, and remove-item proration (`handleItemProration` via `remainingPeriodRatio`) divided the `(new − old)` delta by the **current period length** instead of the **full billing cycle**. On a *stub* period (a customer who started mid-cycle — e.g. a 14-day partial period of a 30-day monthly plan) the current period is shorter than a cycle, so the proration over-charged upgrades and over-credited downgrades. Found on real data: a Start $20 → Pro $50 upgrade with 13 of the stub's days remaining billed **$27.86** — `(5000−2000)×13/14` — when the correct charge is **$13.00** — `(5000−2000)×13/30`. The day-1 stub base fee was already prorated against the full cycle (`14/30`), and `emitBaseSegmentLine` / `BillOnPlanSwapImmediate` already used `fullCycleDays`, so the immediate-proration path was the lone inconsistency. Fixed by deriving the denominator from the full cycle. To kill the defect class (two paths computing the same quantity differently), the anniversary interval-advance is now a single shared helper — `domain.AddBillingInterval` — that both `billing.advanceBillingPeriod` and the subscription handler's new `fullBillingCycleDays` call, so they can't drift again. Full periods are unaffected (`currentPeriod == fullCycle`). Guarded by `TestFullBillingCycleDays`, `TestProration_StubPeriod_DividesByFullCycle` (pins the $13.00 vs $27.86 case), and `TestUpdateItem_PlanChange_StubPeriod_UsesFullCycleDenominator` (end-to-end). The four existing proration-amount handler tests were made deterministic (fixed clock + calendar month) — they were silently wall-clock-dependent (`968` vs `1000` depending on the current month's length once proration divides by the true cycle).

- **Stripe Tax invoice line now shows a clean tax name, not the raw enum (2026-06-05).** A `stripe_tax` invoice's tax line rendered the raw Stripe `tax_type` enum verbatim — `sales_tax (8.875%)` (snake_case, lowercase) on the hosted invoice page, PDF, credit-note PDF, and operator detail. Stripe's `tax_type` is a machine enum (`sales_tax`, `vat`, `gst`, `qst`, `igst`, …) and, critically, the **document-level** `tax_breakdown` carries no `display_name` (only the per-line/shipping breakdowns do, stripe-go v82) — so for the common case (per-line breakdown null) there was no readable label to fall back to. Fixed at the single authoritative point (the Stripe provider's `mapResult`, mirroring the `displayTaxRate` pattern): a new `taxTypeDisplayName` resolver prefers Stripe's `display_name` when present, else maps the enum via a verified table covering all 15 `tax_type` values (`sales_tax → "Sales Tax"`, `vat → "VAT"`, `gst → "GST"`, …), else gracefully title-cases any future enum so a raw snake_case token never reaches the invoice. The clean name lands in `invoices.tax_name` and propagates to every surface (and credit notes inherit it). Manual-provider invoices are unaffected — they already use the operator's configured tax name. `taxability_reason` was already mapped to compliance legends, so this was the only raw Stripe enum leaking to a customer surface. Guarded by `TestTaxTypeDisplayName` + a `TaxName` assertion on `TestMapResult_DocLevelRateFallback`. Forward-only (no backfill); existing invoices keep their stored `tax_name`.

- **Invoices now show the real statutory tax rate, not a rounding-distorted effective rate (2026-06-05, ADR-047).** A $100 `stripe_tax` invoice for a New York customer (combined NYC rate **8.875%**) showed the customer "Sales Tax (**8.88%**)" and stored `invoices.tax_rate = 8.8800`. 8.88% is not a real NY rate — it was `tax_amount × 100 ÷ subtotal` (`888 ÷ 10000`), the *effective* rate, nudged up by the half-cent rounding (`$8.875 → $8.88`). The true `8.8750` was already on the line items (PR #165) but never reached the customer-facing tax line. (`stripe_tax`-only — the manual provider already reports its configured statutory rate; and never a mischarge: the amount was always Stripe's verbatim figure.) Fixed at the single write site: `invoices.tax_rate` now stores the **statutory** rate when every taxed line shares one rate (the common single-jurisdiction case, ignoring exempt lines), falling back to the blended effective rate only for genuine multi-jurisdiction invoices where no single statutory rate exists (new `displayTaxRate` helper in `internal/billing/engine.go`). This unifies `stripe_tax` with the manual provider and propagates to every surface — invoice PDF, credit-note PDF, hosted invoice page, operator invoice detail. Two compounding formatting bugs fixed in the same pass (both truncated even a correct `8.8750` to `8.88`): the frontend's `tax_rate.toFixed(2)` and the Go PDFs' `fmt "%.4g"` (which uses *significant figures* and silently drops precision on rates ≥ 10, e.g. `13.875 → "13.88"`) are replaced by a shared up-to-4-dp, trailing-zeros-trimmed `formatTaxRate` (TS in `web-v2/src/lib/api.ts`; Go in `internal/invoice/pdf.go` + `internal/creditnote/pdf.go`). Per-line tax is deliberately **not** shown — verified against Stripe/Zuora that the standard invoice aggregates tax per rate with a per-jurisdiction breakdown only when lines span >1 jurisdiction (already Velox's shape). Guarded by `TestDisplayTaxRate` (single-rate → statutory; mixed → effective; taxed+exempt → statutory) and `TestFormatTaxRate` (incl. the ≥10% `%g` case). No backfill (pre-launch); new finalizations get the corrected rate.

- **Tax-calculation audit rows now link back to their invoice, restoring the commit-time expiry guard (2026-06-05).** `tax_calculations.invoice_id` was never populated, so it read `NULL` on every row — `RecordCalculation` runs *during* tax application, before the invoice is persisted (the column carries a FK to `invoices`, so a non-null value at that point would violate it). The damage was twofold: (1) the natural audit query `… WHERE invoice_id = $1` silently returned zero rows, and (2) `CommitTax`'s 24h Stripe-calc expiry guard (`LookupCalculationCreatedAt`, which filters on `invoice_id`) never matched, so an expired calculation could slip through to Stripe and leave the invoice with a `tax_calculation_id` but no `tax_transaction_id` (silently-broken Stripe Tax reporting). Fixed by backfilling `invoice_id` at the first moment both ids coexist: `CommitTax` now calls a new `PostgresStore.LinkInvoice(tenant, invoice, provider_ref)` that stamps the id onto the audit row matched by `provider_ref` (= `invoices.tax_calculation_id`). Idempotent and additive-only (`WHERE invoice_id IS NULL` — never clobbers an existing link), best-effort (a failure only degrades the guard lookup to "skip", never blocks finalize), and a no-op for manual/none providers (empty `provider_ref`). Guarded by `TestPostgresStore_LinkInvoice` (backfill + non-clobber + empty-ref no-op). No shipped migration (pre-launch); the fix applies to newly-finalized invoices.

- **Stripe Tax: per-line `tax_rate` and `tax_jurisdiction` no longer lose precision when Stripe omits the per-line breakdown (2026-06-04).** For a `stripe_tax` invoice, Stripe returns the verbatim rate (`percentage_decimal: "8.875"` for NYC) and jurisdiction in its **document-level** `tax_breakdown`, but leaves the **per-line** `tax_breakdown` `null` (the calculation request only expands `line_items`, not `line_items.data.tax_breakdown`). `mapResult` read the rate/jurisdiction *only* from the per-line breakdown, so every line fell back to the rounded **effective** rate (`tax_amount × 100 / subtotal`) with an **empty** jurisdiction — e.g. a $100 NYC invoice stored `invoice_line_items.tax_rate = 8.8800` (not `8.8750`) and a blank `tax_jurisdiction`, defeating the 4-decimal precision ADR-042/043 guarantees. (The tax **amount** was always correct — Stripe computes it at full precision and Velox stores it verbatim — so no customer was mischarged; the defect was the displayed rate + lost jurisdiction/taxability_reason, an audit/PDF-legend problem.) Fixed: when a line's own breakdown is absent, seed it from the **single** document-level rate (rate + jurisdiction + taxability_reason). A genuine per-line breakdown (multi-jurisdiction invoices) still takes precedence. Found by reading a real stored calculation (`vlx_inv_d8gomormajdhcl08grvg`). Guarded by `TestMapResult_DocLevelRateFallback` (NYC: line → `8.8750` + `US-NY`) and `TestMapResult_PerLineBreakdownWins` (per-line rate wins over document-level). Existing invoices finalized before this fix keep their stored rate (no backfill); new finalizations get the correct line rate.

- **Invoice "create preview" no longer logs a bogus "Created invoice" audit row whose "View" link 405s (2026-06-04).** `POST /v1/invoices/create_preview` is a read-only dry-run (gated by the read permission, writes nothing — Stripe's `create_preview` shape), but the audit middleware classifies *every* successful non-GET request as a mutation (POST → `create`), so each preview recorded a green **"Created invoice"** row with `resource_id="create_preview"`. The dashboard's upcoming-invoice card fires the preview automatically on every customer page-open, so the log filled with these phantom creations — and clicking **View** navigated to `/invoices/create_preview`, which the React detail page fetches as `GET /v1/invoices/create_preview`; chi matches the POST-only `create_preview` route ahead of `/invoices/{id}` and returns **405 Method Not Allowed**. Fixed by giving read-only handlers an explicit opt-out: new `audit.MarkSkip(ctx)` (sibling of `MarkHandled`) tells the middleware there is nothing to audit, exactly as it already bypasses GET. Applied to both read-only preview POSTs — `invoices/create_preview` and `recipes/{key}/preview` (the latter logged a phantom "Created recipe"). No row is written for either now. Guarded by `TestAudit_MarkSkip_SuppressesCatchAll`, `TestCreatePreview_OptsOutOfAudit`, and `TestRecipePreview_OptsOutOfAudit`. (Pre-existing phantom rows written before this fix remain in the log; they are local dev noise and can be deleted with `DELETE FROM audit_log WHERE resource_type='invoice' AND resource_id='create_preview'`.)

- **Manual invoice issue + due dates now anchor to finalize, not draft-create (2026-06-04).** A manual (operator-composed) invoice stamped `issued_at` at draft-**create** and never re-stamped it at finalize, so a draft composed at one moment and finalized later showed `issued_at == created_at` — collapsing the "Created" and "Finalized" rows onto one instant on the activity timeline, and running Net terms from composition rather than issuance. Now `Service.Finalize` re-stamps `issued_at` to the finalize moment and recomputes `due_at = issued_at + net_payment_term_days` for operator-composed invoices (new `store.FinalizeWithDates`, atomic with the status flip) — Stripe's `finalized_at` semantics. `ctx` is already bound to the invoice's clock at finalize, so on a clock-pinned customer `issued_at` is the simulated finalize-time (still simulated, just re-anchored); "Due on receipt" (0) keeps `due_at == issued_at`. **Cycle invoices are unaffected** — they're born finalized at build time and keep those dates via the existing `UpdateStatus` path (the gate is `isOperatorComposed`, so the auto-finalize-after-tax-retry path for cycle drafts is untouched too). Guarded by `TestFinalize_ManualInvoice_AnchorsIssuedAndDueToFinalize` (draft at T1, finalize at T2 → `issued_at=T2`, `due_at=T2+term`) and the due-on-receipt case.

- **Invoice activity-timeline correctness: cross-domain cancel-vs-void dedup, stable row keys, and the dropped detail sub-line (2026-06-04).** Three fixes from the activity-log review. (1) **Canceled-vs-void de-dup compared across time domains.** A `payment_intent.canceled` webhook row is suppressed when it co-occurred with a void, via a 5-minute window between `invoice.voided_at` and the Stripe event time. On a clock-pinned (simulated) invoice `voided_at` is *test-clock* time while the Stripe event is *wall-clock* — years apart — so the window never matched and a redundant "Payment canceled" row showed beside the void. Extracted the decision into a pure `dropCanceledForVoid` helper that, for simulated invoices, falls back to the unconditional drop (a void cancels the pending PI); wall-clock invoices keep the 5-min window. Guarded by `TestDropCanceledForVoid`. (2) **Timeline rows keyed by array index** (`key={i}`) flashed/mis-rendered when the polled timeline reordered between refetches (a Stripe row folding into a dunning twin, a new "paid" row sorting earlier); now keyed by a stable `source:event_type:timestamp:payment_intent_id` composite. (3) **The Notifications/Real-time lane dropped the `detail` sub-line** the billing lane renders — so a folded "Customer notified by email" note on a standalone Stripe failure vanished; now rendered in both lanes.

- **Audit log no longer mislabels invoice money/email actions as "Created" (2026-06-04).** The activity-log review found that **Collect payment** (`POST /invoices/{id}/collect`) and **Send invoice** (`POST /{id}/send`) wrote no explicit audit row, so the middleware catch-all recorded them as a generic green **"Created INV-NNN"** — a money-movement and an email action both indistinguishable from the invoice's actual creation. Both now write explicit rows (`collect` / `send`; `MarkHandled` suppresses the catch-all), rendering as **"Collected payment on INV-NNN"** (medium severity) and **"Emailed INV-NNN"**. Adjacent audit-copy fixes from the same pass: refund rows now carry the invoice number and read **"Refunded INV-NNN"** with destructive (high-severity) styling (was a label-less lowercase "refund invoice"); `retry_tax` reads **"Retried tax on INV-NNN"**; and invoice public-token rotation reads **"Rotated hosted-invoice link for INV-NNN"** (was the ambiguous "Rotated INV-NNN"). The invoice handler's `auditLogger` field changed from the concrete `*audit.Logger` to a narrow `auditWriter` interface so these rows are unit-testable (no wiring change). Guarded by `TestCollectPayment_WritesCollectAuditRow`.

- **Subscription plan-change audit rows now carry their test-clock context (2026-06-03).** Reviewing the audit log surfaced `subscription.item_updated` ("Changed plan") rows that showed simulated test-clock times (e.g. 2053 / 2031) with no indication they were simulated. Root cause: the item-update audit writer (`subscription/handler.go`) logged the raw payload, whereas every *other* subscription audit action wraps it in `auditMetaForSub(sub, …)` — so this lone path never recorded `sim_effective_at` / `test_clock_id`, and the audit UI's "Effect on test clock at &lt;sim&gt;" subline + test-clock chip never rendered for plan changes. Fixed by wrapping the payload in `auditMetaForSub` (fetching the post-update subscription for its current `UpdatedAt` + clock pin, mirroring the item-add path); the row's primary timestamp stays wall-clock (`created_at` = `time.Now()`, ADR-030) and the simulated effect-time renders as the subline. To make this unit-testable, the handler's `auditLogger` field changed from the concrete `*audit.Logger` to a narrow `auditRecorder` interface (Log + Query) the concrete logger satisfies — no wiring change. Guarded by `TestHandler_UpdateItem_PlanChangeAuditCarriesSimContext` (clock-pinned → metadata carries `test_clock_id` + `sim_effective_at`) and the unpinned no-op case. (Pre-existing rows written before the 2026-05-28 wall-clock-`created_at` fix may still show a simulated headline date; only newly-written rows are corrected.)

- **Manual invoice "Due on receipt" now works, and net terms fall back to the tenant default (2026-06-03).** The composer offers a "Due on receipt" option (sends `net_payment_term_days: 0`), but `invoice.Service.Create` coerced it with `if netDays <= 0 { netDays = 30 }` — conflating an explicit 0 with "unset" and silently turning Due-on-receipt into Net 30 (due 30 days out). Separately, a manual invoice created via the API without the field always defaulted to a hardcoded 30, ignoring the tenant's configured net terms (the cycle engine honors `settings.NetPaymentTerms`). Fixed by making `CreateInput.NetPaymentTermDays` a `*int`: an explicit value (including 0) is honored verbatim (negative clamped to 0); when omitted (nil), it falls back to the tenant's configured net terms, then to 30 — mirroring the cycle engine via a new `SetTenantSettingsReader`. Backend-only: the create handler hand-decodes JSON, so the wire stays an optional integer (no codegen/openapi/frontend change). Guarded by `TestCreate_NetPaymentTermResolution` (explicit 0 → due == issued; omitted + tenant default 14 → Net 14; omitted + no setting → Net 30).

- **Invoice currency is now normalized to canonical uppercase, fixing revenue/at-risk sums that silently dropped mixed-case invoices (2026-06-03).** The manual composer uppercased the currency ("USD") while the cycle engine's no-currency fallback stored lowercase "usd" — so a tenant could hold both "USD" and "usd" invoices. That breaks the analytics overview and dunning stats, which scope revenue to the tenant default currency with a **case-sensitive** `currency = $1` filter (`analytics/overview.go`, default `'USD'`; `tenant.DefaultSettings` is `"USD"`): any "usd" invoice silently fell out of the revenue / at-risk / ARPU sums. Fixed by normalizing to **uppercase** (the system-wide canonical — tenant default, rating rules, and pricing are all uppercase) at the single store chokepoint both paths funnel through (`PostgresStore.Create` + `createWithLineItemsInTx`, header **and** every line item), with `invoice.Service.Create` uppercasing at the source too. This also retroactively covers the cycle "usd" fallback. PDF (`strings.ToUpper` on read) and the customer portal (`toUpperCase()` before `Intl.NumberFormat`) already uppercase defensively for display, so presentation is unaffected. No migration (pre-launch, per the no-speculative-backfill stance).

- **Tax-inclusive manual invoices no longer double-count tax at finalize (2026-06-03).** `computeAndPersistInvoiceTax` (the shared finalize/tax-retry path) computed the total from the **stored header** subtotal/discount and added the carved tax on top: `inv.SubtotalCents − inv.DiscountCents + taxApp.TaxAmountCents`. In tax-**inclusive** mode `ApplyTaxToLineItems` carves tax *out* of the gross the operator entered (so `taxApp.SubtotalCents` is the net and `taxApp.TaxAmountCents` is the portion already embedded in the gross) — adding it back onto the gross overstated the total by ~one tax amount (a $118 gross invoice finalized at $136). Fixed by reading the net subtotal/discount off the tax application and persisting them — `totalWithTax = taxApp.SubtotalCents − taxApp.DiscountCents + taxApp.TaxAmountCents` — exactly mirroring the cycle build path (`billOnePeriod`), and extending `UpdateTaxAtomic` to write `subtotal_cents`/`discount_cents`. Restores the `subtotal − discount + tax == gross` invariant. **No-op for the common tax-exclusive case** (there `taxApp.SubtotalCents == inv.SubtotalCents`). Guarded by `TestManualInvoice_TaxInclusive_TotalEqualsGross` (gross $118 @ 18% inclusive → net $100 + tax $18 = total $118, not $136).

- **Manual invoice collection now matches cycle invoices (2026-06-03).** A manual-vs-cycle audit found the manual finalize path silently diverged from the engine's cycle path in two ways that made a one-off invoice "look broken" next to an auto-generated one. (1) **No-payment-method finalize did nothing** — when a manual invoice was finalized for a customer with no saved card, the handler's auto-charge block simply wasn't entered: no `auto_charge_pending` flag (so the scheduler's retry loop never picked it up) and no customer email. The invoice silently went overdue — customer never told, never auto-charged when they later added a card. The engine's cycle path has always done both. Manual finalize now mirrors it: on no-PM it sets `auto_charge_pending=true` (the scheduler charges the moment a card is attached, à la Chargebee "Collect on Card Update") **and** emails the customer a payment-update link via the same `NoPaymentMethodNotifier` adapter the engine uses. (2) **Dropped the automatic "here's your invoice" email on finalize.** Velox is PaymentIntent-only — the Stripe `charge_automatically` model — and the industry is unanimous that an auto-charged invoice does **not** email the invoice; it sends a **receipt on payment** (Stripe: *"Stripe doesn't email invoices … when charged automatically"*; Lago/Chargebee/Recurly identical). The cycle path already behaved this way; manual now does too, so both produce identical notification rows. Operators can still send an invoice explicitly via the **Send** button (`POST /v1/invoices/{id}/send`). The post-finalize collection step is extracted into `Handler.collectAtFinalize` and covered by real-path tests (`TestCollectAtFinalize_*`): no-PM → queue + notify, no charge; PM-ready → charge, no notify. A per-invoice "send for manual payment / net-terms" collection mode (Stripe `send_invoice`) is deliberately deferred until a customer needs it — additive, not a divergence.

- **Manual invoice header showed wrong Terms and a zero-length Period (2026-06-03).** Surfaced reviewing a one-off invoice created from the customer page. Two display bugs: (1) **Terms** was rendered from the live tenant setting (`settings.net_payment_terms`) instead of the invoice's own `net_payment_term_days` — so an invoice issued Net 7 was labelled "Net 15" (the current default) and the label disagreed with the Due date (Issued + 7). The backend arithmetic was correct (`due_at = issued_at + the invoice's own term`); only the label read the wrong source. Now Terms reads `invoice.net_payment_term_days` (0 → "Due on receipt"), matching the Due date the invoice was actually issued with. (2) **Period** showed a same-instant "Jan 14 – Jan 14": a one-off invoice has no billing cycle, so the backend defaults `billing_period_start == billing_period_end` (now→now) to satisfy the NOT NULL columns. Industry (Stripe/Chargebee/Lago) omit an invoice-level period for one-off charges; the page now suppresses the Period field when start == end and shows it only for real subscription-cycle spans. Frontend-only.

- **Manual tax: the per-line rounding residual is now apportioned by largest remainder, so a larger line can no longer show *less* tax than a smaller one (2026-06-03, ADR-046).** When several line items are taxed at one flat rate, the per-line taxes are each rounded, but their sum can drift ±1¢ from the exact document-level tax (e.g. three lines of `$33.33 / $33.33 / $33.34` at 7.25%: naive per-line rounding sums to **726¢**, but `$100.00 × 7.25% = 725¢` exactly). The provider reconciles the two by computing the document tax top-down (725¢ — exact, the VAT-correct figure) and distributing it across the lines. The old reconciliation dumped the entire residual on the **positionally-last** line; when the residual was *negative* (−1¢ here) and the last line happened to be the largest, that line was docked below its smaller peers — an operator looking at the invoice saw the `$33.34` line taxed `241¢` while two `$33.33` lines were each taxed `242¢` (a "biggest line, least tax" inversion). The residual now goes to the lines with the largest fractional remainders (ties → lowest index) — the **largest-remainder / minimum-distortion** method every reference indirect-tax engine converges on (Sovos: "split among the lines that have the highest remainder"; Avalara / Dynamics 365: "the line that results in the minimum percentage change"). The document total is unchanged (still 725¢, top-down); only *which* line absorbs the cent changed, and it can never invert base order. Applies to both exclusive and inclusive manual-rate paths; `stripe_tax` is unaffected (Stripe returns per-line amounts directly). The flaw was latent from when the reconciliation was added (`401d990`) and surfaced only on inputs that drive the residual negative onto the largest line. Guarded by `TestManualProvider_LargestRemainderNoInversion` (the `$33.33/$33.33/$33.34` case asserts the `$33.34` line stays at `242¢` and no inversion exists) and a property test fuzzing line counts × rates × bases for sum-exactness and no-inversion.

- **Standalone Stripe payment rows no longer mis-sort in a simulated invoice's activity timeline (2026-06-03, ADR-030 addendum).** Follow-up to the wall-clock/simulated lane split below. Stripe webhook rows (`payment_intent.payment_failed` / `canceled` that survive folding — i.e. no dunning twin to absorb them) carry Stripe's wall-clock `occurred_at`. On a clock-pinned invoice they sorted by real time and landed *before* the simulated billing rows that preceded them. They now join the wall-clock real-time lane **only when the invoice is simulated** (where the two clocks diverge); on a normal one-clock invoice they stay in the Activity timeline where operators expect payment outcomes. When that lane carries a payment outcome it's titled **"Real-time activity"** rather than "Notifications" (a payment event isn't a notification). Frontend-only — the backend already stamped these rows wall-clock (`is_simulated=false`); the dashboard now routes by source × the invoice's authoritative `is_simulated`.

- **Fix false-positive "simulated" badge on every manual invoice (2026-06-03).** The manual-invoice `is_simulated` capture added the day before derived the flag from `clock.IsSimulated(ctx)` — "is the request ctx bound to an effective-now?". But `bindForCreate` binds the ctx via the resolver for **every** customer, and the resolver returns wall-clock (not an error) for an *unpinned* customer — so the binding succeeds and the check returned true for **all** manual invoices, badging non-test-clock invoices as simulated. Caught by a faithful end-to-end test exercising the real resolver path (the original test bound the ctx directly via `WithEffectiveNow`, masking it). Fixed by capturing the flag from the customer's actual pin (`customer.TestClockID != ""`, via `invoice.Service.SetCustomerClockReader`) — the same authoritative `test_clock_id` check the engine uses for cycle invoices — instead of the ctx binding. The ctx binding still drives the simulated *timestamps*; only the *flag* source changed. The misleading `clock.IsSimulated` helper is removed. Guard: `TestManualInvoice_IsSimulatedFromCustomerPin` asserts pinned→true / **unpinned→false**.

- **Invoice "simulated" badges are now authoritative and cover manual invoices; activity timeline no longer interleaves wall-clock email rows with simulated billing rows (2026-06-02, ADR-030 addendum).** On a test-clock-pinned customer, a manual (one-off) invoice's dates *were* simulated but showed **no "simulated" badge**, because the dashboard derived simulation status from the owning subscription's current `test_clock_id` — a manual invoice has no subscription to look through, and the read-time lookup was a mutable snapshot that would also rot when a clock was unpinned. Fixed by persisting an authoritative `invoices.is_simulated` flag at **write time** (migration 0109): the engine stamps it when the subscription is clock-pinned (`sub.TestClockID`), the manual composer stamps it from the customer's `TestClockID`. The activity timeline, invoice header, and invoice list now render the badge from this flag — no re-derivation, no heuristic (per `feedback_no_heuristic_proxies`). The dead `SubscriptionClockReader` snapshot plumbing is removed. Separately, customer-notification emails (dispatched in real wall-clock time) were interleaved into the same chronological activity list as simulated billing events — so a "receipt sent" row at real-time "Jun 2" sorted against a finalize row at simulated "Nov 13", reading as out-of-order. They now render in their own real-time **"Notifications"** lane, keeping each time-domain internally coherent (email dispatch stays wall-clock — it is *not* clock-pinned to fake coherence). Two adjacent timestamp-segregation fixes from the same audit: `dunning_policy.created_at/updated_at` (operator config, not a billing event) flipped from `clock.Now(ctx)` to wall-clock so policy-edit history can't land in simulated time; and `SetPublicToken`'s `updated_at` aligned to SQL `now()` (operational metadata) to match `SetPaymentCard`. The boundary taxonomy (clock-pinned domain time vs wall-clock operational time, backend + UI) is codified in the ADR-030 addendum. Guarded by `TestManualInvoice_IsSimulatedFromCustomerPin` (pinned customer → `is_simulated=true` + simulated `issued_at` + round-trip; unpinned → false).

- **Manual (operator-composed) invoices now compute tax at finalize, and create atomically with their line items (2026-06-02).** An invoice built from the customer-detail composer finalized with `tax_amount_cents=0` regardless of the tenant's tax provider — tax was only ever computed during cycle billing, never for operator-composed drafts, so the composer's "Tax: calculated at finalize" label was aspirational. Now `invoice.Service.Finalize` computes tax for `billing_reason=manual` drafts before issuing, mirroring Stripe (tax is calculated when an invoice finalizes): provider `none` → tax 0; `manual` → flat rate; `stripe_tax` → a calculation parked `tax_status=pending` until committed. It reuses the existing `ApplyTaxToLineItems` machinery through a new draft-only `ComputeTaxForInvoice` — the operator "Retry tax" path keeps its `tax_status in (pending, failed)` gate, while the store's `UpdateTaxAtomic` now guards only the genuine invariant (**draft-only**; tax is frozen once finalized) rather than re-asserting the retry-specific status gate. Two adjacent improvements ship with it: (1) the composer creates the invoice **and all line items in one atomic `POST /v1/invoices`** (new optional `line_items` field) instead of create-then-loop-`add-line-item`, closing the partial-failure window where a mid-loop network drop left a draft with some-but-not-all lines; (2) a **Payment terms** control (Net 0/7/14/30/60 → `net_payment_term_days`, default 30) replaces the silent net-30 default. Also fixed a latent bug surfaced by the manual provider: `UpdateTaxAtomic` bound `tax_provider` / `tax_calculation_id` (both `NOT NULL DEFAULT ''`) via `NullableString`, mapping the manual provider's empty calculation id to SQL `NULL` and tripping the constraint — now bound raw, matching the INSERT path. Guarded by `TestManualInvoice_TaxComputedAtFinalize` ($33.33 + $33.33 + $33.34 @ 7.25% → `tax_amount_cents=725` with the per-line taxes reconciling to it exactly).

- **Cycle billing now prices multi-dimensional meters — the AI `tokens` meter no longer bills `$0` (2026-06-01, ADR-045).** `billOnePeriod` (the cycle / `POST /v1/billing/run` path) priced usage only via a meter's single linked `rating_rule_version_id`. A multi-dim meter (one meter, N rules matched on `{model, token_type}`) has no single linked rule — it's priced by `MeterPricingRule` rows resolved through `AggregateByPricingRules`, which only `create_preview` and the threshold scan used. So the cycle scan **skipped** the AI `tokens` meter entirely and emitted an empty invoice ("no billable lines"), even though `preview.go` claimed "the cycle scan calls the same path." Now `billOnePeriod` emits one invoice line per claimed pricing-rule bucket (input / output / cache_read / …), mirroring `previewMeter` exactly so preview == invoice; meters with no pricing rules keep the legacy single-rule path. Guarded by `TestLiteLLM_WedgeE2E`: a realistic LiteLLM payload (`claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022` + a prompt-cache hit) now rates to an exact invoice (1M input @ $3/M + 1M cache_read @ $0.30/M + 1M output @ $15/M = $18.30) — the CI test that would have caught the wedge breakage.

### Security

- **Account-lockout / failed-login throttling now stays enforced when Redis is unavailable or unconfigured (2026-06-01).** `POST /v1/auth/login` locks an account for 15 minutes after 5 consecutive failed attempts. The counter behind that threshold was wired to Redis **only when `REDIS_URL` was set**, and the service silently no-op'd otherwise — so in any deployment without Redis (and during a Redis outage in deployments that had it) the lockout never fired and dashboard login was unthrottled against password guessing. Fixed by making the failed-login counter **always-on**: a new `FallbackFailureCounter` serves from the shared Redis counter when healthy and transparently degrades to a process-local in-memory counter (per-instance window, lazily pruned, TTL = lockout duration) behind a circuit breaker that trips after 3 consecutive Redis errors and half-opens after 30s. It is now wired unconditionally at startup. The deliberate non-goal was the naive "fail closed → block every login when Redis is down" posture (that trades a brute-force gap for a self-inflicted outage); per OWASP ASVS, authentication controls degrade rather than fail open *or* hard-closed. The lock decision itself (`users.locked_until` in Postgres) was already the source of truth and is untouched by Redis state, so an already-locked account never silently unlocks during an outage. Behind N instances the effective global limit during a Redis outage is ~`threshold × N` — bounded and acceptable, versus the prior unbounded gap. The general/IP rate limiter keeps its existing fail-open-in-nonprod posture by design (a request-volume limiter is not an auth control). No config or API changes.

### Fixed

- **MANUAL_TEST.md audit remediation + anti-rot CI guard (2026-06-01).** A full audit of the manual-test runbook against live code found ~44 drift items (5 critical) — flows that *lied* about current behavior. Corrected the worst: FLOW A1 (account-lockout returns a generic 401, never a 429 — anti-enumeration; the prior 429 assertion was wrong), B10 (manual tax is a flat rate + `tax_status` exemption — the `tax_home_country` / cross-border zero-rating / `tax_rate_bp` / `tax_exempt` model was dropped), X7/P6/Troubleshooting (Stripe-tax failure *defers* to `tax_status=pending`, never charges $0; metric is `velox_tax_outcome_total{outcome="deferred"}`, not the removed `velox_tax_fallback_total`), D2 ("Manually resolved" dunning **full-voids** the invoice — not a no-op), B13 (idempotency replay → 409, not 200), B17 (unpaid prebill auto-relieved per #22), X15 (LiteLLM emits one `tokens` meter per ADR-044), TC9 (`PUT` pause-collection), B7/B21 (`bill_timing` rejection → 422), K1/K2/K4 (generic `invalid or expired API key` per ADR-026), R2/R3/R4 (recipe routes/counts), plus a cluster of contract literals (HTTP status / JSON keys / route verbs). Deleted FLOW D3 (a lying duplicate of TC5's policy-assignment coverage). **New guard:** `scripts/check-manual-test-currency.sh` (wired into the CI lint job + `make lint-manual-test`) fails the build if the runbook names a metric / column / table / meter-key the code no longer has — the cheap prose check CI was missing. Also corrected a stale `ErrAccountLocked` code comment that still claimed a 429 mapping.

- **Migration `0097` down now recreates `customer_payment_setups` instead of no-op'ing, restoring full rollback reversibility (2026-06-01).** `0097`'s up drops the table, but its down was `SELECT 1`. A full `down`-then-`up` left the table missing, so the reverse-order downs of the migrations that built it — `0021` (set_livemode trigger), `0020` (livemode column + RLS), `0015` (explicit-RESTRICT FKs) — and the re-up of the `0095`/`0096` backfills all failed with `relation "customer_payment_setups" does not exist`. That reddened `TestMigrationRoundTrip` and `TestNoTxMigration_GINIndexBuilt` (the integration `test` CI job). The down now restores the v0096 schema verbatim (empty; the data already lived in `customers.stripe_customer_id` + `payment_methods`), matching the `0081`/`0082`/`0083` drop-migrations. Internal/CI only — no runtime behavior change.

- **Dashboard production build restored to zero errors + CI now gates on it (2026-05-31).** The production build (`npm run build` = `tsc -b && vite build`, strict `tsconfig.app.json`) had accumulated **63 TypeScript errors** while CI stayed green — because CI ran the *looser* `npx tsc --noEmit` (root config) plus `vite build` (which strips types without checking). That gap let real bugs land invisibly. Fixed all 63 at the root (no `@ts-ignore`/`as any`/suppressions) and switched CI's frontend step to `npm run build` so the strict build is the gate going forward. Notable **genuine bugs** found inside the noise, not just type hygiene:
  - **Invoice "paid" detection was broken** (`InvoiceDetail.tsx` ×5, `Portal.tsx` ×2). Gates compared `payment_status === 'paid'`, but the domain enum has **no `paid`** — a paid invoice is `payment_status === 'succeeded'`. The comparisons never matched; the "Collect Payment"/amount-due UI and the customer portal's **outstanding-balance** filter + payment badge were relying on an always-true clause (accidentally saved only by a co-`amount_due > 0` guard). A prior partial fix had corrected some sites (`Portal.tsx:1021`) but missed others — completed the migration. (`InvoiceDetail` errored under `tsc -b`; `Portal` did not, because it uses a looser local `payment_status: string` — same bug, caught by exhaustive grep.)
  - **Hosted-invoice pay button crashed on failure** (`HostedInvoice.tsx`). The payment catch called `setError(...)`, but `error` was a derived `const`, never a setter — a failed payment attempt threw `ReferenceError: setError is not defined` and showed nothing. Added a dedicated `payError` state, reset on retry, set on failure, rendered inline by the pay button (kept separate from the full-page invoice-load error shell).
  - **Double currency symbol** on the invoice-attention amount-due label (`InvoiceAttention.tsx`): `getCurrencySymbol(c) + formatCents(amount, …)` rendered `$$10.00`, because `formatCents` already prepends the symbol. Now `formatCents(amount, invoice.currency)` (single, correct-currency symbol).
  - **Undefined references that would crash on use**: `CreditNote` type unimported (`InvoiceDetail.tsx`), `toast` unimported (`Invoices.tsx`).
  - **`showApiError(err)` missing its required fallback message** (4 sites in `SendSetupLinkDialog` / `CustomerDetail`) — errors would surface without a user-facing message.
  - **`Record<AttentionAction, string>` missing the `update_payment_method` key** (`InvoiceAttention.tsx`).
  - **Systemic `asChild` → Base UI `render` prop** (~21 sites across 13 files). The dashboard uses Base UI (`@base-ui/react`), which has no Radix-style `asChild`; `<Button asChild><a/></Button>` and `<TooltipTrigger asChild><span/>` were non-functional. Rewritten to the established `render={<el … />}` form (matches `ui/alert-dialog.tsx`, `ui/dialog.tsx`).
  - **OpenAPI `InvoiceStatus` enum was missing `uncollectible`** — the backend emits it (a dunning policy can give up collecting) but the published contract omitted it, so the generated type rejected a valid state. Added to `api/openapi.yaml` + regenerated bindings.
  - Plus dead-import cleanup across `Dunning`, `Credits`, `CreditNotes`, `TestClocks`, `MeterDetail`, etc.

- **Dashboard `<Select>` triggers show the option label, not the raw value/ID (2026-05-31).** The dashboard wraps Base UI (`@base-ui/react/select`), whose `<Select.Value>` renders the **raw selected value** by default — unlike Radix, it does not auto-extract the chosen `<SelectItem>`'s text. So every picker where the value differed from its label showed the wrong thing: plan pickers (Change Plan / Add Item) and the rating-rule / dunning-policy / test-clock pickers showed opaque IDs (`vlx_pln_…`); enum pickers (pricing model, aggregation, billing interval, bill timing, status, final action, currency, line type) showed the raw code (`in_arrears`, `sum`, `add_on`) instead of the friendly label. Fixed app-wide using Base UI's idiomatic **`items` prop** (`<Select items={[{value,label}]}>`), which makes `<SelectValue>` resolve the label automatically — with a single source of truth per select (a shared label helper for dynamic lists, a `const X_OPTIONS` reused for both `items` and the rendered `<SelectItem>`s for static enums). Covers 8 files: `SubscriptionDetail`, `Pricing`, `MeterDetail`, `PlanDetail`, `InvoiceDetail`, `DunningPolicies`, `CustomerDetail` (`Customers`' test-clock picker already used the equivalent `<SelectValue>` render-fn and was left as-is). Reported on the Change Plan dialog showing `vlx_pln_d8e3a7jmajdheo6c4al0` in the trigger.

- **ADR-043 `tax_rate_bp` → `tax_rate` migration finished across the contract + remaining UI (2026-05-31).** The commit that dropped the columns (`9baf785`) missed five `tax_rate_bp` references the dev server silently tolerated (vite strips types without checking; only the production `tsc -b` build — and, for one case, a real runtime bug — surfaced them):
  - `web-v2/src/pages/Settings.tsx` — inline tax-example preview referenced the dropped `form.tax_rate_bp` in three spots; converted to `tax_rate` (bp = `tax_rate * 100` in the inclusive/exclusive example math).
  - `web-v2/src/pages/InvoiceDetail.tsx` — tax summary row read `invoice.tax_rate_bp / 100`; now `invoice.tax_rate` directly (it is already a decimal percent).
  - `web-v2/src/pages/HostedInvoice.tsx` — **silent runtime bug**, not a compile error: the page's local payload type still declared `tax_rate_bp`, so `invoice.tax_rate_bp` was `undefined` against the backend's `tax_rate` field and the rate parenthetical (`(18.50%)`) never rendered on customer-facing hosted invoices. Type + render fixed.
  - `api/openapi.yaml` — the published contract still advertised `tax_rate_bp` on the `Invoice` and `InvoiceLineItem` schemas (required + property) while the backend serialized `tax_rate`. Replaced with `tax_rate` (`number`/`double`, percent), and regenerated the Go (`internal/api/generated/api.gen.go`) and TypeScript (`web-v2/src/lib/api.gen.ts`) bindings via `make gen`. `tax_rate_bp` now appears nowhere in the repo.

- **Billing cycle / catchup invoice creation repaired + clock-catchup made loop-proof (2026-05-31).** A regression from ADR-043 (`9baf785`) left the three `invoice_line_items` INSERTs in `internal/invoice/postgres.go` with a column/placeholder mismatch — when `tax_rate_bp` was removed, the column name and Go arg were dropped but a trailing `$23` placeholder stayed in `VALUES` (22 columns, 22 args, 23 placeholders) → `ERROR: INSERT has more expressions than target columns (SQLSTATE 42601)`. **Every** cycle-close, test-clock-catchup, and one-off invoice creation failed. It slipped through because `go build` doesn't validate SQL strings and `go test -short` skips the integration tests that exercise real INSERTs against postgres. Fixed all three; audited all five INSERTs in the file (the two `invoices` INSERTs were already balanced). **Defense-in-depth:** `RunCycleForClock`'s outer loop re-fetched due subs every pass — a sub that fails to bill never advances `next_billing_at`, so it stayed perpetually "due" and was re-billed in a tight ~34/sec loop that pegged CPU and flooded `tax_calculations` with orphan rows; worse, because `RunCycleForClock` never returned, the worker never reached `MarkFailed`, so the clock stayed `advancing` and was re-enqueued on every boot. Now each sub is attempted at most once per catchup call; when no due sub can make progress the loop breaks and the worker marks the clock `internal_failure` (operator's "Retry advance" resumes once the cause is fixed). Verified e2e: invoice + catchup integration tests pass; a live run went from 272 failed-bills/8s to 0, the stuck 8h-`advancing` clock completed to `ready`, and `tax_calculations` growth dropped from ~150/8s to 2/8s.

- **Invoice line-item period sub-line no longer lies "(in advance)" on partial cycles (2026-05-31).** Pre-fix `web-v2/src/pages/InvoiceDetail.tsx` hard-coded `(in advance)` whenever a line item's `billing_period_*` differed from the invoice header's period — based on the assumption that period mismatch only happens under ADR-031's `in_advance` base on a mixed invoice. But period mismatch has multiple legitimate causes: partial cycle from mid-period subscription activation, segment-aware billing under plan changes, and (yes) `in_advance` base mixed with elapsed-period usage. Surfaced by an `in_arrears` Pro plan invoice where the subscription activated mid-period — line's `period_start` was ~11h later than the invoice header's, dashboard rendered "(in advance)" despite the plan being `in_arrears`. Fix: drop the parenthetical label; the explicit "Covers <start> – <end>" dates convey what the line covers without us guessing the cause. Comment updated to reflect the multi-cause reality.

### Removed

- **`tax_rate_bp` columns dropped immediately — no transition window (2026-05-31, ADR-043).** ADR-042 added `tax_rate NUMERIC(7,4)` alongside the legacy `tax_rate_bp bigint` with the standard "add + populate + switch readers + drop later" migration pattern. The dual-column state is the right shape for production systems with staged rollouts — but Velox has zero deployments, single local DB, single binary, no mid-deploy mix. Per `feedback_no_belt_and_suspenders` + `feedback_pre_launch_scoping`, the dual-column state was textbook debt: code complexity of two storage shapes without the staged-rollout benefit. Cut now while there's no production behind us. Migration 0105 drops `tax_rate_bp` from `invoices`, `invoice_line_items`, `tenant_settings`. All Go domain types lose the `TaxRateBP` field. `tax.Result.EffectiveRateBP` / `tax.ResultLine.TaxRateBP` / `tax.Breakdown.RateBP` all removed; only `Rate` / `TaxRate` / `EffectiveRate` `float64` fields remain. `engine.TaxApplication.TaxRateBP` removed. Postgres store simplified: ~10 SQL statements lose one column each. `subscription.ProrationTaxResult.TaxRateBP`, `creditnote.OriginalInvoiceInfo.TaxRateBP`, `hostedinvoice.InvoicePayload.TaxRateBP` all become `TaxRate float64`. PDF renderers print decimal directly (`%.4g%%`). TypeScript types: `tax_rate_bp` → `tax_rate`. Frontend Settings → Tax rate input takes decimal percent directly (`8.875`) instead of bp-as-integer with multiply-by-100 dance. **`ManualProvider`** constructor switches from `rateBP int64` to `rate float64`; internal math uses parts-per-million scaling (`× ratePPM / 1_000_000` where `ratePPM = int64(math.Round(rate × 10000))`) preserving 4-decimal precision in integer arithmetic without float drift. Migration 0104's backfill data is preserved (the NUMERIC column was already authoritative); the down migration of 0105 recreates `tax_rate_bp` from `tax_rate` for symmetry. **Pattern recorded in ADR-043:** at zero deployments, "keep legacy during transition" wording in PRs is a code smell — the window never ends. Migrate-and-drop in one motion when there's no staged-rollout cost.

### Changed

- **Canonical AI token-metering model: one `tokens` meter + `token_type` dimension, replacing the two-meter LiteLLM shape (2026-06-01, ADR-044).** The `anthropic_style`/`openai_style` recipes priced tokens on one `tokens` meter via `operation`+boolean `cached` dimensions, but the LiteLLM ingestion mapper emitted *two* meters (`tokens_input`/`tokens_output`) with no role dimension — so LiteLLM-ingested usage never rated against the recipe rules and the AI-native wedge demo couldn't bill end-to-end. Verified industry research (Lago, OpenMeter, Orb, Metronome converge on one dimensional token meter; OpenAI/Anthropic itemization sets the role floor) settled the canonical shape: **one `tokens` meter; token role on a `token_type` dimension** (`input`, `output`, `cache_read`, `cache_write_5m`, `cache_write_1h`); `model`/`provider` dimensions; matrix pricing on `{model, token_type}`. A boolean `cached` is provably insufficient — Anthropic prices cache-read (0.1×), 5-minute cache-write (1.25×) and 1-hour cache-write (2×) as three distinct rates. Changes: both recipes rewritten (`operation`→`token_type`, boolean `cached` → disjoint cache-role values, dropped the `priority=200` cached-wins hack since roles no longer overlap; `anthropic_style` now carries full 5-role parity per model); the LiteLLM mapper emits one `tokens` meter with `token_type` (input/output now — cache-token parsing is a fast-follow once the payload exposes `prompt_tokens_details`/`cache_creation`, normalized to additive-disjoint quantities at the mapper). No schema migration (dimensions are free-form JSONB; pre-launch, no live data). Provider mappers own all role normalization; the rating engine never does role arithmetic. Supersedes ADR-033's two-meter mapping.

- **Canceling a subscription with an UNPAID prebilled (in-advance) invoice now settles that invoice to the consumed portion instead of chasing the full amount (2026-06-01, ADR-031 amendment).** When an in-advance plan is canceled mid-period, the unused-time relief depends on whether the invoice for that period was paid. The paid case (credit the unused amount to the customer's balance) is unchanged. The **unpaid** case previously did nothing — the full-period invoice stayed open and rode the dunning path, so a customer who canceled on day 3 of a 30-day prebilled period was still pursued for all 30 days (a behavior no major billing platform endorses). Now `BillOnCancel` settles the unpaid invoice itself: **nothing consumed** (canceled at/near period start, nothing paid) → the invoice is **voided** (full tax reversal); **partially consumed** → an **adjustment credit note** reduces `amount_due` down to the consumed portion (the unused base is grossed up by the invoice's tax ratio so the unused portion's tax is reversed too); a partial payment present → reduce only (never void collected money). No customer-balance credit is granted on the unpaid path (no cash was funded). Verified across Stripe / Orb / Lago / Chargebee, which converge on "settle to consumed, never the full amount, never an unfunded credit." The consumed-portion residual stays collectible via the normal dunning path. Hardcoded default for v1 (no per-tenant Skip/Reduce/Void/Refund setting yet). Wires via two new engine seams: `SetInvoiceVoider` (invoice.Service) and `SetCreditNoteAdjuster` (creditnote.Service).

- **Tax-rate precision upgrade + proration integer day-ratio (2026-05-31, ADR-042).** Closes two HIGH-severity gaps from the 2026-05-31 financial-precision audit (B7.3 + B7.4 on the roadmap).
  - **Tax rate storage now NUMERIC(7,4)** matching Stripe Tax's 4-decimal precision. Pre-fix `tax_rate_bp bigint` (0.01% precision) silently truncated NYC 8.875% to 8.88%, Quebec QST 9.975% to 9.97%, Hawaii GET 4.7120% to 4.71%, and made Tennessee local sub-rates at 0.25% precision unrepresentable. Migration 0104 adds `tax_rate NUMERIC(7,4)` columns to `invoices`, `invoice_line_items`, `tenant_settings`, backfilled from `tax_rate_bp / 100`. `tax_rate_bp` columns retained for backward compat during transition; future migration drops once readers are confirmed switched.
  - **Stripe ingestion parses `percentage_decimal` precisely** via new `internal/tax/stripe.go:parseStripeRate`. Pre-fix the call site did `int64(v * 100)` (truncate toward zero), losing the trailing 0.005% on Stripe's `"8.875"`. Now returns the precise float for the NUMERIC column AND the banker's-rounded bp for legacy compat.
  - **Domain types gain `TaxRate float64` fields** on `Invoice`, `InvoiceLineItem`, `InvoiceDiscountUpdate`, `InvoiceTaxRetryUpdate`. `tax.Result.EffectiveRate` and `tax.ResultLine.TaxRate` carry the precise float from provider. `ManualProvider` populates from `rateBP / 100` (manual-entered rates stay bp-precision pending operator-UI follow-up).
  - **Engine threads `TaxRate` through `TaxApplication`** → invoice rows + line items. `internal/invoice/postgres.go` reads + writes both `tax_rate_bp` and `tax_rate` on all INSERT/UPDATE statements (8 call sites updated). `tenant_settings` derives `tax_rate = tax_rate_bp::numeric / 100` at the SQL boundary (operator UI unchanged).
  - **Proration math switches from `float64` factor to integer day-ratio.** Pre-fix `internal/subscription/handler.go` used `prorationFactor float64` (hours / 24, divided again) and `diff * prorationFactor` then `math.RoundToEven` — introduced ULP error on large amounts and was non-deterministic across architectures. Industry peers (Stripe Billing, Lago, Orb) all use integer day-ratio. Velox's engine path already used this pattern (`engine.go:655`); the subscription handler path had drifted. Fix: `remainingPeriodFactor` → `remainingPeriodRatio` returning `(remainingDays, totalDays int64)`. `itemProrationSpec.prorationFactor` → `remainingDays, totalDays int64`. Atomic add/update/remove proration signatures take the two int64s. The cents math becomes `money.RoundHalfToEven((newAmount-oldAmount) * spec.remainingDays, spec.totalDays)` — integer math, banker's rounding, deterministic. `ProrationDetail.ProrationFactor` public field preserved as derived `float64` for downstream display.
  - **What's tested via FLOW B2 (updated in this commit):** rate stored at full precision (NYC 8.875% case); 8.875% × $100 invoice → exact `tax_amount_cents=888` with `tax_rate=8.8750`; 3-line $33.33+$33.33+$33.34 still residual-absorbs to exact invoice tax.
  - **Backward compat:** dashboard/PDF rendering continues to work without UI changes. Operator Settings → Tax rate input still accepts basis points; follow-up cuts the decimal-input UI (~30 LOC).
  - **Industry refs:** Stripe Tax Rate API, Lago BigDecimal, Chargebee multi-decimal, Recurly TaxInfo (all cited in ADR-042).
  - **Out of scope for this cut, queued for follow-up:** B7.1/B7.2 currency precision table + ISO 4217 full coverage (latent 100× JPY bug — blocks any non-USD tenant); B7.5 cosmetic polish of `float64(.../100)` display strings in credit / credit-note error messages; operator UI decimal-input.

### Fixed

- **Cancel + plan-swap proration distinguishes "no invoice" from "lookup failed" (2026-05-30).** Two call sites in `internal/billing/engine.go` (BillOnCancel ~line 3230, BillOnPlanSwapImmediate ~line 3356) called `FindBaseInvoiceForPeriod` and on ANY error logged `WARN ... source in_advance invoice not found; skipping credit grant` then `return 0, nil`. Conflated two distinct cases: (a) legitimately no in_advance invoice for the period (customer was never billed, e.g. trial cancel) — skip is correct; (b) transient lookup error (DB blip, contention) — silently shortchanges the customer by the unused-portion refund credit they were owed, with no signal to the operator. Fix: `errors.Is(lookupErr, errs.ErrNotFound)` → log INFO + skip (the legitimate path); any other error → return wrapped error so the caller fails the proration flow rather than silently producing wrong customer balance. Per `feedback_no_silent_fallbacks`: fail loud on uncertain-answer paths in money flows.

- **StartDunning failure no longer silently drops the dunning run on transient blips (2026-05-30).** Two call sites in `internal/payment/stripe.go` — the inline-after-known-failed-charge path (line ~423) and the `payment_intent.payment_failed` webhook handler (line ~727) — previously logged `WARN failed to start dunning` and continued, with the dismissive trailing comment *"Non-fatal: invoice is already marked failed, dunning can be started manually."* Pre-launch reality: the operator gets no signal beyond the WARN line, and the invoice sits in `payment_status=failed` with no dunning run, so no auto-retries fire and revenue silently leaks. Both call sites now route through a new `startDunningWithRetry` helper with bounded inline retry (3 attempts, 0/100ms/500ms backoff). StartDunning is already idempotent by invoice (migration 0085 UNIQUE on `dunning_runs`), so the retry is safe — a slow concurrent caller resolves to the existing row, not a duplicate. The bounded retry absorbs the typical transient case (DB connection hiccup, brief contention). Persistent failures (Stripe outage, sustained DB unavailability) bubble out as the helper's wrapped error; both call sites now log at `slog.Error` (not WARN) with a structured message naming the operator-action path *"dunning will NOT auto-retry; operator must start manually from invoice attention banner"* — alertable signal. **Out of scope for this cut**: a proper PaymentFailed-without-dunning-run reconciler scanner (the long-term fix for non-transient failures). Documented in the design-debt roadmap; webhook handler's "always return 200 to Stripe" + event-level dedup at `IngestEvent` mean the agent's first-pass "return error → Stripe retries" suggestion doesn't actually work in this codebase. Inline retry is the highest-leverage fix that respects the existing architecture.

- **Invoice-finalize email moved out of the detached goroutine (2026-05-30).** Pre-fix: `internal/invoice/handler.go:475-527` rendered the invoice PDF and enqueued the customer email inside `go func() { … }()` bounded to 60s with a `context.WithoutCancel`-detached ctx. Original motivation was keeping the HTTP response fast (PDF render is ~1-3s CPU-bound). Same shape as the receipt-email + payment-failed-email goroutines fixed in Phase 2 — and same bug class: a transient failure (DB blip on customer lookup, line-item fetch, render error, outbox INSERT failure) disappeared past the goroutine's WARN/ERROR log line with no observable signal to the operator. With the always-on outbox path (ADR-040), `SendInvoice` is a fast DB INSERT once the PDF is rendered; the dispatcher owns delivery + retry. Operator finalize is interactive (one click → 200 response), so ~2s render latency inline is an acceptable trade for observable enqueue failure. Cross-flow audit confirmed this was the last surviving non-test detached goroutine around money-adjacent flows in the codebase. Fix: inline the customer lookup, line-item fetch, RenderPDF, and SendInvoice call. Failure logs WARN (or ERROR for enqueue failure) — invoice is already durably finalized + customer can fetch PDF from the portal.

- **Cycle close fails loud on item-change-log or segment-plan-lookup failure (2026-05-30).** Two silent-skip paths in `internal/billing/engine.go` removed. Pre-fix at line 1724: `ListItemChangesInPeriod` failure logged `WARN list item changes failed; falling back to single-line cycle close billing` and set `itemChanges = nil`. A sub that actually had a mid-period plan/quantity change would then bill as if it had no change — wrong amount on the invoice. Pre-fix at line 1745: failure to load a plan referenced by the change log (`GetPlan` returned an error for `FromPlanID` or `ToPlanID`) logged `WARN segment plan lookup failed; segment under that plan will be skipped` and dropped the segment from the invoice. End state: invoice missing one or more line items, undercharging the customer. Per `feedback_no_silent_fallbacks`, both paths now return the error to the per-sub handler; the engine's per-sub error isolation (other subs in the cycle continue) is unchanged. The cost-of-failure trade is correct invoice or no invoice (operator can retry), not wrong invoice + silent log line.

- **Credit-application failure no longer silently overcharges the customer (2026-05-30).** Pre-fix: a transient DB error from `e.credits.ApplyToInvoiceAt` during cycle close would log `WARN failed to apply credits` and continue execution. The downstream auto-charge block would then call Stripe with the PRE-CREDIT amount (`totalWithTax`), charging the customer the full sticker price while their credit balance stayed untouched in the ledger. End state: customer overcharged by exactly their credit balance; operator never sees a signal until the customer complains. The credit ledger and the invoice's `amount_due_cents` were both atomic-unchanged by `ApplyToInvoiceAt`'s failure (correct by itself), but nothing gated the subsequent charge on that failure. Caught in the 2026-05-30 design-debt audit. Fix at `internal/billing/engine.go:2245-2275`: a `creditApplyOK` flag tracks the apply outcome; on failure the engine calls `SetAutoChargePending(true)` and the MarkPaid + auto-charge blocks (engine.go:2281, 2309) are gated on the flag — so the cycle still advances (the invoice is durably persisted) but no charge fires until the next `RetryPendingCharges` tick re-applies credits atomically with the charge. Same shape as the auto-charge-failed handling at engine.go:2325. Pre-launch with zero DPs, no customer was actually overcharged; this is proactive correctness.

### Removed

- **Tax `fallback_manual` policy removed — block-only post-migration (2026-05-30, ADR-041).** Migration 0039 had introduced `tenant_settings.tax_on_failure` with two values, defaulting new tenants to `block` but auto-setting all existing tenants to `fallback_manual` to "preserve behavior at migration time." The 2026-05-30 design-debt audit found this was the last surviving silent-fallback path in the engine: when `ManualProvider` runs as a fallback and no manual rate matches the customer's jurisdiction, it returns **zero tax** — silently producing a different answer than the operator intended (charge SOME tax) without an actionable signal. Lago wiki-style framing: "fall back to my manual rate" is what operators thought they were buying; "fall back to zero" is what they actually got for every jurisdiction they hadn't pre-configured. Per `feedback_no_silent_fallbacks` + `feedback_no_belt_and_suspenders`, the path is debt — TaxRetrier already handles transient Stripe failures (the legitimate use case) without the silent-zero edge case.
  - **Cut**: `handleFailure` in `internal/tax/stripe.go` always returns the error; the `p.fallback *ManualProvider` field and constructor parameter removed. `NewStripeTaxProvider(clients)` now takes only the resolver. `OnFailureFallbackManual` constant removed; `OnFailureBlock` is the only valid `Request.OnFailure` value. `internal/tax/resolver.go` Resolve returns an explicit error when `tax_provider=stripe_tax` is set without a wired Stripe client — operators wanting manual must select `tax_provider=manual` at the tenant level. `internal/tenant/settings.go` validation accepts only `block`. `internal/domain/audit.go` `TaxOnFailure` comment updated. Prometheus metric `velox_tax_outcome_total` no longer emits the `outcome="fallback"` label.
  - **Migration 0103** sets every tenant currently at `fallback_manual` to `block` and tightens the CHECK constraint to `tax_on_failure = 'block'`. The column itself stays for forward-compat (future failure-handling shapes can reuse it without another migration).
  - **Test rewritten**: `stripe_tax_without_clients_falls_back_to_manual` flipped to `stripe_tax_without_clients_errors_post_ADR_041` — asserts the loud-error behavior is the new contract.
  - **Revisit trigger**: a signed DP names "Stripe preferred, MY configured manual rate as fallback for jurisdictional gaps" — but the rebuild must add a no-rate-match-then-block guard so the silent-zero edge case doesn't return. Until then, block-only.

### Removed

- **Outbox env flags cut — outbox is the only path (2026-05-30, ADR-040).** `VELOX_WEBHOOK_OUTBOX_ENABLED` and `VELOX_EMAIL_OUTBOX_ENABLED` shipped as migration escape hatches when the outboxes were introduced. Each flag controlled BOTH producer wiring (`OutboxSender` ↔ `*email.Sender`, `OutboxDispatcher` ↔ direct `Service.Dispatch`) AND dispatcher worker startup — so flipping either to `false` silently downgraded the call site's contract from "durable + retried" to "one-shot synchronous; lost on transient failure," with no signal at the call site. Per `feedback_no_silent_fallbacks` + `feedback_no_belt_and_suspenders`, the "off" path violated both principles: same line of code, different correctness; outbox failure modes (DB unreachable, dispatcher crashed) are NOT independent of direct-send failure modes (SMTP/HTTP unreachable, sender crashed), so neither can rescue the other. Pre-launch with zero customers + no DP asking for the flag, the cost of carrying it was halved test surface area, dual doc shapes, and a real testability block (FLOW E7 couldn't test "dispatcher stopped, row sits pending" because the same flag also disabled producer enqueue).
  - **Cut**: `os.Getenv("VELOX_WEBHOOK_OUTBOX_ENABLED")` + `os.Getenv("VELOX_EMAIL_OUTBOX_ENABLED")` parsing in `internal/api/router.go:249-256, 475-519` collapses to unconditional `OutboxDispatcher` / `OutboxSender` wiring. The seven typed email interface variables flatten from `var X type; if … { X = a } else { X = b }` to inline-initialized one-liners. Boot WARN/INFO logs ("outbox DISABLED — using legacy direct-dispatch path" / "outbox enabled — producers will enqueue…") gone. `Server.OutboxEnabled` and `Server.EmailOutboxEnabled` fields removed. `cmd/velox/main.go:234-255` `if server.OutboxEnabled { … }` and `if server.EmailOutboxEnabled { … }` wrappers gone — both dispatcher workers start unconditionally. `.env.example:168-175` flag block deleted. `internal/domain` import in `router.go` becomes unused (the only consumer was `var eventDispatcher domain.EventDispatcher = webhookOutSvc`) and is removed.
  - **What runtime concerns the flag was supposedly addressing — and how each is actually solved**:
    - *Multi-replica safety*: already handled by the dispatcher's advisory-lock gating (`LockKeyWebhookDispatcher` / `LockKeyEmailDispatcher` in `internal/platform/postgres/advisory_lock.go`). One claimant drains, others sleep. Flag was duplicative.
    - *Emergency runtime pause*: `SELECT pg_advisory_lock(76540004);` from any psql session holds the email dispatcher lock until released. No restart required. Same for the webhook lock key. These are the canonical runtime pause primitives.
    - *Separate worker / API binary*: a deployment topology decision (split into `cmd/velox` API mode + a future `cmd/velox-worker` dispatcher-only mode), not a feature flag. Defer until a DP names a need.
    - *Local dev quiet*: no traffic = no rows = quiet dispatcher (5s tick claims nothing).
  - **What stays**: `*email.Sender` (the direct-SMTP client) and `webhook.Service.Dispatch` (the direct dispatcher entry) — but only the dispatcher worker calls them now. That's their real purpose: convert an outbox row into an actual SMTP send / HTTP POST. Outbox tables, migrations, DLQ, the dispatcher itself, the advisory-lock primitives — all unchanged.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW E7 updated**: replaced the unrunnable "stop the dispatcher" verb with two real techniques — (a) the 5s polling-window observation (fire webhook → query within 100ms for `pending`, wait 5-10s, re-query for `dispatched`), and (b) the determinism variant using `pg_advisory_lock(76540004)` to pause the dispatcher cluster-wide from an external psql session.
  - **In-code references updated**: `internal/payment/stripe.go` comment block describing the receipt-email path no longer mentions the flag; `internal/email/outbox_integration_test.go` comment describes the contract as the always-on production wiring per ADR-040.
  - **Revisit trigger**: a DP names a use case where producer enqueue must be skipped cluster-wide (e.g. compliance regime prohibiting transient PII storage), OR a binary split is shipped and one side needs to know its role. Until then "outbox on" is an invariant.
  - **Net change**: ~85 lines deleted, ~25 added (the simpler unconditional wiring + the new comment blocks). Plus ADR-040 + this CHANGELOG entry.

- **Coupons cut completely pre-launch (2026-05-30, ADR-039).** Two rounds of industry research validated that coupons are a SaaS-era promotional construct vestigial for Velox's AI-native positioning. Traditional SaaS peers (Stripe Billing, Chargebee, Recurly, Lago) ship coupons as table-stakes with zero load-bearing customer-evidence in case studies. AI-native peers diverge sharply: Metronome ships no coupon product, Orb subordinates them to "adjustments," Lago's own AI billing pages explicitly recommend **credits over coupons** for usage-based billing, and Stripe Token Billing (their newest AI-native product) doesn't mention coupons at all. Lago wiki verbatim: *"A coupon is not a refund. It's an engagement to discount future invoices."* Velox already ships the better primitive — event-sourced credit ledger (`internal/credit`) with prepaid allowances, manual grants, three-channel CN allocation, atomic apply-to-invoice. Coupons duplicate the discount-intent surface without adding capability the credit ledger lacks.
  - **Code deleted**: `internal/coupon/` (package, store, service, handler, errors, tests); `internal/api/coupon_idempotency_e2e_test.go`; `internal/creditnote/service_coupon_void_test.go`; `web-v2/src/pages/Coupons.tsx`; `web-v2/src/pages/CouponDetail.tsx`; `docs/coupons-semantics.md`. ~2k lines net.
  - **Surface removed**: `/v1/coupons*`, `/v1/customers/{id}/coupon`, `/v1/invoices/{id}/apply-coupon`. Dashboard nav entry, command-palette entry, `CustomerDetail.tsx` Active Discount card + `AssignCouponDialog`, `InvoiceDetail.tsx` Apply Coupon button + `ApplyCouponDialog`. All `Coupon*` TypeScript types.
  - **Engine hooks removed**: `CouponApplier` interface, `SetCouponApplier`, `RedeemForInvoice`, `MarkPeriodsApplied`, `MarkCustomerDiscountPeriodsApplied`, `ApplyCouponToInvoice`, redemption-tracking arrays in cycle close + threshold scan. Proration coupon applier from `internal/subscription`. Credit-note coupon-redemption voider.
  - **Metric removed**: `RecordCouponRedemption` + `velox_coupon_redemptions_total` counter.
  - **Audit / webhook constants removed**: `AuditActionApplyCoupon`, 8 `EventCoupon*` / `EventCustomerCoupon*` / `EventInvoiceCouponApplied` constants.
  - **Schema NOT dropped**: `coupons` / `coupon_redemptions` / `customer_discounts` tables and migrations 0025 / 0042-0046 left in place per `feedback_no_speculative_backfill` — destructive drops have asymmetric risk pre-launch, the tables are cheap to keep, and a future rebuild starts from existing schema if a DP names a coupon use case.
  - **Revisit trigger**: first DP names a load-bearing promo-code use case (referral codes, Black Friday, annual prepay discount). Until then the credit ledger covers every observed discount intent.
  - **README** updated: coupons removed from shipped-primitives list, credit ledger highlighted as the discount mechanism.
  - **MANUAL_TEST** FLOW C3 replaced with a placeholder pointing at ADR-039.
  - **Pre-launch local DBs only** — production never ran the coupon code. Pre-cut audit_log rows carrying `action=apply_coupon` remain readable but render as unknown action types in the dashboard.
  - **Phase B roadmap** for the AI-native primitives (LLM provider cost-table ingestion, embeddable cost dashboard, commits + draw-down, price-book versioning) drafted in `docs/roadmap-ai-native-2026.md`.

### Changed

- **Velox→Stripe customer sync gap-closure, phase 2 (2026-05-29).** Three follow-on gaps closed in the same session as phase 1:
