  - **Receipt email + payment-failed email now use the outbox retry path inline (no detached goroutine).** `payment.Stripe.handlePaymentSucceeded` and `handlePaymentFailed` previously fired email sends inside `go func() { … }()` with a fresh detached ctx — a pattern that was originally introduced to outlast slow direct-SMTP sends, but voided every retry guarantee: a transient Postmark 5xx or SMTP timeout silently dropped the email past the goroutine's `slog.Error` log line. With the outbox-enabled deployment (`receiptEmail` is `*email.OutboxSender`), `SendPaymentReceipt` / `SendPaymentFailed` is a fast DB INSERT — there's no slow SMTP to detach from, and the dispatcher's retry loop owns delivery. Failure logs but doesn't fail the webhook (payment state already committed; returning an error would re-fire `MarkPaid` + double-fire the customer-facing event). Both call sites changed in one pass per the cross-flow audit pattern. Removed unused `internal/platform/postgres` import from `stripe.go`.
  - **Tax-calculation expiry guard at CommitTax.** Stripe Tax calculations are valid for 24h after creation; the operator-facing draft-then-finalize path (`invoice.Service.Finalize` → `engine.CommitTax`) could hold a draft past expiry, then silently fail at `tax_transaction.CreateFromCalculation` and leave the invoice with `tax_calculation_id` populated but no `tax_transaction_id` — Stripe Tax reporting silently broken for that invoice. New `TaxCalculationWriter.LookupCalculationCreatedAt(tenantID, invoiceID, providerRef)` reads the audit row's `created_at`; `CommitTax` returns `errs.InvalidState("tax calculation expired (age X, max 23h) — retry tax to refresh, then finalize")` before calling Stripe. 23h cap (1h safety buffer below Stripe's 24h). Engine-internal cycle-close paths (`billOnePeriod`, `subscription_create`) Calculate→CreateInvoice→CommitTax in microseconds — guard never trips there. Tests without `SetTaxCalculationStore` are unaffected (early-return).
  - **Stripe Customer `tax_ids[]` reconcile.** Velox stores a single `(tax_id, tax_id_type)` on `customer_billing_profiles`; Stripe stores a collection keyed by an `txi_*` ID. Pre-fix, the Stripe Dashboard's Tax IDs tab was permanently empty even when the operator had filled in VAT/GST. Phase-2 closure: `StripeBillingSync.reconcileTaxIDs` lists existing tax_ids → deletes any that don't match the operator's current (type, value) → creates if not present. Idempotent (re-running with the same desired pair is a no-op). Empty desired = clear all. Fires automatically from `SyncBillingProfile` after every billing-profile update. `paymentmethods.StripeAdapter.EnsureStripeCustomer` additionally seeds `TaxIDData` on the create call so a brand-new Stripe Customer never shows an empty Tax IDs tab. Best-effort: failures bubble up from `SyncBillingProfile` (treated as the rest of the customer-sync failure mode — logged WARN, doesn't unwind the local commit).
- **Velox→Stripe customer sync gap-closure, phase 1 (2026-05-29).** Industry-research baseline (Lago + Recurly + Chargebee + Metronome docs + Stripe's own integration guidance): every platform that uses Stripe as the payment rail pushes Velox-side mutations to the Stripe Customer object on every write, best-effort. Failure to sync NEVER fails the local operator action — local state is source of truth, Stripe is the downstream mirror, and divergence is recovered via retry / "sync now". Pre-fix, three high-leverage flows wrote local-only and quietly desynced:
  - **Stripe Customer pre-population at create time**: `paymentmethods.StripeAdapter.EnsureStripeCustomer` previously created the Stripe Customer with metadata only — email, name, address, and tax-status were all null on Stripe. Stripe Checkout couldn't pre-fill the email field, the Stripe Dashboard showed a blank customer row for support, and only the lazy `UpsertBillingProfile` path ever filled those fields in. Now reads the Velox `customers` row + the `customer_billing_profiles` row (when present) and pushes email + display_name + legal_name + phone + address + tax_exempt status on the create call. Matches Lago / Recurly / Chargebee's "create-with-fields-known" pattern. Added `CustomerStripeLink.GetBillingProfile` for the new read.
  - **Customer update → Stripe Customer update**: `customer.Service.Update` now calls `StripeBillingSync.SyncBillingProfile` after the local commit when `StripeCustomerID != ""`. Email, legal_name, phone, address, tax_status changes propagate immediately. Best-effort: Stripe failure logs `WARN failed to sync customer update to Stripe` but doesn't roll back the local save.
  - **SetDefault payment method → Stripe Customer `invoice_settings.default_payment_method`**: `paymentmethods.Service.SetDefault` previously updated the local `payment_methods.is_default` row only; Stripe Customer's default stayed stale, and any Stripe-side off-session auto-charge (today or post-Phase-4) would use whatever Stripe last had — including a PM the operator had just demoted. Now resolves the linked Stripe Customer via the adapter's `customerLink` and calls `V1Customers.Update(invoice_settings.default_payment_method)`. Failure logs + writes `stripe_sync_error` to the audit row so ops can spot the divergence and retry. New `paymentmethods.StripeAPI.SetDefaultPaymentMethod(tenantID, customerID, stripePMID)` method on the interface; `StripeAdapter` implements it, fakes in `service_test.go` + `full_loop_integration_test.go` updated.
  - **Pattern: "best-effort + audit on failure"** — chosen after WebSearch over Lago / Recurly / Chargebee / Metronome / Stripe Integration docs (2026-05-29). No platform documents the transactional alternative ("fail the local write if Stripe is down"); every reference uses local-wins with eventual sync. Velox follows the convergent pattern.
  - **Tests**: `TestSetDefault_PushesToStripe` + `TestSetDefault_StripeFailureIsBestEffort` in `internal/paymentmethods/service_test.go` lock the two halves of the new contract — happy path pushes to Stripe, failure path keeps local state and surfaces the error to the audit row.
  - **Out of scope for phase 1, queued for phase 2**: tax_ids[] (separate Stripe API), receipt-email retry semantics, Stripe-tax-calculation 7-day expiry guard. Each is its own write surface and tracked independently.

### Removed

- **GDPR data export + right-to-erasure removed pre-launch (2026-05-29).** Surfaced during a Velox→Stripe sync audit: the prior `customer.GDPRService.DeleteCustomerData` flow anonymized PII locally but **did not propagate erasure to Stripe** — the Stripe Customer object kept email, name, and any attached payment methods, so PII actually persisted in Stripe's systems after the operator clicked "Delete." It also lacked the acknowledgement-window tracking (GDPR's 30-day response requirement) and the audit-trail-of-erasure-requests that a real regulator-facing GDPR flow needs.
  - **Decision**: at zero design partners, shipping a half-fix that signals "we handle GDPR" without actually being compliance-grade is worse than nothing — it's the kind of partial implementation that gets cited in a non-compliance finding. Rebuild properly when the first EU-targeting DP defines actual regulatory scope (regulator-of-record, downstream-system inventory, acknowledgement-window expectations).
  - **Files deleted**: `internal/customer/gdpr.go`, `gdpr_handler.go`, `gdpr_integration_test.go`, `gdpr_multidim_integration_test.go`.
  - **Wiring removed**: `Handler.SetGDPR`, the `gdpr` field on `customer.Handler`, the `/customers/{id}/export` + `/customers/{id}/delete-data` routes, and the `customer.NewGDPRService` wiring in `internal/api/router.go`.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW CU3**: gutted with a placeholder explaining the removal + rebuild trigger.
  - **No data migration** — the customers table's `display_name`/`email`/`status` columns are unchanged; existing rows are untouched. The removal is purely API-surface.
  - **Roadmap entry**: "GDPR / right-to-erasure / SOC2 — triggered when first EU-targeting design partner signs."

### Changed

- **Outbox payload now driven off struct tags, not a hand-written map (2026-05-29).** Surfaced live: operator clicked "Send setup email" from the dashboard → Postmark delivered → customer received an email reading "Use the secure link below" with NO button. Tracing the outbox row's `payload` JSON: every other field was there with empty strings, but `setup_url` and `operator_note` were missing entirely. Root cause was a manual `map[string]any` in `OutboxSender.enqueue` (the wire-payload composer) that listed 18 hand-coded keys — when `SetupURL` + `OperatorNote` were added to the `outboxMessage` struct, nobody updated the map, and the Stripe Checkout URL silently dropped before being persisted. The dispatcher then read the row, found empty CTAURL, and rendered the email through the template's silent `{{if .CTAURL}}` guard — button vanished, copy didn't.
  - **`internal/email/outbox_sender.go enqueue`**: replaced the manual `map[string]any` with `json.Marshal(msg)` + `json.Unmarshal` into `map[string]any`. Now drives the wire payload off the struct's `json:` tags directly — adding a new field to `outboxMessage` automatically flows through to the persisted JSON without a parallel map update. The bug class can't recur.
  - **Cross-flow audit: 5 email types where the link IS the email**. The cross-flow audit (per `feedback_long_term_means_cross_flow_audit`) checked every `Send*` method on both `Sender` and `OutboxSender` for the same bug class — required URL field that could silently drop and produce a broken email. The 5 types where the link is the email's entire purpose (no graceful degradation) all gained boundary validation: `SendPaymentSetupLink` (`setupURL`), `SendPaymentSetupRequest` (`updateURL`), `SendPortalMagicLink` (`magicLinkURL`), `SendPasswordReset` (`resetURL`), `SendMemberInvite` (`acceptURL`). Empty URL → error at the boundary → 502 to the caller. Per `feedback_no_silent_fallbacks`: fail loud, never produce partial mail.
  - **Soft-warn (not hard-fail) on the invoice family**: `SendInvoice` / `SendPaymentReceipt` / `SendDunningWarning` / `SendDunningEscalation` / `SendPaymentFailed` take a `publicToken` to build the hosted-invoice URL — but the email's body still has the invoice number + amount, so it degrades gracefully without the link. Validation here would be over-strict; the operator can still pay via other means.
  - **Existing outbox rows**: any pre-fix `payment_setup_link` rows in `email_outbox` with empty `setup_url` are stuck (and have already dispatched as broken mail). Operators can either ignore them (already sent) or `DELETE FROM email_outbox WHERE email_type='payment_setup_link' AND (payload->>'setup_url' IS NULL OR payload->>'setup_url'='') AND status='pending';` if the dispatch is still pending. Pre-launch local DBs only; production never ran the buggy enqueue.
- **SMTP bounce classification: 5xx codes routed by sender/recipient class (2026-05-29).** Surfaced when a wrong Postmark Server Token landed in `.env` — Postmark returned `535 5.7.8 Error: authentication failed`, Velox classified it as a recipient bounce, flipped `customers.email_status='bounced'` on every send target, and the suppression gate then blocked every subsequent send to those addresses. Operator had to manually `UPDATE customers SET email_status='unknown'` to recover. The 535 was a sender-side problem (Velox couldn't authenticate to Postmark) — recipients weren't involved.
  - **`internal/email/sender.go` `isPermanentSMTPBounce`**: rewrote the classifier to distinguish sender errors from recipient errors per RFC 5321 + RFC 3463:
    - **Bounce (recipient-rejection)**: basic codes 550/551/552/553 OR enhanced status `5.1.x` (addressing) / `5.2.x` (mailbox).
    - **NOT a bounce (sender/server)**: 521 (server doesn't accept mail), 530 (access denied), 534 (auth too weak), 535 (auth failed), 538 (encryption required), 554 (ambiguous), 5.7.x (security/policy), 5.3.x (system).
  - **Enhanced status takes precedence**: `5.1.1 user unknown` without a leading `550 ` still classifies as a recipient bounce — some MX servers return only the enhanced code. RFC 3463 explicitly says the enhanced code is the authoritative signal when both forms are present.
  - **Conservative bias**: previously every 5xx mapped to bounce; flip-cost was a manual SQL UPDATE per affected recipient. Now ambiguous codes (e.g., 554 "transaction failed") default to NOT bounced — the operator sees the raw error in logs without recipients getting flagged. Per `feedback_no_silent_fallbacks` — when the system can't authoritatively classify, fail loud and don't mutate state.
  - **Tests**: 21-case suite in `internal/email/sender_test.go TestIsPermanentSMTPBounce` covers every basic code + every enhanced class + Postmark's specific 535 message + the historical zip-code false-positive guard.
  - **No retroactive backfill** for customers whose `email_status='bounced'` came from the pre-fix classifier. Operators can identify them with `SELECT email, email_bounce_reason FROM customers WHERE email_bounce_reason LIKE '%535%' OR email_bounce_reason LIKE '%authentication%';` and bulk-reset via UPDATE. Pre-launch local DBs only; production never ran the buggy classifier.
- **Cursor pagination on the three high-write list endpoints (2026-05-29).** Stripe/Lago/Orb-shape `?after=<token>` + `next_cursor` in response. Stable across the cycle-close write burst that otherwise page-skews operator pagination through "all invoices for last month" / forensic audit walks / usage debugging. Replaces the page-skew + slow-deep-offset failure mode of OFFSET-based pagination on the three domains where it actually mattered:
  - **`internal/usage/postgres.go`**: seek-method `WHERE (timestamp, id) < (after_ts, after_id) ORDER BY timestamp DESC, id DESC LIMIT N+1`. `usage_events` is the highest-write table in Velox (per-API-call ingestion); offset-pagination page-skewed reliably whenever ingestion fired between operator pages.
  - **`internal/invoice/postgres.go`**: seek-method on `(created_at, id)`. Cycle-close write bursts no longer skew operator pagination. Only the default `created_at DESC` sort supports cursor today; custom-sort cursor combinations are routed to the legacy offset path by the handler.
  - **`internal/audit/audit.go`**: seek-method on `(created_at, id)`. Forensic walks ("what happened on 2026-04-15") were the slow-deep-offset case — `OFFSET 50000` ran in O(N). Cursor is O(log N) per page regardless of depth.
  - **Additive, not breaking**: each store's `List` signature is unchanged. The `Offset` field on `ListFilter` is retained for the legacy offset path (dashboard "Page X of N" UX). Cursor is opt-in via `?after=` query param + `AfterCreatedAt`+`AfterID` on the filter. Handler routes by query param presence; cursor takes precedence over offset when both are set. Skips the `COUNT(*)` query on the cursor path — that's where the O(N) cost actually came from on deep audit_log walks.
  - **Wire format**: opaque base64-encoded JSON of `{id, created_at}` — same as the existing `internal/api/middleware/pagination.go EncodeCursor`/`DecodeCursor` so SPA clients can pass cursors interchangeably across endpoints. Audit handler inlines its own encode/decode because `internal/api/middleware` already imports `internal/audit` (for the row-writer middleware) — circular dep otherwise; the wire shape is identical so the duplication is cosmetic.
  - **Other 6 list endpoints stay on offset** (customers, subscriptions, dunning runs, webhook events, credit ledger, credit notes). Per `feedback_pre_launch_scoping`: at zero design partners, offset works fine for tables with low row counts AND low write rates. Migrate the rest when a real DP names the scale pressure.
  - **Response shape on the cursor path**:
    ```json
    { "data": [...], "has_more": true, "next_cursor": "<token>" }
    ```
    Mirrors Stripe's `has_more` + `next_cursor` shape; no `total_count` (the cursor path skips COUNT, which is the whole point).
- **Subscription activity timeline: "simulated" chip is now per-row, not a sub-level heuristic (2026-05-29).** Surfaced during EX3 manual test: the sub-detail Activity card showed every audit row with a "simulated" chip even when its timestamp was clearly wall-clock (May 28-29 2026 next to "Item added", "Proration failed", etc.). Root cause was a stale heuristic in `subscription.handler.go activityTimeline`: `subOnClock = sub.TestClockID != ""` → every event flagged `IsSimulated: subOnClock`. After the 2026-05-28 ADR-030 amendment that made `audit_log.created_at` wall-clock everywhere, the heuristic became actively wrong — operator audit row timestamps are real time, regardless of which clock the affected sub is pinned to. Cross-flow audit found the same shape was correct on the invoice payment timeline (events sourced from invoice/dunning row timestamps which ARE in sim-time when bound), so the fix is scoped to the audit-fed surface.
  - **`internal/subscription/handler.go`**: `timelineEvent` gained `SimEffectiveAt` + `TestClockID` fields. The per-row `IsSimulated` is now derived from `metadata.sim_effective_at` (authoritative — set by `auditMetaForSub` at write time on clock-pinned subs, per ADR-030 amendment). Dropped the `subOnClock` heuristic and the now-unused sub fetch. Stale comments around the `IsSimulated` field updated to reflect the post-amendment shape.
  - **`web-v2/src/pages/SubscriptionDetail.tsx`**: chip label changed from "simulated" to "test clock" so operators don't misread it as "this timestamp is fake" — it's not, it's wall-clock now. Mirrors the AuditLog page chip pattern. Added a "Effect on test clock `<id>` at `<sim time>`" subline rendered under the wall-clock primary timestamp when `sim_effective_at` is present. Hover tooltip explains the two-time model.
  - **`web-v2/src/lib/api.ts` `TimelineEvent`**: added `sim_effective_at` + `test_clock_id` optional fields. Inline comment documents the per-surface semantics (sub timeline: timestamp is wall-clock + sim_effective_at is the effect time; invoice timeline: timestamp IS sim-time, no sim_effective_at).
  - **Invoice payment timeline NOT changed**: events there are sourced from `invoice.issued_at` / `paid_at` / dunning row timestamps — those fields ARE simulated when the sub is clock-pinned (engine + webhook + dunning handlers all bind ctx via the resolver after today's earlier reconciler/dunning fixes). The `subOnClock` per-event flag is correct there.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW SUB-CARD**: new assertion verifying activity row timestamps are wall-clock on operator actions + the "test clock" chip + sim_effective_at subline appears only when set.
- **Subscription items are now soft-deleted (migration 0102, 2026-05-29).** Surfaced during EX3 manual test: `DELETE /v1/subscriptions/{id}/items/{itemID}` returned 500 with `"update or delete on table "subscription_items" violates foreign key constraint "invoices_source_subscription_item_id_fkey" (SQLSTATE 23503)"` whenever the item had been involved in a proration event (any item past the first cycle). Industry standard (Stripe / Chargebee / Lago / Orb): soft-delete subscription items — the row stays for FK back-pointer integrity, a `deleted_at` column hides it from live-state queries. Velox had been hard-deleting which fought the existing FK.
  - **Migration `0102_subscription_items_soft_delete.up.sql`**: adds `deleted_at TIMESTAMPTZ NULL`. Recreates the `(subscription_id, plan_id)` unique constraint as a *partial* index `WHERE deleted_at IS NULL` so a soft-deleted item doesn't block re-adding the same plan to the sub. Adds a hot-path partial index `idx_subscription_items_live ON (subscription_id) WHERE deleted_at IS NULL` for active-state hydration.
  - **`internal/subscription/postgres.go removeItemInTx`**: `UPDATE deleted_at = now()` instead of `DELETE`. Returns `ErrNotFound` when no row matches (already deleted or never existed).
  - **Live-state queries filtered**: `GetItem`, `listItemsTx` (the sub.Items hydration), the `JOIN subscription_items` in `ListFilter.PlanID` filter, `CountLiveSubsByPlan`, `analytics/overview.go totalMRR` + `New MRR` + `Churned MRR` queries, `analytics/mrr_movement.go` New + Churned queries — all gained `AND si.deleted_at IS NULL`.
  - **Historical analytics caveat**: the New/Churned movement queries count items live AS OF NOW for a historical activation bucket. Items soft-deleted between the historical activation and the current moment are excluded — slight under-count on historical buckets if items were removed later. Pre-launch analytics tolerate this; documented as a follow-up to revisit when historical accuracy becomes a customer ask. Inline comment in `mrr_movement.go` flags the limitation.
  - **Existing data unaffected**: every existing row has `deleted_at IS NULL` (the migration's default), so all current queries return the same set as pre-migration. No backfill needed.
  - **MANUAL_TEST**: new B3-block assertion verifying RemoveItem on an item with proration history now succeeds (200) and the item disappears from `sub.Items` while remaining queryable via `psql` with `deleted_at IS NOT NULL` for audit.
- **AddItem-with-proration is now atomic (ADR-030 atomic-proration follow-through, 2026-05-29).** Closes the half-committed orphan-item path that the constraint-routing fix (2026-05-28) made rarer but didn't eliminate: pre-fix the handler called `svc.AddItem` (commits the sub item in its own tx) THEN `handleItemProration` (runs the proration write in a separate tx) — a failure on the proration side left the item on the sub with no matching proration invoice or credit, silently undercharging the customer at next cycle close. The error message admitted the gap (`"item add succeeded but proration generation failed — retry or contact support to reconcile"`). Stripe / Lago / Orb all do this in one transaction.
  - **Tx-variant store methods at every layer**:
    - `subscription.PostgresStore.AddItemTx` (new) + `Store` interface gains `AddItemTx`
    - `invoice.PostgresStore.CreateWithLineItemsTx` (new)
    - `tenant.SettingsStore.NextInvoiceNumberTx` (new) + `invoice.InvoiceNumberer` interface gains it
    - `credit.PostgresStore.AppendEntryTx` (new) + `credit.Store` interface gains it
    - `credit.Service.GrantTx` (new)
  - **Service layer**: `subscription.Service.AddItemTx` wraps validation + mixed-interval guard + `store.AddItemTx` so the handler can compose it atomically with downstream writes.
  - **Narrow interfaces (in `subscription/handler.go`)**: `ProrationInvoiceCreator` gains `CreateInvoiceWithLineItemsTx` + `NextInvoiceNumberTx`; `ProrationCreditGranter` gains `GrantProrationTx`. Adapters in `api/adapters.go` implement them by forwarding to the underlying stores' Tx methods.
  - **Handler refactor (`subscription.Handler.addItem`)**: when `h.db` is wired AND a proration emission is needed, opens an outer `BeginTx(TxTenant, tenantID)`, calls `svc.AddItemTx(tx, ...)`, then `handleItemProration(ctx, ..., tx)` which uses Tx variants for its 3 internal write sites (NextInvoiceNumber, CreateInvoiceWithLineItems, GrantProration). Commits on success; the `defer postgres.Rollback(tx)` unwinds both writes on any failure. Falls back to the legacy non-atomic flow when `h.db` is nil (test scaffolding) — same observable behavior as pre-fix for that path.
  - **`handleItemProration` signature**: gained a `tx *sql.Tx` parameter (nil-tolerant). When nil, uses the non-Tx interface methods (backwards-compat path). When non-nil, uses the Tx variants so all writes share the caller's tx. Three call sites (addItem, updateItem, removeItem) updated to pass `nil` to preserve their legacy behavior pending follow-up.
  - **Router wiring**: `subH.SetDB(db)` co-located with the existing resolver / audit / proration-deps wirings.
  - **Test fakes**: every fake (`memStore` in subscription + credit, `invoicesMock` + `creditsMock` in subscription/handler_test.go, `memNumberer` in invoice/service_test.go) gained Tx-variant stubs that forward to the non-Tx implementations. Existing tests pass unchanged.
  - **Extended to UpdateItem (simple paths) + RemoveItem in the same change**: `updateItem` quantity-change + same-interval-immediate-plan-change paths now go through `Handler.atomicUpdateItemWithProration` → `svc.UpdateItemTx` → `store.UpdateItemQuantityTx`/`ApplyItemPlanImmediatelyTx` in one outer tx. Scheduled changes (no proration) + cross-interval / cross-cadence plan swaps (multi-write engine flow via `BillOnPlanSwapImmediate`) return a sentinel `errAtomicNotApplicable` from `svc.UpdateItemTx` so the handler falls back to the legacy non-atomic path — those still have the multi-write boundary as a documented follow-up. `removeItem` now goes through `Handler.atomicRemoveItemWithProration` → `svc.RemoveItemTx` → `store.RemoveItemTx`, so a failed remove-proration credit grant rolls back the delete.
  - **Cross-interval / cross-cadence plan swap still legacy**: that path triggers `engine.BillOnPlanSwapImmediate` (writes a credit grant) + `store.ApplyItemPlanImmediately` + `store.UpdateBillingCycle` + (optionally) `engine.BillOnCreate` — making it atomic would require Tx variants on the billing engine itself, which is a bigger refactor than the rest of this change. The handler falls back to legacy for those paths; the orphan-risk is real but rare in practice (the engine writes succeed individually in the common case, and the failure mode is the same shape the rest of the codebase has lived with since pre-2026-05-29).
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW B3**: new assertion verifying atomicity (induce proration failure → confirm no orphan sub-item row).
  - **No migration**. The change is pure code — store row schema unchanged, existing data unaffected.
- **Unique-violation routing: constraint-name → distinct error codes; proration invoices exempted from cycle-dedup index (2026-05-28).** EX3 manual test surfaced a half-committed item-add: a second `AddItem` on the same sub at the same simulated instant committed the sub item but errored with `"proration dedup lookup: not found"`. Root cause was a two-layer conflation:
  - **Migration 0101_billing_idempotency_excludes_proration**: `idx_invoices_billing_idempotency` (cycle-dedup index, `(tenant, sub, period_start, period_end) WHERE status<>'voided'`) was firing on proration invoices because two distinct mid-cycle item adds shared the same partial billing period. The index was designed for cycle dedup, not proration — proration has its own dedicated `idx_invoices_proration_dedup`. Migration narrows the partial predicate to `WHERE status<>'voided' AND source_plan_changed_at IS NULL` so cycle invoices keep their dedup contract while proration invoices are governed only by their proper index.
  - **`internal/invoice/postgres.go` mapInvoiceUniqueViolation helper**: was mapping every unique violation to a single generic `errs.AlreadyExists("billing_period", ...)` or `("invoice_number", ...)` — callers couldn't tell which of the 7 unique indexes fired. Reworked to use `postgres.UniqueViolationConstraint(err)` and route each of the 7 indexes to a distinct DomainError with a unique `Code()` (`invoice_billing_period_taken`, `invoice_proration_source_taken`, `invoice_number_taken`, `invoice_public_token_collision`, `invoice_threshold_cycle_taken`, `invoice_stripe_id_taken`, plus `invoice_unique_violation` for future indexes). Unknown-constraint case surfaces the constraint name in the message so the operator and logs can identify what fired without code changes. Same pattern applied to `internal/credit/postgres.go AppendEntry` (proration_dedup vs credit_note_dedup, previously squashed). 9-case unit test (`postgres_unique_violation_test.go`) locks the routing.
  - **`internal/subscription/handler.go` proration retry**: branches on `errs.Code(err) == "invoice_proration_source_taken"` (and `"credit_proration_source_taken"`) instead of catching any `ErrAlreadyExists`. Pre-fix: any unique violation triggered the dedup-lookup retry, which queried `GetByProrationSource(item_id=...)` and returned "not found" when the actual collision was on a different constraint. Now only the actual proration-source collision retries; other constraints surface as their own distinct errors.
  - **Reference pattern**: `internal/coupon/postgres.go` already implemented constraint-name routing for customer-discount idempotency since the coupons-v2 work. This change brings invoice + credit to the same shape.
  - **Cross-flow audit (advisory)**: customer/plan/meter/rating-rule stores each have 1+ unique constraints beyond the documented one but currently map to a single field. Risk is low (other constraints are on cost_dashboard_token / stripe_customer_id / pkey — all 256-bit random or generated IDs, astronomically unlikely to collide). Left as-is; can extend to the same routing pattern when a real second-constraint collision surfaces.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW B3** gained an assertion: two AddItems on the same sub at the same simulated instant produce two distinct proration invoices, both successfully persisted, with the new item committed AND its proration recorded.
  - **Demo-data note**: the local demo's `vlx_sub_d8b9nf3majdnam65j6k0` has the 3rd item attached without its proration recorded (committed before the fix). Delete the orphan item or run `psql` cleanup — not a migration concern since the data is local/pre-launch only.
- **List-store `limit` over-cap behavior: silent fall-back → explicit clamp across 17 sites (2026-05-28).** Every list store in `internal/` shared the same pattern: `if limit <= 0 || limit > N { limit = X }` where `X < N`. So when a caller asked for `limit=1000`, the store silently returned `X` (often 50) without surfacing that the request was capped. Direct contradiction of `feedback_no_silent_fallbacks` ("never silent zero, fail loudly, not substitute a default"). The bug compounded with `internal/api/exports.go`, which asked for `exportPageSize=1000` and looped while `len(rows) < exportPageSize` — so the export only ever streamed the *first 50 rows* of every entity before the loop broke. A tenant with 931 invoices exported as 50; a tenant with 200 customers exported as 50; nobody got an error or warning. Surfaced live during EX2 manual test (`?from=2026-01-01&to=2026-12-31` on 931 simulated-2053 invoices returned a header-only CSV because the first 50 rows ORDER BY created_at DESC were all 2053-dated and filtered out by the 2026 range — the other 881 invoices that included 63 matching 2026 rows were never fetched).
  - **17 list-cap sites converted** to clamp-instead-of-fall-back:
    - Postgres stores: `audit`, `auth`, `coupon` (x2), `credit`, `creditnote`, `customer` (x2), `dunning`, `invoice`, `subscription`, `tenant`, `usage` (1000-cap), `webhook`.
    - HTTP handlers: `portalapi/handler.go` (x2 — subs + invoices list).
    - Shared middleware: `api/middleware/pagination.go`.
  - **Pattern after**: `if limit <= 0 { limit = DEFAULT } else if limit > MAX { limit = MAX }`. Default branch preserved for unset/invalid asks; over-cap branch now clamps honestly so the caller's `len(rows)` matches what they asked for (up to the documented MAX).
  - **`internal/api/exports.go`**: `exportPageSize` 1000 → 100 (aligned with the new clamp ceiling). Comment documents the dependency on the store cap — if a future store lowers its cap, the export's loop-termination check (`len(rows) < exportPageSize`) breaks again until exportPageSize is lowered to match. Long-term we should switch to a `len(rows) == 0` termination, but that costs one extra round-trip per export; deferred until a real customer asks for it.
  - **Behavior change for clients asking for limit>cap**: pre-2026-05-28 they got `DEFAULT` rows back (smaller); post-fix they get `MAX` rows. Almost certainly what they intended. No client-visible API change otherwise.
  - **MANUAL_TEST EX1 + EX2** updated with row-completeness assertions verifying the export matches the `SELECT COUNT(*)` for the tenant.
- **Payment reconciler now binds ctx to invoice's clock pin before `MarkPaid` (2026-05-28).** Continuation of the ADR-030 cross-flow audit: the `payment.Reconciler` (cron-driven fallback that resolves `payment_status=unknown` invoices by polling Stripe) used an injected wall-clock `r.now()` for the `paid_at` stamp. For invoices belonging to clock-pinned customers, that meant a wall-clock 2026 paid_at landed on a simulated 2053 timeline row — split-brain against `issued_at` / `due_at` / `billing_period_*` on the same invoice. Same shape as the `dunning.Handler.resolveRun` leak fixed earlier the same day.
  - **`internal/payment/reconciler.go`**: added `resolver clock.Resolver` field + `SetResolver` method. In `reconcileOne` "succeeded" branch, ctx now binds via `clock.BindEffectiveNow(ctx, r.resolver, clock.Pin{TenantID, InvoiceID})` before `MarkPaid`; `paid_at` = `clock.Now(ctx)`. The cool-off window calculation at the top of `Run` still uses `r.now()` (deliberately wall-clock — that's elapsed-real-time since the unknown landed, not anything in the entity's domain).
  - **Router wiring**: `paymentReconciler.SetResolver(engine)` co-located with `dunningSvc.SetResolver(engine)` / `dunningH.SetResolver(engine)` / `stripeAdapter.SetResolver(engine)` so all resolver wirings live in one block.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW TC5**: new assertion verifying simulated paid_at on reconciler-resolved clock-pinned invoices.
  - **Surfaced during** the EX2 invoice-export flow test — a row showed `paid_at=2026-05-08T06:09:13Z` (wall-clock) on a `billing_period_start=2053-05-01` invoice (simulated 2053 timeline). Cross-flow audit identified the reconciler as the last unbound `paid_at` writer.
- **Unified `?from=` / `?to=` date-filter parsing across operator endpoints (2026-05-28).** Cross-flow audit found four endpoints with three different contracts for the same query parameter: audit-log accepted both RFC3339 and `YYYY-MM-DD`; CSV exports + customer-usage accepted RFC3339-only and 400'd on date-only; usage-summary silently swallowed parse errors and fell back to the current month (latent bug — typo'd `?from=` gave the wrong window with no signal). Operators learning one endpoint tripped on the next. Consolidated on the shared lenient contract.
  - **New shared helper** at `internal/api/timefilter`. Single `ParseRange(r, fromParam, toParam) (from, to time.Time, err error)` function accepts BOTH RFC3339 instants and bare `YYYY-MM-DD` dates. Date-only `from` anchors at UTC 00:00:00; date-only `to` anchors at UTC 23:59:59 so YYYY-MM-DD ranges are inclusive on both ends. Enforces `to > from`. Param names are caller-controlled (audit-log uses legacy `date_from`/`date_to`; everywhere else uses `from`/`to`) to avoid an operator-visible URL contract change. Returns structured `errs.Invalid` for malformed input — handlers pipe through `respond.FromError` to surface a 400 with field-level error.
  - **Test coverage** for the helper: 10 cases including missing params, mixed formats, invalid input on either side, equal-or-inverted ranges. Lives at `internal/api/timefilter/timefilter_test.go`.
  - **Migrated callers**: `internal/api/exports.go` (4 CSV endpoints), `internal/usage/customer_usage_handler.go` (`parseUsagePeriodQuery`), `internal/usage/summary.go` (silent-fallback bug fix — now 400s on bad input instead of swallowing the error), `internal/audit/handler.go` + `audit.go` (`QueryFilter.DateFrom` / `DateTo` changed from `string` to `time.Time`; postgres-go driver handles TIMESTAMPTZ binding natively). Local `normalizeDateFilter` in `audit.go` deleted.
  - **Behavior change for operators**: every `?from=`/`?to=` endpoint now accepts the lenient format. Existing RFC3339 curl-paste and dashboard-issued URLs continue to work unchanged. The usage-summary silent fallback is gone — operators will now see 400s for bad dates instead of mysterious month-defaulting.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW EX1 + FLOW P2** updated to assert both date formats and the field-level error envelope.
- **Audit-log `created_at` is wall-clock for every row; simulated effect-time moves into metadata (2026-05-28).** ADR-030's table line 131 always said "Audit log row recorded_at: wall-clock | Forensics" but two weeks of code drift produced a mixed-domain `audit_log.created_at` column — subscription mutations on clock-pinned subs wrote simulated `created_at` (via the `auditCtxForSub` helper that bound ctx to `sub.UpdatedAt`), while invoice / dunning / middleware-catchall writes on the same customer wrote wall-clock. The auditor couldn't tell from a row "when did Sagar click" because the answer depended on which handler wrote it. Industry research across Stripe / Chargebee / Orb / Lago / Recurly confirmed the convergent pattern is "one timestamp per row," but the right cut is the *actor*, not the resource — operator actions are real-time events regardless of which clock the affected entity is pinned to.
  - **`internal/audit/audit.go`**: `created_at = time.Now().UTC()` unconditionally; dropped the `clock` package import. Comment now points at the ADR-030 amendment.
  - **`internal/api/middleware/audit.go`**: middleware catch-all also stamps wall-clock; handler-bound `effective-now` no longer leaks into the catch-all.
  - **`internal/subscription/handler.go`**: deleted `auditCtxForSub`. New `auditMetaForSub(sub, extra) map[string]any` helper injects `sim_effective_at` (sub.UpdatedAt formatted RFC3339Nano) + `test_clock_id` into the metadata bag for clock-pinned subs. All 11 audit call sites updated to pass `r.Context()` directly and wrap their metadata through the helper.
  - **`internal/dunning/handler.go`**: separate pre-existing leak — `resolveRun` writes `invoice.paid_at` from unbound ctx, so clock-pinned invoices' `paid_at` always landed in wall-clock even though every other timestamp on the same invoice was simulated. Added `Handler.SetResolver(clock.Resolver)`; `resolveRun` now binds ctx via `clock.BindEffectiveNow(...)` before `invoices.MarkPaid`. Wired `dunningH.SetResolver(engine)` in `internal/api/router.go`.
  - **UI (`web-v2/src/pages/AuditLog.tsx`)**: rows with `metadata.sim_effective_at` render an amber **test clock** chip next to the action label and a "Effect on test clock `<id>` at `<sim-time>`" subline under the wall-clock primary timestamp in the expanded detail. `sim_effective_at` + `test_clock_id` excluded from the generic metadata key-value list so they don't appear twice.
  - **ADR-030 amendment** at `docs/adr/030-simulated-time-everywhere-on-clock-pinned-entities.md` documents the actor model (operator → wall-clock; engine-generated → simulated; external/async → wall-clock) and the migration.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW TC5**: two new assertions verifying wall-clock `created_at` on the audit row + matching `metadata.sim_effective_at`, and simulated `invoice.paid_at` on dunning-resolve for clock-pinned invoices.
  - **No schema migration** — `audit_log.created_at` is already TIMESTAMPTZ. Existing rows with simulated timestamps stay as-is (the contract was always "wall-clock" — the drifted writes were a bug, not a documented format).
- **Dual-email architecture collapsed to single canonical recipient (2026-05-28).** Migration `0100_drop_billing_profile_email` drops `customer_billing_profiles.email`; `customers.email` is now the single source of truth for the customer recipient. Closes the structural defect that drove yesterday's BP→customer sync hack: every send path read `bp.Email || cust.Email`, but the bounce/suppression keys were blinded on `customers.email_bidx` only — so once the two values diverged, sends went to BP while suppression checked customer (silent skew). Industry research across Stripe, Chargebee, Recurly, Lago, and Orb found zero precedent for the override pattern; all single-canonical-email today, with Chargebee adding an additive `additional_contacts` table for multi-recipient. Phase 1 ships the Stripe shape; Phase 2 (Chargebee shape) is additive when a design partner names the multi-recipient requirement — the resolver indirection in `customerEmailFetcherAdapter` is the swap point.
  - **Domain**: `domain.CustomerBillingProfile.Email` field removed; inline comment documents the Phase 1 / Phase 2 split.
  - **Store**: encrypt/decrypt drops the email crypto path; `UpsertBillingProfile` + `GetBillingProfile` SQL renumbered params.
  - **Service**: removed email validation + the BP→customer sync hack; `UpsertBillingProfile` no longer touches `customers.email` or `email_status`.
  - **Send/PDF sites updated to canonical**: `api.customerEmailFetcherAdapter`, `invoice.handler` (send + PDF bill-to), `creditnote.handler`, `hostedinvoice.handler` (2 PDF sites), `portalapi.handler`, `payment.StripeBillingSync` (now takes `customerEmail` as a separate arg, plumbed from `cust.Email` in the caller).
  - **GDPR**: BP wipe drops the email line; `customers.email` is the canonical wipe target.
  - **Frontend**: `BillingProfile.email` removed from `api.ts`; `CustomerDetail.tsx` edit form drops the email field + zod schema entry + fill-from-customer line; bill-to display drops the email row; invoice-create recipient resolver now reads `customer.email` directly.
  - **Tests**: `gdpr_integration_test.go` and `postgres_test.go` fixtures updated; obsolete Case 3 in `TestService_Update_ResetsBounceStateOnEmailChange` (BP→customer sync) removed — the underlying behavior no longer exists.
- **Bounce state resets on customer email edit (2026-05-27).** When an operator (or customer via portal self-edit) changes `customers.email`, the new address inherited the OLD address's bounce flag — silently suppressing all future sends to a brand-new untested address. `customer.Service.Update` now compares prior-vs-new email and calls a new `store.ResetEmailStatus` (NULLs `email_status`, `email_bounce_reason`, `email_last_bounced_at`). The reset only fires when the email value actually changes — display-name-only edits preserve real bounce signal.
  - **`ResetEmailStatus` method** on `customer.Store` interface + `*PostgresStore` impl. Idempotent. Best-effort: failure here only logs WARN and doesn't fail the parent update (the bounce flag is diagnostic, not a hard correctness gate).
  - **`memoryStore` fake updated** to satisfy the extended interface.
  - **Integration test** (`TestService_Update_ResetsBounceStateOnEmailChange`) covers two cases: email-change resets, no-op-email preserves bounce. (Case 3 — BP.email sync — deleted by the 2026-05-28 dual-email collapse.)
- **Recipient suppression gate + RFC-compliant email validation (2026-05-27).** Closed the loop between bounce detection and future-send suppression. Before this, a customer's email could bounce (5xx detected, `email_status='bounced'` written), but the next email producer would still enqueue/send to the same dead address — wasting SMTP quota + sender reputation. Two changes:
  - **Send-time gate**: new `email.RecipientSuppressionChecker` interface; both `Sender.send*` (direct SMTP) and `OutboxSender.enqueue` (queued) consult it before every send. Bounced/complained recipients return `ErrRecipientSuppressed` (soft-skip, INFO log). Errors from the lookup **fail open** — a flaky DB lookup shouldn't block all outbound mail.
  - **Production adapter**: new `suppressionCheckerAdapter` in `internal/api/adapters.go` mirrors the existing `bounceReporterAdapter` — uses the same email blind index to look up customer rows by `(tenant, email)`, returns suppressed=true when any matching customer's `email_status ∈ {bounced, complained}`. Wired symmetrically with the bounce-reporter setup so it's enabled iff `VELOX_EMAIL_BIDX_KEY` is set.
  - **`validateEmail` upgraded to `net/mail.ParseAddress`** — RFC 5322-compliant parsing replaces the hand-rolled `@`+dot regex check. Catches more malformed input at write time without changing the contract.
  - **Tests**: two new unit tests cover the suppression path — `TestOutboxSender_SuppressedRecipient` (returns `ErrRecipientSuppressed` when checker says yes), `TestOutboxSender_SuppressionCheckerErrorFailsOpen` (proceeds on lookup error).
- **Operator "Send setup email" routed through the email outbox (2026-05-27).** The send-setup-email endpoint was the only operator-action email producer still on the direct-SMTP path — every other producer (invoice / dunning / receipt / magic-link / payment-setup-request / payment-failed / password-reset) routes through the outbox for resilience. The mismatch surfaced as a FLOW E3 hole: unsetting `SMTP_HOST` produced a 502 to the operator but no row in `email_outbox`, so the retry-with-backoff + DLQ assertions had no observable side effect to verify. Industry standard (Stripe Dashboard, Chargebee, Recurly all queue operator-action emails the same way customer-facing ones go through). Fix:
  - **New `TypePaymentSetupLink` outbox type** + `OutboxSender.SendPaymentSetupLink` enqueue method + `SetupURL` / `OperatorNote` payload fields on `outboxMessage` + dispatcher routing case.
  - **`EmailDeliverer` interface extended** with `SendPaymentSetupLink` so the dispatcher can route the row back to the SMTP `Sender` on dequeue.
  - **Router wiring**: new `setupLinkEmail` variable mirrors the existing mode-aware pattern (`outboxSender` when `VELOX_EMAIL_OUTBOX_ENABLED=true`, direct `emailSender` otherwise). `paymentMethodsH.SetEmailer(setupLinkEmail)`.
  - **Handler semantics**: error code renamed `email_send_failed` → `email_enqueue_failed`; message pivots to "queued" framing. SMTP failures now surface on the email_outbox dashboard (stuck `pending` rows with `last_error` populated, eventually DLQ at attempts=15) instead of failing the operator's request.
  - **Test fakes** (`fakeDeliverer` in outbox_integration_test.go) updated to satisfy the new interface method.
- **All remaining useEffect+fetch anti-patterns migrated to React Query (2026-05-27).** Audit across the SPA found 9 surfaces still on the legacy `useEffect(() => api.something().then(setData), [])` pattern, doubling fetches in StrictMode dev and missing the cache/dedupe/refetch-on-focus benefits the rest of the app gets from RQ. All 9 migrated:
  - **Tier 1 (page-level, high impact):** `components/Layout.tsx` (settings + analytics overview on every dashboard mount), `pages/Credits.tsx` (full anti-pattern stack with `setLoading`/`setError` — balances + customers + per-customer ledger), `pages/AuditLog.tsx` (entries list + filter dropdown options).
  - **Tier 2 (user-action gated, medium impact):** `components/CommandPalette.tsx` (⌘K — 4 parallel lists), `pages/Coupons.tsx` (CouponDialog plans fetch), `pages/CreditNotes.tsx` (CreditNoteDialog invoices fetch — finalized + paid).
  - **Tier 3 (public token routes):** `pages/UpdatePayment.tsx`, `pages/HostedInvoice.tsx` — token-validated public flows. `retry: false` on these so a genuinely invalid token doesn't pound the server.
  - Net: ~150 lines of `setLoading` / `setError` / `useCallback`-wrapped-load / try-finally boilerplate deleted. Every page now uses the same data-fetching pattern (React Query 5 with `useQuery` / `useMutation`).
  - Verified clean: `grep` for any `useEffect` block containing `api.*` / `portalFetch` / `apiRequest` / `fetch(` returns zero hits across `web-v2/src/**/*.tsx`.
- **Portal.tsx migrated to React Query (2026-05-27).** The customer portal was the last major page on the raw `useEffect` + `useState` + `portalFetch` pattern; the rest of the dashboard had already moved to TanStack Query. Migration:
  - **6 GETs** (subscriptions, invoices, payment-methods, profile, credit-balance, branding) now run as `useQuery` calls under a shared `PORTAL_KEYS` registry. StrictMode dev-mode double-mount no longer fires duplicate HTTP requests — RQ dedupes by query key.
  - **7 writes** (cancel sub, resume sub, pay-now invoice, set default PM, remove PM, save profile, setup-session) now run as `useMutation` calls. Each invalidates only the query key(s) it actually changes; affected sections refetch automatically without the old "call `load()` to refresh everything" pattern.
  - **Auth-error redirect** consolidated in one `useEffect` that watches every query's error; `PortalAuthError` on any GET routes to `/portal/login`. Mutations share an `onError` helper with the same semantics.
  - **First-paint loading** derived from `OR` of all six `isLoading` flags; subsequent refetches don't trigger the skeleton (RQ keeps the previous data visible).
  - **`acting`** preserved as a derived `OR` of every mutation's `isPending` so the existing JSX disable bindings keep working without refactor.
  - The legacy `load()` function, `setLoading` / `setError` / `setActing` / six matching `useState` setters are gone. Net: ~80 fewer lines of state-juggling.
- **Payment methods dedupe by Stripe card fingerprint (2026-05-27).** Stripe mints a new `pm_xxx` object every time a customer completes Checkout, even for the same physical card. Without dedupe, the portal renders the same card twice (or more). Velox now stores `card_fingerprint` (Stripe's stable hash of the card number — CVC + expiry don't affect it) and collapses duplicates on attach. Industry standard — Stripe explicitly recommends app-side dedupe by fingerprint.
  - **Migration 0099** adds `payment_methods.card_fingerprint TEXT` (nullable for legacy rows) + a partial unique index on `(tenant_id, livemode, customer_id, card_fingerprint) WHERE detached_at IS NULL AND card_fingerprint IS NOT NULL`.
  - **`paymentmethods.StripeAdapter.FetchPaymentMethodCard`** now returns a `CardMetadata` struct including the Stripe-supplied `Fingerprint`. Old `(brand, last4, exp_month, exp_year)` return tuple replaced for clarity.
  - **`PostgresStore.Upsert`**: before inserting a new `pm_xxx`, looks up any active row for the same `(tenant, customer, livemode, fingerprint)`. On match, detaches the old row in the same transaction and carries its `is_default` flag onto the new row. NULL-fingerprint rows skip dedupe (legacy data + non-card types). The new partial unique index enforces the invariant at the DB level.
  - **Dedupe integration test** (`TestAttach_DedupesByFingerprint`) asserts: re-attaching the same fingerprint collapses to one row with `is_default=true` inherited; attaching a different fingerprint adds a row without stealing default. Lock-in for the new invariant.
  - **Legacy rows**: payment methods attached before 0099 have `card_fingerprint=NULL` and won't dedupe against new attaches. They'll collapse the next time the customer re-adds (the new row gets a fingerprint, but the legacy row doesn't match it so both stay until the customer removes the old one). Lazy convergence — no backfill needed since pre-launch.
- **Portal + dashboard PM UX polished e2e (2026-05-26).** Two surfaces (customer portal + operator dashboard CustomerDetail) had drifted in title, CTA labels, badge variants, and confirmation behavior despite serving identical concepts. Closes the gap between them so they read like one product.
  - **Section title**: both now say "Payment methods" (plural). Portal was singular.
  - **CTA label**: both use "Add payment method" — future-proofs for non-card methods (ACH/SEPA) and matches Stripe/Chargebee/Lago convention. Was a mix of "Add card", "Add another card", "Add Card", "Send Setup Link".
  - **Empty-state copy**: harmonized — portal reads "No payment method on file — Add one to autopay invoices."; dashboard reads "No payment methods on file — Click 'Add payment method' to email the customer a secure setup link."
  - **Remove confirmation**: portal now wraps Remove in an AlertDialog ("Remove this payment method?" with brand+last4 in body) — operator side already had this; the two destructive paths are now symmetric.
  - **Default badge**: both surfaces use `variant="outline"` (Stripe-style). Dashboard previously used `variant="success"`.
  - **`?status=success|cancel` toast on portal return**: Portal.tsx now reads the query param Stripe appends to the SetupSession return URL — shows "Payment method added" toast + refetches PM list on success, "Setup canceled" toast on cancel. Was silent before.
- **PM-link send paths unified into one e2e flow (2026-05-26).** Closes the consistency audit that found three parallel "send add-card link" code paths (operator dashboard, customer portal, engine no-PM-at-finalize). Each had its own URL minting, template, and audit behavior — a textbook cross-flow drift that would inevitably let the next regression land in the wrong path. One path now, single template, single audit shape.
  - **Deleted** `internal/payment/portal.go` + `POST /v1/payment-portal/{customerId}/update-payment-method` route. Frontend `api.updatePaymentMethod` / `api.setupPayment` / `api.getPaymentStatus` + the `PaymentSetup` type + `pollIntervalForPaymentSetup` helper all removed (no remaining callers). `handleSetupPayment` dead-code path in `CustomerDetail.tsx` deleted.
  - **`InvoiceAttention` banner migrated** from the legacy "open Stripe URL in operator's tab" flow to the shared `SendSetupLinkDialog`. When an invoice is in attention state, operator clicks "Update Payment Method" → same email-primary + copy-link-secondary dialog as CustomerDetail, pre-populated with invoice context ("We couldn't process payment for invoice X — $Y…"). The customer gets the link, not the operator.
  - **`InvoiceDetail` switched** from `getPaymentStatus` (legacy summary read) to `listCustomerPaymentMethods` for the "hasPaymentMethod" disable-button check.
  - **Engine no-PM-at-finalize audit** (`noPaymentMethodNotifierAdapter`): now writes an `action=setup_link_sent`, `trigger=finalize_no_pm` audit row when it ships the email. Previously silent; operator AuditLog page now shows engine-fired sends alongside operator-initiated ones.
  - **Email templates unified.** `renderPaymentSetupLinkHTML` is the single internal renderer; `paymentSetupLinkContext` carries an optional invoice context (number + amount) that drives the invoice-flavoured subject + body when set. `renderPaymentUpdateRequestHTML` is now a thin wrapper that delegates. `Sender.SendPaymentSetupRequest` (back-compat signature) and `Sender.SendPaymentSetupLink` both route through the unified template.
  - **`SendSetupLinkDialog` shared component** (`web-v2/src/components/SendSetupLinkDialog.tsx`) lifts the email-primary + copy-link-secondary dialog out of `CustomerDetail.tsx`. Accepts optional `invoiceContext` to prefill the operator note when opened from an invoice-attention surface. Used by `CustomerDetail` + `InvoiceAttention`; future surfaces (e.g. dunning detail) plug in trivially.
  - **Per-customer cooldown on send-setup-email.** Redis-backed GCRA limiter at 1 send / (tenant, customer) / 60s. Operator double-click + refresh-then-click no longer ships duplicate emails. Fails open under Redis outage (a Redis hiccup shouldn't block the operator's legitimate action — worst case is two identical emails, no money/state at risk). New `RateLimiter.AllowKey(ctx, key)` exported on `internal/api/middleware/ratelimit.go` so handlers can enforce custom-keyed buckets without going through middleware.

### Added

- **Audit-log coverage sweep + operator-side PM management (2026-05-26).** Closes a thorough audit that found ~12 state-changing flows landing no `audit_log` row — operator Activity feed and AuditLog page were silently missing them. Adds operator-side PM list/setDefault/detach + "send setup link" to match Chargebee/Lago/Orb/Recurly industry shape (no card-data entry, tenant stays in PCI SAQ-A).
  - **Migration 0098:** `audit_log.actor_type` CHECK expands to admit `'customer'`. Customer-portal-driven mutations now log with `actor_type='customer'`, `actor_id=<customer.id>` so the operator Audit Log page renders "by <Customer Name>" instead of the misleading `system` fallback.
  - **Plumbing:** `auth.WithCustomerActor` / `auth.CustomerActorID` ctx helpers; `customerportal.Service.Middleware` now stamps the customer-actor into ctx; `audit.Logger.Log` resolves customer → api_key → system in that order; `audit.Logger.Query` LEFT JOINs `customers` so the AuditLog page surfaces the actual display name.
  - **Portal-driven audit writes** (previously missing — only outbound webhooks fired): subscription cancel, subscription resume (clear scheduled cancel), profile update, pay-now attempt.
  - **Engine auto-fire audit:** `Engine.advanceCycleOrCancel` writes `AuditActionCancel` with `canceled_by='schedule'` when the scheduled cancellation actually fires at period end. Previously the timeline showed "Cancellation scheduled" with no terminal event partner.
  - **Webhook payload normalized:** `subscription.canceled` event ships `canceled_by ∈ {"customer", "operator", "schedule"}` across all three paths (was `triggered_by` for engine, `canceled_by` for portal, nothing for operator).
  - **Operator handler audit gaps:** `invoice.recordOfflinePayment` + `invoice.markUncollectible` (frontend was already rendering `meta.action='payment_recorded'` / `'marked_uncollectible'` — handler-side write was missing, so the render branches were dead code); `customer.update` + `customer.upsertBillingProfile` (tax-status / email / dunning-policy reassignment was silent); `paymentmethods.Service.{AttachFromSetupIntent, SetDefault, Detach}` writes `resource_type='payment_method'`.
  - **Tier 2 audit handlers** — API key (create/revoke/rotate), dunning (policy CRUD + run resolution), pricing (plan/meter/rating-rule/override CRUD + plan updates), test clock (create/advance/retry/delete), Stripe credentials (connect/disconnect/webhook-secret), webhook endpoint (create/delete/rotate-secret/replay). Each gets a forensics row without leaking sensitive values (no raw key, no webhook secret, no PAN).
  - **Operator PM API:** new `/v1/customers/{customer_id}/payment-methods` surface — `GET` lists masked PMs, `POST /{pmID}/default` promotes, `DELETE /{pmID}` detaches, `POST /setup-session` mints a Stripe Checkout SetupSession URL the operator hands to the customer (copy / Slack / SMS), `POST /send-setup-email` mints the session AND dispatches a branded "Add a payment method" email to the customer's address on file in one atomic operator action (optional `note` field prefaces the email body). Backed by the same `paymentmethods.Service` as the existing `/v1/me/payment-methods` portal surface. Industry parity verified against Stripe (Send Payment Method), Chargebee (Request Payment Method), Recurly, Lago, Orb — email is the primary path, copy-link is the fallback for non-email channels.
  - **New email template** `SendPaymentSetupLink` (operator-initiated, no invoice context — distinct from the dunning-context `SendPaymentSetupRequest`). Customizable via the optional operator note; falls back to a generic body emphasizing PCI scope ("your card details go directly to our payment processor and never touch our servers").
  - **CustomerDetail dashboard:** Payment Methods card replaces the legacy single-card panel — lists every attached PM with set-default + remove (with confirm). "Add Card" opens a dialog with the customer's email pre-filled, an optional note field, primary "Send email" button (one-click branded email send), and a secondary "Copy link" path for Slack/SMS/etc. The dialog never exposes the URL on the email path (URL is minted server-side and only the recipient sees it); copy-link mints on demand. Send-email disables with a tooltip when the customer has no email on file.
  - **AuditLog.tsx renders:** `actor_type='customer'` → resolved name; `resource_type='payment_method'` → "Added / Removed / Set as default {brand} ····{last4}"; new sub-action descriptors wired (cancel_cleared, profile_updated, billing_profile_upserted, portal_pay_attempted, resolved, set_default, advanced, retry_advance, replayed, webhook_secret_set, connected, marked_uncollectible, payment_recorded); resource-type filter list extended.
- **Payment-method architecture refactor — `customer_payment_setups` table dropped (2026-05-26).** Completed e2e: the legacy denorm cache table is gone, the `domain.CustomerPaymentSetup` struct survives as a pure wire shape composed at runtime from canonical sources, all readers route through `compositePaymentSetupStore` (no SQL read of the dropped table is possible). The dual-table design lumped three concerns — Stripe Customer ID mapping, default-PM cache, setup-status state machine — into one row that had to be kept in sync with `payment_methods`. Each concern now has a single canonical home.
  - **Migration 0096** adds `customers.stripe_customer_id TEXT` with a partial unique index on `(tenant_id, livemode, stripe_customer_id)`. Backfilled from `customer_payment_setups` (10 rows in local dev). `customers` is now the single source of truth for the 1:1 customer ↔ Stripe Customer mapping.
  - **`payment_methods` is now solely canonical** for PM data. `paymentmethods.Service` no longer writes `customer_payment_setups` — removed `PaymentSetupSummaryWriter` interface and the `syncSummary`/`clearSummary` helpers entirely. Attach/SetDefault/Detach operate on the canonical table only.
  - **`paymentmethods.StripeAdapter.EnsureStripeCustomer`** reads/writes `customers.stripe_customer_id` (via a new `CustomerStripeLink` narrow interface) instead of the summary row.
  - **`customer.PostgresStore.SetStripeCustomerID`** is the single writer for the new column. `Get` exposes the field via the existing `domain.Customer` shape.
  - **Billing engine refactored to read from canonical sources.** `PaymentSetupReader` interface replaced with `PaymentReadiness.ResolveForCharge` — returns `(stripeCustomerID, hasDefaultPM)` in one call. Implementation `paymentReadinessAdapter` queries `customers` + `payment_methods` directly. All 5 call sites in `engine.go` + `threshold_scan.go` migrated.
  - **`compositePaymentSetupStore`** (`internal/api/adapters.go`) presents the legacy `domain.CustomerPaymentSetup` wire shape on top of canonical sources. `GetPaymentSetup` composes the response from `customers.stripe_customer_id` + the default `payment_methods` row; `UpsertPaymentSetup` extracts only the `stripe_customer_id` field and forwards to `customer.PostgresStore.SetStripeCustomerID` (other fields ignored — card details flow through `paymentmethods.Service` via the webhook attach path). Lets the remaining legacy writers (`payment/checkout.go`, `payment/portal.go`, `payment/stripe.go::checkout.session.completed` webhook) keep their `PaymentSetupStore`-shaped wiring without ever touching the dropped table.
  - **Migration 0097** drops the table. `customer.PostgresStore.UpsertPaymentSetup` + `GetPaymentSetup` methods deleted; `customer.Store` interface no longer surfaces them. `customer.PaymentSetupReader` interface stubbed to `interface{}` for back-compat with `SetStripeSyncer` signature (the field is no longer used — sync reads `customers.StripeCustomerID` directly).
  - **GDPR export** no longer includes a `PaymentSetup` block — the Stripe Customer mapping lives on `customers` (already in the export) and PM card details on `payment_methods` rows (non-PII, not surfaced in the export by design).
  - **Tests:** unit suite green. Test fixtures updated (`gdpr_integration_test.go` seeds Stripe Customer via `SetStripeCustomerID`; `full_loop_integration_test.go` asserts canonical `payment_methods` state instead of summary-sync; `testutil/db.go` truncate list trimmed; `paymentmethods/service_test.go` mocks rewritten to assert default-PM via List instead of summary-sync; `billing/engine_test.go::fakePaymentSetups` implements `PaymentReadiness`).
- **Customer portal — Phase 2 completion: billing-details self-edit + multi-PM list management (2026-05-26).** Closes the last two Phase 2 gaps. Customer can now self-edit their display_name + email without operator intervention, and the PM section renders as a list with set-default / remove / add-another affordances (rather than a single-card view).
  - **New `PATCH /v1/me/profile`**: narrow allow-list (display_name + email only, both optional pointers). Status, dunning policy, livemode, tax fields stay operator-only — the portal can't reach them. Reuses `customer.Service.Update` for validation (empty-string ignore, RFC-5322 email regex). Returns the updated profileResponse.
  - **`CustomerUpdater` interface** + `portalCustomerWriterAdapter` in router.go — narrow seam that filters the operator's wider `customer.UpdateInput` down to the self-serve subset. Portal callers structurally cannot mutate the locked fields even if the SPA misbehaves.
  - **Portal UI:**
    - **Billing details card** (above credit balance / PM): inline view → click Edit → form for name + email → Save / Cancel. Validates against the current profile state to skip the network call when nothing changed.
    - **PM section** rebuilt as a list when ≥1 PM exists: each row shows brand + last4 + exp + Default badge + Set-default + Remove buttons. Remove is disabled (with hover tooltip) when removing the last PM would leave the customer with no default. "Add another card" CTA appears below the list. Empty state (zero PMs) keeps the original "No card on file" + Add card affordance.
    - Wired existing `/v1/me/payment-methods/{id}/default` (POST) and `/v1/me/payment-methods/{id}` (DELETE) endpoints — backend was already there; UI just exposes them.
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW CP3 + new CP7** updated with the multi-PM list assertions and PATCH /v1/me/profile contract.
- **Customer portal — Phase 2 self-serve actions: Pay Now, Resume cancel-at-period-end, scheduled-cancel surfacing (2026-05-26).** Three new operator-free actions on the customer portal, matching Stripe / Lago / Chargebee parity for in-portal self-serve. None of these required new domain modeling — every backend primitive already existed (`payment.Stripe.ChargeInvoice`, `subscription.Service.ClearScheduledCancel`); the work was the customer-scoped endpoint wrappers + UI affordances.
  - **New `POST /v1/me/invoices/{id}/pay`** — triggers a real-money charge against the customer's default PM. Pre-flight rejects with 409 + typed code (`invoice_already_paid`, `payment_in_flight`, `invoice_not_payable`, `no_payment_method_on_file`) so the SPA can translate to friendly toasts instead of surfacing raw Stripe errors. 202 Accepted on success since the charge is async; payment_intent.succeeded webhook reconciles final state. Cross-customer guard returns 404 (no enumeration leak).
  - **New `POST /v1/me/subscriptions/{id}/resume`** — undoes a pending `cancel_at_period_end=true` by clearing the scheduled cancel. Already-canceled subs (status=canceled) return 409 `subscription_canceled` — reactivation requires operator intervention because of billing-cycle reset + proration semantics. Fires `subscription.cancel_cleared` webhook with `resumed_by=customer`.
  - **`portalSubscription` payload exposes `cancel_at_period_end`** so the portal UI can distinguish "regular active sub" (shows Cancel button) from "scheduled-to-cancel sub" (shows Resume button, amber pill).
  - **Portal UI:**
    - Sub rows with `cancel_at_period_end=true` get an amber `cancels at period end` badge, a "Will end ... · won't renew" subtitle, and a **Resume** button in place of Cancel.
    - Invoice rows with `status=finalized AND payment_status != succeeded` get a primary **Pay now** button (or "Processing…" when `payment_status=processing`).
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW CP2 + CP6 updated** to cover the new Resume + Pay-now flows.
- **Customer portal — Phase 1 information density: profile, credit balance, PM details, invoice breakdown (2026-05-26).** Continued the portal UX uplift past the PM section's state-aware rendering shipped earlier today. The portal page is no longer a placeholder shell — every section now tells the customer something useful, and the surface matches Stripe + Lago + Chargebee parity for "at-a-glance" personal-billing view.
  - **New `GET /v1/me/profile`**: returns `{customer_id, display_name, email}`. Drives header personalization. Narrow allow-list — no tax status, no livemode, no encrypted-PII raw bytes.
  - **New `GET /v1/me/credit-balance`**: returns `{balance_cents, total_granted, total_used, total_expired, recent_entries[<=10]}`. Recent entries are time-desc, capped at 10 (operator API for full ledger). Empty-state safe — zero balance + zero history → `balance_cents: 0, recent_entries: []` (200, never 4xx).
  - **`CreditReader` interface** + `portalCreditReaderAdapter` in router.go — thin shape bridge so portalapi doesn't gain a reverse dependency on `internal/credit`.
  - **Portal UI:** header now shows `<company_name> · <customer_name> · <email>` when profile loads. New credit-balance card renders above PM section ONLY when balance != 0 OR there are ledger entries (hidden for accounts that never use credits). Card has collapsible "Show history" toggle revealing the recent-entries table with entry_type badges, descriptions, dates, and signed amounts. Invoice rows surface the `credits_applied_cents` API field added yesterday (italic subtitle + right-column sub-line for card-paid portion). Canceled subscription rows correctly say "Ended" not "Next bill".
  - **MANUAL_TEST FLOW CP3 + CP5 rewritten** to match the bootstrap-aware multi-PM surface + the new profile/credit endpoints. FLOW CP3 documents the full self-serve PM lifecycle including set-default and detach.

### Fixed

- **Customer portal PM flow — single source of truth, true self-serve (2026-05-26).** The portal had a legacy `POST /v1/me/payment-method/update` (singular) endpoint that required an existing Stripe Customer (`400 missing_payment_setup` otherwise), forcing an operator-driven initial-setup step before customers could ever add their first card — i.e. NOT self-serve. Meanwhile a complete bootstrap-aware surface already existed at `/v1/me/payment-methods/*` (plural — list, set-default, detach, setup-intent, setup-session) backed by `internal/paymentmethods` with `StripeAdapter.EnsureStripeCustomer` lazily creating the Stripe Customer on first PM action. Two divergent code paths for the same operation.
  - **Removed the legacy endpoint** + its `PaymentMethodUpdater` interface + the `portalPaymentMethodUpdaterAdapter` in `router.go`. portalapi.Handler no longer carries any PM dependencies.
  - **Portal SPA** (`Portal.tsx::handleUpdatePM`) now calls `POST /v1/me/payment-methods/setup-session` — the bootstrap-aware path. Customer with no Stripe Customer can add their first card via the portal without any operator step. Same single button handles both "add first card" and "update existing card".
  - **Industry parity:** Stripe portal / Chargebee self-serve portal / Lago portal all bootstrap the Stripe Customer lazily on first PM action; no platform requires an operator-initiated initial setup. Velox now matches.
  - **End-to-end self-serve loop:** customer requests magic link → clicks email → portal session → clicks "Add card" → portal POSTs to `/setup-session` → `EnsureStripeCustomer` creates the Stripe Customer if missing → Stripe Checkout URL minted → customer adds card → Stripe webhook attaches the PM → portal refresh shows the new card. Zero operator touchpoints.
- **Invoice PDF — ASCII-safe glyphs for channel + tax-reversal lines (2026-05-25).** The PDF render path I shipped earlier today used `→ card` / `→ credit` / `↳ Tax reversed` (Unicode arrows U+2192 / U+21B3), but the embedded Noto Sans subset doesn't cover the Arrows block — those glyphs would render as missing-glyph boxes in the downloaded PDF. Dashboard kept the arrows (browsers have system-font fallback); PDF now reads "to card | to credit | out of band" and "Tax reversed $X (Stripe Tax)" indented as a sub-line. Verified font coverage with `fontTools`: Latin + currency + basic punctuation in; arrows / checkmarks / non-Latin scripts out. Documented the embedded-font character coverage on `internal/pdffonts/fonts.go` so future PDF additions stay within the supported glyph set.
- **Customer-portal magic link dedupes within a tenant — one email per request (Stripe parity, 2026-05-25).** Pre-fix: when multiple customers at the same tenant shared the lookup email (legitimate at-scale data: an AR contact email spread across several legal-entity customers), `RequestByEmail` minted a token and dispatched a magic-link email for EACH match. A single `POST /v1/public/customer-portal/magic-link` could send N emails, confusing the recipient. Industry survey ([Stripe docs verbatim](https://docs.stripe.com/customer-management/configure-portal): *"selects the most recently created customer that has both that email and an active subscription"*; [Chargebee](https://www.chargebee.com/docs/billing/2.0/kb/billing/how-to-prevent-multiple-users-or-subscriptions-with-the-same-email-address): same-email customers route to an account-selection screen after one OTP). Both peers converged on **one email per request**, disambiguating downstream. Fix: new `pickOnePerTenant` helper collapses same-tenant matches to the most-recently-created customer (xid-based IDs are time-sortable lex, so id-desc is created_at-desc — no schema change needed). Cross-tenant matches are preserved: a person who's legitimately a customer of two merchants through Velox still gets one link per merchant.
  - **Customer model unchanged.** Audit confirmed Velox's customer/email design (decisions 1-4 — customer-as-billing-entity, non-unique email, layered customer/billing_profile email, encryption + bidx) matches industry verbatim. Only the magic-link dispatch step was off-pattern.
  - **Tests:** `TestRequestByEmail_SameTenantDuplicateEmail_PicksMostRecent` (two customers at one tenant → 1 delivery to newest), `TestRequestByEmail_CrossTenantDuplicates_StillFanOut` (two tenants, one with duplicates → 2 deliveries with each tenant's newest). Existing `TestMagicLink_FullLoop_E2E` integration test (cross-tenant fan-out) still green.
  - **Operator escape hatch unchanged:** if an older/inactive customer at the same tenant needs portal access, the operator-authenticated `POST /v1/customer-portal-sessions` flow mints a per-customer session directly — bypassing the email-based dedup entirely.
- **Credit note tax — smart-bucket residual absorption to match Stripe Tax (2026-05-25).** Pre-fix: proportional tax via integer-division (`floor(inv.tax × cn.total / inv.total)`) accumulated rounding residuals when an invoice was split into multiple CNs. A $82.60 invoice ($70 net + $12.60 IGST) split into a $2.60 CN + an $80 CN would reverse `$0.39 + $12.20 = $12.59`, leaving a 1-cent gap vs the original `$12.60` invoice tax. Stripe Tax's internal credit-note flow smart-allocates the residual ("rounding errors are allocated to the last line item"), so the gap also showed up as a Velox-vs-Stripe-Dashboard reconciliation discrepancy. Fix: when a CN exhausts the invoice (`existingTotal + subtotal == inv.TotalAmountCents`), `taxAmount = inv.TaxAmountCents − existingTaxReversed` — the exhausting CN absorbs the rounding residual so cumulative tax reversed equals the original tax exactly. Non-exhausting CNs keep pure proportional behavior. Single-source change in `creditnote.Service.Create`; persisted `tax_amount_cents` drives both the dashboard display and the upstream Stripe Tax reversal, so both surfaces converge on the same total.
  - **Tests:** `TestCreate_SmartBucketTaxResidual` asserts a $2.60 + $80 split sums to exactly `$12.60` (cnA=$0.39, cnB=$12.21 — residual absorbed). `TestCreate_PartialCNUsesPureProportional` pins that a single $40 partial CN (doesn't exhaust the invoice) keeps the pure floor() proportional behavior at `$6.10`.
  - **Concurrency caveat (documented, not blocking):** two simultaneous CN creates against the same invoice could both compute "I'm not the last one" if neither sees the other's row. Worst case is the pre-fix residual behavior (1-cent gap), which degrades gracefully. Tightening to a FOR UPDATE lock on the invoice during CN create is deferred — concurrent operator CN creates on the same invoice are vanishingly rare in practice.
- **Invoice PDF + hosted invoice page + portal sync with three-channel CN + tax reversal (2026-05-24).** The dashboard surface and the customer-facing PDF / hosted page had drifted: dashboard rendered "$X → card · $Y → credit · $Z → out of band · ↳ Tax reversed" while the PDF still showed only "(refunded)" / "(credited to balance)" and the filter that decides pre-payment vs post-payment CNs ignored the out-of-band channel — meaning an OOB-only CN was wrongly classified as pre-payment and reduced the invoice's apparent total.
  - **`CreditNoteInfo` struct** in `internal/invoice/pdf.go` gains `OutOfBandAmountCents`, `TaxAmountCents`, `TaxTransactionID`.
  - **Pre-payment / post-payment classifier** now checks all three channels (`refund OR credit OR out_of_band > 0` → post-payment); OOB-only CNs correctly render as post-payment adjustments.
  - **Completed CN filter** now treats credit-balance grants AND out-of-band amounts as immediate-at-issue (only the refund leg requires `refund_status=succeeded` before display).
  - **Post-payment row layout** matches the dashboard: channel-breakdown line (`$X → card · $Y → credit · $Z → out of band`) plus a `↳ Tax reversed $W (Stripe Tax)` or `↳ Tax: $W (no upstream provider)` sub-fact when the CN reversed tax.
  - **Three construction sites updated** to pass the new fields: `invoice.handler.go` (operator PDF download), `hostedinvoice.handler.go` (public hosted page), `portalapi.handler.go` (customer portal). Single struct definition keeps them in sync.
  - **Preview surface** (`/v1/invoices/create_preview`) is line-item-only — no CN data, no tax in projection. Verified no changes needed.
  - **Tests:** `TestRenderPDF_ThreeChannelCN_WithTaxReversal` exercises the full split-with-tax render; `TestRenderPDF_OutOfBandOnlyCN_IsPostPayment` is a regression guard for the filter bug that would have under-rendered the invoice total on OOB-only CNs.
- **Invoice Void + MarkUncollectible now reverse the upstream tax transaction (2026-05-24).** Pre-fix: voiding a finalized-but-unpaid invoice (or writing it off as uncollectible via the operator action / dunning final action) flipped status locally but left the Stripe Tax `tax_transaction` (committed at finalize time) untouched — Stripe Tax dashboard kept reporting the tax as collected, over-reporting tax liability to the authority. Industry mandate (Stripe Tax docs verbatim: *"When an invoice is voided or marked uncollectible, you must reverse the corresponding tax transaction to keep your tax records accurate"*).
  - **New `invoice.TaxReverser` interface** + `Service.SetTaxReverser` wiring. Implemented by `billing.Engine` (same code path as credit-note tax reversal). Wired in `internal/api/router.go::SetTaxReverser(engine)`.
  - **`Void` + `MarkUncollectible`** both call `ReverseTax(Mode=Full)` against `inv.TaxTransactionID` before the status flip. Best-effort: failures log `WARN` but never block the state transition — the invoice is the operator's primary record and must stay flippable even when the upstream provider is unreachable. Manual reconciliation surfaces in `slog`.
  - **Distinct `Reference` per path** — `inv_void_<id>` vs `inv_uncoll_<id>` — so retries converge cleanly and the two flows can't collide on Stripe's Reference uniqueness constraint.
  - **Skipped paths:** draft invoices (no upstream tax_transaction yet), manual/none providers (no upstream state), legacy invoices pre-dating `invoice.tax_transaction_id`. The `inv.TaxTransactionID != ""` guard handles all three uniformly.
  - **`tax.ReversalRequest.Reference` field** added (back-compat falls through to the older `CreditNoteID` field). Lets non-CN callers (invoice void / uncollectible) supply their own unique identifier.
  - **Stripe SDK `IdempotencyKey: "velox_tax_rev_<reference>"`** now passed on every `V1TaxTransactions.CreateReversal` call.
