Matches the refund-idempotency pattern; defense-in-depth against transient network failures between Stripe accepting the request and the SDK returning. Stripe's Reference uniqueness gave semantic dedup; the IdempotencyKey gives transport-level dedup.
  - **Dashboard surfaces the tax reversal.** `CreditNote` TypeScript interface now exposes `tax_amount_cents` + `tax_transaction_id`. Invoice detail's post-payment adjustments row appends `· $6.10 tax reversed` when present, with the upstream `tax_tx_xxx` in a hover title so operators can cross-reference in Stripe Dashboard. Backend always returned these fields; the frontend just wasn't reading them.
  - **Tests:** `TestVoid_ReversesUpstreamTaxTransaction` (3 sub-cases — happy path, upstream failure still voids, skipped when no tax_transaction) + `TestMarkUncollectible_ReversesUpstreamTaxTransaction` (locks Reference distinct from void). `fakeTaxReverser` mock in `internal/invoice/service_test.go`.
- **Dashboard credit grant/deduct now send `Idempotency-Key` (2026-05-24).** Closes a real money risk: a double-click or transient-network-retry on the Grant or Deduct button would create two ledger entries. The API-level idempotency middleware (`mw.Idempotency(db)`) was already wrapped around all `/v1/*` writes, but `web-v2/src/lib/api.ts::adjustCredits` and `grantCredits` weren't passing a key — the dashboard relied on its own retry behavior alone. Industry-standard SDK pattern (Stripe SDK auto-generates UUIDv4 on POSTs; Lago / Orb / Chargebee similar): every state-changing call carries a key. Velox's coupon SDK already followed this; credit grant + deduct were missed in the original rollout. Fix: `apiRequest` accepts an optional `idempotencyKey` and sets the `Idempotency-Key` header; `CreditDialog` generates `crypto.randomUUID()` once per dialog open and passes it through. A retry within the same dialog session replays through the middleware and converges on the original ledger entry; a fresh dialog open gets a new key so a deliberate second deduct still posts a second entry.
- **Credit ledger — per-block `consumed_cents` attribution for ALL negative entries (Orb credit-block model, 2026-05-24).** Symptom that surfaced the bug: a customer with $30 actual balance + an open grant carrying $80 remaining-to-drain (because a prior $50 clawback adjustment reduced balance without bumping any grant's consumed_cents) got an $80 invoice fully credited via `ApplyToInvoiceAtomic`, driving the ledger to -$50. Same drift made `processExpiry` over-deduct on grant expiry. Root cause: only `usage` entries (via `ApplyToInvoiceAtomic`) attributed to grants' consumed_cents; clawback adjustments mutated balance globally without per-block attribution. The drain query was also scoped to `entry_type='grant'`, so positive adjustments (goodwill credits) and invoice-void reversals inflated balance but were not drainable.
  - **`drainPositiveBlocks` helper** centralizes the FIFO drain across any positive ledger entry (grants + positive adjustments + reversals — anything with `amount_cents > 0` and `consumed_cents < amount_cents`). Used by both `ApplyToInvoiceAtomic` (usage) and `AdjustAtomic` (clawback). Returns the actual drained amount so callers handle partial-application uniformly.
  - **Negative `AdjustAtomic`** now FIFO-drains positive blocks inside the same transaction as the adjustment entry insert. Balance and `sum(block.remaining)` stay reconciled — the invariant `balance == drainable` holds for every operation that follows.
  - **`ApplyToInvoiceAtomic` drain query** drops the `entry_type='grant'` filter — goodwill positive adjustments and CN reversals now fund invoices like grants do.
  - **Per `feedback_no_belt_and_suspenders`**: removed the `drawCap = min(invoice, balance)` cap I'd added as a defense-in-depth — once attribution is correct, `drainable == balance` and the helper naturally caps at drainable. Same with the "drainable short of drain" error in the helper — unreachable in a clean ledger, so dropped.
  - **Tests:** `TestApplyToInvoiceAtomic_CapsAtCurrentBalance` reproduces the original drift symptom; `TestAdjustAtomic_ClawbackAttributesToGrants` verifies FIFO consumed_cents bumps across two grants; `TestApplyToInvoiceAtomic_DrainsPositiveAdjustments` proves goodwill credits fund invoices. All three are integration tests against postgres.
  - **Note on legacy drift:** pre-launch (zero customers), the only drift is in the dev box's ledger. New ledgers stay consistent. The user's local customer with the -$50 balance needs the ledger reset; no production backfill needed per `feedback_no_speculative_backfill`.
- **`credit.Service.Adjust` + `credit.Service.ReverseForInvoice` now bind effective-now from the customer pin (2026-05-24).** Symptom: a manual deduct (or invoice void / dunning writeoff) on a clock-pinned customer stamped the ledger entry's `created_at` at wall-clock-now instead of the customer's simulated time, making the row appear out-of-band on the Credits tab. Root cause: `Grant` called `bindForCustomer(ctx, …)`; `Adjust` and `ReverseForInvoice` didn't. Audit follow-up to `feedback_ctx_attr_audit` — same bug class as the test-clock async-catchup tenant_id pin from 2026-05-04 (a ctx-detached path missed an attribute the resolver depended on). Fix: both methods now bind ctx at the top, matching `Grant`. `PostgresStore.AdjustAtomic` already read `clock.Now(ctx)` correctly — the gap was upstream. memStore.AdjustAtomic in unit tests updated to mirror the postgres behaviour so the missing bind can't slip past tests again. New sub-case `TestAdjust/clock-pinned_customer_stamps_ledger_at_sim_time` locks in the contract.

### Added

- **Credit notes — three-channel allocation (Stripe + Lago shape, 2026-05-24).** Replaces the binary `RefundType: "refund" | "credit"` dropdown with three explicit allocation fields on the create payload: `refund_amount_cents` (Stripe refund to the original PM), `credit_amount_cents` (restored to customer credit balance), `out_of_band_amount_cents` (handled outside Velox — cash, ACH, manual adjustment; audit-trail only). The three fields must sum to the CN total for paid invoices.
  - **Industry research (verified across 6 platforms 2026-05-24):** No major billing engine does "auto-split" the way Velox previously framed it. Stripe and Lago both expose three explicit allocation fields with a sum invariant; Chargebee picks the type from invoice status; Orb keeps everything in customer balance; Recurly offers ordered priority (credit-first vs transaction-first); Metronome doesn't support refunds at all. The dominant pattern is **operator-explicit allocation** — Stripe + Lago alignment chosen for Velox.
  - **Migration 0094** adds `out_of_band_amount_cents BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0 CHECK (>= 0)` to `credit_notes`.
  - **Validation:** sum = total (after tax), `refund_amount_cents ≤ AmountPaidCents − prior refunds` (the PM-refundable cap), all amounts ≥ 0. Error message steers the operator to `credit_amount_cents` or `out_of_band_amount_cents` when refund exceeds PM-paid.
  - **Default:** on a paid invoice with all three fields zero and no legacy `RefundType`, defaults to `credit_amount_cents = total` (Orb-style — no cash movement, restorable later).
  - **Legacy `RefundType` still honored** as a single-channel shortcut when the three explicit fields are zero. Existing SDK callers don't break.
  - **Removes** the previous strict-reject error for `RefundType=refund` with subtotal > pmRefundable — replaced by per-channel validation (`refund_amount_cents` itself is capped, the rest of the total can be routed to credit or out-of-band).
  - **Dashboard:** Issue-credit-note dialog now shows three amount inputs (Refund to card / Credit balance / Outside Stripe) with a live "Allocated $X / $Y ✓" indicator and auto-balance — typing in Refund auto-fills the Credit remainder so the simple case stays one input + Save. CN list view labels rows with the actual channel breakdown ("refund + credit") instead of a binary Refund/Credit; CSV export adds Refund/Credit/Out-of-band columns. Invoice detail's post-payment adjustments block surfaces each CN's per-channel split.
  - **Tests:** 8 new sub-cases in `TestCreate_ExplicitAllocation` — refund+credit split (the $80 CN on $82.60 invoice example), three-channel split, default-when-all-zero, sum mismatch reject, refund > pmRefundable reject, negative-amount reject, out-of-band-only on credit-paid invoice, legacy `RefundType` translation.
- **Coupon `MaxRedemptionsPerCustomer` race fix + voided-redemption exclusion (2026-05-24).** Pre-fix: the per-customer cap check ran in `validateRedeem` BEFORE the coupon FOR UPDATE lock in `RedeemAtomic`. Two concurrent redeems by the same customer both saw `current=cap-1`, both passed, both committed → customer ended up with `cap+1` redemptions. Fix: re-check inside `RedeemAtomic` after the lock — the second redeem serializes behind the first, sees `current=cap`, and is rejected.
  - **New gate `GatePerCustomerMaxed`** in the store + corresponding service-layer translation to the existing `CodePerCustomerMaxed` error code.
  - **Voided-redemption exclusion.** Both `CountRedemptionsByCustomer` (pre-tx service check) and the inline `RedeemAtomic` count now filter `WHERE voided_at IS NULL`. A customer whose redemption was voided (via `VoidRedemptionsForInvoice` when an invoice was fully credited or refunded) can now re-redeem the coupon up to the cap — pre-fix they'd be locked out because the voided row still counted.
  - **Tests:** `TestRedeem_PerCustomerCapEnforcedInsideTx` asserts the 3rd redemption hits the gate; `TestRedeem_VoidedRedemptionsDontCountTowardPerCustomerCap` verifies the voided-row exclusion. mockStore mirrors the postgres filter.
  - **Bug B (`FirstTimeCustomerOnly` race) deferred:** the "has succeeded invoice" check has a cross-domain dependency (invoice store), and the race scenario (customer redeeming two first-time-only coupons in parallel) is hypothetical at zero customers. Documented as known limitation.
- **Consistent past-expires_at rejection across operator-facing expiry inputs (2026-05-24).** Auditing for the same DOA bug class found two more sites:
  - **`auth.Service.CreateKey`** — NO validation on `ExpiresAt`; operator could create an API key that expires immediately. Now rejects with 422 (`must be in the future`). Wall-clock comparison (API keys are tenant-level, not customer-scoped).
  - **`coupon.Service.Create`** — used `Before(time.Now())` which allowed `expires_at == now` (also DOA). Tightened to `!After(time.Now())` for strict-future, matching the credit-grant gate.
  - **Already safe (verified): subscription `cancel_at`, `resumes_at`, `ExtendTrial` newTrialEnd, testclock `Advance` frozen_time, subscription `TrialDays` (must be > 0).**
  - Tests: 4 new sub-cases in `TestCreateKey_PastExpiresAt` (past rejected, ==now rejected, future accepted, nil accepted).
- **`credit.Service.Grant` rejects past `expires_at` (2026-05-24).** Operator-driven grants with `expires_at <= now` are now rejected with 422 instead of silently creating a dead-on-arrival grant that auto-expires on the next clock advance. Industry parity (Stripe credit-grant API returns 422 on past expires_at). Comparison uses `clock.Now(ctx)` — the `bindForCustomer` seeded ctx with the sim clock for clock-pinned customers, so the gate evaluates in the customer's reference frame, not wall-clock. Internal engine callers (`BillOnCancel` / `BillOnPlanSwapImmediate` / CN `Issue` `GrantForCreditNote`) don't set `ExpiresAt` on their grants, so refund flows are unaffected. Tests: 4 new sub-cases in `TestGrant` — past expires_at rejected, expires_at == now rejected, future accepted, nil (forever credit) accepted.
- **Credit-note operator-retry for stuck Stripe refunds (Bug D + E completion, 2026-05-22).** Closes the last gap from the credit-note audit: a CN can issue successfully but the Stripe-refund leg can fail (Stripe outage / network error) or land in `pending` state (Stripe not connected at Issue time). Industry parity (Stripe `credit_notes.refunds` array): the CN is a financial document that stays in its final state while the refund leg has its own status and is independently retriable.
  - **New service method `creditnote.Service.RetryRefund(ctx, tenantID, id)`** re-attempts the Stripe refund for an already-issued CN. Uses the SAME idempotency key as `Issue()` (`velox_cn_<id>`) so a retry after "Stripe actually succeeded but Velox lost the response" scenario converges — Stripe returns the existing refund_id, Velox persists it. Rejects on: status != issued (drafts use Issue, voided is terminal); refund_status not in (failed, pending); credit-only CN with no refund leg; missing refunder / PaymentIntent.
  - **New endpoint `POST /v1/credit-notes/{id}/retry-refund`** wired through `handler.retryRefund`.
  - **SDK `api.retryCreditNoteRefund(id)`** added to `web-v2/src/lib/api.ts`.
  - **Dashboard "Retry refund" button** on `/credit-notes` rows where `status=issued` and `refund_status in (failed, pending)`. Disabled when the mutation is in flight; success/failure surfaced via toast.
  - **Tests:** 5 sub-cases in `TestRetryRefund` covering successful retry (asserts same idempotency key as Issue), reject on already-succeeded, reject on draft, reject on credit-only CN, reject when invoice has no PI.
- **Credit-note `Issue()` retry-safe credit-grant dedup (Bug B fix, 2026-05-22).** Migration **0093** adds `source_credit_note_id` to `customer_credit_ledger` + partial unique index `idx_credit_ledger_credit_note_dedup` (`WHERE source_credit_note_id IS NOT NULL`). `credit.Service.GrantForCreditNote(ctx, tenantID, cnID, input)` is the retry-safe variant — sets the column on the new row; on ErrAlreadyExists fetches the existing grant via `GetByCreditNoteSource`. `creditnote.Service.Issue()` now uses `GrantForCreditNote` instead of `Grant`. A retry after partial-failure of Issue() can no longer create a duplicate grant row → no customer over-crediting. `fakeCreditGranter` test mock mirrors the dedup behavior.
  - **Concurrent-Issue safety, summarized.** Two operators clicking Issue simultaneously on the same draft CN both pass the in-service `cn.Status != Draft` check, both run side effects: (1) Stripe refund is deduped by the `velox_cn_<id>` idempotency key — effectively ONE refund; (2) credit grant is deduped by migration 0093 partial unique index — effectively ONE grant. Both then UPDATE `status` to issued — idempotent same-value writes. End state is correct without any additional CAS / lock. (We considered a `UPDATE ... WHERE status='draft'` CAS guard but reverted as redundant secondary mechanism per `feedback_no_belt_and_suspenders`.)
- **Credit-note `Issue()` retry-safe: Stripe refund idempotency key + persist-refund-id-immediately (2026-05-22).** Audit caught a real money-loss bug: `creditnote/service.go::Issue()` called Stripe's refund API with NO idempotency key, AND persisted `stripe_refund_id` AFTER the credit-grant step. If the credit-grant step failed (DB hiccup), the function returned an error with the CN still `status=draft` and the refund_id never persisted. Operator retries → Stripe called again with no dedup → **DUPLICATE refund** → customer over-refunded.
  - **Fix 1 — Stripe idempotency key.** `payment.StripeRefunder.CreateRefund` now takes an `idempotencyKey` parameter. `Issue()` passes `velox_cn_<cn_id>` (deterministic, same key on every retry of the same CN). Stripe's idempotency contract: same key + same params → cached response, no duplicate refund.
  - **Fix 2 — persist refund result IMMEDIATELY after Stripe success, before any other side effects.** The `UpdateRefundStatus` call moved from post-credit-grant-post-tax-reversal to immediately after the Stripe call returns. Even if downstream steps fail, the refund_id is durable on retry.
  - **Fix 3 — guard on `cn.StripeRefundID == ""` so retries skip the Stripe call entirely** when the prior attempt's refund was persisted. The Stripe idempotency key is defense-in-depth for the rare case where Stripe succeeded but our local persist failed.
  - **`Refunder` interface signature change** propagated to all callers + the `fakeRefunder` test mock. `internal/api/router.go` wiring unaffected (interface-driven).
  - **Tests:** `TestIssue_PassesIdempotencyKeyToStripe` asserts the deterministic key shape; `TestIssue_SkipsStripeRefundIfAlreadyRefunded` simulates the retry-with-pre-existing-refund-id case and asserts the Stripe call count is 0.
  - **Known-deferred limitations:** (1) duplicate credit-grant on retry — the CN-driven `s.credits.Grant(...)` call lacks a CN-level dedup since `idx_credit_ledger_proration_dedup` only matches subscription-source grants. Mitigation: the narrow remaining window is "credit grant succeeded → UpdateStatus failed → retry creates 2nd grant." Documented in code as needing a follow-up migration (add `source_credit_note_id` column + partial unique index). (2) Concurrent `Issue(cn)` calls by two operators can each pass the `status != Draft` check and both proceed; Stripe idempotency key catches the refund-side double-call, but the credit-grant path has no concurrent protection. Mitigation: `UPDATE ... WHERE status='draft' RETURNING` CAS guard is the proper fix — also deferred.
- **Credit-note `RefundType='refund'` strict reject when amount > PM-refundable (2026-05-22).** When operator explicitly picks "Refund -- return to payment method" in the dashboard, the server now REJECTS amounts above what was actually charged via PM rather than silently auto-splitting the excess to credit balance. Reasoning: Velox's UI presents Refund vs Credit as an explicit binary choice (Lago/Chargebee shape) — silently routing 30 of the operator's $80 refund to credit balance would violate that contract. Operator's options on reject: lower the amount to the PM-refundable max, switch to `RefundType='credit'` for the full amount, or issue two CNs (one refund-type, one credit-type). `RefundType='credit'` remains unrestricted (operator can credit the customer up to the combined PM+credit refundable cap). Tests updated to verify the new reject behavior at the edge cases (credit-only-paid invoice rejects refund-type with helpful steering error; mixed-paid invoice rejects when amount > PM portion; refund at exactly PM max succeeds).
- **Credit-note refund routes back to source payment (Stripe + Lago industry rule, 2026-05-22).** When an invoice was paid partially or fully via customer credits (`customer_credit_ledger` drainage), a refund-type credit note now correctly splits between Stripe-PM refund and credit-balance restoration. Pre-fix bug: refund-type CN on a 100%-credit-paid invoice set `refund_amount_cents=subtotal` but `Issue()` couldn't actually refund (no PI), leaving `refund_status=pending` forever AND the credits never restored — customer effectively out the refund amount.
  - **Industry verification (verbatim from docs):**
    - Stripe customer-balance: *"If you issue a credit note for 50 USD or less, the funds are refunded to the customer's payment method. Anything above 50 USD is added to the customer's credit balance."*
    - Lago wallet: *"On subscription invoices, prepaid credits and credit notes applied cannot be refunded. These can only be credited back to the customer's account balance."*
  - **Rule implemented:** `refund_amount = min(subtotal, pmRefundable)` + `credit_amount = subtotal - refund_amount`. PM-portion exhausted first (Stripe rule), excess auto-routes to credit balance (Lago rule). Both can be non-zero on the same credit note for mixed-paid invoices.
  - **Tracking:** `pmRefundable = AmountPaidCents - sum(existing CN refund_amount_cents, non-voided)`. `creditRefundable = CreditsAppliedCents - sum(existing CN credit_amount_cents, non-voided)`. Caps prevent over-refunding either channel.
  - **`RefundType="credit"` semantics preserved:** operator can still explicitly choose credit-only (e.g. courtesy credit on a Stripe-paid invoice), honored verbatim.
  - **Tests:** `TestCreate_CreditNote` adds 4 sub-cases — PM-paid full refund, credit-only-paid full restore-to-credits, mixed-paid split per Stripe rule, refund within PM portion stays 100% PM, over-cap rejection. Updates the pre-existing "refund for paid invoice" test fixture which was incomplete (didn't set `AmountPaidCents`).
- **`MarkPaid` invariant — invoice state-machine gate on the store (2026-05-22).** Adds a hard guard at `invoice/postgres.go::MarkPaid`: status must be one of `finalized` / `uncollectible` / `paid` (idempotent), and `tax_status` must be `ok`. Returns `errs.InvalidState` otherwise. Closes a real customer-visible bug where `billOnePeriod`'s "credits cover 100% → mark paid immediately" branch transitioned a tax-pending draft directly to paid — locking the customer at subtotal-only ($7000 total, $0 tax) and blocking tax retry forever (retry requires `status='draft'`, but status was now `paid`). Invoice `DEMO-000906` reproduced the bug; gate prevents it across all callers.
  - **Engine caller-level gates (defense-in-depth):** `billOnePeriod`'s and `threshold_scan`'s credit-fully-paid blocks now skip `MarkPaid` unless `inv.Status == finalized`. For draft (tax-pending / pause-collection) invoices that get fully covered by credits, the credits stay applied and the invoice stays draft; tax retry's auto-finalize chain transitions draft → finalized → paid once tax resolves.
  - **Auto-pay chain after tax-retry auto-finalize:** `Service.RetryTax` now chains into `MarkPaid` when the post-finalize `amount_due_cents <= 0` (i.e., credits applied at draft time already covered the new tax-included total). Closes the loop on the tax-pending + credit-cover scenario.
  - **Audit (2026-05-22) of all paths that transition invoice state:** confirmed the bug pattern existed at exactly 2 sites (`billOnePeriod` + `threshold_scan`). `BillOnCreate`, `BillFinalOnImmediateCancel`, `Cancel`, dunning resolutions, Stripe webhooks, reconciler — all operate on already-finalized invoices and pass the new store gate. `Service.RecordOfflinePayment` had its own service-level gate at line 460-462 (already correct). `Finalize` blocks `tax_status` pending/failed (already correct). `Void` / `MarkUncollectible` have state-machine gates at service level (already correct).
  - **Tests:** `TestMarkPaid_StoreGate_RejectsDraftAndTaxPending` (6 sub-cases: rejects draft, rejects tax_status=pending on finalized, rejects voided, allows finalized + tax_status=ok, allows uncollectible recovery, idempotent on already-paid). In-memory mocks in `internal/billing/engine_test.go::mockInvoices` and `internal/invoice/service_test.go::memStore` mirror the postgres gate so the invariant is enforced in unit tests too.
- **Credit-ledger adopts Orb's credit-block model — `consumed_cents` per grant (2026-05-22).** Velox's flat-ledger model previously tracked `balance = SUM(amount_cents)` with no per-grant remaining state, which had two production bugs visible on the customer Credits page:
  - **Bug A — expiring a fully-consumed grant double-debits the balance.** A $50 grant followed by a $50 usage drains the balance to $0; the expiry CRON then appended a -$50 row, taking balance to -$50. Without per-grant remaining tracking, the expiry had no way to know the grant was already drained.
  - **Bug B — expiry row's `created_at` lands at wall-clock today, not the grant's `expires_at`.** Two compounding causes: (1) `ListExpiredGrants*` queries omitted `expires_at` from the SELECT, so `processExpiry` couldn't stamp the expiry row at the grant's actual expiry instant; (2) the catchup orchestrator didn't bind ctx via `clock.WithEffectiveNow`, so the store's `clock.Now(ctx)` fallback returned wall-clock instead of the simulated time.
  - **Industry shape (verified 2026-05-22 from Orb docs):** balance = sum of remaining across unexpired credit blocks; usage FIFO-drains blocks by soonest-expiring then earliest-created; expiry deducts the BLOCK'S REMAINING, not the original amount. Velox adopts the same shape.
  - **Migration 0092** adds `consumed_cents BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` to `customer_credit_ledger` with a CHECK constraint (`>= 0 AND (entry_type != 'grant' OR consumed_cents <= amount_cents)`) and a partial index `idx_credit_ledger_active_grants` for the FIFO-drainage scan.
  - **`ApplyToInvoiceAtomic` refactored to FIFO-drain active grants.** Scans grants ordered by `(expires_at NULLS LAST, created_at, id)`, deducts from each grant up to its remaining (`amount_cents - consumed_cents`), updates `consumed_cents` per grant, and writes one summary usage row. Skips expired grants (they don't contribute to balance — the expiry path will retire them).
  - **`processExpiry` deducts only remaining.** For each candidate grant: `remaining = amount_cents - consumed_cents`; if 0, skip; else append expiry row with `amount_cents = -remaining` stamped at the grant's `expires_at`. `ListExpiredGrants` + `ListExpiredGrantsForClock` now SELECT `expires_at` + `consumed_cents` and filter `consumed_cents < amount_cents` so already-drained grants don't even reach `processExpiry`.
  - **Catchup ctx binding (`testclock/service.go`).** The orchestrator now reads `frozen_time` once at the top of `runOneJob` and binds it via `clock.WithEffectiveNow(ctx, frozen)`. Every downstream phase inherits — including `clock.Now(ctx)` fallbacks deep in stores. The duplicate frozen-time read for Phases 4 + 5 was consolidated.
  - **Tests:** `TestProcessExpiry_SkipsFullyConsumed` (fully-drained grant → no ledger row), `TestProcessExpiry_DeductRemaining` (partially-drained → expiry deducts remaining only AND stamps `created_at` at `expires_at`).
  - **e2e verified against `make dev`** on a real Postgres-backed instance:
    - Bug B fix: fresh grant with sim-past `expires_at`, advance clock → expiry row's `created_at` = grant's `expires_at` (not wall-clock today).
    - Bug A fix: grant with `consumed_cents == amount_cents` (simulated drain), advance clock → 0 expiry rows created for that grant.
  - **Historical bug-artifact rows in existing deployments stay in place** (the pre-fix expiry row at wall-clock today with `amount_cents = -full_grant`). Operator cleanup is a one-line SQL: `DELETE FROM customer_credit_ledger WHERE entry_type='expiry' AND created_at > '<sim_now>'` followed by a balance reconciliation pass.
- **Immediate same-cadence cross-interval plan-swap (yearly ↔ monthly) — industry alignment (2026-05-22).** Velox previously rejected `immediate=true` plan-swaps that changed the billing interval. 2026-05-22 industry verification across Stripe / Lago / Orb / Chargebee / Recurly with quoted source lines confirmed cross-interval immediate swap is documented across peers — all allow it, though they split on mechanics: Stripe / Lago prorate the unused portion (like Velox), while Recurly / Chargebee restart the term unprorated. Reject dropped for same-cadence cross-interval; cross-cadence (in_advance ↔ in_arrears) remains rejected for billing-safety (prepay/postpay overlap) — matching Zuora, while Stripe permits it in-place (offloading the overlap to the operator); Lago (per-plan `pay_in_advance`) documents same-cadence transitions only.
  - **Engine `BillOnPlanSwapImmediate(sub, at)`** issues a refund credit grant for the unused `(at, period_end)` portion of an OLD in_advance period — mirrors `BillOnCancel`'s refund math + paid-check gate (no credit if the source in_advance invoice wasn't paid). Caller invokes BEFORE applying the swap so plan lookups still resolve the outgoing rate. No-op for OLD in_arrears plans.
  - **Engine `emitBaseSegmentLine` segment-skip (Pass 1).** The segment-aware in_arrears branch of `billOnePeriod` (Pass 1, currently-present items) now skips segments whose plan is in_advance — matches the Pass 2 (removed items) and `BillFinalOnImmediateCancel` guards already in place. Defense-in-depth against future changes that might loosen the cross-cadence reject; doesn't itself enable any new flow. Regression test `TestRunCycle_SegmentAware_SkipsInAdvanceSegment` locks the contract.
  - **Stub-period refund denominator fix.** `BillOnCancel` + `BillOnPlanSwapImmediate` switched denominator from `periodDays` to `fullCycleDays` to avoid over-refund on stub periods. On a 7-of-30 stub the customer paid `baseFee × 7/30`; pre-fix the unused refund was `baseFee × unusedDays / 7` which returned up to the full baseFee. Now refund is `baseFee × unusedDays / fullCycleDays` — matches the prepaid amount. Regression test `TestBillOnPlanSwapImmediate/stub_period_refund_uses_fullCycleDays` locks the contract. Verified e2e against a clock-pinned in_advance sub: 7-day stub at $70/mo, mid-stub swap → refund 1633c = $16.33 (= $70 × 7/30); pre-fix would have been $70 (over-refund). Latent bug fix unrelated to the orchestrator — fixes stub-period cancel refunds too.
  - **Service `applyCrossIntervalPlanSwap` orchestrator** branches by cadence:
    - **in_advance** (both sides): refund unused OLD → apply swap → jump `current_period` to `(now, NextBillingPeriodEnd for NEW interval)` → synchronous `BillOnCreate` (stub-prorated if calendar snap shortens it).
    - **in_arrears** (both sides): plan swap applied; period truncated to `(oldPS, now)` with `next_billing_at=now`. Scheduler closes the partial period under OLD plan rate via segment-aware billing, then opens NEW period under NEW plan's interval.
  - **Handler `OrchestratedCrossAxis` flag.** `ItemChangeResult` carries a `OrchestratedCrossAxis bool` set when the service took the orchestrator path. The handler skips its legacy `handleItemProration` block when this is true — without the guard, a cross-interval swap would emit a second credit on top of the orchestrator's refund (the legacy block's paid-check gate isn't tight enough; a freshly auto-charged new in_advance invoice would pass).
  - **Operator UX:** for in_advance swaps the new invoice + refund credit materialize immediately; for in_arrears swaps the closing invoice materializes on the next scheduler tick (consistent with every other in_arrears cycle close in Velox).
  - **Tests:** `TestBillOnPlanSwapImmediate` (5 sub-cases including stub-period); `TestRunCycle_SegmentAware_SkipsInAdvanceSegment` (defense-in-depth segment skip); service tests in `TestPeriodAnchoring` cover the in_advance-jump path, the in_arrears-truncate path, and the cross-cadence reject (both immediate and scheduled).
  - **e2e verified against `make dev`** on a real Postgres-backed instance: clock-pinned in_advance sub, monthly $70 → yearly $120 cross-interval swap on a 7-day calendar-snap stub. Artifacts: refund grant 1633c ($70 × 7/30), plan swapped, period jumped (now, +1y), `BillOnCreate` synced the new $120 yearly invoice, audit `subscription.item_updated` written, no double-credit.
- **Shared `DatePicker` upgraded to dropdown captions (month + year selectors).** Pre-fix, jumping to a year far from today required clicking the prev/next arrows ~12 times per year — first surfaced on the pause-collection resume-date picker. Now uses react-day-picker's `captionLayout="dropdown"` (Stripe / Linear / Vercel dashboard pattern) — month and year are both selectable dropdowns sitting between the arrows, which still work for fine adjustments. Year range bounded by `startMonth` (5 years past, or `minDate.year` when provided so disabled years don't pollute the menu) and `endMonth` (10 years future — covers annual-billing trial extensions and credit-grant expiries). Change lives in the shared component, so all 9 callers inherit automatically (Pause-collection, Extend-trial, Coupons, ApiKeys, Invoices, AuditLog, Credits, UsageEvents, CouponDetail, TestClocks via `DateTimePicker`).
- **Calendar-billing subs auto-realign at cycle close (Velox-specific divergence from preserve-anchor industry norm).** Adopts a position partway between Stripe-flexible/Lago/Chargebee (always preserve day-of-month) and Stripe-legacy/Recurly (always re-anchor on interval change): **respect the operator's configured `billing_time`**. Calendar+monthly cycles snap to first-of-next-month at every cycle close, even when the prior period started mid-month (e.g. inherited from a yearly→monthly plan swap). Anniversary subs preserve day-of-month as before (unchanged).
  - New `domain.NextBillingPeriodEnd(periodEnd, billingTime, interval, loc)` is the canonical cycle-close boundary computation, shared between `subscription.Service` (initial activation / trial-end / reset) and `billing.Engine` (cycle close).
  - The legacy interval-only `advanceBillingPeriod(from, interval)` is kept for non-cycle-close contexts (segment-length computation, in_advance base-fee projection, cancel-proration math) where we want the natural interval roll regardless of `billing_time`. The three cycle-close call sites in `engine.go` are migrated to the new helper.
  - Existing subs whose anchor drifted in the past now self-heal on the next cycle close — no migration, no operator action required (user explicitly said "don't worry about old data, new flows should work correctly").
  - Two regression tests lock the contract: `TestRunCycle_CalendarMonthly_AutoRealignsOnCycleClose` (May 20 → Jun 20 calendar+monthly → next period correctly anchors May 20 → Jul 1 stub then snaps to day-1) and `TestRunCycle_AnniversaryMonthly_PreservesDayOfMonth` (negative guard: anniversary keeps day-20).
- **In_advance cycle-close stub proration fix (2026-05-21).** User-surfaced: yearly→monthly scheduled plan-change on a calendar-billing in_advance sub. At cycle close (yearly anniversary), the engine correctly applied the pending plan, computed the new period via `domain.NextBillingPeriodEnd` = `(yearly_end, first-of-next-month)` (7-day calendar-snap stub for a Jun 24 swap), then **billed the full monthly $70 base for the 7-day stub instead of $16.33 prorated**. `billOnePeriod`'s in_advance branch (line 1759-1796) lacked the `periodDays < fullCycleDays` proration check that `BillOnCreate` and `emitBaseSegmentLine` already implement. Latent bug — pre-cycle-close-auto-realign, plan-swap cycle closes always produced full-cycle next periods (day-of-month preserved), so this branch never saw a stub. The auto-realign shipped earlier this session is what exposed it. Fix mirrors `BillOnCreate`'s proration shape (days-based math, not nanoseconds). Regression test: `TestRunCycle_PlanIntervalChange_InAdvance_StubProrated` ($70/mo plan, 7-day stub of 30-day cycle → 1633 cents = $16.33).
- **`BillOnCancel` int64-overflow fix.** Cancel-proration math used nanoseconds (`baseFee × unusedNanos / periodNanos`); for in_advance plans with base > ~$36 the intermediate product overflowed int64 and the credit grant silently returned 0. Latent bug affecting any real-world plan size — only the synthetic small-amount cancel-proration test passed pre-fix. Swapped to day-based math (`baseFee × unusedDays / periodDays`), same pattern `emitBaseSegmentLine` already uses for segment proration. MANUAL_TEST FLOW B17 gets an explicit regression item.
- **Subscription billing-cycle card surfaces "Renews on <date>" + alignment tooltip (Stripe + Lago + Chargebee + Recurly research, 2026-05-20).** Cross-platform research found three converging patterns: (1) show the *computed* next-renewal date as a concrete primary label (Recurly "Renews On", Chargebee "Next Billing Date", Stripe's `current_period_end`); (2) keep the configured `billing_time` policy separate from the computed dates (Lago's `billing_time` vs `subscription_at` shape); (3) plan-interval changes preserve the historical day-of-month anchor (Stripe `billing_mode=flexible` / Lago / Chargebee — three-platform convergence; only Stripe legacy mode + Recurly auto-re-anchor). Velox already matches the preserve-anchor behavior; the UX was misleading because the page showed `Calendar` + period like `May 20 → Jun 20` and operators reasonably assumed bug. The fix in this PR is UX-only — behavior is unchanged.
  - **`SubscriptionDetail` stat card** changes the primary label from "Current period: May 20 — Jun 20" to "Renews Jun 20, 2029" with the period range demoted to a muted secondary line. Eliminates the "is this a bug?" misread when the anchor doesn't match the configured alignment.
  - **Details panel** adds a "Renews on" row above the "Current period" row so the two reads stay distinct (Lago split between configured policy + computed value).
  - **"Billing Time" row renamed to "Billing alignment"** (operator-friendly per `feedback_ui_copy_no_engineering_jargon`) and gets a `?` tooltip explaining: "Anniversary"/"Calendar" alignment + how the first period anchors at activation + that plan-interval changes (yearly→monthly) preserve the existing day-of-month anchor and don't auto-re-snap to the calendar boundary. Closes the "Calendar config + day-20 anchor = bug?" interpretation gap.
  - **No operator-driven "Reset billing cycle" action** — initially planned, briefly shipped, then reverted. The cycle-close auto-realign covers the drifted-anchor case naturally on the next cycle close (no operator action needed). Standalone reset is segment-specific (Stripe / Chargebee / Recurly have it; AI-native peers Orb / Lago / Metronome don't ship it as a standalone verb), so deferred per `feedback_pre_launch_scoping` until a named DP demands it.
- **Invoice detail action surface collapsed into primary CTA + overflow menu (Stripe / Linear / Vercel pattern).** Pre-fix the header could host 8-10 buttons flowing across the page (Add Line Item, Apply Coupon, Finalize, Void, Email, Issue Credit, Record Payment, Mark Uncollectible, Copy Link, Rotate, Collect Payment, Preview PDF, Download PDF) — every action shipped this session compounded the crowding. New shape:
  - **One primary CTA** per state: Finalize (draft), Collect Payment (finalized-unpaid with PM), Download PDF (terminal: paid/voided/uncollectible). Processing-state has no primary (transient — operator waits).
  - **One overflow menu** (⋯) holds everything else, grouped: recovery/state-change (Record Payment, Mark Uncollectible) → customer-facing (Email, Copy Link, Rotate) → document (Preview/Download PDF, Issue Credit) → destructive (Void, separated and red).
  - **Draft retains inline edit buttons** (Add Line Item, Apply Coupon) — they're editing actions mutating the line-items table directly below, not state-transitions, so they belong in the editing-page chrome rather than the action menu.
- **Uncollectible invoice e2e flow redesigned for Stripe + Chargebee + Recurly parity.** Cross-platform research 2026-05-20 (quoted source lines from each vendor's docs in the audit memo) showed three converging contracts: (1) uncollectible is bad-debt write-off, distinct from void; (2) subscription stays active, operator decides separately; (3) Stripe allows forward transition to paid or void. The pre-fix Velox surface diverged from this on five points:
  - **Dunning resolve dialog cross-flow gap.** Picking "Write off invoice" in the resolve dialog updated only `dunning_runs.resolution` to a stringly-typed `invoice_not_collectible` value (no enum constant existed); the underlying invoice stayed `finalized`+`payment_status=failed`. Now: `ResolutionInvoiceNotCollectible` constant added; `dunning.Service.ResolveRun` cross-flows into `invoice.Service.MarkUncollectible` when that resolution is picked (per `feedback_audit_overlapping_flows` — same operator intent, two entry points, must converge). Test `TestResolveRun_InvoiceNotCollectible_CascadesToInvoice` locks the contract; `TestResolveRun_OtherResolutionsDoNotCascade` gates the branch.
  - **Service-layer audit + event dispatch for MarkUncollectible.** Pre-fix the audit-write lived only in the HTTP handler — the dunning automated `mark_uncollectible` final-action AND the new cross-flow resolve path bypassed it. Now `invoice.Service` carries an `AuditLogger` + `EventDispatcher` wiring; `MarkUncollectible` writes `invoice.update` audit (`action=marked_uncollectible`) and dispatches `invoice.marked_uncollectible` (Stripe-matched event name) regardless of caller.
  - **InvoiceAttention banner no longer surfaces on uncollectible.** `domain.ClassifyInvoiceAttention` short-circuits to `nil` for `InvoiceUncollectible` alongside the existing `InvoicePaid`/`InvoiceVoided` carve-out — the operator has already acknowledged the bad debt, surfacing a `payment_failed` attention banner on top contradicts that decision.
  - **OperatorContext / Diagnosis card hidden on uncollectible.** SPA `InvoiceDetail.showOperatorContext` gate dropped the carve-out for `voided && last_payment_error` (Velox's pre-uncollectible-status stand-in) and now explicitly excludes uncollectible. The page hosts a new amber **status banner** instead: "Marked uncollectible — recorded as bad debt. Dunning halted. Subscription remains active — cancel separately if needed." with deep-link to the owning subscription.
  - **Stripe-parity recovery affordance.** New `POST /v1/invoices/{id}/record-payment` endpoint accepts an optional operator memo (cheque #, wire ref) and flips the invoice to `status=paid` via `Store.MarkPaid` (atomic status + payment_status + amount transition). Works on finalized-unpaid AND uncollectible (Stripe's `paid_out_of_band=true` shape). `StripePaymentIntentID` is prefixed `out_of_band:` so reporting can distinguish engine-collected charges from operator-recorded ones. Active dunning runs resolve to `payment_recovered`. New SPA **Record Payment** button on the invoice detail page; new event `invoice.payment_recorded`.
  - **New direct endpoint `POST /v1/invoices/{id}/mark-uncollectible`** for operator-driven write-off without going through dunning. Halts any active dunning run server-side.
  - **Copy fixes:** the dunning resolve dialog's "Write off invoice" branch no longer claims it'll "void the invoice, reverse credits, cancel the Stripe PaymentIntent" — that was the void contract. Now reads: "Marks the invoice uncollectible (bad debt). Halts dunning automation. The invoice stays on the books for audit. Subscription stays active — cancel separately if needed." The Void confirm dialog also separates the two concepts ("Voiding annuls the invoice… For 'we tried to collect and failed', use Mark Uncollectible instead").
- **`pause_collection` auto-resume promoted to a dedicated scan (Stripe-parity).** Pre-fix the auto-resume gate lived inside `billOnePeriod` — it only fired when a cycle was due. A sub whose `resumes_at` had passed but whose `next_billing_at` was still in the future stayed paused indefinitely (first surfaced via test-clock advance past `resumes_at` on a sub whose cycle wasn't due). The new mechanism has two entry points that pair with the existing trial-expiry phases: (1) catchup orchestrator Phase 0.7 (`subscription.Service.ProcessExpiredPauseCollectionsForClock`) runs in the Advance worker before cycle billing; (2) wall-clock scheduler step 0.95 (`subscription.Service.ProcessExpiredPauseCollections`) runs on every cron tick before `RunCycle`. Both clear `pause_collection_*` AT `resumes_at`, write `subscription.update` audit with `triggered_by=schedule`, and dispatch `subscription.collection_resumed`. The engine's in-cycle gate has been removed — no belt-and-suspenders per `feedback_no_belt_and_suspenders` (single canonical resume path). New store methods `ListExpiredPauseCollections` + `ListExpiredPauseCollectionsForClock` (ADR-028 disjoint partition). One regression test: `TestProcessExpiredPauseCollections` covers three cases (resumes_at past → resume, future → keep, indefinite/nil → keep). Engine test `TestRunCycle_PauseCollection_AutoResumesWhenResumesAtPasses` removed since the behavior no longer lives there.
- **Subscription audit log moved to the service layer for pause / resume collection.** Pre-fix the audit write lived inside the HTTP handler — which meant dunning's `final_action=pause` path (which goes through `subscriptionPauserAdapter` → `subscription.Service.PauseCollection`, bypassing the handler) produced no audit row, leaving the Activity timeline blank for every sub paused by exhausted dunning. New shape: `subscription.Service.SetAuditLogger(AuditLogger)` wired in router.go; `Service.PauseCollection` writes `subscription.update` with `action=collection_paused` and a new `triggered_by` discriminator (`"operator"` for handler, `"dunning"` for the adapter); `Service.ResumeCollection` writes the matching `collection_resumed` row. Handler's duplicate audit-write was removed — single canonical write path. Activity renderer differentiates the trigger: dunning-driven pause shows **"Collection paused by dunning"** vs operator pause **"Collection paused"** (matches the same pattern as the schedule-driven auto-resume already adopted). Cross-flow audit per `feedback_audit_overlapping_flows` — any future system caller of `Service.PauseCollection` / `ResumeCollection` (PSP webhook callback, scheduled API call, etc) automatically produces an audit row without duplicating logic at each entry point.
- **Activity timeline now records auto-resume of `pause_collection` from the cycle scan.** Pre-fix, manual `POST /v1/subscriptions/{id}/resume-collection` wrote an audit row but the schedule-driven auto-resume (engine's cycle scan clearing `pause_collection_*` once `resumes_at` has passed) only dispatched the webhook + slog — Activity tab on the dashboard showed nothing for the schedule path, breaking Stripe-parity activity feeds (manual visible, automatic invisible). Engine now exposes `SetAuditLogger(AuditLogger)`; the auto-resume branch writes `subscription.update` with `action=collection_resumed`, `triggered_by=schedule`. Activity renderer distinguishes the two paths: schedule-driven shows **"Collection auto-resumed — Scheduled resume date reached"**; manual stays **"Collection resumed"**.
- **Pause Collection "Auto-resume on" picker swapped to the shared `DatePicker`** — consistent with the seven other places in the SPA using it (Coupons, ApiKeys, Invoices, AuditLog, Credits, UsageEvents, CouponDetail). Native `<input type="datetime-local">` renders inconsistently across Safari/Chrome/Firefox and accepted no typed-date variations; the shared component is `react-day-picker` + popover + format-tolerant typed input (matches Stripe / Linear / Vercel dashboard pattern). Date-only precision is intentional — catchup picks the pause back up on the next cycle close on or after `resumes_at`, matching Stripe's dashboard pause UX.
- **Extend Trial "New trial end" picker swapped to the shared `DateTimePicker`** (same component TestClocks uses) — date + minute-precision time, both keyboard-typeable, tenant-TZ-aware via `fromZonedTime`. Pre-fix the dialog used the native `datetime-local` input which had the same browser-inconsistency + typed-input gaps as the pause picker. Minute precision retained because trial end is wall-clock-significant (a customer's trial countdown widget shows the exact minute).
- **Dunning final-action enum aligned with industry (ADR-036 amendment)** — verified 2026-05-16 across [Stripe](https://docs.stripe.com/billing/revenue-recovery/smart-retries) (Cancel default + Mark Uncollectible + Pause), [Lago](https://getlago.canny.io/feature-requests/p/trigger-automatic-subscription-termination-based-on-dunning-campaigns) (terminate), [Orb](https://docs.withorb.com/invoicing/advanced-dunning) (retry + email only), [Recurly](https://docs.recurly.com/recurly-subscriptions/docs/dunning-management) (expire + leave overdue + mark failed). Velox now exposes the converging four-action set: `manual_review`, `pause`, `mark_uncollectible`, `cancel_subscription`. Two semantic fixes: (1) `pause` previously called hard `PauseAtomic` (silently skipped invoice generation per ADR-035 analysis); now calls `subscription.Service.PauseCollection(behavior=keep_as_draft)` — Stripe-aligned, cycle keeps drafting. (2) Renamed pre-amendment `write_off_later` → `mark_uncollectible` (industry-standard spelling); added net-new `cancel_subscription` (Stripe-default, was missing from Velox). Migration 0088 expands the `dunning_policies.final_action` CHECK; migration 0089 adds `uncollectible` to the `invoices.status` CHECK (new `InvoiceStatusUncollectible` enables true Stripe-parity for the mark-uncollectible terminal — distinct from voided, preserves invoice in financial reporting). New `invoice.Service.MarkUncollectible` method; new `dunning.SubscriptionCanceler` + `InvoiceUncollectibleMarker` interfaces with router-side adapters. SPA `DunningPolicies` dropdown shows the four Stripe-aligned labels ("Pause collection (keep drafting invoices)" makes the keep_as_draft semantics explicit). Old `write_off_later` rows backfilled to `mark_uncollectible` in the up-migration.
- **Dunning campaigns model (ADR-036)** — multi-policy-per-tenant + per-customer assignment, replacing the singleton policy + partial-field-override shape. Verified industry shape against [Stripe](https://docs.stripe.com/billing/revenue-recovery/smart-retries) (account-level only, segments via Automations), [Lago](https://doc.getlago.com/guide/dunning/automatic-dunning) (named campaigns + per-customer assignment), [Orb](https://docs.withorb.com/invoicing/advanced-dunning) (rules + schedules), [Recurly](https://docs.recurly.com/recurly-subscriptions/docs/dunning-management) (campaigns + per-account assignment) — all four converge on **named templates + assign-to-customer**. Velox adopts the superset shape used by Lago/Recurly: multiple `dunning_policies` per tenant (one `is_default=true`, enforced by a partial UNIQUE index), customers carry an optional `dunning_policy_id` FK (NULL = use tenant default). Per-run `policy_id` persists at `StartDunning` time so mid-flight retries stay on their original policy even if the customer's assignment changes — the new assignment takes effect on the next run. Save-time validation now rejects `max_retry_attempts > len(retry_schedule) + 1`; the runtime "reuse last interval when index out of bounds" silent-fallback branch is removed (`feedback_no_silent_fallbacks`). New endpoints: `GET / POST / PATCH / DELETE /v1/dunning/policies/{id}`, `POST /v1/dunning/policies/{id}/set-default`. New `dunning_policy_id` field on `PATCH /v1/customers/{id}`. Dropped: singleton `/v1/dunning/policy`, all `/v1/dunning/customers/{id}/override` endpoints, the `customer_dunning_overrides` table (migration 0086 drops it — pre-launch zero data to migrate). Frontend: new `/dunning-policies` admin page (list, create, edit, set-default, delete with assigned-customer guard); `CustomerDetail` page replaces "Dunning Override" card with "Dunning policy" card + `AssignDunningPolicyDialog` picking from the policy list; `/dunning` page drops the Policy tab in favor of a single Runs view with a "Manage policies" link to the admin page. ADR-036 documents the design + rejection of alternatives (`CustomerDunningOverride.retry_schedule` extension, Stripe-style account-level-only, Orb-style rules engine).
- **"Sent emails" section on customer detail page.** Operators can now see every customer-facing email Velox dispatched for a given customer (last 30 days, newest first) without leaving the dashboard. **Anchored on Stripe specifically** ([docs.stripe.com/invoicing/send-email](https://docs.stripe.com/invoicing/send-email) — explicit "Sent emails" section on the customer page, 30-day window), not on a converging industry pattern: 2026-05-16 multi-platform verification found that Recurly explicitly lacks this surface ("does not have native, user-facing reports or data exports specifically for email deliveries"), Lago / Orb docs don't describe an operator-facing email log either way. Kept the feature because the operator audit gap it fills (dunning testing produces multiple emails per invoice; without this view the only trail is Mailpit or raw SQL) earns its keep regardless of broader convergence. New backend endpoint `GET /v1/customers/{id}/sent-emails` returns `[{id, email_type, recipient, status, invoice_number?, last_error?, created_at, dispatched_at?}]`. Backed by `email.OutboxStore.ListByCustomer` which joins `email_outbox → invoices` on `invoice_number` and filters by `customer_id` with a 30-day window. Frontend: new "Sent emails" card on `CustomerDetail.tsx` rendering type, recipient, send time, status pill (dispatched / failed / pending); failed rows surface `last_error` inline. Invoice number is a navigable link. As part of this change, `dunning_warning` and `dunning_escalation` email rows are now suppressed from the invoice activity timeline composer — those rows surface exclusively in the customer-page section, eliminating the wall-clock-vs-simulated-time visual mismatch on the invoice timeline (email actually sent at real-world May 16; the engine retry it represented was at simulated Mar 4).

### Removed

- **"Reset billing cycle" operator action — reverted (2026-05-21).** Shipped on a 3-of-4-platform "industry convergence" framing (Stripe + Chargebee + Recurly + Lago). Subsequent peer-set audit added Orb + Metronome and showed the AI-native peers (Velox's actual target market per `project_positioning_wedge`) are 1-of-3 on this feature, not convergent: Orb has it bundled into the plan-change endpoint (not a standalone verb), Lago + Metronome require terminate+recreate. Traditional SaaS billing (Stripe + Chargebee + Recurly) all ship it; the convergence is segment-specific. Per `feedback_pre_launch_scoping`, at zero customers with no named DP demand, the feature is premature. The load-bearing fix it was originally pitched against — calendar-billing day-of-month drift after yearly→monthly plan swaps — is fully addressed by the cycle-close auto-realign (separate fix, kept). Removed: `POST /v1/subscriptions/{id}/reset-billing-cycle` endpoint, `subscription.Service.ResetBillingCycle`, `billing.Engine.BillOnCycleReset`, `Biller.BillOnCycleReset` interface method, `domain.EventSubscriptionBillingCycleReset` constant, SPA "Reset cycle" button + dialog, SDK `resetSubscriptionBillingCycle`, activity-timeline `billing_cycle_reset` renderer case, two engine tests + one service test. Kept: `BillOnCancel` int64-overflow fix (separate latent bug), cycle-close auto-realign (separate fix), `domain.NextBillingPeriodEnd`/`BeginningOfDayIn`/`BeginningOfMonthIn` shared helpers. Pattern lesson: industry-research peer set must match Velox's target market segment, not default to the traditional SaaS billing platforms.
- **Hard-pause API surface fully removed (PR-8, Tier 1 + Tier 2).** PR-6 took the misleading "Pause subscription" option out of the dashboard but left the backend in place; PR-8 finishes the deletion. **Tier 1 (API + frontend):** routes `POST /v1/subscriptions/:id/pause` + `/resume` deleted, `Handler.pause` + `Handler.resume` deleted, `Service.Pause` + `Service.Resume` deleted, `Store.PauseAtomic` + `Store.ResumeAtomic` deleted (interface + postgres + memstore), SDK `api.pauseSubscription` + `api.resumeSubscription` deleted, dead `resumeMutation` + `status === 'paused'` Resume button block deleted from `SubscriptionDetail.tsx`, `EventSubscriptionPaused` + `EventSubscriptionResumed` enum constants deleted. **Tier 2 (schema):** `domain.SubscriptionPaused` enum constant deleted; migration **0090** drops `'paused'` from `subscriptions.status` CHECK with a safety guard that errors loudly if any row is in paused state (pre-launch: zero data, moot in practice); OpenAPI spec updated and types regenerated. **Industry framing corrected in ADR-037**: the earlier "no industry analog" claim was wrong — Chargebee and Recurly both ship hard pause with cycle skip (quoted source lines in the ADR). Velox deferred for scope and lack of named demand from the AI-infra Series A-B wedge market; `pause_collection` (Stripe-style soft pause) covers the legitimate "operator wants to freeze charging" use case. The ADR captures the Chargebee/Recurly e2e shape (paused_at + resume_at + remaining_pause_cycles + unbilled-charges decision tree) as the re-implementation starting point if a future DP names the need.
- **Hard "Pause subscription" option removed from the dashboard (Bug #12).** The Pause button now goes straight to **Pause collection** (Stripe-style soft pause — cycle keeps drafting invoices, no charge attempt until resumed). The previous radio-card choice exposed a second "Pause subscription" mode described as *"Freezes the cycle entirely. No usage metering, no invoices generated."* — a description that lied about the implementation: paused subs were excluded from the cycle scan, but on resume the engine immediately caught up and billed every "missed" cycle as if no pause had happened. Industry research found no analog: Stripe's only pause is `pause_collection` (keep_as_draft), Lago's subscription model has cancel-and-recreate, no platform ships true cycle-skip pause. Pre-launch with zero customers and no named use case for cycle-skip semantics (`feedback_pre_launch_scoping`), shipping a description that doesn't match behavior violates `feedback_design_for_production`. Backend API (`POST /v1/subscriptions/{id}/pause`, `Service.Pause`, `PauseAtomic`, `domain.SubscriptionPaused` status) is preserved as-is — no operator can reach it from the dashboard anymore, but external API callers are unbroken. The dashboard's `pauseSubscription` SDK method in `api.ts` is kept for the same reason. If a future design partner demands true cycle-skip semantics, re-expose with a `paused_at` column migration + proper period-anchor reset on resume; right now the cleanest move is to stop exposing the lie.

### Changed

- **Subscription detail page now reads simulation time on clock-pinned subs and renders trial-specific dots while `status=trialing`.** Two UX bugs fixed in one pass.
  - **(#5) Timeline `isPast` baseline used `new Date()` (wall-clock).** For a clock-pinned sub at sim-Nov-29 viewed in May-2026, every dot was painted as "past" (filled checkmark) because wall-now > every dot's date. Operator saw "completed" markers for events that hadn't happened yet in simulation time. Fix: `const now = sub.test_clock_id && testClock?.frozen_time ? new Date(testClock.frozen_time) : new Date()` — same pattern the `ExpiryBadge` already uses for the trial countdown.
  - **(#4) Timeline labels and the "Billing Period" card mislabeled trialing subs.** Pre-fix labels read `Created → Last Period → Period End → Next Billing` with the period dates pointing at the first POST-trial cycle (Dec 13 → Jan 1 after PR-2). Confusing two ways: (a) "Last Period" implied a billing period had already happened — none had; (b) the trial window itself (Nov 29 → Dec 13) was invisible. Fix: when `status === 'trialing'`, the timeline renders `Created → Trial ends → First charge`, and the "Billing Period" stat card switches its heading to `Trial period` showing `trial_start_at → trial_end_at`, with a small `First billing: …` sub-line for the post-trial cycle. The details panel below mirrors the same labelling, surfacing both the trial window and the first-chargeable-period in distinct rows. Active / paused / canceled subs are unchanged — they still use `Period Start / Period End / Next Billing`. Industry parity: Stripe's dashboard surfaces `Trial ends` as the dominant trialing-state field; Lago's customer detail does the same.

### Changed

- **"Billing Period" stat card renamed to "Current period" on the subscription detail + plan detail pages.** Same data (`current_period_start → current_period_end`); the old label implied "what's about to be billed," which lies for `in_advance` plans where the period was billed at its start (a customer reading the label after Phase 0.5 fired BillOnCreate could legitimately think the dashboard was showing an unbilled period). "Current period" matches Stripe's terminology and means what it says: the consumption window the customer is in, agnostic of when each line on the corresponding invoice fires. The trialing-state copy ("Trial period" + sub-line "First billing: …") is unchanged. The details panel below the stat card uses "First billing period" while trialing and "Current period" once active.
- **ADR-037 amended (2026-05-18) with cross-platform verification of the `in_advance` + metered usage invoice shape.** Stripe, Lago, and Chargebee each researched with quoted source lines. Result: Stripe + Lago both ship the hybrid invoice (next-period base + just-elapsed-period usage on one invoice at cycle close); Chargebee diverges (disallows the combination — metered subs cannot bill the base in advance). Velox follows the Stripe + Lago pattern; the Chargebee-strict validation guard is intentionally not adopted. Operator-facing implication captured in the ADR: a single invoice combines period-(N+1) base lines with period-N usage lines for an in_advance metered customer; the dashboard's per-line `billing_period_start/end` surfaces the distinction.
- **Cross-bill-timing plan-swap now rejected (in_arrears ↔ in_advance).** Pre-fix, the UI's Change Plan dialog accepted any active plan as the swap target; the backend's `rejectMixedItemIntervals` validation only checked `BillingInterval`, not `BaseBillTiming`. An operator could swap a single-item sub from in_arrears $29/mo to in_advance $49/mo, and the engine's hybrid invoice shape — which assumes a uniform bill_timing across items — was never exercised end-to-end for cross-bill-timing transitions (no E2E test for the boundary swap or the immediate-prorated path). Two guards added: (1) `rejectMixedItemIntervals` extended to also reject mixed `BaseBillTiming` on the post-change item set — covers Create / AddItem / multi-item UpdateItem; (2) explicit single-item guard inline in `UpdateItem` that rejects when the current item's plan timing differs from the new plan's timing — covers the single-item swap case that the post-change-set check can't catch (len < 2). Empty `BaseBillTiming` defaults to `in_arrears` to match the engine's lenient defaults so pre-ADR-031 plans validate cleanly. Error message steers the operator to cancel + recreate the sub. Four new tests: `Create rejects mixed in_arrears + in_advance items`, `UpdateItem rejects plan-swap that changes bill_timing on single-item sub (immediate=false)`, `(immediate=true)`, and a `UpdateItem allows plan-swap when bill_timing matches` no-regress guard.
- **UpdateItem plan-change now also rejects mixed intervals.** Closes the gap left by the original mixed-interval validation, which only fired at `Create` + `AddItem`. Pre-fix an operator could create a multi-item monthly sub and then swap one item's plan to a yearly plan — sub silently became mixed-interval and the per-sub period anchor drifted. Both immediate and scheduled plan-changes are gated at request time (Stripe parity — you can't queue a state that would be invalid when it lands). Single-item plan-change to a different interval is NOT covered — that's a clean interval swap, not a mix, and other platforms permit it. New test `UpdateItem rejects plan-change that would mix intervals on a multi-item sub`.
- **Mixed billing-interval items now rejected at Create + AddItem (Stripe / Lago / Chargebee parity).** Pre-fix, a sub with one monthly plan and one yearly plan would have an incoherent cycle (the period anchor is per-sub and uses the first item's interval). Validation runs after Create's item-dedupe + billing_time check and after AddItem's status check; `s.rejectMixedItemIntervals(items)` fetches each item's plan via the wired `PlanReader` and asserts every interval matches the first. Empty `BillingInterval` is treated as monthly (matches the engine's `advanceBillingPeriod` default — old plans validate cleanly). Plan-fetch errors surface as `errs.Invalid("items", ...)` so the operator sees a 400, not a 500. Skipped when PlanReader isn't wired (narrow unit tests). Two new test cases: `Create rejects mixed monthly + yearly items` and `AddItem rejects mismatched interval against existing sub`. UpdateItem plan-change doesn't yet re-validate — separate follow-up.
- **Trial-expiry scan paths now fire `subscription.trial_ended` webhook to match the engine auto-flip path.** Pre-fix, only the engine's `billOnePeriod` auto-flip at cycle close dispatched the event. The catchup orchestrator's Phase 0.5 (clock-pinned, PR-4) and the scheduler's phase 0.9 (wall-clock, PR-5) flipped status without firing the webhook — consumers downstream missed the trial-end signal for subs activated by the new orchestrator phases. Fix: `Subscription.Service` gains `SetEventDispatcher(eventDispatcher)`; both `ProcessExpiredTrialsForClock` and `ProcessExpiredTrials` now dispatch `EventSubscriptionTrialEnded` with `triggered_by="schedule"` after each successful activation (mirrors the engine path's payload shape). New regression test asserts the webhook fires with the correct event type, `triggered_by`, and `subscription_id`. Wiring in `router.go`: `subSvc.SetEventDispatcher(eventDispatcher)` next to the existing `subH.SetEventDispatcher` line.
- **ADR-037 — Trial-end and activation period anchoring.** New ADR documents the post-Bug-1/2/6/8/10/11 contract — the centralized period helpers, the `(billing_time × billing_interval)` matrix, the catchup Phase 0.5 / cron phase 0.9 transitions, and the design tradeoffs (e.g., yearly forces anniversary regardless of billing_time; PlanReader fails open to monthly). Industry shape verified across Stripe and Lago with quoted source lines. Indexed in `docs/adr/README.md`.

### Added

- **Per-event detail sub-lines on subscription activity timeline.** Previously every `update`-action row rendered as "Subscription updated" — operators couldn't tell pause from resume from schedule from threshold change. `describeSubscriptionAction` now exhaustively maps every meta `action` discriminator written by the handler to a meaningful pair of (description, detail sub-line), mirroring the invoice timeline shape:
  - `cancel_scheduled` → "Cancellation scheduled" · "At end of current period" / "On {date}"
  - `cancel_cleared` → "Scheduled cancellation cleared"
  - `collection_paused` → "Collection paused" · "Auto-resumes {date}" / "Cycle keeps drafting; no charge until resumed"
  - `collection_resumed` → "Collection resumed"
  - `trial_ended` → "Trial ended early"
  - `trial_extended` → "Trial extended" · "New trial end: {date}"
  - `billing_thresholds_set` → "Billing thresholds set" · "Amount ≥ N¢ · M item thresholds"
  - `billing_thresholds_cleared` → "Billing thresholds cleared"
  - `item_added` → "Item added" · "Plan {plan_id} · qty N"
  - `item_removed` → "Item removed" · "Item {item_id}"
  - `cancel_pending_item_plan_change` → "Pending plan change canceled"
  - `subscription.item_updated` (plan changed) → "Plan changed" · "{old_plan_id} → {new_plan_id} · Immediate | At next period"
  - `subscription.item_updated` (quantity changed) → "Quantity changed" · "To qty N · Immediate | At next period"
  - `subscription.proration_failed` → "Proration failed" · {error}
  - New `Detail` field on the backend `timelineEvent` struct (matches invoice shape); frontend renders it as a sub-line below the description with the same styling as InvoiceDetail.tsx. RFC3339 timestamps in meta (`cancel_at`, `resumes_at`, `trial_end`) humanize via `formatAuditTimestamp` to `Jan 2, 2006 3:04 PM UTC`. Dead `AuditActionPause` / `AuditActionResume` cases removed (hard pause was deleted in PR-8). Unknown meta actions fall through to "Subscription updated" — feed never silently drops a row.
- **"simulated" chip on subscription activity timeline rows (matches invoice timeline shape).** Backend stamps `is_simulated` on each timeline event — `true` for audit-sourced rows on a clock-pinned sub (their `created_at` is in frozen-time via PR-11/12 + b46bdee), `false` on wall-clock subs. SPA renders the existing amber-tinted "simulated" pill on flagged rows, identical to `InvoiceDetail.tsx`. Authoritative backend flag — no client-side timestamp heuristic, per `feedback_no_heuristic_proxies`. Caveat acknowledged in the handler comment: pre-PR-11 audit rows in the DB were stamped wall-clock and will be incorrectly flagged simulated; pre-launch DB-only issue, no migration needed since the operator can spot wall-clock timestamps at a glance.

### Fixed

- **Scheduled plan-swap at period boundary now bills the closing period under the outgoing plan (industry parity).** Pre-fix, `billOnePeriod` ran the pending-swap atomic (`engine.go:1252`) BEFORE the plans map was loaded (`engine.go:1395`), so the just-elapsed period's base fee + usage lines used the INCOMING plan's price and meter set. For a `monthly $29 → yearly $588` scheduled swap, the closing invoice billed $48.33 (yearly prorated to 30 days) instead of $29 (outgoing monthly rate). For same-interval different-price swaps, the closing invoice silently overcharged or undercharged. For usage, meters present on the old plan but not the new plan had their just-elapsed consumption silently dropped. Stripe, Lago, Orb, Recurly all bill the closing cycle under the OUTGOING plan; new plan takes effect from the next period. Velox now matches: a new `outgoingPlanByItem` snapshot is captured BEFORE the swap fires, and the in_arrears base + every usage line on the closing invoice price against the outgoing plan. in_advance plans are unchanged (their boundary line covers the UPCOMING period, which IS under the new plan — correct as-is). Existing regression test `TestRunCycle_AppliesScheduledPlanChangeAtBoundary` re-asserted (was encoding the buggy behavior); new regression `TestRunCycle_ScheduledPlanSwap_CrossInterval_BillsElapsedAtOutgoingPlan` locks the contract for the monthly→yearly case.
- **Immediate cross-interval plan-swap now rejected at request time.** The `(newAmount - oldAmount) * remainingPeriodFactor` proration math only produces a coherent number when both plans share an interval — comparing a monthly $29 to a yearly $588 inside a "remaining-month proportion" factor charges 2/3 of the YEARLY delta for the rest of a month. Stripe requires aligned schedules; Lago and Orb don't allow immediate cross-interval either. `Service.UpdateItem` now returns `errs.Invalid("immediate", …)` with steering to set `immediate=false` (scheduled at next period boundary, which the engine fix above handles correctly). New test `UpdateItem rejects immediate cross-interval plan-swap` covers both rejection and the no-regress scheduled allow.
- **Audit log page consistency — dotted actions resolved + resource_label populated.** Two inconsistencies the user surfaced from the global Audit log view: (1) every subscription audit row showed "subscription" as the resource name (`resource_label` column always empty), and (2) `subscription.item_updated` / `subscription.proration_failed` actions fell through to the default-case formatter, rendering as ugly `"subscription.item updated subscription"` next to clean labels like "Created" / "Canceled".
  - `AuditLog.tsx` `describeAction`: explicit cases for `subscription.item_updated` (reads `metadata.action` discriminator → "Changed plan for X" / "Changed quantity for X") and `subscription.proration_failed` → "Proration failed on X". `subscription.item_updated` also added to MEDIUM_SEVERITY so the row highlights correctly.
  - Subscription handler: new `subAuditMeta(sub, extra)` helper always sets `resource_label = sub.Code` on the audit metadata; resource_label always wins over any extra-supplied value. Applied to 11 audit Log call sites where `sub` is locally available (create, activate, cancel, scheduleCancel, pauseCollection, resumeCollection, endTrial, extendTrial, billing-thresholds set/cleared, clearScheduledCancel). Item-level paths that have only `subID` (proration_failed, item_added, item_removed) skipped — separate follow-up if needed (would require an extra DB round-trip per audit row).
- **Cancel-proration credit now surfaces on the subscription activity timeline.** Pre-fix the credit grant fired correctly (in_advance unused-base refund) but the only place an operator could find the amount was the customer's credit ledger. The subscription's activity timeline showed "Subscription canceled" with no link to the resulting credit. Industry standard — Stripe / Lago / Chargebee / Orb all surface the credit on the subscription's event feed AND on the customer's credit balance, so operators can answer "what happened on cancel?" without cross-referencing.
  - `engine.BillOnCancel(ctx, sub) error` → `(int64, error)` returning the credit cents granted (0 when none — in_arrears sub, clean cancel, unpaid source invoice).
  - `subscription.Service.Cancel(ctx, tenantID, id) (Subscription, error)` → `(Subscription, int64, error)` propagating the credit amount up to the handler.
  - `Handler.cancel` adds `prorated_credit_cents` to the cancel audit-log entry's metadata when > 0.
  - `describeSubscriptionAction`'s `AuditActionCancel` case now renders the detail sub-line: "Prorated credit issued: $24.50".
  - `credit.GrantInput.SourceSubscriptionID` populated from BillOnCancel so the credit ledger entry is bidirectionally linked to the sub (was previously nil — credit was orphaned at the ledger level).
  - Two callers updated for the Service signature change (handler + customer-portal SubscriptionCanceler adapter). `portalapi.SubscriptionService` interface updated. Test fakes (`fakeBiller`, `fakeSubscriptionService`) extended with the new return value. Existing `TestBillOnCancel_PaidCheck` extended to assert the returned cents amount matches the granter's input (downstream timeline math depends on this).
- **Empty cycle-close invoices ($0, zero line items) no longer emitted.** Closes a known-but-deferred follow-up from PR-9 (the in_advance + scheduled-cancel-at-period-end fix). When the base-fee + usage assembly produces zero line items at cycle close, the engine now advances the cycle but does NOT persist an invoice. Matches Stripe / Lago / Chargebee / Orb — none of them emit $0 cycle invoices. Also matches the existing zero-subtotal guards in `BillOnCreate` and `BillFinalOnImmediateCancel`; `billOnePeriod` was the outlier.
  - Three common triggers: (1) `in_advance` + scheduled cancel-at-period-end (upcoming base skipped because customer won't use it; no usage to bill either); (2) `in_arrears` item removed mid-period leaving no current items billable at next cycle; (3) free plan with no usage events.
  - `subtotal == 0 && len(lineItems) == 0` → `advanceCycleOrCancel` + return without persisting invoice. No invoice number consumed (the monotonic sequence stays gap-free). Existing `TestRunCycle_InAdvance_ScheduledCancelAtPeriodEnd_NoOvercharge` updated to assert zero invoices instead of "$0 invoice OK"; new `TestRunCycle_SkipEmptyCycleInvoice_NoChargeAttempt` locks the general free-plan / zero-usage case.
- **Activity timeline now shows plan names instead of raw IDs.** Pre-fix the subscription activity feed surfaced raw `vlx_pln_d83g2obmajdtlif0mk00`-style identifiers in the detail sub-line for `item_added`, `item_plan_changed`, etc. — operator-illegible noise that no industry billing platform (Stripe / Lago / Chargebee / Orb) exposes in user-facing copy. Detail-page surfaces (MeterDetail, plan detail) still show the ID with a Copy button — that's industry-standard developer affordance and stays.
  - New `planLabel(planID, planNames)` helper resolves to the plan name when the lookup hits; falls back to the raw ID only when the plan is deleted / RLS-gapped / unwired-test path.
  - `describeSubscriptionAction` signature extended to accept the lookup map. Refactored at three call sites: `item_added` ("Pro Monthly · qty 1" not "Plan vlx_pln_… · qty 1"), `item_plan_changed` ("Pro Monthly → Enterprise" not "vlx_pln_old → vlx_pln_new"), `item_removed` (dropped the `vlx_si_…` item_id entirely — "Item removed" alone reads clean).
  - `activityTimeline` handler batch-fetches every plan_id referenced in the audit entries' metadata (`plan_id`, `old_plan_id`, `new_plan_id`, `plan_ids[]`) before invoking `describeSubscriptionAction` so the per-entry render is single-pass.
- **"Outstanding balance" card on customer detail page (AR exposure surface).** Velox previously showed Credit Balance (positive, what the merchant owes the customer) but had no operator-facing surface for the inverse — total unpaid invoice amount this customer owes the merchant. Industry parity: Stripe customer overview tile, Lago / Chargebee / Recurly all show "Outstanding balance: $X" on the customer page. Without this, operators had to walk per-invoice to sum exposure for a delinquent customer.
  - New `invoice.Store.GetOutstandingBalance(tenant, customer)` returns `{total_cents, unpaid_count}` across all finalized invoices in `payment_status` pending / failed / unknown, excluding voided + uncollectible + draft (the three states that don't count as collectable AR).
  - Customer overview endpoint (`/v1/customer-portal/{id}/overview`) extended with the new `outstanding_balance` block.
  - `CustomerDetail.tsx` renders a stat cell next to Credit Balance: red-tinted amount + sub-text "N invoices", links to the customer's invoice list. Hidden when zero — keeps the row uncluttered on healthy customers.
- **Card declines no longer escalate a test-clock catchup to `internal_failure`.** Pre-fix `engine.processAutoCharge` returned every `ChargeInvoice` error to its caller without classification — including routine card declines. The test-clock catchup orchestrator (`testclock.Service`) treated any returned error as a fatal failure, flipped the clock to `status='internal_failure'`, and stamped `last_failure_reason` with the concatenated decline messages. Observed in user testing: a clock advanced through 30+ months ended up in `internal_failure` with `last_failure_reason='Card was declined: …; Card was declined: …; …'` even though dunning was correctly running for each declined invoice.
  - Fix in `processAutoCharge` (`engine.go:3237`): classify the error before returning. `*payment.PaymentError` with non-empty `DeclineCode` → expected business outcome, **don't escalate**. `ChargeInvoice` already inline-fires `StartDunning` and stamps `invoice.payment_status='failed'` (stripe.go:401-426), so dunning takes over. `payment.ErrPaymentTransient` (breaker open / pre-Stripe timeout) → also skipped silently; next catchup tick retries. `Unknown=true` payment errors (5xx, network drop, ambiguous PI state) AND non-Stripe errors (config, infrastructure) still escalate — the catchup operator needs visible feedback for those, and the reconciler needs to follow up on Unknown.
  - `AutoChargePending` is cleared on decline so the next catchup tick doesn't re-pick the same invoice — dunning's retry schedule drives subsequent attempts. Industry parity: Stripe Test Clocks don't fail when a tester uses a decline-card.
  - New regression test `TestRetryPendingCharges_CardDeclineDoesNotEscalate` locks the contract: a charger returning `*payment.PaymentError{DeclineCode: "card_declined"}` produces zero escalated errors AND clears `AutoChargePending`.
- **Four invoice-emitting paths now share one draft-finalized gate.** Pre-fix only `engine.billOnePeriod` correctly forced an invoice to `draft` when tax was deferred (`tax_status='pending'`); the three sibling paths (`engine.BillOnCreate`, `engine.BillFinalOnImmediateCancel`, `subscription.handleItemProration`) hardcoded `InvoiceFinalized` regardless. Result: an invoice with `tax_status=pending` and `tax_error_code=customer_data_invalid` could finalize with `TaxAmountCents=0`, lying about authoritative amounts — exactly the scenario the user surfaced (`subscription_create` invoice finalized while the next-cycle invoice on the same sub stayed draft). Industry rationale: a finalized invoice's `TotalAmountCents` is the customer-facing owed amount; finalizing with deferred tax means the books understate liability until the retry worker resolves it.
